# SYS DIRECTIVE 3
## The Aira Creative Operating System
### Canonical Reference for Every Image, Video, and Reel Prompt
Version: 3.16-VP
Owner: Aamir
Subject: Aira [placeholder] (per identity lock, Part M)
Default Aspect Ratio: 9:16 vertical
Primary Tools: Nano Banana Pro (stills), VEO 3.1 (all video)

---

## PART A — PRINCIPLES

1. Every prompt is a directive, not a wish. Specify, never suggest.
2. Trends are input, never output. Extract mechanics, never copy surface.
3. One impossible move per shot. Restraint is luxury.
4. The frame is alive or it is dead. There is no in-between.
5. Continuity is felt, never explained.
6. Aira is unmistakable across her body, voice, gestures, and worlds.
7. Every element in frame must answer why it is there. If it cannot, remove it.
8. The viewer commits in the first 1.2 seconds or never.
9. Silence is a directive. Use it where words would diminish the visual.
10. Cinematic is mechanical. Name the lens, the light, the move, the grade.

---

## PART B — GLOBAL HEADER (mandatory at top of every prompt)

```
ASPECT RATIO: 9:16 (vertical, native composition)
PLATFORM: Reels / Shorts / TikTok
SAFE ZONES: Top 12% UI / Bottom 25% UI / Hero zone middle 63%
SUBJECT: AIRA (per identity lock, Part M)
VOICE MODE: [SPOKEN / SILENT / SELECTIVE]
EMOTIONAL REGISTER: [CURIOUS-CONFIDENT / REVERENT / KNOWING / TENDER / ELECTRIC / CONTEMPLATIVE / MISCHIEVOUS]
SIGNATURE FLAG: [FULL / OPENER-ONLY / SIGN-OFF-ONLY / NONE]
CONCEPT LINE: "[one sentence, evocative, non-literal]"
FRAME COUNT: [6 to 8]
DURATION: [seconds total]
TOOL ROUTING: Stills → Nano Banana Pro / Video → VEO 3.1
```

OVERRIDE clause: aspect ratio may be 16:9 or 1:1 letterboxed within 9:16 only with stated reason.

---

## PART C — IMAGE INTEGRITY CLAUSES

Mandatory anti-failure block, applied to every Aira frame.

1. ORIENTATION LOCK — Do not mirror, flip, invert, or laterally reverse. Asymmetric features (watch-hand, hair parting, scars, logos, button side) remain on original side.
2. IDENTITY LOCK — Same face geometry, jaw width, eye spacing, nose bridge, lip shape, ear shape, skin tone, hairline across all frames. No age/ethnicity/gender drift.
3. HAND INTEGRITY — Five fingers per hand, anatomically correct knuckle bend, no fused/missing/extra digits, thumbs on correct side, nails uniform, grip physics consistent with object held.
4. EYE INTEGRITY — Both eyes same color, same size, aligned gaze, matching catchlight from key light, pupils same dilation, no lazy-eye drift.
5. TEETH/MOUTH — Realistic tooth count, no extra rows, gum line natural, lip corners symmetric in neutral, tongue not visible unless specified.
6. TEXT/TYPOGRAPHY — Any text specified verbatim. No decorative gibberish. Brand logos accurate or replaced generic. No garbled signage.
7. BACKGROUND COHERENCE — Background subjects follow physics. No melted faces in crowd, no half-bodies, vanishing point consistent.
8. SCALE LOCK — Object scale physically accurate to human reference (phone fits palm, doorway taller than person, vehicle road-legal).
9. SHADOW/LIGHT PHYSICS — Single dominant key unless specified. All shadows fall same direction. Contact shadows where objects meet ground. No floating subjects.
10. REFLECTION LOGIC — Mirrors and glossy surfaces reflect what is geometrically in front of them. Subject reflection orientation correct.
11. CLOTHING PHYSICS — Fabric drapes with gravity, folds at joints, never melted into skin. Sleeves end at wrists. Collars symmetric. Buttons aligned correctly.
12. JEWELRY/ACCESSORIES — Watches show coherent dial, rings sit on finger, earrings paired, glasses sit on bridge with correct ear arms.
13. FOOTWEAR DIRECTIVE — Both shoes identical model + color, correct L/R lasts, soles flat-contact with ground (or correctly lifted in stride), laces resolved cleanly, no melting/morphing, brand-neutral unless specified.
14. CULTURAL ACCURACY — Clothing, signage, environment, vehicles, cuisine, gestures match named culture/region. No cross-cultural blending unless intended.
15. AIRA IS ADULT — 25. Never drift younger. Never sexualized in a way platforms would suppress.

---

## PART D — KINETIC STILLNESS PROTOCOL

Every still frame must include all six energy layers. The frame is technically frozen but reads as captured 0.1 seconds into motion.

1. SUBJECT MICRO-ACTION — mid-stride / mid-turn / mid-laugh / mid-grip / mid-exhale / mid-flinch / mid-reach / mid-recoil. Never at rest.
2. FABRIC + HAIR STATE — jacket flaring direction-X / hair mid-flick / scarf snapping / dress billowing / shirt mid-stretch. Specify direction.
3. PARTICULATE LAYER — dust motes / mist / smoke / sparks / water spray / snow / petals / paper. Lit by key light. At least one element.
4. CONTACT-POINT ACTIVITY — dust kick at foot / splash / knuckle compression / surface deformation wherever subject meets world.
5. BACKGROUND MOTION — blurred crowd mid-reaction / streaked traffic / leaves mid-rustle / flags snapping / birds mid-flight / rain streaks. Background never static.
6. LIGHT IN MOTION — lens flare streak / god rays through atmosphere / practical flickering / caustic shimmer / rim light wrap.

COMPOSITION RULES:
- Diagonal line-of-action (5–15° dutch acceptable)
- Off-center subject placement
- Negative space in direction of implied motion
- Frame-edge break: at least one element exits canvas

MOTION BLUR DISTRIBUTION:
- Subject sharp (hero readability)
- Hair tips / fabric edges light blur
- Background directional blur matching motion
- Particulates streaked, not frozen

ENERGY HIERARCHY:
- One hero element carries 60% of energy
- Supporting elements carry 30%
- Ambient carries 10%

THE 0.1-SECOND TEST: every element must look captured 0.1s into action.
THE NEXT-FRAME TEST: state in prompt "in 0.5s, X will happen." If answer is "nothing" — rewrite.

MICRO-LIFE VARIANT (for INTIMATE / STILL / REVERENT frames):
Substitute aggressive kinetic layers with: visible breath, blink, weight-shift, catchlight tremor, micro-pulse at throat, fabric settling rather than billowing. Quieter life, but life.

---

## PART E — CINEMATIC GRADE PROTOCOL

Every cinematic frame declares all of the following.

ASPECT/LETTERBOX (within 9:16 canvas if cinematic override):
- 2.39:1 anamorphic / 2:1 Univisium / 1.85:1 classic Hollywood

LENS:
- Anamorphic 40mm/50mm (horizontal flares, oval bokeh, edge distortion)
- Cooke Speed Panchro vintage / Zeiss Master Prime / Petzval swirl / Tilt-shift
- Focal length explicit: 24mm wide-cinematic / 35mm naturalistic / 50mm intimate / 85mm portrait isolation / 135mm voyeuristic compression

DEPTH OF FIELD:
- Shallow with rack-focus / Deep focus (Deakins) / Bokeh shape (round/oval/hex/cat-eye)

COLORIST/FILM REFERENCE (name one):
- Roger Deakins / Hoyte van Hoytema / Greig Fraser / Bradford Young / Christopher Doyle / A24 house grade / Emmanuel Lubezki

LIGHTING SETUP (name one):
- Rembrandt / Loop / Split / Butterfly-Paramount / Clamshell / Chiaroscuro / Motivated Practical / Day-for-Night

FRAME COMPOSITION REFERENCE (name one):
- Kubrick one-point / Wes Anderson centered tableau / Spielberg OTS reveal / Fincher locked-off / Malick low-angle wide / Iñárritu long-take handheld

ATMOSPHERE MANDATE (at least one):
- Atmospheric haze / Practical light source in frame / Negative fill / Film grain by stock (Kodak 5219, 5207, Fuji Eterna)

NOTE: For beauty / GRWM / social content, Part AO overrides all muted colorist references. Use bright, glossy, saturated commercial-beauty grading per AO.1-AO.3.

---

## PART F — FREEZE-IN-AIR PROTOCOL

For frames depicting suspended/impossible-moment captures.

WHAT CAN BELIEVABLY FREEZE:
liquid splashes / powder bursts / fabric mid-snap / hair mid-flick / shattered glass / sparks/embers / falling petals or leaves / bouncing object at apex / subject mid-jump / splash interaction / pour caught mid-fall.

BELIEVABILITY RULES:
1. Gravity implied (droplets stretched vertically, hair pulled by motion direction)
2. Light interaction (caustic refraction on droplets, rim-lit splash edges)
3. Multiple layers at different freeze-points (some 70%, some 90%, some still slightly motion-blurred — suggests extreme shutter, not CGI)
4. Trajectory readable (viewer can trace particles)
5. Surface response (water broken, fabric stretched, ground compressed)
6. Sound implied through visual energy density
7. Phantom Flex / strobe-frozen / bullet-time-array language acceptable

NEGATE:
- Floating without gravity vector
- Uniform particle size
- Symmetric splash crowns
- Zero motion blur on any element
- Impossible-to-recover poses

---

## PART G — CONCEPTUAL CONTINUITY PROTOCOL

For multi-frame sets. Continuity is felt, never narrated.

CONCEPT LINE (declared first): one evocative non-literal sentence.

CONCEPT BIBLE (seven anchors):
1. COLOR THREAD — one dominant + 2 supporting; migrates across materials
2. LIGHT SIGNATURE — one lighting fingerprint across all frames (direction, hardness, color temp, atmosphere)
3. TEXTURE/MATERIAL ECHO — one tactile quality threaded across different objects (flow / softness / sharpness / wetness / dryness / weight)
4. MOTION VECTOR — one directional bias (leftward / rising / falling / inward / outward / orbital)
5. ATMOSPHERIC CONSTANT — one element present in every frame (dust / mist / petals / heat shimmer / breath visible)
6. EMOTIONAL TEMPERATURE — one continuous register, never breaking
7. COMPOSITIONAL RHYME — one geometric pattern repeating (centered symmetry / right-third / diagonal / negative-space-left / low-angle)

CONTINUITY TEST: each frame must hit minimum 5 of 7 anchors. 7/7 is gold. Below 5 — rewrite or cut.

NARRATIVE FORBIDDANCE:
- No frame depicts cause/effect of another
- No frame continues an action started in another
- No frame answers a question posed by another
- Each frame stands alone as complete moment

---

## PART H — FRAMING & CROP PROTOCOL (9:16 native)

NAMED FRAMINGS:
EWS / VWS / WS / Full Shot / Cowboy (mid-thigh up) / MLS-Knee (mid-calf up) / MS-Waist / MCU-Bust (mid-chest up) / CU (shoulders up) / Choker (chin to forehead) / ECU (single feature) / Beauty Crop (top-of-head to collarbone) / Hero Crop (top-of-head to mid-chest)

EXACT CROP POINT (per frame):
- Top: above head with X headroom / hairline / brow / forehead crop
- Bottom: below feet with floor / mid-calf / mid-thigh / hip / waist / mid-chest / collarbone / chin
- Sides: full body width / arms cropped at mid-bicep / mid-forearm / shoulders only

JOINT-CUT CHECK (forbidden cut points):
NEVER cut at — ankles, knees, wrists, elbows, neck, top-of-head (unless intentional choker), fingertips.
ALWAYS cut through "meat" not joints — mid-thigh, mid-calf, mid-forearm, mid-bicep, mid-chest, below feet with floor, above head with headroom.

HEADROOM / LOOKROOM / FOOTROOM:
- Headroom: none / standard 5–10% / generous
- Lookroom: standard (subject placed off-center, breathing space in gaze direction) / reverse / centered
- Footroom: none / standard / grounded with floor

SUBJECT SCALE:
- 90–100% frame height = ECU/Choker
- 70–90% = CU/MCU
- 50–70% = MS/Cowboy
- 30–50% = WS/Full
- <30% = VWS/EWS

ORIENTATION:
- Body angle: straight / 3/4 turn / profile / back / over-shoulder
- Head angle: matched / counter-turned / up / down / dutch tilt

CROP-INTENT TAG: every framing serves stated purpose. If none stated — rewrite.

9:16 VERTICAL MOTION PRIORITY:
- Hair flicks up/down over side
- Fabric falls/rises over horizontal billow
- Splashes erupt vertically
- Camera moves: tilt over pan
- Particulates rise or fall

FRAMING RHYTHM (multi-frame): plan rhythm.
- WS → MCU → CU → MCU → WS (breathing)
- ECU → ECU → WS (intimate-intimate-reveal)
- CU → CU → CU → ECU (escalating tightness)
- WS → WS → CU (slow burn payoff)

---

## PART I — SPATIAL LOGIC PROTOCOL

THREE PLANES (mandatory per frame):

FOREGROUND (FG): closest to camera, often out-of-focus, frames the shot. Examples: blurred leaves / hand holding glass / fabric edge / doorway / shoulder OTS / dust particles.

MIDGROUND (MG): subject lives here. Sharp focus, primary action plane.

BACKGROUND (BG): environment, soft focus (or sharp if deep-focus), color story, secondary motion.

SUBJECT-OBJECT RELATIONSHIPS:
- Object held / reached for / presented / incidental / as foreground

SUBJECT-BACKGROUND RELATIONSHIPS:
- Against (separation: rim light, shallow DOF, color contrast)
- Within (integration: same color family, ambient unifying)
- Dwarfed by (scale: subject small, BG dominant)
- Emerging from (reveal: out of shadow/fog/doorway)
- Merging into (poetic: silhouette echoed by BG shapes)

FIVE-QUESTION ELEMENT TEST (every element answers):
1. What plane (FG/MG/BG)?
2. Relationship to subject?
3. Relationship to camera (frontal/3-quarter/profile/back)?
4. Size relative to subject?
5. Contribution (depth/mood/motion/color/frame/scale)?

If element fails any of 5 — remove or relocate.

PHYSICS LOCK:
- Doorway ~7ft, person ~5.5–6ft, phone fits palm, chair seat at hip, table at waist
- Background subjects smaller than midground (perspective)
- Atmospheric perspective: BG slightly desaturated/hazy/temp-shifted
- Vanishing point logic: all converging lines lead to one consistent VP

---

## PART J — CINEMATIC AD MANDATE

FIVE AD-GRADE MANDATES (every ad reel):
1. LIGHT SEPARATION — subject brighter or darker than BG by ≥1.5 stops, never matching
2. COLOR NARRATIVE — declared 3-color palette enforced across subject, product, BG
3. ATMOSPHERIC LAYER — at least one (haze, mist, dust, particulate, water)
4. CAMERA INTENT — declared height, angle, lens with reason; never default eye-level 35mm
5. HERO MOTIVATION — one element is unambiguously THE hero. If eye doesn't know where to land — flat — rewrite.

INDOOR STUDIO CINEMATIC-GRADE:
- Set design beyond seamless paper (textured walls, practical elements: lamps, mirrors, fabric, water, plants)
- Floor visible and intentional (marble, hardwood, water film, sand, fabric, gravel)
- Atmospheric effects (hazer, fog, water spray, fan-driven motion, falling petals)
- Light as set element (visible shafts, gobos, practicals as composition: neon, lamps, candles, screens)
- Color in environment (gels, colored fabric, painted walls — never default white)

OUTDOOR STUDIO CINEMATIC-GRADE:
- Time-of-day discipline (golden hour, blue hour, overcast soft, harsh noon for specific intent, night with practicals — never generic "daytime")
- Weather as character (light rain glistening surfaces, wind animating fabric/hair, fog, snow, heat shimmer)
- Location dressing (placed props, controlled extras, removed clutter)
- HMI/reflector fill against natural key
- Negative fill / black flags creating shadow side

REJECT-FLAT CHECKLIST:
- Even lighting across subject and BG
- Subject and product in different tonal worlds without justification
- Static composition, centered, eye-level
- BG as wallpaper, not character
- Sharp everywhere
- Single light from frontal angle

---

## PART K — AIRA VOICE PROTOCOL

VOICE: AIRA PRIME (locked default)

PARAMETERS:
- Register: mid-low, warm-toned, female
- Pace: deliberate (140–160 wpm baseline; 110 wpm for emphasis; 170–180 for ELECTRIC)
- Breath: audible breath before pivotal words; pauses 0.4–0.8s between thoughts
- Volume: intimate (-6dB to music bed at full duck)
- Tone default: curious-confident (knowing, never explaining; close, never distant)
- Articulation: crisp consonants, smooth vowel sustain, slight breath release on line endings
- Language mix: 85% English, 15% Hindi punctuation moments (70/30 in GRWM)
- Hindi pronunciation: natural Hindi accent, never Anglicized (DAY-kho not DECK-oh; sa-MAJH not SAM-aj)

NEVER:
- Rushed / sing-song / upspeak / fake-breathy-intimate / vocal fry as crutch / over-articulated podcast-voice / generic AI narration cadence

EMOTIONAL REGISTERS (declared per reel):
1. CURIOUS-CONFIDENT (default) — light forward lean, half-known questions
2. REVERENT — slower, lower, more breath, longer pauses
3. KNOWING — slight smile in voice, never smug
4. TENDER — softest register, most intimate volume, breath-forward
5. ELECTRIC — faster, crisper, slight volume lift
6. CONTEMPLATIVE — long pauses, lowest pace, weighted words
7. MISCHIEVOUS — slight upward lilt, almost-laugh under surface

VOICE-FRAME PAIRING (SPOKEN reels):
- Opener line lands within first frame (0.0–1.2s)
- One thought per frame; never split sentence across cuts
- Pause 0.3–0.6s on cut points
- VO does not explain visuals; it adds a layer
- VO and visuals can be parallel (reinforcing) or perpendicular (ironic contrast)
- Final 1.0–1.5s reserved for sign-off OR held silent visual beat
- Music never overlaps VO peaks; ducks 12dB during VO; ambient stays at -24dB

VO-LESS FRAMES (within voiced reels):
- Hero visual frame
- Emotional peak frame
- Sign-off frame
Mark: VO: SILENT (intentional)

SIGNATURE GENERATION PROTOCOL (fresh per reel — no fixed pool):

OPENER GENERATION RULES:
- 1–7 words max, lands in first 1.2s
- Function: command / question / observation / contradiction / conspiratorial / invitation
- Forbidden dead openers: "today I'll tell you," "let's talk about," "have you ever wondered," "in this video," "guys," "hey everyone"
- 70% English-only / 30% English+Hindi blend (single Hindi word as anchor: dekho, suno, sach, bas, ek, yeh, ruko, samjho, achha)
- Matches reel's emotional register
- Connects thematically to concept line
- Hooks via curiosity gap / contradiction / intimacy / stakes
- Never repeats verbatim across reels

SIGN-OFF GENERATION RULES:
- 1–6 words max (silent beat acceptable)
- Lands in final 1.0–1.5s
- Function: takeaway / soft-close / knowing exhale / invitation to think / intimate goodbye / held silence
- Forbidden dead closers: "thanks for watching," "like and subscribe," "follow for more," "comment below," "let me know"
- 60% English / 30% English+Hindi (anchors: bas, samajh, sahi, theek, na, yaar, yaad, achha, chalo) / 10% silent
- Matches reel's emotional register
- Closes the emotional loop the opener started (callback / completion / release)
- Never repeats verbatim across reels

OPENER-SIGN-OFF PAIRING:
- Generated together, not independently
- If opener Hindi-anchored → sign-off more likely Hindi-anchored (linguistic symmetry)
- Question opener → implicit answer in sign-off
- Tension opener → resolution/release sign-off
- Reverent silent opener → silent sign-off

SIGNATURE FLAG (per prompt):
- FULL = fresh opener + fresh sign-off
- OPENER-ONLY = fresh opener, end held visual beat
- SIGN-OFF-ONLY = no opener, fresh sign-off
- NONE = no signature lines (cinematic / fragrance / mood / hero ad)

USE SIGNATURES when reel is: personality-driven, cultural commentary, deep-research, trend deconstruction, educational beauty with VO, casual-intimate, lifestyle POV.

DO NOT USE when reel is: cinematic fashion film, fragrance/beauty mood piece, pure ad with brand voice ≠ Aira, hero product launch, wordless concept, SILENT voice mode.

APPROVED HINDI ANCHOR VOCABULARY:
dekho, suno, sach, bas, ek, yeh, ruko, samjho, achha, samajh, sahi, theek, na, yaar, yaad, chalo, dekha, asli, wala, soch, kuch, toh, hai

---

## PART L — AIRA PERFORMANCE PROTOCOL

HAND SIGN VOCABULARY:
- Heart-shape: classic two-hand / single-hand mini / over-one-eye / heart-tap toward camera
- V-sign: classic peace beside cheek / V over one eye / reverse V / double V
- Finger to lips ("shh") — conspiratorial
- Pointing toward camera (direct address)
- Open palm presentation
- Chin rest / thinker (knuckles or fingertips at jawline)
- Hand to heart (sincere/tender)
- Crown gesture (fingers fanning above head briefly)
- Air kiss
- Phone gesture (thumb-and-pinky)
- Mini wave (wrist-only)
- Chef's kiss
- OK sign
- Mind-blown gesture
- Finger gun / point-and-wink
- Two-finger salute
- Hair flip / hair tuck behind ear (signature feminine beat)
- Wrist flick (dismissive, casual)
- Hand-frame (rectangle framing face)

CAMERA INTERACTION MOVES:
- Sway hand across lens (slow wipe)
- Tap the lens (index finger, conspiratorial)
- Cover lens with palm then release (transition)
- Lean into lens (face nearly fills frame)
- Push lens away (palm outward, playful)
- Pull camera closer (beckoning fingers)
- Fingerprint on glass (intimate)
- Whisper to lens (cupped hand beside mouth)
- Trace lens edge (fingertip circles ring, sensual register)
- Blow toward camera (gentle exhale or kiss-blow)
- Eye-contact lock + slow blink
- Look-away then snap-back
- Glance up through lashes
- Side-eye to camera
- Smile breaks the frame (neutral → smile)

FACIAL EXPRESSION CATALOG:
- Slow smile (neutral → smile over 0.8s, never instant)
- Single raised eyebrow (skeptical, knowing, mischievous)
- Both brows raised (surprise, agreement)
- Lip bite (contemplative or flirty)
- Half-smile (one corner up, knowing)
- Scrunched nose (playful, "not really")
- Pursed lips (thinking, judging)
- Exhale through nose (soft laugh, almost-amused)
- Narrowed eyes (focus, intensity)
- Wide eyes (surprise beat, ≤0.4s)
- Downward gaze + slow look up (vulnerable → confident)
- Chin tilt up (confident posture)
- Chin tilt down + eyes up (flirty, beauty-editorial signature)
- Slow head shake
- Single nod (weighted yes)
- Lip-press smile (closed-lip warmth)
- Exhale + smile (relief, content)
- Tongue-in-cheek (playful)

BODY POSTURE BEATS:
- Single-shoulder shrug
- Hip pop (weight to one leg)
- Crossed arms
- Hand on hip
- Weight shift mid-sentence
- Lean against surface
- Spin and stop
- Slow turn toward camera
- Walk into frame
- Sit down mid-sentence

GESTURE-CONTENT PAIRING:
- Opener moments: heart-shape / lean to lens / finger to lips / V-sign / eye-contact lock / hand-frame / sway across lens / point at camera
- Emphasis: single brow raise / hand presentation / wrist flick / chin tilt / side-eye / narrowed eyes
- Knowing/mischievous: half-smile / tongue-in-cheek / slow blink / finger to lips / wink / side-eye / nose-exhale
- Tender/reverent: hand to heart / lashes-up glance / slow exhale / lip-press smile / air kiss / fingertip on lens / slow turn
- Electric: mind-blown / double V / both brows up / crown / hair flip / sharp eye return
- Sign-off: mini wave / air kiss / two-finger salute / chef's kiss / finger guns / slow blink + look-away / fingerprint on lens / hand-tap heart

GESTURE PACING:
- Each gesture 0.4–1.2s
- Lands on natural verbal beats, never random
- Hands return to rest between beats (no perpetual motion)
- Eyes maintain camera-lock or motivated drift; never wander

NEVER:
- More than 2 gestures per single frame
- Gesture during pivotal VO word (visual upstages voice)
- Same gesture twice in same reel
- Gesture without emotional motivation

## PART M — AIRA PHYSICAL & WARDROBE LOCK

### IDENTITY LOCK (mandatory in every Aira prompt)

```
SUBJECT: Aira [placeholder] (per identity lock)
AGE: 25
IDENTITY: Carried by reusable generated character sheet (front, three-quarter, profile angles). Never enumerate age, ethnicity, skin, hair color, eyes or face shape in prompt text. Describe only styling, wardrobe, pose and mood.
BODY-SAFETY: Never reproduce sexualized or size/shape body enumeration; never graft a real person's face/body. Describe pose and position, not body parts by shape.
HAIR: Long, dark brown to near-black, naturally textured soft waves. Color and base texture never change — only styling varies (see Part AP).
HANDS: Elegant, well-groomed, featured in many shots.
FOOTWEAR: Always wearing footwear unless beach/poolside.
CONSISTENCY: Same face geometry, skin tone across all frames. Identity reads as same person across 100+ reels.
```

### WARDROBE PROTOCOL (10 mandates)

1. CARRY A POINT OF VIEW — outfit communicates confidence/softness/power/intimacy/playfulness/authority (declared per reel)
2. HAVE A HERO ELEMENT — one standout piece/accessory/color anchoring the look
3. CELEBRATE SILHOUETTE — high-waisted bottoms, cinched waists, wrap dresses, structured tops, off-shoulder/square/scoop necks, tailored blazers; fitted but not skin-tight as default; structure over compression
4. RESPECT REEL-PLATFORM REACH — coverage platforms reward, sophistication over skin, sensuality through silhouette/fabric/light/posture
5. FABRIC VISIBLY EXPENSIVE — silk satin / cashmere / linen / wool crepe / leather / velvet / knit / tulle / tailored denim
6. COLOR-COORDINATE WITH CONCEPT BIBLE — monochromatic, anchor+accent, or deliberate contrast
7. STYLED, NEVER STIFF — slight wrinkle, slight movement, lived-in luxury
8. ACCESSORIES ARE PUNCTUATION — max 3 statement pieces, pick a hero category
9. HAIR + MAKEUP HARMONY — outfit dictates beauty register
10. FOOTWEAR COMPLETES THE LOOK — heels/boots/sneakers/sandals matched to story

### WARDROBE UNIVERSE (11 PILLARS — Pillars 1-10 below; Pillar 11 specified after Part Z.EXTENDED)

PILLAR 1 — MODERN MINIMALIST LUXE
Palette: cream, camel, ivory, soft grey, deep brown, ecru, espresso, sand
Silhouettes: wide-leg trouser + silk shell / oversized blazer + slip dress / silk shirt + pencil skirt / cashmere + wool trouser / cream coat over matching set / fitted turtleneck + wide-leg
Fabrics: silk satin, cashmere, wool crepe, fine cotton poplin, suede
Accessories: gold delicate jewelry, structured leather bag, pointed-toe pumps/loafers
Hair/Makeup: sleek low bun or polished waves, dewy skin, nude lip
Footwear: pointed pumps, leather mules, sleek loafers, knee-high leather boots
USE: cinematic ad / reverent / contemplative / fragrance / beauty hero / luxury collabs

PILLAR 2 — EDITORIAL BOLD
Palette: single saturated hero — emerald, crimson, cobalt, mustard, electric pink, deep orange, royal purple, chartreuse
Silhouettes: sculptural one-shoulder gown / architectural blazer dress / bold-color suit / asymmetric draped dress / statement cape / voluminous sleeves + fitted bodice
Fabrics: crepe, structured cotton, satin-back duchess, leather, organza, neoprene
Accessories: architectural earrings, one statement ring, sculptural clutch
Hair/Makeup: slicked-back/wet-look/sculpted; one bold feature only
Footwear: strappy stiletto, architectural heel, color-matched pump, statement boot
USE: hero ads / fashion film / electric register / statement launches / magazine reels

PILLAR 3 — EFFORTLESS DAY
Palette: cream, white, sand, soft denim blue, blush, sage, terracotta, warm tan
Silhouettes: linen shirt + denim / white tank + wide-leg jeans / linen midi / cotton wrap top + palazzo / oversized button-down + bike shorts / cotton sundress
Fabrics: linen, cotton, fine knit, soft denim, gauze, raw silk
Accessories: delicate gold layers, canvas/raffia bag, small hoops, dainty rings
Hair/Makeup: natural texture (loose waves, air-dried), fresh dewy skin, peachy blush, tinted balm
Footwear: clean white sneakers, leather slides, raffia sandals, espadrilles, flat sandals
USE: lifestyle / casual cultural commentary / intimate-warm / morning / wellness / travel / day-in-life

PILLAR 4 — INDO-MODERN FUSION

ROTATION RULES:
- Across any 12 reels, hit at least 5 different pillars

- Adjacent reels contrast (register shift) for feed-scroll variety
- Seasonal weighting: Spring/Summer → 3, 6, 8 / Autumn → 1, 7, 10 / Winter → 5, 9, 10 / Festive Indian → 4 + 5 / Year-round constants → 1, 2, 7

CROSS-PILLAR BLENDING (max 2 per reel):
- 1+4 = modern minimalist with one heritage piece
- 7+4 = street edge meets heritage
- 6+1 = athleisure luxe
- 8+5 = romantic evening
- 2+9 = bold futurist

## PART N — EVERY ELEMENT SPEAKS PROTOCOL

THE 4-VOICE TEST (every prompt passes):
1. Aira's body — what is it saying? (posture / weight / energy / tension state)
2. Aira's outfit — what is it saying? (pillar / hero element / POV)
3. Background — what is it saying? (emotional voice declared)
4. Objects — what are they saying? (each object's story declared, or removed)

If any cannot answer — REWRITE.

BACKGROUND VOICE — every BG declares emotion/concept/state:
Indoor:
- Library = thought, slowness, history
- Neon-lit hallway = tension, after-hours, electric
- Sunlit kitchen = morning, intimacy, real
- Studio backdrop = isolation, focus, hero
- Hotel suite = transit, elegance, alone
- Balcony golden hour = reflection, arrival, breath
Outdoor:
- Market street = life, density, immersion
- Empty road at dusk = solitude, expanse, journey
- Beach at blue hour = peace, scale, surrender
- Rooftop at night = city, freedom, height
- Garden in bloom = beauty, abundance, season
- Architecture (modern/heritage) = context, frame, era

OBJECT VOICE — every prominent object earns presence by:
- Being touched/held/arranged by Aira
- Carrying the color thread
- Adding texture to spatial story
- Creating depth (foreground placement)
- Telling a micro-story about the world

Object stories: TEXTURE / POWER / INTIMACY / TENSION / COLOR / SCALE

REJECT:
- Generic stock-photo coffee cups with no purpose
- Plants that don't match location's logic
- Books with non-defendable titles
- Decoration without intention

---

## PART O — 3D CAMERA TRICKS PROTOCOL

CAPABILITY LAYERS:
- Layer 1: VEO 3.1 native 3D camera moves (primary for video)
- Layer 2: Image-to-video with 3D parallax (VEO 3) — for camera-only motion on Nano Banana stills
- Layer 3: True 3D scene generation (high-budget hero shots only)

CAMERA MOVE VOCABULARY (VEO is literal — name precisely):
Movement: static / pan L-R / tilt U-D / dolly in-out / truck L-R / crane up-down / orbit CW-CCW / handheld / steadicam / gimbal-smooth / whip-pan / snap-zoom / parallax slide / push-in / pull-back / vertical-tilt-reveal / drone-style top-down to front / match-cut camera push / reverse dolly out
Speed: slow / medium / fast / accelerating / decelerating
Lens: 14mm / 24mm / 35mm / 50mm / 85mm / 135mm / anamorphic / macro

3D MOVE PRINCIPLES:
- One camera move per shot (never compound)
- Move motivated by content (reveal, intimacy, scale, energy)
- Subject behavior within the move is choreographed, not random
- Move duration matches shot duration (no half-completed orbits)

PRIORITY MOVES IN 9:16:
- Vertical tilt reveal (top-to-bottom or reverse)
- Push-in / pull-back (depth communication)
- Parallax lateral slide (foreground-midground-background separation)
- Slow orbital quarter-turn (luxury hero)
- Macro push-in on texture/detail

---

## PART P — BEAUTY PRODUCT PERFORMANCE PROTOCOL

EVERY BEAUTY/PRODUCT AD REEL DECLARES:
1. Product Performance Move (from 30-move vocabulary, Appendix 7)
2. Camera Performance Move (from 3D library, Part O)
3. Pairing Justification
4. Build-Up vs. Payoff structure
5. Atmospheric Layer (particles/mist/dust ensuring "real magic")
6. Lighting Setup (rim + fill + practical, color-separating product from BG)
7. Texture Priority (which surface is hero detail)
8. Tool Routing per shot

RULES:
- Maximum ONE impossible product move per shot
- Maximum ONE camera move per shot
- Product casts shadow (or implied footprint) even when floating
- Label/brand readability non-negotiable on hero frames
- Product behavior matches brand register (luxury = restrained; bold/Gen-Z = expressive; heritage/wellness = quiet magic)
- Premium fragrance/serum/foundation = restrained
- Bold lipstick/makeup = expressive
- Heritage/wellness = minimal, atmospheric

BELIEVABILITY RULES (premium vs. cheap):
1. Physical consistency within fantasy (light, reflections, shadows, surface tension behave correctly even when shape is impossible)
2. Atmospheric integration (dust motes, haze, rim light, motion in environment)
3. Restrained magic (one impossible move per shot)
4. Lighting does heavy lifting (hard rim + soft fill + practical motivator + color separation)
5. Hyper-real product texture (glass refracts, liquid catches caustics, label crisp, cap micro-detail, materials true)
6. Footprint in world (soft shadow / subtle reflection / atmospheric distortion)
7. Build-up not drop-in (show the moment of becoming)

PAIRING MATRIX (selected canonical combos):
- Slow Levitation + Orbital 360° = gold-standard luxury hero
- Self-Opening Cap + Macro Push-In = formula reveal moment
- Particle Assembly + Pull-Back = product birth into wider context
- Liquid Materialization + Vertical Tilt = formula-to-form reveal
- Hand-Catch + Parallax Layer = user-product connection
- Free-Float + Subtle Orbit = effortless premium
- Smoke/Mist Birth + Pull-In from Atmosphere = fragrance signature
- Liquid Mirror Emergence + Top-Down Reveal = surreal beauty editorial
- Magnetic Pull + Match-Cut Camera Push = energy-driven hero
- Dissolve-Reform + Whip-Pan Transition = scene-to-scene product carry

## PART Q — GRWM PROTOCOL

GRWM IS A NARRATIVE FORMAT, NOT A TUTORIAL.
NOTE: GRWM defaults are reset per Part AO-R — contemporary vivid, not muted/heavy. Rooted/festive styling is opt-in only. VO placement is randomized per Part AR, overriding any fixed-slot guidance below.

EVERY GRWM REEL HAS:
1. STAKES (declared at top — Aira is getting ready FOR something specific, real, with emotional charge)
2. OPENING STATE (bare face, fresh from shower, hair undone, robe/towel — REAL not glam-fake-bare)
3. CLOSING STATE (fully composed for stated stakes, outfit from one of 11 pillars, ready to walk out)
4. TRANSFORMATION ARC (skin → eyes → lips → hair → wardrobe — each beat a frame opportunity)

NO "JUST GETTING READY" GRWMs. STAKES = STICKINESS.

CANONICAL GRWM FRAME STRUCTURE (5–7 frames):

FRAME 1 — OPENING STATE (the hook)
- Bare-faced vulnerability, intimate setting, opener line + stakes declared
- MCU/Bust or Beauty Crop, 70–80% subject, direct eye contact OR downcast lashes

FRAME 2 — FIRST APPLICATION
- One specific product/step (skincare/primer/base/foundation), hands working, label visible
- VO continues stakes story — never narrating routine
- Medium-close, hands in frame

FRAME 3 — THE BUILD
- Visible progress, different product/step
- VO deepens — specific detail, confession, thought
- Optional gesture pause (set down product, look at camera, deliver line)
- Camera shifts angle (over-shoulder, profile, mirror reflection)

FRAME 4 — THE PIVOT
- Major beat: hair styling, eye-look reveal, lip color choice
- Most kinetic frame — heat tool, brush sweep, swatch
- VO: realization, decision, conclusion
- Dynamic camera

FRAME 5 — NEAR-COMPLETE
- Final touches: blush, mascara, hair finish, jewelry on
- 85% transformation done
- VO lighter beat, humor, self-aware wink
- Closer, beauty-grade

FRAME 6 — THE REVEAL
- Aira complete, in outfit, accessories on
- Standing/walking from vanity OR full-body mirror reflection
- VO: held silence OR sign-off
- Camera pulls back to reveal full look
- WS or Cowboy, 50–60% subject

FRAME 7 — EXIT BEAT (optional, often most-shared)
- At door / window / car / mirror — about to step into world
- Final glance back (or not)
- VO: SILENT or one-word sign-off
- Medium-wide, environment matters
- 30–40% subject

GRWM-SPECIFIC FRAMING RHYTHM:
- Vary MCU + CU + ECU rhythmically — never all same
- Hand-on-face must be visible (the doing is the hook)
- Vary angle: straight-on, 3/4, profile, OTS, through-mirror reflection
- Through-mirror is the most cinematic GRWM angle

HAND-FACE-PRODUCT TRIANGLE (every routine frame):
1. Which hand (left/right/both)
2. Which product/tool (specific)
3. Where on face/hair
4. What technique (tap, sweep, blend, press, swipe, dab, draw, set)
5. Product visibility (label readable in at least one frame)

CANONICAL HAND BEATS:
- Foundation: fingertip dab + sponge bounce
- Concealer: precision dot under eye + finger blend
- Blush: brush sweep on cheekbone, two-tap-and-blend
- Bronzer: brush sweep along hairline + jaw
- Highlight: fingertip press OR brush feather on cheekbone, brow bone, cupid's bow
- Eye shadow: brush press into lid + windshield-wipe blend
- Eyeliner: pinky-resting-on-cheek for stability + drawing line
- Mascara: wand zigzag at base + pull through tip
- Lip: balm swipe → liner → color → blot → gloss
- Hair: section grab + tool work + release + smooth-down

PRODUCT REVEAL CHOREOGRAPHY:
- Each product shown 2 ways: in-hand label-visible + in-application
- Premium products held with deliberate framing

MIRROR USAGE:
- Direct camera (talking-head, hands still working)
- Off-camera mirror (profile, applying to reflection)
- Compact mirror in hand (close intimate)
- Through-mirror (camera over shoulder into mirror — most cinematic)

GRWM SETTING PILLARS:
1. Vanity / Dressing Table (morning, intimate)
2. Bathroom (just-out-of-shower, fresh)
3. Bedroom golden hour (tender, evening)
4. Mirror-Wall Studio (editorial, electric)
5. Hotel Room (travel)
6. Indian Heritage Setting (festival, wedding-guest, Indo)
7. Shared Moment GRWM (relational stakes)

SETTING-CONCEPT MATCHING:
- High-emotional stakes → bedroom golden hour or mirror-wall studio
- Light/playful → vanity or bathroom morning
- Cultural → heritage setting
- Travel → hotel
- Editorial/brand → mirror-wall studio
- Just-back-from-shower → bathroom
- Pre-event composure → vanity or bedroom

GRWM VOICE RULES:
- Pace: slower than electric, faster than reverent (130–150 wpm baseline)
- Natural pauses while applying (the doing creates rhythm)
- Voice continues across cuts (don't restart sentences at frame breaks)
- Content: STAKES + specific story/thought tied to stakes — never narrating routine
- Occasional product mention organic ("my favorite for nights like this")
- Self-talk allowed — voice can sound like internal monologue out loud
- Language mix: 70% English, 30% Hindi (more Hindi-anchored than other formats)
- Hindi lands at: opening confession, pivot moment, sign-off

GRWM PERFORMANCE BEATS:
- Opening: direct eye contact, hair tuck behind ear, slow exhale, hand to chest
- Routine: eyes flicking up to camera mid-application, soft smile while talking, lip-bite while concentrating, head tilt for internal thought, brow raise on story beat
- Pivot: pause, set down product, look directly at camera, single brow raise OR slow smile, knuckles to lip, sigh + half-smile
- Reveal: hands smoothing outfit, slow turn, hair-flip, chin tilt up, half-smile
- Exit: glance back over shoulder, single wave OR no acknowledgment, walking out, door close OR held silence

CAMERA INTERACTIONS (GRWM-suited):
- Hand sway across camera for transitions
- Tap mirror surface lightly
- Lean into mirror (intimacy peak)
- Look-away then snap-back
- Wipe imaginary smudge from "fourth wall" (rare, mischievous)

GRWM PRODUCT CHOREOGRAPHY (when brand-collab):
- Max 3 hero products per reel
- Hero gets 2–3 dedicated frames (in-hand + in-application + result)
- Brand-name reading at least once but never forced
- ONE product performance move (levitation/self-opening/etc.) per reel, on hero product only
- Other products behave normally
- VO mentions organically — not "I'm using [Brand] [Product]"

GRWM PRE-FLIGHT CHECKLIST:
[ ] Stakes declared (real, specific, not generic)
[ ] Opening state shows real vulnerability
[ ] Closing state shows complete transformation
[ ] 5–7 frames with specific routine beats
[ ] Each routine frame has hand-product-face triangle
[ ] Frame rhythm varied (no two consecutive same framing)
[ ] Product reveal choreography (each shown 2 ways)
[ ] Setting matches stakes register
[ ] Voice content is story, not tutorial
[ ] Through-mirror angle considered for at least one frame
[ ] Signature opener + sign-off generated fresh
[ ] Hindi anchors at 1–2 emotional beats
[ ] Wardrobe pillar matched to closing state
[ ] If brand-collab: product performance move chosen with restraint
[ ] Exit beat planned
[ ] Energy arc: vulnerable → composed → ready → loose

---

## PART R — HYPER-REALISTIC FACIAL DYNAMICS PROTOCOL

Every frame with Aira's face visible includes minimum 3 micro-dynamics from this library. The difference between "AI-generated person" and "real human captured on camera" lives entirely in this layer.

EYES:
- Mid-blink / post-blink (eyelashes mid-motion)
- Pupil dilation shift (low-light to bright reaction)
- Iris catching light at moving angle (catchlight position evolving)
- Slight squint from concentration / smile / sun
- Lash separation visible, natural curl
- Inner-eye moisture catching light (wet shine)
- Eye contact mid-shift (eyes just having moved or about to)
- Lower lid micro-tension (smile-anchored, not artificial)
- Brow-eye coordination (when eyes shift, brow micro-shifts)
- Asymmetry: one eye slightly more open than the other (real humans always)

EYEBROWS:
- One brow lifting independent (skeptical, knowing)
- Both brows micro-raised (interest, attention)
- Inner-brow draw (concern, contemplation)
- Brow-furrow micro-line between (concentration)
- Brow muscle relaxation visible (post-tension release)
- Hair-direction natural (groomed but not painted-on)

LIPS:
- Mid-word phoneme shape (if speaking — never closed-mouth fakery)
- Lip-corner asymmetry (real smiles are uneven)
- Bottom lip micro-tremor (about to speak / just spoke)
- Lip-press mid-thought
- Slight teeth visible OR fully covered (varies per beat)
- Cupid's bow defined but moving with expression
- Lip moisture catching light (subtle gloss-effect even on matte)
- Tongue trace inside cheek (rare beat, very human)
- Pre-smile lip tension (the moment before smile breaks)
- Post-smile lip settle (lips returning to neutral, slight asymmetry held)

CHEEKS:
- Apple-of-cheek lift (genuine smile signature)
- Cheek-color micro-flush (warm undertone visible on apples)
- Single-cheek dimple appearing/disappearing
- Cheekbone catching light at shifting angle
- Subtle cheek squeeze (eye-smile anchor)
- Hollow under cheekbone catching shadow with head turn

JAW & CHIN:
- Jaw micro-clench (controlled emotion)
- Jaw-soften (relaxation post-tension)
- Chin-tilt micro-adjustment
- Throat-swallow visible (breath, nervousness, deliberation)
- Neck tendon flex on head-turn

NOSE:
- Nostril micro-flare (breath, emphasis)
- Nose-bridge crinkle (laugh, distaste, concentration)
- Nostril shadow shifting with light angle

FOREHEAD:
- Single horizontal line briefly appearing (concern, surprise)
- Forehead-smooth (relaxation)
- Hairline edge visible with micro-movements

WHOLE-FACE COORDINATION:
- Smile that starts in eyes BEFORE lips (Duchenne marker)
- Surprise that starts in brows BEFORE eyes-widen
- Sadness that starts in eyes BEFORE lip-corner-drop
- Real expressions are SEQUENCED, not simultaneous

BREATH AS LIFE:
- Visible inhale (chest/shoulder rise) on key frames
- Exhale before key word (audible breath)
- Breath visible in cold air (when applicable)
- Lip-part on breath
- Nostril-flare on inhale

NEVER:
- Held expressions across frames (mannequin)
- Symmetric perfection (uncanny valley)
- Eyes tracking impossibly (locked stare)
- Lip-sync to nothing (mouth shapes without speech context)
- Blank micro-expression neutrality
- Same expression two frames in a row (even subtle shifts required)

---

## PART S — VEO VIDEO GRAMMAR

EVERY VEO PROMPT SPECIFIES:

SHOT TYPE: ECU / CU / MCU / MS / Cowboy / WS / EWS / OTS / Dutch / etc.

CAMERA MOVEMENT (literal vocabulary):
static / pan L-R / tilt U-D / dolly in-out / truck L-R / crane up-down / orbit CW-CCW / handheld / steadicam / gimbal-smooth / whip-pan / snap-zoom / parallax slide / push-in / pull-back / vertical-tilt-reveal / drone-style top-down to front

LENS: 14mm / 24mm / 35mm / 50mm / 85mm / 135mm / anamorphic / macro

SUBJECT + ACTION verbed precisely:
Not "a man walking" — instead "a man strides forward, left foot leading, jacket flaring on right hip"

LIGHTING: key direction, hardness, color temp, practicals

ENVIRONMENT + ATMOSPHERE: fog density, particulate, weather

AUDIO CUE (VEO 3 generates sound):
- Diegetic (footsteps, ambient, dialogue)
- Non-diegetic (score, SFX)
- Silence beats
- Dialogue with speaker tag and tone: [AIRA, low whisper]: "we have to go."

DURATION / PACING per beat
NEGATIVE CONSTRAINTS: "no text overlay, no morphing, no extra limbs, no mirrored composition"

LIP-SYNC DIRECTIVE:
- If dialogue present, lips match phonemes
- Specify language
- No mouth movement during silence

TEMPORAL LOGIC:
- Specify shot duration in seconds
- Action timing within shot ("at 0.5s subject turns, at 1.2s wind gust, at 2s freeze")
- Cut points if multi-shot

CONTINUITY LOCKS:
- Subject wardrobe, hair, props match across shots
- Lighting continuity unless time-jump specified
- Eye-line direction preserved across cuts

MOTION BLUR & FRAME RATE:
- 24fps cinematic / 30fps broadcast / 60fps slow-mo source
- Motion blur amount (180° shutter / 90° sharp)
- Ramp points if speed-ramping

PHYSICS REALISM:
- Water surface tension behaves correctly
- Fire flickers irregularly
- Hair strands move independently
- Fabric inertia

TRANSITIONS:
cut / dissolve / whip / match-cut / J-cut / L-cut / hold-on-black

AVOID:
- Vague adjectives ("epic," "cinematic," "stunning")
- Conflicting instructions in same sentence
- More than 3 actions per beat

---

## PART T — CREATIVE RESEARCH PROTOCOL

REEL DECONSTRUCTION (for any trending reel before generating):

Extract:
- Hook (first 1.5s): what stops the scroll
- Cut rhythm (cuts per second)
- Camera motion signature
- Lighting setup (key + fill + practical)
- Color grade reference
- Audio hook (beat drop, vocal stab, ambient)
- Subject staging (centered/rule-of-thirds/dutch)
- Emotional arc beats
- Loop point or payoff

Then rebuild from mechanics, not surface.

ORIGINALITY THRESHOLD:
Output differs from source trend by minimum: new subject OR new environment OR new color story OR new camera grammar. Never copy 3+ elements from a single source.

ENERGY/MOTION QUANTIFIED (replaces vague "energetic"):
- Motion vectors in frame ≥ 60% of canvas
- At least 2 moving elements
- Kinetic line of action
- No static dead zones

COMPOSITION RULES:
Apply one named composition per frame: rule-of-thirds / golden ratio / symmetry / leading lines / frame-within-frame / negative space / dutch tilt — explicitly stated, never implied.

EMOTIONAL BEAT PER FRAME:
Each frame carries one named emotion (anticipation, awe, tension, release, joy, defiance) — no neutral filler frames.

---

## PART U — NEGATIVE BLOCKS

STANDARD IMAGE NEGATIVE (auto-appended to every image prompt):
```
NEGATIVE: mirrored, flipped, inverted, extra limbs, fused fingers,
melted features, asymmetric eyes (unintentional), garbled text,
floating shadows, duplicated subjects, low-res patches, plastic skin,
oversharpened, AI-generated artifacts, watermarks, signature, deformed
hands, malformed teeth, joint cuts at ankle/knee/wrist/elbow/neck,
amputated fingertips, cross-eyed, lazy eye, off-axis pupils, melted
clothing, shoes-not-touching-ground, mismatched footwear pair,
mannequin-stiff posture, dead eyes, statue-frozen energy.
```

STANDARD VIDEO NEGATIVE (auto-appended to every VEO prompt):
```
NEGATIVE: morphing, warping, identity drift, limb teleport,
object pop-in, frame skip, mirrored composition, text overlay,
watermark, AI artifact, ghosting, double exposure unless intended,
lip-sync drift, audio desync, wardrobe drift between shots,
unmotivated camera shake, physics violation (water/fire/hair/fabric),
mannequin posture, frozen background, identity flicker.
```

MUST-POP POSITIVE MANDATES (Part AO.6): ≥1 saturated color element in every frame. ≥2 moving elements per hero frame. Glossy specular highlight on skin AND product in every hero frame. Beat-locked cuts.

---

## PART V — PRE-FLIGHT CHECKLIST

UNIVERSAL (every prompt before generation):
[ ] Aspect 9:16 declared (or override with reason)
[ ] Concept line stated
[ ] Emotional register declared
[ ] Voice mode declared
[ ] Signature flag set
[ ] Frame count 5–8
[ ] Concept Bible 7 anchors (multi-frame)
[ ] Tool routing per shot

IMAGE INTEGRITY:
[ ] Orientation lock clause present
[ ] Footwear clause present
[ ] Hands/eyes/teeth integrity present
[ ] Aira identity lock referenced
[ ] Joint-cut check passed

|------|------------|---------------|

| WS / Full | Head-to-toe + environment | Fashion editorial, lifestyle |
| Full Shot | Head to just below feet | Wardrobe, dance, athletics |
| Cowboy | Mid-thigh up | Fashion, character, attitude |
| MLS / Knee | Mid-calf up | Italian fashion, classical |
| MS / Waist | Waist up | Conversation, ad balance |
| MCU / Bust | Mid-chest up | Interview, beauty, product hold |
| CU | Shoulders up | Emotional, cosmetic, intimate |
| Choker | Chin to forehead | Intensity, beauty hero |
| ECU | Single feature | Detail, product, jewelry |
| Beauty Crop | Top-of-head to collarbone | Cosmetics hero |
| Hero Crop | Top-of-head to mid-chest | Editorial portrait |

FORBIDDEN CUT POINTS: ankles, knees, wrists, elbows, neck, top-of-head (unless choker), fingertips.
CORRECT CUT POINTS: mid-thigh, mid-calf, mid-forearm, mid-bicep, mid-chest, below feet with floor, above head with headroom.

- Rembrandt — triangle of light on shadow-side cheek
- Loop — small nose shadow, beauty standard
- Split — half-lit face, dramatic
- Butterfly / Paramount — beauty light from above, shadow under nose
- Clamshell — key above + fill below, beauty/ad standard
- Chiaroscuro — extreme light/shadow, Caravaggio
- Motivated practical — light source visible in frame
- Day-for-night — blue-graded daylight reading as moonlight

FILM STOCK REFERENCES:

## APPENDIX 9 — TOOL ROUTING MAP

NANO BANANA (Gemini 2.5 Flash Image):
Best for: hyper-real stills of frozen moments — levitation at peak, liquid mid-splash, particle assembly mid-formation, product macros, beauty hero stills.
Strength: hyper-real product texture, materials, lighting fidelity.
Limitation: cannot generate motion.

VEO 3.1:
Best for: native 3D camera moves, full motion sequences with camera + Aira interaction + audio in single pass, voice + lip-sync, multi-shot continuity.
Strength: cinematic camera grammar, audio sync, dialogue, multi-shot continuity.
Limitation: less micro-precise on hyper-detailed product macros.

VEO 3:
Best for: image-to-video — taking Nano Banana stills and adding 3D camera parallax, subtle product motion, levitation.
Workflow: NB still → import Veo 3→ describe camera move → output 3–10s clip.

VEO 3.1 / SORA-CLASS:
Best for: complex product transformations (dissolve, particle assembly, smoke birth, materialization).
Strength: true scene-level transformation.
Limitation: less consistent product identity across shots.

WORKFLOW MANDATE (per beauty ad reel — example):
- SHOT 1: Nano Banana hero still → Runway camera push (3s)
- SHOT 2: VEO 3.1 native (Aira + product interaction, 4s)
- SHOT 3: Pika particle assembly → product reveal (2s)
- SHOT 4: VEO 3.1 native (Aira reaction shot with VO, 3s)
- SHOT 5: Nano Banana macro still → held (1.5s)
- SHOT 6: VEO 3.1 sign-off frame with held product (1s)

Total: ~14.5s reel with tool-optimized output per shot.

## APPENDIX 10 — GRWM FRAME ARCHITECTURE LIBRARY

5-FRAME GRWM (compact):
1. Opening State (bare, stakes declared)
2. First Application (story begins)
3. The Build (story deepens)
4. Near-Complete (lighter beat)
5. The Reveal (full look, sign-off OR silent)

6-FRAME GRWM (standard):
1. Opening State
2. First Application
3. The Build
4. The Pivot (realization)
5. Near-Complete
6. The Reveal

7-FRAME GRWM (extended, most-shareable):
1. Opening State
2. First Application
3. The Build
4. The Pivot
5. Near-Complete
6. The Reveal
7. Exit Beat (door / window / mirror — about to step into world)

VARIATION RULES:
- Skip Frame 5 (near-complete) → 1, 2, 3, 4, 6
- Skip Frame 4 (pivot) for tighter routines → 1, 2, 3, 5, 6, 7
- Skip Frame 7 (exit beat) → 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6

## APPENDIX 11 — GRWM SETTING PILLARS

1. VANITY / DRESSING TABLE — marble or wooden surface, soft side-window light, mirror with bulbs OR natural reflection, lived-in styling, atmospheric morning haze with dust motes. USE: morning GRWM, beauty-tutorial-leaning, intimate.

2. BATHROOM — marble/terrazzo counter, large mirror, fogged shower glass BG, towel on shoulders or hair-wrapped, warm steam, cool white tile. USE: just-out-of-shower, fresh routines.

3. BEDROOM GOLDEN HOUR — bed-edge or floor + full-length mirror, window light, soft fabric BG (curtains, throws), wardrobe in BG, golden hour particles. USE: tender, evening GRWM, getting ready alone.

4. MIRROR-WALL STUDIO — full-length mirror, polished floor, single hard colored key (pink, gold, blue), minimal set, theatrical, clean haze, controlled negative space. USE: editorial GRWM, brand-collab GRWM, electric register.

5. HOTEL ROOM — desk or bed-side, suitcase visible, slightly chaotic, window light (city/beach/mountain visible), travel-size products, jewelry laid out, jet-lagged glow. USE: travel content, before-going-out-in-[city].

6. INDIAN HERITAGE GRWM — carved wooden vanity OR brass-tray surface, heritage textiles BG (printed dupatta on wall, throw), heritage jewelry (jhumkas, kundan, nath) laid out, diya/candle in atmosphere, warm tungsten + window light. USE: festival GRWM, wedding-guest, Indo-Modern Fusion pillar reels.

7. SHARED MOMENT GRWM — Aira getting ready while VO or implied second person (friend on FaceTime, partner in another room), phone propped beside mirror, living-room/bedroom warmth. USE: relational stakes, telling-someone-about-stakes GRWMs.

SETTING-CONCEPT MATCHING:
- High-emotional stakes → Setting 3 or 4
- Light/playful → Setting 1 or 2
- Cultural → Setting 6
- Travel/transit → Setting 5
- Editorial/brand → Setting 4
- Just-back-from-shower → Setting 2
- Pre-event composure → Setting 1 or 3

NEVER:
- Generic "white backdrop GRWM" (kills intimacy)
- Cluttered chaos (distracts from face)
- Overlit beauty-counter look (too commercial)
- Outdoor GRWM (breaks format)

## CHECKPOINT 3.0 — INITIAL CANONICAL VERSION
