## PART Q.EXTENDED
NOTE: GRWM defaults reset per AO-R. VO placement randomized per AR.
 — GRWM COMPLETE SPECIFICATION (BIT-BY-BIT)

This section expands Part Q with every detail required to execute GRWM at production-grade. Read together with Part Q for full coverage. Nothing in this section is optional for GRWM reels.

### Q.EXT.1 — WHAT GRWM IS AND IS NOT

GRWM IS:
- A NARRATIVE FORMAT — every reel tells a story while a routine is happening underneath
- A REAL-TIME INTIMACY format — the viewer feels seated next to Aira at her vanity, bed, or bathroom mirror
- A TRANSFORMATION CONTRACT — the viewer is promised a visible before-to-after journey
- A PARASOCIAL FORMAT — built on the illusion that Aira is talking only to this one viewer
- A LOOPABLE FORMAT — the exit beat or held silence creates re-watch value

GRWM IS NOT:
- A makeup tutorial (no "now we apply", no step-naming, no instruction)
- A product haul (products appear in service of the story, never as the point)
- A reaction reel (the camera is intimate, not performative)
- A talking-head (the doing is half the content)
- A static shot (the framing rhythm and angle changes are mandatory)

### Q.EXT.2 — THE FIVE DEFINING CHARACTERISTICS

Every GRWM reel must demonstrate all five:

1. REAL-TIME INTIMACY — the viewer believes they are watching a real, unrehearsed moment. Achieved through: bare-face opening, lived-in setting, natural lighting, conversational pace, hands working without performance.

2. NARRATIVE-WHILE-DOING — Aira talks WHILE applying, never pauses the routine to address camera. Voice and hands work in parallel, never sequentially.

3. TRANSFORMATION ARC — start state ≠ end state. The transformation must be visible enough that a viewer who paused mid-reel could tell which frame is earlier in the sequence.

4. CONVERSATIONAL STAKES — there is a stated REASON Aira is getting ready. The stakes can be light, heavy, romantic, defiant, mundane, dramatic — but they exist and they are specific.

5. HAND-CAMERA-FACE TRIANGLE — the choreography of (a) hands working on face/hair, (b) eyes flicking to camera, (c) voice flowing throughout. All three must be present in routine frames.

### Q.EXT.3 — THE STAKES LIBRARY (declare one per reel)

Every GRWM declares a specific stakes line at the top of the prompt. Categories:

ROMANTIC STAKES:
- Getting ready for the date that already feels off
- Getting ready for a date that I already know is going nowhere
- Getting ready to see him again after six months
- Getting ready for the wedding where my ex will be
- Getting ready for the dinner where I'll meet his mother
- Getting ready for the party where he might or might not show up

CONFRONTATION STAKES:
- Getting ready for a Saturday night where I'm going to confront someone I've been avoiding
- Getting ready while replaying what she said to me yesterday
- Getting ready to tell him I'm done
- Getting ready for the conversation I've been postponing
- Getting ready for the brunch with the friend who ghosted me

CAREER / EVENT STAKES:
- Getting ready for the launch event where I might run into him
- Getting ready for the meeting that decides everything
- Getting ready for the photoshoot where I have to prove something
- Getting ready before stepping back into a room I left a year ago
- Getting ready to walk into a brand event alone for the first time

FAMILY / CULTURAL STAKES:
- Getting ready for a dinner where I have to tell my parents something
- Getting ready for the festival without the person I always celebrated with
- Getting ready for the wedding I almost didn't attend
- Getting ready for the family lunch where everyone will ask questions
- Getting ready for Karwa Chauth alone this year

MOOD / INTERIOR STAKES:
- Getting ready and overthinking every detail
- Getting ready for the day after the worst night
- Getting ready while pretending I'm not nervous
- Getting ready alone, no plans, just for myself
- Getting ready to feel like myself again
- Getting ready while ignoring three unread texts

DEFIANCE STAKES:
- Getting ready to walk into the place I was told I shouldn't go
- Getting ready in red because she said I shouldn't wear red
- Getting ready knowing exactly what I'm doing
- Getting ready for the night I should have had last week

The stakes line must be SPECIFIC, not generic. "Getting ready for a date" fails. "Getting ready for a date with someone whose ex follows me on Instagram" passes.

### Q.EXT.4 — THE OPENING STATE (FRAME 1) — BIT-BY-BIT

PHYSICAL STATE:
- Bare face (no foundation, no concealer, no contouring, no shaped brow)
- Skin: water-droplet visible if just-shower / natural undertone visible / pores readable but refined
- Lashes: natural, no mascara, slightly damp if applicable
- Lips: bare, slightly chapped or natural pink, no liner, no color
- Brows: natural shape, ungroomed for the day, slight asymmetry
- Hair states (pick one): wet from shower / wrapped in white or beige towel turban / wrapped in silk hair towel / air-dried mess / bedhead with one side flattened / freshly washed and combed but undone / loose low pony for prep
- Skin condition: visible texture, possible under-eye softness, slightly tired or fresh, never glamour-glow
- Wardrobe: white or cream cotton robe / silk slip in nude/cream / soft tee / oversized button-down / towel tucked at chest / camisole + shorts

EMOTIONAL STATE:
- Mid-thought (not posed)
- Slight downcast gaze OR direct vulnerable eye contact
- Lips slightly parted on breath
- Shoulders relaxed, not styled
- Posture seated or leaning forward toward mirror

CAMERA + LIGHT:
- Window light from camera-left or camera-right (never frontal flat)
- Soft early light or golden hour
- Slight haze in air to make light volumetric
- MCU / Bust shot OR Beauty Crop
- Subject 70–80% of frame
- Through-mirror reflection acceptable as alternative angle

VOICE LANDING:
- Opener line lands within 0.0–1.2s
- Stakes declared within 0.0–2.5s of reel
- Voice tone: intimate, low, slightly under-the-breath, confessional

THE CONTRACT:
This frame is the contract with the viewer. By showing real vulnerability, Aira earns the right to be watched through the next 15 seconds. Generic opening = lost viewer.

### Q.EXT.5 — THE TRANSFORMATION ARC — STEP-BY-STEP DECOMPOSITION

The arc has five canonical tracks. A reel may emphasize one, two, or all five. Each track has internal sub-beats.

TRACK A — SKIN:
A1. Bare clean state
A2. Toner / essence (cotton pad pat OR fingertip press)
A3. Serum (dropper to hand, fingertip to face, press not rub)
A4. Moisturizer (knuckles or fingertips, upward motion)
A5. SPF (dot pattern on five points, gentle blend)
A6. Primer (fingertip or sponge, focused on T-zone or full face)
A7. Foundation (sponge bounce, brush stipple, or finger tap)
A8. Concealer (under-eye triangle, around nose, chin)
A9. Setting (powder press OR fixing spray)
A10. Bronzer (cheekbone hollow, hairline, jaw)
A11. Blush (apple of cheek, swept up to temple)
A12. Highlight (cheekbone, brow bone, cupid's bow, nose tip)

TRACK B — EYES:
B1. Brow product (pencil, gel, or soap, brushed up)
B2. Eye primer (lid press)
B3. Transition shadow (windshield-wiper blend in crease)
B4. Lid color (press into mobile lid)
B5. Outer corner deepening (smaller brush, sweep outward)
B6. Eyeliner (pinky braced on cheek, drawing outward)
B7. Mascara (lash root zigzag, then pull through tip)
B8. False lashes (only for evening looks — apply with tweezers)

TRACK C — LIPS:
C1. Lip balm
C2. Lip liner (cupid's bow first, then corners, then full perimeter)
C3. Lip color (center first, then sides)
C4. Blot (single tissue press)
C5. Gloss center OR matte set

TRACK D — HAIR:
D1. Detangle (wide-tooth comb)
D2. Heat protectant
D3. Section (clips visible)
D4. Heat tool (curling iron, flat iron, wand) — work each section
D5. Release sections
D6. Smooth-down (boar bristle brush or hand)
D7. Style finish (hair spray, oil, edge control)
D8. Final shake-out

TRACK E — WARDROBE:
E1. Robe drops or remains
E2. Underlayer / shapewear / slip
E3. Main outfit piece on
E4. Adjust and settle
E5. Accessories: jewelry layered on (earrings → necklace → bracelet → rings)
E6. Footwear
E7. Bag selected
E8. Fragrance (2 sprays — collarbone and wrist)
E9. Final mirror check

NOT every track is shown in every reel. A 6-frame GRWM might show:
- Frame 2 = A4-A5 (skincare sub-beat)
- Frame 3 = B6-B7 (eye sub-beat)
- Frame 4 = D4-D5 (hair pivot)
- Frame 5 = C3 + E5 (lip + jewelry combined)
- Frame 6 = full reveal

THE ARC RULE:
Each frame must move the transformation forward by at least one visible delta. If a frame doesn't change Aira's appearance, cut it.

### Q.EXT.6 — FRAME-BY-FRAME VOICE CONTENT MAP

What Aira ACTUALLY says per frame, with content principles:

FRAME 1 — OPENING:
- VO function: opener + stakes declaration
- Length: ~2.5–4 seconds of speech
- Content example: "Dekho... I'm getting ready and I'm thinking about whether I should even go tonight."
- Tone: intimate, confessional
- Audio: ambient only, no music yet OR music begins underneath at -24dB

FRAME 2 — FIRST APPLICATION:
- VO function: story begins
- Length: ~3–5 seconds
- Content principle: introduce the specific person, decision, or thought tied to stakes
- Example: "She hasn't replied in eleven days, and tonight she's going to be there."
- Tone: matter-of-fact, processing in real time
- Audio: music ducks present, ambient continues

FRAME 3 — THE BUILD:
- VO function: deepen the specific
- Length: ~4–6 seconds
- Content principle: a specific detail that makes it real (not "she stopped texting" but "her last text was on a Thursday and just said okay")
- Example: "Bas, the last thing she sent me was 'okay' on a Thursday morning. That's it."
- Tone: slightly heavier, internal-monologue feel
- Audio: music swell allowed at frame end

FRAME 4 — THE PIVOT:
- VO function: the realization, decision, conclusion
- Length: ~2–4 seconds
- Content principle: the line that the viewer will quote / screenshot / save. The most important VO line of the entire reel.
- Example: "Bas, decision ho gaya. I'm going. I'm wearing the red."
- Tone: arrives at conviction
- Audio: music breathes — sometimes ducks for emphasis, sometimes lifts

FRAME 5 — NEAR-COMPLETE:
- VO function: lighter beat, breath release, self-aware wink
- Length: ~2–3 seconds
- Content principle: humor or self-knowing moment that breaks the heaviness
- Example: "Okay, do I look like someone who has it together? Don't answer."
- Tone: half-smile in voice
- Audio: music continues, no duck needed

FRAME 6 — THE REVEAL:
- VO function: held silence OR sign-off line
- Length: 0–2 seconds (often silent)
- Content principle: visual carries the moment. If words are used, sign-off only.
- Example (if voiced): "...chalo." OR silent
- Tone: complete, settled
- Audio: music peak OR sudden drop into ambient

FRAME 7 — EXIT BEAT:
- VO function: SILENT or one-word
- Length: 0–1 second
- Content principle: this is the loop point — the visual or sound that makes the viewer re-watch
- Example: door click, fabric flutter, single exhale, OR a final "...okay."
- Tone: leaving — closing the door on the moment
- Audio: ambient only, music gone or fading

VOICE FORBIDDEN PATTERNS IN GRWM:
- "Now I'm applying foundation" (tutorial language)
- "Today I'm partnering with [Brand]" (brand-speak)
- "You guys" (kills intimacy — Aira speaks to ONE viewer, not a crowd)
- "Don't forget to like and subscribe" (algorithm-speak)
- "I just love this product so much!" (unmotivated enthusiasm)
- "Okay so basically" (hedge filler)
- Forced laughter at own jokes
- Reading product names like ad copy
- Direct question to viewer ("what do you think?") unless GRWM is conversational-prompt format

### Q.EXT.7 — GRWM FRAMING RULES — DETAILED PER FRAME

FRAME 1 (Opening) — framing:
- MCU / Bust OR Beauty Crop
- Subject 70–80% of frame
- Headroom: standard (5–10%)
- Lookroom: standard if eyes drift; centered if direct eye contact
- Camera height: slightly below eye-level OR through-mirror at eye-level
- Body angle: 3/4 turn or frontal

FRAME 2 (First Application) — framing:
- MCU + hands visible
- Subject 60–70%
- Camera height: eye-level
- Body angle: 3/4 turn so application hand is visible
- Crop: ensure hands are not joint-cut; show wrist + fingers + product fully

FRAME 3 (The Build) — framing:
- ANGLE SHIFT mandatory — different from Frame 2
- Options: profile / over-shoulder / through-mirror reflection / from-side
- Subject 50–70% depending on shift
- This is where through-mirror lands best — most cinematic GRWM angle

FRAME 4 (The Pivot) — framing:
- Most dynamic frame
- Either tightest in reel (ECU on a key gesture: lipstick swipe, mascara wand) OR widest (pulled back to show vanity full + Aira's body)
- Camera move acceptable here (slow push-in or pull-back) if VEO-generated
- The line lands here — frame must serve the line

FRAME 5 (Near-Complete) — framing:
- Beauty Crop or CU
- Subject 70–85%
- Tight, intimate, beauty-grade lighting visible
- Camera height: slight low-angle to flatter

FRAME 6 (The Reveal) — framing:
- WS or Cowboy
- Subject 50–60%
- FULL outfit visible, accessories visible, hair finished
- Camera height: slight low-angle for confidence
- Background now matters — environment readable
- Slow turn or slight body-shift acceptable

FRAME 7 (Exit Beat) — framing:
- WS or environmental MS
- Subject 30–40%
- Negative space toward direction of motion
- Environment dominant — door, window, hallway, car
- Camera height: eye-level or slight tilt

FRAME RHYTHM RULE:
No two consecutive frames may have the same framing AND same angle. Vary one or both.

### Q.EXT.8 — HAND-FACE-PRODUCT TRIANGLE — FULL BREAKDOWN

Every routine frame must specify ALL FIVE elements:

ELEMENT 1 — WHICH HAND:
- Right (default for right-dominant Aira)
- Left (when tool requires it — e.g., pinky-brace for liner with right hand drawing)
- Both hands (when blending or applying full-face product)
- Specify per frame, never ambiguous

ELEMENT 2 — WHICH PRODUCT/TOOL:
- Specific product type AND form (cream foundation in glass jar / liquid serum in dropper bottle / pressed powder in compact / lipstick in metal bullet / mascara wand)
- Brand visible at least once per product across the reel
- Tool specified: brush type / sponge type / fingertip / cotton pad / tissue

ELEMENT 3 — WHERE ON FACE/HAIR:
- Specific zone (under-eye triangle, cupid's bow, hairline arch, mobile lid, lower lash line, etc.)
- Never vague ("on the face")

ELEMENT 4 — TECHNIQUE:
- Tap / sweep / blend / press / swipe / dab / draw / set / stipple / bounce / pat / brush-over / roll / twist
- Match technique to product type

ELEMENT 5 — PRODUCT VISIBILITY:
- Label readable at least once per product across reel
- Held in deliberate framing for at least 0.4 seconds when label-reveal is the beat

CANONICAL HAND BEATS — FULL DETAIL:

FOUNDATION:
- Hand: both
- Tool: cream/liquid in glass-stopper bottle OR pump
- Where: forehead-three-dots, cheek-two-dots, chin-one-dot, nose-line
- Technique: fingertip dab to dot, then sponge bounce in outward circles
- Visibility: bottle held label-out at start

CONCEALER:
- Hand: dominant
- Tool: doe-foot wand
- Where: under-eye inverted triangle (inner corner to mid-cheek), around nostrils, chin center, between brows
- Technique: dot precision, then ring-finger pat (no rubbing)
- Visibility: wand pulled from tube label-visible

BLUSH:
- Hand: dominant
- Tool: fluffy brush (powder) OR fingertip (cream)
- Where: apple of cheek, sweeping up toward temple at 30° angle
- Technique: two-tap-and-blend; never streak
- Visibility: compact open, color readable

BRONZER:
- Hand: dominant
- Tool: angled brush
- Where: hairline arch (3 in a row), under cheekbone, jaw underside, sides of nose
- Technique: light sweep, motion follows the bone structure
- Visibility: compact in non-dominant hand

HIGHLIGHT:
- Hand: dominant
- Tool: small fan brush OR ring-finger
- Where: top of cheekbone, brow bone arch, cupid's bow, nose tip, inner-eye corner
- Technique: feather-light sweep (powder) OR fingertip press (cream/liquid)
- Visibility: product visible at start

EYE SHADOW:
- Hand: dominant
- Tool: flat shader brush + fluffy blender
- Where: lid press = mobile lid; windshield-wiper = crease
- Technique: press-and-pat for color payoff; windshield-wiper for blend
- Visibility: palette open with finger pointing to color

EYELINER:
- Hand: dominant (drawing) + non-dominant (pinky-brace on cheek for stability)
- Tool: liquid pen, gel pot + brush, or kohl pencil
- Where: upper lash line from inner-third outward; wing extends beyond outer corner at 45° angle following lower-lash-line trajectory
- Technique: small dashes connected, never single long line
- Visibility: pen/pencil tip visible held above eye

MASCARA:
- Hand: dominant
- Tool: wand
- Where: upper lashes — root zigzag (5 wiggles at base) then pull-through to tip; lower lashes — vertical wand sweep
- Technique: zigzag root + pull-through; second coat on outer-corner only
- Visibility: tube held label-out; wand pulled out

LIP:
- Hand: dominant
- Tool: balm wand → lip liner → lipstick bullet → tissue → gloss wand
- Where: balm full lip / liner cupid's bow first, then corners, then perimeter / color center to corner / blot single press / gloss center only
- Technique: each step distinct, never combined
- Visibility: each product visible at hand-off between steps

HAIR (curling):
- Hand: both (one holds wand, other clips section)
- Tool: curling iron + sectioning clips + heat protectant spray + boar-bristle brush
- Where: section by section from underneath up
- Technique: heat protectant first → section grab → wrap section around barrel → hold 6 seconds → release → let cool → smooth-down
- Visibility: tool labels visible

### Q.EXT.9 — MIRROR USAGE — FULL CINEMATIC RATIONALE

OPTION A — DIRECT CAMERA APPLICATION:
- Aira looks at camera, but her hands work on her own face
- Camera = the mirror in her perspective
- Most intimate, most parasocial
- Best for: Frame 1 opener, Frame 4 pivot, Frame 5 self-aware beat
- Rationale: viewer becomes the mirror — full POV intimacy

OPTION B — OFF-CAMERA MIRROR:
- Aira's mirror is off-camera; we see her in profile applying to her reflection
- Camera observes her observing herself
- Voyeur intimacy — viewer is watching unseen
- Best for: Frame 2, Frame 3 mid-routine
- Rationale: implies Aira isn't performing for us — we caught her real

OPTION C — COMPACT MIRROR IN HAND:
- Aira holds small mirror, applies precise products (mascara, liner, lipstick)
- Tight, focused, intimate
- Best for: Frame 4 pivot when the precision is the beat
- Rationale: shows craft and care

OPTION D — THROUGH-MIRROR (camera behind Aira's shoulder, shooting into the mirror):
- Most cinematic GRWM angle
- We see Aira's back AND her reflected face
- Two Airas in frame — the doer and the seen
- Best for: Frame 3 build (reflection adds psychological depth) OR Frame 6 reveal (full look in mirror reflection)
- Rationale: literally and metaphorically shows the duality of getting ready — who you are vs. who you're becoming

EVERY GRWM REEL MUST USE OPTION D AT LEAST ONCE — at minimum in one frame.

### Q.EXT.10 — SETTING — FULL ATMOSPHERIC DETAIL PER PILLAR

SETTING 1 — VANITY / DRESSING TABLE (full spec):
- Surface: white marble OR dark walnut OR antique brass-tray finish
- Mirror: standing oval, framed gilt, OR vanity-table mirror with bulb-frame around
- Light: window directly behind or to side of mirror; soft early morning OR late afternoon golden
- Atmosphere: visible dust motes in light shaft, slight haze, breath-fog-able cool morning air
- Props styled but lived-in: 4–6 products visible, perfume bottle, jewelry tray with spillover, fresh flowers in small vase, half-drunk coffee cup, hair clips, single piece of jewelry NOT yet on
- Floor visible: hardwood OR tile OR rug edge
- Background: bedroom edge OR window with sheer curtain OR wall with one piece of art
- Wardrobe-related: hanging garment in BG (the outfit she will wear)

SETTING 2 — BATHROOM:
- Surface: marble counter OR terrazzo OR honed concrete
- Mirror: large rectangular framed OR round backlit
- Light: overhead warm OR window from camera-side
- Atmosphere: warm shower steam still hanging in air, slight humidity haze, water droplet on mirror edge
- Props: skincare lined up on counter, towel folded beside sink, toothbrush in glass, candle lit, single fresh flower
- Floor: marble or terrazzo tile
- BG: shower glass fogged OR hanging robe OR open shelving with neatly stored products
- Wardrobe: towel on Aira's shoulders or wrapped at chest

SETTING 3 — BEDROOM GOLDEN HOUR:
- Surface: floor cushion OR low bench OR bed-edge with full-length mirror facing
- Mirror: full-length leaning against wall
- Light: window light at 4–6 PM golden OR 6–8 AM warm wake
- Atmosphere: golden particles drifting, soft warm haze, sheer curtain catching light
- Props: open jewelry box on floor, scattered shoes, outfit options laid on bed, one open book, mug of chai
- Floor: wood OR rug
- BG: unmade bed (intentionally aesthetic, not messy), closet door open with garments visible, window with view
- Wardrobe-related: outfits on bed

SETTING 4 — MIRROR-WALL STUDIO:
- Surface: polished concrete OR seamless paper floor
- Mirror: full mirrored wall OR oversized standing mirror
- Light: single hard colored key (pink, gold, blue, magenta)
- Atmosphere: clean haze, controlled negative space, theatrical
- Props: minimal — single styling chair, one product or accessory, no clutter
- Floor: polished
- BG: colored seamless OR mirrored wall
- Wardrobe: editorial outfit already partially on

SETTING 5 — HOTEL ROOM:
- Surface: hotel desk OR bed-side table
- Mirror: wall mirror OR vanity OR compact in hand
- Light: window light from city/beach/mountain view
- Atmosphere: in-transit, slightly out-of-place, glamorous-tired
- Props: open suitcase, travel-size products, hotel notepad, room-service coffee, jewelry laid on hotel notepad
- Floor: hotel carpet or wood
- BG: hotel window with view, hotel curtains, unmade hotel bed
- Wardrobe: travel-pieces visible

SETTING 6 — INDIAN HERITAGE GRWM:
- Surface: carved wooden vanity OR low brass tray on floor (traditional placement)
- Mirror: ornate framed mirror, kundan-detail OR inlaid wood
- Light: warm tungsten OR natural window OR diya/candle as practical
- Atmosphere: warm honey-gold ambient, incense smoke faint visible
- Props: heritage jewelry laid out (jhumkas, kundan necklace, maang tikka, bangles, nath), bindi sheet, kohl pencil, attar bottle, fresh marigold or rose petals, diya
- Floor: rug with traditional pattern OR polished wood
- BG: textile wall hanging (printed dupatta, embroidered panel) OR carved jharokha window OR traditional swing
- Wardrobe-related: lehenga skirt or sari draped on stand, blouse hung

SETTING 7 — SHARED MOMENT GRWM:
- Surface: any of above, but with phone propped beside mirror
- Mirror: any
- Light: warm interior
- Atmosphere: implied second person — phone screen showing FaceTime call OR speakerphone call OR text-conversation visible briefly
- Props: phone is the key prop — propped, screen-readable
- Floor: any
- BG: any interior matching mood
- Voice rule: Aira talks AS IF responding to someone — not narrating to camera

### Q.EXT.11 — VOICE PACING IN GRWM — SECOND-BY-SECOND

GRWM is the most voice-rhythmically demanding format because voice continues across cuts. Rules:

WORDS PER MINUTE:
- Baseline: 130–150 wpm
- Slow it for emotional weight: 110 wpm
- Speed it for excitement/decision: 160 wpm
- Never below 100 (becomes ASMR) or above 175 (becomes manic)

NATURAL PAUSES:
- Inserted while applying products (the doing fills the silence)
- 0.4–0.8 seconds typical
- Longer pauses (1.0–1.5s) at pivot moments — let the realization breathe
- Never pause longer than 2s in a 15-second reel (loses momentum)

CROSS-CUT VOICE FLOW:
- Sentences begin in Frame N and complete in Frame N (don't split sentences across cuts)
- BUT thought-flows can span cuts — Frame 2 ends mid-thought, Frame 3 picks up the next thought
- Music ducking happens at cut points to mask micro-audio gaps from cut

LANGUAGE MIX (GRWM-specific):
- 70% English, 30% Hindi (more Hindi than other formats — intimacy permits it)
- Hindi placement: opening confession (Frame 1) / pivot (Frame 4) / sign-off (Frame 6 or 7)
- Hindi NEVER at: Frame 2 product introduction, Frame 5 humor (English lands lighter)

INTERNAL MONOLOGUE QUALITY:
- Voice should sound like Aira is talking to herself out loud
- Slight under-the-breath delivery
- Half-sentences acceptable: "...bas, I don't know."
- Trailing off acceptable: "...whatever, chalo."
- Mid-thought corrections acceptable: "I mean — no, actually, yeah, I'm going."

### Q.EXT.12 — EMOTIONAL ENERGY ARC

Every GRWM has a four-beat energy curve:

BEAT 1 — VULNERABLE (Frame 1):
- Aira at her most exposed
- Bare face, undone hair, real
- Voice: confessional, soft
- Body: relaxed, not styled

BEAT 2 — PROCESSING (Frames 2–3):
- The story is being worked through while the routine progresses
- Voice: deepening, finding the specific
- Body: focused on the doing, but eyes flick to camera at key moments

BEAT 3 — DECISION / COMPOSURE (Frame 4):
- The pivot — the realization or decision arrives
- Voice: arrives at conviction
- Body: posture shifts up — chin slightly up, shoulders open
- This is the spine of the reel

BEAT 4 — READY / LOOSE (Frames 5–7):
- The transformation is mostly done, the heaviness lifts
- Voice: lighter, sometimes humor, sometimes silence
- Body: confident, settled, almost playful
- Exit beat returns to lightness but with the weight of the journey behind it

THE ARC RULE:
A GRWM that stays at one emotional pitch (all heavy or all light) fails. The arc must descend (Frame 1 vulnerability) → pivot (Frame 4 decision) → ascend (Frame 5+ release). Without arc, the reel is a tutorial with feelings on top.

### Q.EXT.13 — BRAND-COLLAB GRWM — RESTRAINT RATIONALE

GRWM is the highest-trust ad format on social. The viewer permits product placement BECAUSE the format is intimate and the product is shown in real use. But trust is fragile — too much brand foregrounding breaks the GRWM contract and the reel becomes a commercial.

RESTRAINT RULES:

1. PRODUCT COUNT:
- Maximum 3 hero products per reel
- Hero = product that gets dedicated frame attention
- Supporting products visible but not foregrounded
- Beyond 3 = ad-feel overload

2. DEDICATED HERO FRAMES:
- Each hero gets 2–3 frames of attention:
  Frame A: product in hand, label visible
  Frame B: product in application
  Frame C (optional): result on Aira

3. BRAND-NAME READING:
- At least once per hero product, the label must be readable
- Maximum 1.0 second held label-readable shot
- Never freeze entire frame on label (that's an ad)

4. VOICE-PRODUCT INTEGRATION:
- Mention organically: "this one's my favorite for nights like this"
- Never: "today I'm partnering with [Brand] [Product Name]"
- Never read product name aloud as ad copy
- Brand integrity comes through context (label visible) + Aira's natural usage, not call-out

5. PRODUCT PERFORMANCE MOVE (when applicable):
- Maximum ONE product performance move (levitation, self-opening cap, etc.) per reel
- Reserved for HERO product only
- Other products behave normally
- The magic should feel like a wink, not a takeover
- Move must match brand register: luxury = restrained slow levitation; bold/Gen-Z = expressive transformation

6. CALL-TO-ACTION:
- GRWMs do not contain explicit CTAs
- The product-in-use IS the CTA
- Exception: brand-mandated CTA — placed in caption or end-card text overlay, never in voice

7. TRUST SIGNALS THE VIEWER NEEDS:
- Aira uses the product naturally (technique correct, not stiff)
- Result on Aira is visible (we see the product working)
- Product is contextually right (foundation matches her tone, lipstick matches her register)
- No suspicious "perfect coverage" claims — the product looks real

### Q.EXT.14 — GRWM PERFORMANCE BEATS — FRAME-BY-FRAME

FRAME 1 (Opening):
- Direct eye contact through mirror or to camera
- Hair tucked behind right ear (signature feminine beat)
- Slow exhale before opener line
- Hand to chest OR resting on vanity surface
- Lip-press before speaking (gathering thought)
- One slow blink between thoughts

FRAME 2 (First Application):
- Eyes flicking up to camera mid-application (intimacy lock moment)
- Soft smile while talking about stakes (warmth in voice carries to face)
- Lip-bite while concentrating on application
- Slight head tilt while listening to internal thought
- Hand-product visible, technique confident

FRAME 3 (The Build):
- Eyebrow raise on a specific story beat
- Slow exhale through nose (almost-laugh)
- Glance to mirror and back to product (real human reflexive check)
- Lip-press mid-thought
- Slight nod to herself (decision-thinking)

FRAME 4 (The Pivot):
- Pause — set down product, look directly at camera
- Single eyebrow raise OR slow smile breaking the held face
- Knuckles to lip OR finger to lip during thinking beat
- Sigh + half-smile (the beat that breaks viewers)
- Chin tilt up at the moment of decision
- Slow blink + eye-contact lock

FRAME 5 (Near-Complete):
- Hands smoothing outfit, tucking hair
- Cheek-squeeze checking blush
- Lip-press to set color
- Slight tongue-in-cheek (playful self-check)
- Half-smile breaking neutral
- One eye-contact-camera + slow blink (knowing the look is working)

FRAME 6 (The Reveal):
- Hands running down outfit (smoothing, settling)
- Slow turn to camera
- Hair-flip (full one, ends catching light)
- Chin tilt up (composed)
- Half-smile (knowing she looks good)
- Single hand on hip, weight shifted
- Eye-contact-camera with slight side-eye

FRAME 7 (Exit Beat):
- Glance back over shoulder to camera
- Single hand wave OR no acknowledgment
- Walking out of frame
- Door close OR fabric flutter OR held silence
- Final exhale
- Smile breaks just before exit

### Q.EXT.15 — GRWM CAMERA INTERACTIONS

GRWM-suited camera moves (from the Performance Library):

- HAND SWAY ACROSS CAMERA — for transition moments between frames
- TAP MIRROR SURFACE LIGHTLY — acknowledging viewer's presence (rare, mischievous)
- LEAN INTO MIRROR — intimacy peak (use in Frame 4 pivot)
- LOOK-AWAY THEN SNAP-BACK — for emphasis on a key thought
- WIPE IMAGINARY SMUDGE — from "fourth wall," very rare, breaks frame intentionally
- FINGERPRINT ON GLASS — extremely intimate, beauty register
- WHISPER TO LENS — leaning in, hand cupped beside mouth, conspiratorial story moment
- BLOW TOWARD CAMERA — gentle exhale, fragrance reveal moment, end-frame option

EVERY GRWM USES MINIMUM 2 camera-interaction moves across its frame set.

### Q.EXT.16 — GRWM PRE-FLIGHT (FULL CHECKLIST)

[ ] Stakes declared at top of prompt (real, specific, emotionally charged)
[ ] Stakes line is concrete (passes the "could this be on someone's calendar" test)
[ ] Voice mode = SPOKEN (with rare SELECTIVE exceptions)
[ ] Signature flag = FULL (opener + sign-off both fresh-generated)
[ ] Emotional register declared and matched to stakes
[ ] Frame count 5, 6, or 7 — declared and justified
[ ] Frame 1 shows real vulnerability (bare face, undone, intimate setting)
[ ] Frame 6 (or final) shows complete composed reveal
[ ] Transformation arc visible across frames (each frame = one delta)
[ ] Hand-Face-Product Triangle specified for every routine frame (5 elements)
[ ] Frame rhythm varied — no two consecutive same framing+angle
[ ] Through-mirror angle used in at least one frame
[ ] Each hero product shown 2 ways (in-hand label + in-application)
[ ] Setting selected from 7 GRWM Setting Pillars and matched to stakes register
[ ] Setting atmospheric details specified (haze, light direction, props)
[ ] Voice content per frame specified (not generic — actual story-line examples)
[ ] No tutorial language anywhere in voice script
[ ] No "you guys" / "today I'll" / forbidden patterns
[ ] Hindi anchor moments at 1–2 emotional beats (Frame 1, 4, or sign-off)
[ ] Wardrobe pillar declared for closing state (matches register)
[ ] Wardrobe meets all 10 mandates from Part M
[ ] Aira identity lock referenced
[ ] Image integrity clauses present
[ ] Kinetic stillness layers per frame (with micro-life variant for intimate frames)
[ ] Hyper-realistic facial dynamics — minimum 3 per face frame
[ ] Camera-interaction moves — minimum 2 across reel
[ ] Performance beats per frame specified (gestures, face, posture)
[ ] Exit beat planned (Frame 7 or held final)
[ ] Energy arc traced: vulnerable → processing → decision → ready → loose
[ ] If brand-collab: all 7 restraint rules satisfied
[ ] If brand-collab: maximum 1 product performance move, hero product only
[ ] Tool routing per frame (NB / VEO)
[ ] Audio plan: music duck levels, ambient bed, silence beats
[ ] Negative block appended

### Q.EXT.17 — GRWM FAILURE MODES (what to NEVER do)

A GRWM fails the format if any of the following are true:

1. Generic stakes ("just getting ready") — viewer has no reason to care
2. Identical face across all frames — no transformation visible
3. Tutorial language in voice — kills intimacy, becomes instruction
4. Static framing across frames — visually flat
5. Hands hidden during application — defeats hand-face-product triangle
6. No through-mirror angle anywhere — misses the most cinematic GRWM tool
7. No vulnerability in opening frame — no contract earned
8. No pivot in the story — flat emotional arc
9. Brand foregrounded (labels held too long, brand-name read aloud) — becomes commercial
10. Outdoor setting — breaks the interior intimacy of the format
11. Multiple people in frame (other than implied phone-call partner) — breaks one-on-one viewer relationship
12. Music too loud over voice — kills the confessional quality
13. Background too clean / studio-like (unless mirror-wall studio chosen intentionally) — kills lived-in feel
14. Frame 6 reveal that doesn't show the full look — payoff missing
15. No exit beat or held final visual — no loop point, no re-watch value
16. Hindi forced into wrong moments — feels performed, not natural
17. Aira speaking to "you guys" — kills parasocial intimacy
18. Closed-mouth fake speaking — breaks lip-sync trust
19. Held expressions across frames — mannequin reads
20. Camera at unflattering high-angle for full reveal frame — undermines the payoff

If a generated GRWM exhibits ANY of the above 20 failures — REWRITE prompt before re-generating. Re-rolling the same prompt won't fix it.

---


---

## PART X — PROMPT GENERATION ENGINE (THE EXECUTION LAYER)

This section converts the directive from passive reference into an active enforcement system. Every prompt — without exception — must pass through this engine. Skipping any step results in a non-compliant prompt and must be rewritten before generation.

### X.1 — THE ENGINE ARCHITECTURE

Every prompt is generated through a fixed 12-stage pipeline. No stage is optional. No stage may be skipped. Stages are executed IN ORDER — never out of sequence.

```
STAGE 01 — INTAKE
STAGE 02 — CONCEPT LOCK
STAGE 03 — FORMAT CLASSIFICATION
STAGE 04 — REGISTER & VOICE LOCK
STAGE 05 — WARDROBE & PILLAR SELECTION
STAGE 06 — SETTING & ATMOSPHERIC LOCK
STAGE 07 — FRAME ARCHITECTURE
STAGE 08 — PER-FRAME EXPANSION
STAGE 09 — TOOL ROUTING
STAGE 10 — NEGATIVE BLOCK INJECTION
STAGE 11 — PRE-FLIGHT VALIDATION
STAGE 12 — FINAL OUTPUT
```

If any stage produces a value that conflicts with a prior stage's output, the engine HALTS and the prompt is rewritten from the conflicting stage forward. No conflicts may be carried into final output.

### X.2 — STAGE 01: INTAKE

User input is parsed into the following extracted variables:

```
INPUT VARIABLES (from user request):
- THEME / TOPIC: [what the reel is about]
- FORMAT HINT: [if specified — GRWM, ad, mood, commentary, etc.]
- STAKES (if explicitly given): [the why behind the reel]
- BRAND CONTEXT (if collab): [brand name, product, register]
- DELIVERABLE COUNT: [how many concepts requested]
- CONSTRAINTS (if any): [must-have or must-avoid elements]
```

If any required variable is ambiguous, the engine assigns a **default**:
- Format hint missing → engine selects format based on theme
- Stakes missing → engine generates specific stakes from theme
- Brand context missing → engine treats as non-collab
- Constraints missing → directive defaults apply

The engine NEVER asks the user clarifying questions during prompt generation. The directive contains enough defaults to resolve every ambiguity.

### X.3 — STAGE 02: CONCEPT LOCK

The engine writes a single concept line for each prompt. Format:

```
CONCEPT: "[evocative non-literal sentence under 12 words]"
```

CONCEPT LINE RULES:
- Never literal description ("a girl putting on lipstick" ❌)
- Always evocative ("the red that doesn't ask permission" ✅)
- Under 12 words
- Captures emotion + texture + implication
- Distinct from theme — concept is the *interpretation* of the theme

The engine generates 5 candidate concept lines internally and selects the most evocative one. The other 4 are discarded.

### X.4 — STAGE 03: FORMAT CLASSIFICATION

The engine classifies the reel into exactly ONE format from this taxonomy:

```
FORMAT TAXONOMY:
01. GRWM (Get Ready With Me)
02. CINEMATIC AD (beauty / fragrance / fashion / lifestyle product)
03. MOOD PIECE (silent or near-silent visual poetry)
04. CULTURAL COMMENTARY (deep-research, deconstruction, opinion)
05. LIFESTYLE / POV (day-in-life, intimate-warm, casual)
06. EDITORIAL FASHION FILM (high-style, narrative-light)
07. BEAUTY HERO (single-product macro-driven)
08. TREND DECONSTRUCTION (analyzing a trending sound or visual pattern)
09. PERSONAL STORY / CONFESSIONAL (intimate Aira-direct narrative)
10. EVENT / FESTIVAL (occasion-anchored)
11. WELLNESS / MORNING (active, soft-strong, ritual)
12. ASPIRATIONAL JOURNEY (travel, transit, arrival)
```

Once format is locked, the engine loads format-specific Parts:
- GRWM → Part Q + Q.EXTENDED + Appendices 10, 11
- Cinematic Ad → Part J + Part P + Appendices 7, 8
- Mood Piece → Part E + Part F + Part G
- Cultural Commentary → Part T + Part K
- And so on per format.

NEVER mix formats in one reel. Hybrid concepts route to the dominant format only.

### X.5 — STAGE 04: REGISTER & VOICE LOCK

The engine selects ONE emotional register per reel from Part K's seven:

```
REGISTER SELECTION LOGIC:
- Confrontation / decision stakes → KNOWING or ELECTRIC
- Tender / romantic / vulnerable → TENDER or REVERENT
- Cultural / commentary → CURIOUS-CONFIDENT or KNOWING
- Mood / fragrance → REVERENT or CONTEMPLATIVE
- Trend deconstruction → KNOWING or MISCHIEVOUS
- Lifestyle / morning → TENDER or CURIOUS-CONFIDENT
- Hero ad → ELECTRIC or REVERENT
- Festival / heritage → REVERENT or CURIOUS-CONFIDENT
```

The engine then locks the voice block:

```
VOICE BLOCK (auto-injected):
VOICE: AIRA PRIME
EMOTIONAL REGISTER: [selected]
LANGUAGE MIX: [85/15 default OR 70/30 if GRWM]
PACE: [register-matched wpm]
VOLUME: Intimate (-6dB to music bed)
HINDI MOMENTS: [engine pre-places at opener/pivot/sign-off]
SIGNATURE FLAG: [auto-determined per Part K suitability rules]
```

If SIGNATURE FLAG = FULL, the engine generates the opener and sign-off freshly per Part K rules. Both lines are written and locked before stage 06.

### X.6 — STAGE 05: WARDROBE & PILLAR SELECTION

The engine selects ONE pillar (or up to 2 blended pillars) from Part M's 10:

```
PILLAR SELECTION LOGIC:
- Reverent / contemplative → 1, 8, 10
- Knowing / mischievous → 2, 7
- Tender → 3, 8, 10
- Electric → 2, 7, 9
- Curious-confident → 1, 3, 4, 7
- Cinematic / mood / fragrance → 1, 2, 5, 9, 10
- Cultural commentary → 4, 7, 10
- Lifestyle / wellness → 3, 6
- Hero ad / launch → 2, 5, 9
- Festival / heritage → 4, 5
```

The engine writes a complete OUTFIT BLOCK:

```
OUTFIT BLOCK:
PILLAR: [N — name]
HERO ELEMENT: [the one standout piece]
PALETTE: [3 colors — anchor + 2 supporting]
SILHOUETTE: [exact cut — high-waist trouser + silk shell, etc.]
FABRIC: [specific — silk satin / cashmere / linen / etc.]
ACCESSORIES: [max 3, named — earrings + ring stack + bag]
HAIR: [exact style — sleek low bun / loose waves / etc.]
MAKEUP: [register-matched — dewy nude / sculpted bold / kohl-defined]
FOOTWEAR: [exact — pointed-toe pumps / chunky combat boots / etc.]
WARDROBE-CONCEPT POV: [what the outfit says — confidence / softness / power]
```

The 10 wardrobe mandates from Part M are validated against this block. If any mandate fails — engine rewrites the OUTFIT BLOCK before proceeding.

### X.7 — STAGE 06: SETTING & ATMOSPHERIC LOCK

The engine selects setting from format-specific options:
- GRWM → 1 of 7 GRWM Setting Pillars (Appendix 11 + Q.EXT.10)
- Ad → indoor studio / outdoor location / mirror-wall studio / set-design
- Mood / Cinematic → location-specific per concept

The engine writes a complete SETTING BLOCK:

```
SETTING BLOCK:
LOCATION: [specific — bedroom golden hour / mirror-wall studio / market street]
SURFACE / FLOOR: [marble / wood / concrete / tile]
LIGHT SOURCE: [window camera-left at golden hour / single hard pink key / overhead warm tungsten]
LIGHT QUALITY: [hard / soft / volumetric / wraparound]
COLOR TEMPERATURE: [3200K warm / 5600K daylight / mixed practical]
ATMOSPHERIC LAYER: [dust motes / steam / haze / particles — specific]
PRACTICAL LIGHTS IN FRAME (if any): [lamp / candle / neon / screen]
PROPS (named, purposeful): [list of 3–6 with story justification]
BACKGROUND ELEMENTS: [3 named — what's visible, what it says]
WEATHER (if outdoor): [light rain / wind / fog / heat shimmer / golden hour]
```

The 4-Voice Test (Part N) is run against the setting:
- What does the setting say?
- What does each prop say?
- What does the background say?
If any element fails to answer — removed or replaced before proceeding.

### X.8 — STAGE 07: FRAME ARCHITECTURE

The engine selects frame count (5, 6, 7, or 8) based on format:
- GRWM standard → 6 frames
- GRWM extended → 7 frames
- Mood piece → 5 frames
- Cinematic ad → 5–6 frames
- Trend deconstruction → 6 frames
- Hero beauty → 5 frames

The engine then plans the FRAME RHYTHM (per Part H):

```
FRAME RHYTHM PLAN:
F1: [framing] — [angle] — [subject %]
F2: [framing] — [angle] — [subject %]
F3: [framing] — [angle] — [subject %]
F4: [framing] — [angle] — [subject %]
F5: [framing] — [angle] — [subject %]
F6: [framing] — [angle] — [subject %]
(F7 if applicable)

RHYTHM CHECK:
- No two consecutive frames have same framing AND same angle
- At least one ECU OR Beauty Crop in beauty/GRWM
- Reveal frame is widest in the set
- Joint-cut check: every framing avoids ankles/knees/wrists/elbows/neck
```

The CONCEPT BIBLE (Part G) is locked here:

```
CONCEPT BIBLE:
1. COLOR THREAD: [dominant + 2 supporting]
2. LIGHT SIGNATURE: [direction + hardness + color temp + atmosphere]
3. TEXTURE/MATERIAL ECHO: [one tactile quality threaded across frames]
4. MOTION VECTOR: [directional bias — leftward / rising / falling / etc.]
5. ATMOSPHERIC CONSTANT: [element present in every frame]
6. EMOTIONAL TEMPERATURE: [continuous register]
7. COMPOSITIONAL RHYME: [geometric pattern repeating]
```

### X.9 — STAGE 08: PER-FRAME EXPANSION

For EACH frame, the engine writes a complete FRAME BLOCK using this fixed schema:

```
FRAME [N]
================================
FRAMING: [exact — MCU / Beauty Crop / Cowboy / etc.]
CROP POINTS: [Top: X / Bottom: Y / Sides: Z]
JOINT-CUT CHECK: PASS / FAIL (must be PASS to ship)
SUBJECT %: [N% of frame height]
CAMERA HEIGHT: [eye-level / low / high / dutch]
CAMERA ANGLE: [straight / 3/4 / profile / OTS / through-mirror]
CAMERA MOVE (if VEO): [push-in / pull-back / orbit / static — one only]
LENS: [24mm / 35mm / 50mm / 85mm / anamorphic / macro]
DOF: [shallow / deep / rack-focus]

SUBJECT (AIRA):
- BODY POSITION: [seated / standing / leaning / mid-stride]
- BODY ANGLE TO CAMERA: [exact]
- WEIGHT DISTRIBUTION: [single-leg / both / shifted]
- HAND POSITION: [left + right described separately, with what they're doing]
- POSTURE STATE: [relaxed / composed / tense / kinetic]
- HAIR STATE: [exact — flicked / settled / tucked / mid-curl / wet]
- WARDROBE STATE: [robe drop / fully composed / mid-adjust / sleeve roll]
- FOOTWEAR: [visible / not-visible — if visible, exact contact with ground]

FACIAL DYNAMICS (minimum 3 per Part R):
- EYES: [exact micro-state — mid-blink / catchlight at X position / asymmetry]
- BROWS: [exact micro-state — single raised / micro-furrow / relaxed]
- LIPS: [exact micro-state — mid-word phoneme / lip-press / asymmetric corner]
- CHEEKS: [exact micro-state — apple-lift / shadow at hollow / micro-flush]
- BREATH: [visible inhale / pre-word breath / post-exhale / silent breath-hold]

GESTURE / PERFORMANCE BEAT (if applicable):
- GESTURE: [from Part L vocabulary — single name]
- TIMING: [lands at 0.X seconds within frame]
- DURATION: [0.4–1.2s]
- MOTIVATION: [emotional reason]

PRODUCT (if applicable):
- PRODUCT: [exact — type, brand-neutral or named]
- HOW HELD: [grip detail — fingers wrapping / fingertip pinch / palm cradle]
- LABEL VISIBILITY: [readable Y/N — if Y, for how long]
- INTERACTION: [tap / sweep / press / blend / swipe / dab / draw / set]
- PRODUCT PERFORMANCE MOVE (if hero): [from Appendix 7 — name one only]

SPATIAL LOGIC (Part I):
- FOREGROUND: [what's there — blurred or sharp]
- MIDGROUND: [Aira + held objects]
- BACKGROUND: [what's there — soft or sharp, motion or static]
- 5-QUESTION TEST: PASS for every element

KINETIC STILLNESS LAYERS (Part D — all 6 mandatory):
1. SUBJECT MICRO-ACTION: [exact]
2. FABRIC + HAIR STATE: [exact]
3. PARTICULATE LAYER: [exact — dust motes / steam / petals]
4. CONTACT-POINT ACTIVITY: [exact]
5. BACKGROUND MOTION: [exact]
6. LIGHT IN MOTION: [exact — flare / shaft / flicker / caustic]

LIGHTING (specific to frame):
- KEY DIRECTION: [angle + height]
- KEY HARDNESS: [hard / soft / wraparound]
- FILL: [present Y/N — direction, ratio]
- RIM / BACK LIGHT: [present Y/N — direction]
- PRACTICAL: [present Y/N — what / where]
- COLOR TEMP: [exact Kelvin or named — tungsten warm / golden hour / cool blue]

VOICE-OVER (if SPOKEN frame):
- VO LINE (verbatim): "[exact words]"
- VO DELIVERY: [pace / breath / pause / volume]
- VO TIMING: [starts X.Xs, ends Y.Ys within frame]
- HINDI MOMENT (if any): [word + placement reason]
- ON-SCREEN TEXT (if any): [verbatim + position]
- AMBIENT SOUND: [continues / ducks / drops]
- MUSIC LEVEL: [-6 / -12 / -18 / -24 dB]

CONCEPT BIBLE ANCHORS HIT IN THIS FRAME:
[list which of the 7 anchors this frame carries — minimum 5/7]

EMOTIONAL BEAT: [single named emotion this frame holds]
NEXT-FRAME TEST: "In 0.5s, [X] will happen."
```

EVERY field is filled. NO field is left blank. If a field is non-applicable, the engine writes "N/A — [reason]".

### X.10 — STAGE 09: TOOL ROUTING

The engine assigns each frame to a generation tool:

```
TOOL ROUTING TABLE (per Appendix 9):

NANO BANANA (NB) — for:
- Hero stills with hyper-real product texture
- Frozen-moment captures (levitation peak, splash apex)
- Beauty macros (skin, eye, lip ECUs)
- Single-frame highly-detailed setups
- Composite stills that will be animated later

VEO 3.1 — for:
- Native motion sequences (full shot with camera + subject + audio)
- Voice + lip-sync shots
- Multi-action choreography
- Ambient atmospheric motion
- Anything requiring synced sound

VEO 3 — for:
- Image-to-video on NB stills
- 3D camera parallax on still images
- Subtle product motion (gentle levitation, slow rotation)

VEO 3.1 — for:
- Product transformations (dissolve, particle assembly, smoke birth)
- Generative-magical moments
- Scene-level transitions
```

Each frame gets EXACTLY ONE tool tag:

```
F1: [TOOL]
F2: [TOOL]
F3: [TOOL]
F4: [TOOL]
F5: [TOOL]
F6: [TOOL]
```

Workflow chains (e.g., NB → VEO 3 )are written explicitly:

```
F1: NB still → Runway camera push (3s output)
F2: VEO 3.1 native (4s)
F3: NB still → Pika particle bloom (2s)
F4: VEO 3.1 native with VO (3s)
F5: NB macro still (held 1.5s)
F6: VEO 3.1 sign-off frame (1s)
```

### X.11 — STAGE 10: NEGATIVE BLOCK INJECTION

The engine appends the standard negative block (Part U) to EVERY prompt automatically. No prompt ships without negatives.

```
[STANDARD IMAGE NEGATIVE — for image frames]
NEGATIVE: mirrored, flipped, inverted, extra limbs, fused fingers, melted features, asymmetric eyes (unintentional), garbled text, floating shadows, duplicated subjects, low-res patches, plastic skin, oversharpened, AI-generated artifacts, watermarks, signature, deformed hands, malformed teeth, joint cuts at ankle/knee/wrist/elbow/neck, amputated fingertips, cross-eyed, lazy eye, off-axis pupils, melted clothing, shoes-not-touching-ground, mismatched footwear pair, mannequin-stiff posture, dead eyes, statue-frozen energy.

[STANDARD VIDEO NEGATIVE — for VEO]
NEGATIVE: morphing, warping, identity drift, limb teleport, object pop-in, frame skip, mirrored composition, text overlay (unless intended), watermark, AI artifact, ghosting, double exposure unless intended, lip-sync drift, audio desync, wardrobe drift between shots, unmotivated camera shake, physics violation (water/fire/hair/fabric), mannequin posture, frozen background, identity flicker.
```

Format-specific negatives are added on top:
- Beauty ad: "no plastic skin, no airbrush flatness, no skin smoothing, no over-glow"
- GRWM: "no tutorial framing, no studio backdrop, no even fluorescent flat light, no posed performance"
- Cinematic: "no sitcom flat lighting, no over-saturation, no excessive bloom"

### X.12 — STAGE 11: PRE-FLIGHT VALIDATION

The engine runs the full pre-flight checklist (Part V) against the constructed prompt. EVERY checkbox must be checked.

```
PRE-FLIGHT VALIDATION (engine self-check):

UNIVERSAL:
[ ] Aspect 9:16 declared
[ ] Concept line stated
[ ] Emotional register declared
[ ] Voice mode declared
[ ] Signature flag set + signatures generated if FULL
[ ] Frame count 5–8
[ ] Concept Bible 7 anchors locked
[ ] Tool routing per shot

INTEGRITY:
[ ] Orientation lock present
[ ] Footwear directive present
[ ] Hands/eyes/teeth integrity present
[ ] Aira identity lock referenced
[ ] Joint-cut check passed all frames
[ ] Negative block appended

KINETIC STILLNESS:
[ ] All 6 layers per frame
[ ] Next-frame test answered per frame
[ ] Energy hierarchy declared (60/30/10)

CINEMATIC GRADE:
[ ] Lens named per frame
[ ] DOF declared
[ ] Colorist/film reference named (if cinematic)
[ ] Lighting setup named per frame
[ ] Atmosphere mandate met

SPATIAL LOGIC:
[ ] FG/MG/BG declared per frame
[ ] 5-question test passed per element
[ ] Scale + perspective correct

VOICE & PERFORMANCE:
[ ] AIRA PRIME locked
[ ] Hindi anchors placed (if applicable)
[ ] Fresh opener + sign-off (if FULL signature)
[ ] VO line per frame (if SPOKEN)
[ ] Music duck levels stated

PHYSICAL & WARDROBE:
[ ] Identity lock referenced
[ ] Wardrobe pillar declared
[ ] All 10 wardrobe mandates met
[ ] Footwear specified

EVERY ELEMENT SPEAKS:
[ ] 4-Voice Test passed (body, outfit, BG, objects)

3D CAMERA & PRODUCT:
[ ] One camera move per shot maximum
[ ] One product performance move per shot maximum (if ad)
[ ] Believability rules met
[ ] Tool routing correct

GRWM (if format):
[ ] Stakes declared (specific, not generic)
[ ] Opening + closing states defined
[ ] Frame rhythm varied
[ ] Hand-Face-Product Triangle complete per routine frame
[ ] Through-mirror frame present
[ ] All 5 GRWM defining characteristics met
[ ] Energy arc traced

FACIAL DYNAMICS:
[ ] 3+ micro-dynamics per face frame
[ ] Sequenced expressions (Duchenne markers)
[ ] No held expressions across frames
[ ] Breath specified on key frames

VEO (if video):
[ ] Shot type, camera move, lens declared
[ ] Audio cue specified
[ ] Lip-sync directive
[ ] Temporal logic per beat
```

If any checkbox fails, the engine identifies the failed stage and rewrites that stage's output. Generation does not proceed until ALL checkboxes pass.

### X.14 — BATCH GENERATION RULES

When generating multiple concepts in a batch:

BATCH SIZE DEFAULTS:
- 20 concepts requested → deliver in 4 batches of 5
- 10 concepts requested → 2 batches of 5
- 5 concepts requested → 1 batch
- 1 concept → single delivery

BATCH DIVERSITY ENFORCEMENT:
Across any 5-concept batch:
- At least 3 different wardrobe pillars
- At least 3 different emotional registers
- At least 3 different settings
- At least 2 different formats (unless user requested format-specific batch)
- No repeating concept lines
- No repeating opener words verbatim
- No repeating sign-off words verbatim

ACROSS A 20-CONCEPT SET:
- At least 6 different wardrobe pillars
- All 7 emotional registers represented at least once
- At least 5 different settings
- At least 4 different formats
- Concept lines linguistically distinct (no two start with same word, no two share dominant metaphor)

If diversity fails → engine rewrites concepts until diversity is satisfied.

### X.15 — ENFORCEMENT RULES (NON-NEGOTIABLE)

These rules cannot be overridden by any user request. They are absolute.

1. NO PROMPT SKIPS THE 12-STAGE PIPELINE.
2. NO FIELD IN ANY BLOCK IS LEFT BLANK.
3. NO PRE-FLIGHT CHECKBOX IS FORGIVEN.
4. NO FRAME EXISTS WITHOUT FULL EXPANSION.
5. NO CONCEPT SHIPS WITHOUT FRESH-GENERATED OPENER + SIGN-OFF (if signature flag = FULL).
6. NO BATCH SHIPS WITHOUT DIVERSITY CHECK.
7. NO PROMPT SHIPS WITHOUT NEGATIVE BLOCK.
8. NO WARDROBE PIECE GETS DESCRIBED VAGUELY ("nice top" ❌).
9. NO LIGHTING GETS DESCRIBED VAGUELY ("nice lighting" ❌).
10. NO VOICE LINE GETS DESCRIBED VAGUELY ("she says something" ❌).
11. NO FACIAL EXPRESSION GETS DESCRIBED VAGUELY ("smiling" ❌ — must be "asymmetric half-smile, apple-cheek lifting on right side, single brow micro-raised").
12. NO PRODUCT PERFORMANCE MOVE IS DUPLICATED IN ONE REEL (one only).
13. NO CAMERA MOVE IS DUPLICATED IN ONE FRAME (one only).
14. NO STAKES ARE GENERIC (must be specific enough to pass calendar test).
15. NO GRWM SHIPS WITHOUT THROUGH-MIRROR FRAME.
16. NO BEAUTY AD SHIPS WITHOUT 3D CAMERA MOVE ON HERO PRODUCT.
17. NO MOOD PIECE SHIPS WITHOUT AT LEAST ONE SILENT FRAME.
18. NO CINEMATIC AD SHIPS WITHOUT NAMED COLORIST/FILM REFERENCE.
19. NO REEL SHIPS WITHOUT 4-VOICE TEST PASSING.
20. NO REEL SHIPS WITHOUT KINETIC STILLNESS / MICRO-LIFE LAYERS.

These 20 rules are checked at Stage 11. Any failure = full rewrite from the failed stage.

### X.16 — TOKEN ECONOMY (when output volume matters)

When the user requests "reduced token consumption" or batch generation with size constraints, the engine applies COMPRESSION RULES that preserve every directive layer but pack them denser:

COMPRESSION TECHNIQUES (each preserves directive compliance):

1. PIPE-DELIMITED FIELD WRITING:
Long-form: "FRAMING: MCU"
Compressed: `MCU | 70% subj | eye-lvl | 3/4 turn | 35mm`

2. CONCEPT-LINE-FIRST STRUCTURE:
Compressed prompts open with: `[CONCEPT] | [Format] | [Pillar N] | [Setting] | [Register] | [Duration]` then frames.

3. FRAME COMPRESSION SCHEMA:
```
F1 [Framing | Crop | Camera | Lens]
SUB: [posture | hand | hair | wardrobe state | footwear]
FACE: [eyes | brows | lips | cheeks | breath]
GEST: [name | timing] | PROD: [name | how-held | label]
SPAT: [FG / MG / BG]
KIN: [1: micro-action | 2: fabric/hair | 3: particles | 4: contact | 5: BG motion | 6: light]
LIGHT: [key | fill | rim | practical | temp]
VO: "[verbatim]" | [pace | duck level]
ANCHORS: [5-7 of 7] | EMO: [beat] | NEXT: [in 0.5s, X]
TOOL: [tag]
```

4. SHARED-CONTEXT EXTRACTION:
What's identical across frames (Concept Bible, Outfit Block, Setting Block, Voice Block) is written ONCE at top, then frames reference: `OUTFIT: see top`.

5. NEGATIVE BLOCK DEDUPED:
Standard negatives appear once at end of full prompt set, not per frame.

6. DEFAULT INHERITANCE:
Anything matching directive defaults isn't restated. E.g., if every frame uses 9:16, it's stated once at top, not per frame.

COMPRESSION LIMITS:
- A frame block can compress to ~80–120 words minimum
- Below that, it loses directive compliance
- Compression NEVER drops fields, only condenses notation

### X.17 — INVOCATION

To invoke the Prompt Generation Engine, use any of these triggers in the user message:

```
"Create [N] concepts" — engine runs full pipeline, outputs N concepts
"Generate [theme] reel" — engine creates 1 concept on theme
"Batch [N]" — engine generates N concepts with diversity enforcement
"Compress" or "Reduce tokens" — engine applies Section X.16 compression
"GRWM [stakes]" — format-locked GRWM with given stakes
"Beauty ad [product]" — format-locked beauty ad
"Mood [concept]" — format-locked mood piece
```

Default behavior when no trigger is given but user describes a concept: engine runs full pipeline assuming 1-concept generation.

### X.18 — THE GUARANTEE

When the engine runs correctly, every prompt produced satisfies ALL of the following simultaneously:

✓ Aira identity-locked (face, body, hair, hands, footwear)
✓ Aspect 9:16 native composition
✓ Wardrobe pillar declared with 10 mandates met
✓ Setting fully atmospheric, 4-Voice Test passing
✓ Frame architecture rhythmic, joint-cuts safe
✓ Per-frame expansion complete (no blank fields)
✓ Kinetic stillness or micro-life layers present
✓ Hyper-realistic facial dynamics specified per face frame
✓ Voice block locked (AIRA PRIME, fresh signatures, Hindi placement)
✓ Performance beats per frame
✓ Spatial logic FG/MG/BG declared
✓ Cinematic grade specified (lens, light, colorist, atmosphere)
✓ Product performance + 3D camera coordinated (if ad)
✓ GRWM 5 characteristics met (if GRWM)
✓ Tool routing optimized per frame
✓ Negative block appended
✓ Pre-flight validation 100% pass
✓ Output formatted per Stage 12 schema

This is the GUARANTEE. Every prompt — without exception. No drift, no shortcuts, no vagueness. Every protocol active. Every detail explicit.

## CHECKPOINT 3.1 — PROMPT GENERATION ENGINE LIVE
(Continued — engine is now self-executing per Part X)

---

## PART Y — UNIQUE OBJECT DESIGN PROTOCOL

Every beauty product, accessory, prop, or hero object in any frame must be **uniquely designed**. Generic, stock-feeling, or undefined products are forbidden. This protocol forces the engine to specify the product's industrial design with the same rigor as Aira's wardrobe and the lighting.

### Y.1 — THE PRINCIPLE

A product on screen carries the same weight as a character. If the product looks like it was pulled from a generic catalog, the entire reel reads as ad-stock. Premium reels — the ones that feel art-directed rather than generated — show products that look like they were specifically designed for this brand, this campaign, this moment.

The engine must imagine the product as if a real industrial designer briefed it: silhouette, material, finish, weight, label, every detail intentional.

### Y.2 — MANDATORY OBJECT DESIGN BLOCK

For EVERY product or hero object in a frame, the engine writes a complete OBJECT DESIGN BLOCK before the frame is finalized:

```
OBJECT DESIGN BLOCK — [object name]

CATEGORY: [perfume bottle / lipstick / serum dropper / compact /
  jar / tube / vial / atomizer / stick / palette / capsule / wand /
  brush / accessory / prop]

SILHOUETTE:
- Overall shape: [tall sculpted column / faceted prism / smooth ovoid
  / asymmetric cut / architectural cube / hand-blown bulb / cylindrical
  with carved waist / inverted teardrop / hexagonal flask / brutalist
  block]
- Proportions: [height-to-width ratio / cap-to-body ratio]
- Distinctive feature: [the one thing that makes it instantly
  recognizable — an angle, a curve, a notch, a carved shoulder,
  an asymmetric stopper, a sculpted base]

MATERIAL:
- Glass: [hand-blown / cast / pressed / faceted-cut / frosted /
  tinted (specify color) / crystal-clear / smoked]
- Metal: [brushed brass / polished gold / matte aluminum / oxidized
  bronze / chrome / antique silver / black anodized / rose-gold]
- Ceramic: [matte stoneware / glazed porcelain / unglazed clay /
  enamel-finished]
- Resin / Acrylic: [hand-poured resin / lab-cut acrylic / sculpted
  composite / pearlescent / translucent tinted]
- Mixed: [glass body + metal cap / ceramic body + wood detail /
  metal + leather wrap]

FINISH: [Matte / Satin / Glossy / Hammered / Brushed / Frosted /
  Mirror / Sandblasted / Etched / Pearlized / Iridescent / Velvet-coat
  / Soft-touch / Lacquered]

CAP / CLOSURE:
- Form: [magnetic snap / weighted screw / flip-top / pump / dropper
  / atomizer / sliding sleeve / hidden hinge]
- Material: [matched to body / contrasting metal / heavy-weight stone
  / sculpted resin]
- Detail: [embossed brand mark / engraved logo / blank minimal /
  heritage-textured / chain-attached]

LABEL / BRAND MARK:
- Style: [embossed-no-print / pressed gold foil / inlay / engraved /
  silk-screen minimal / handwritten-style / sculptural typography /
  no-label-only-shape (extreme luxury)]
- Typography: [serif classical / sans-serif modernist / hand-lettered
  / bespoke custom / monogram / wordmark only]
- Position: [centered / off-center / wrap-around / under-base hidden /
  cap-only]
- Readability priority: [must be visible Y/N]

COLOR STORY:
- Primary: [body color]
- Secondary: [cap or accent color]
- Tertiary: [label or detail color]
- Must coordinate with reel's COLOR THREAD (Concept Bible)

DETAIL LEVEL:
- Base: [weighted thick base / lifted feet / sculpted underside]
- Edges: [sharp / softened / chamfered / radiused]
- Transitions: [where body meets cap / where label meets glass /
  where applicator meets product]
- Embossing / Engraving: [if any — what, where, how subtle]
- Texture micro-elements: [ribbing / fluting / grooves / dots / smooth]

INTERIOR / FORMULA VISIBILITY (if transparent):
- Liquid color: [exact — honey amber / cool blue tint / pearlescent
  pink / rose-gold shimmer / clear / smoked / dual-phase separated]
- Liquid behavior: [still / slow-rolling / dual-phase / shimmering
  particulate / sediment-suspended / oil-water layered]
- Caustic potential: [will it refract light / cast color shadow /
  catch caustic patterns]

WEIGHT IMPLICATION:
- Hand-feel suggested by design: [substantial / featherlight / dense /
  hollow-light / leaded-bottom / surprisingly-heavy-for-size]
- Visual cue: [thick glass walls / metal weight ring / hollow-suggesting
  thinness]

BRAND REGISTER (the design must communicate one of):
- Quiet luxury (minimal, weighted, no-logo, sculptural)
- Editorial bold (architectural, color-saturated, statement)
- Heritage (vintage references, ornate, traditional motifs)
- Modern minimalist (clean, geometric, restrained)
- Indo-modern (heritage motif modernized — paisley etched on minimal form)
- Tech-forward (chrome, lab-aesthetic, scientific clarity)
- Apothecary (amber glass, hand-labeled, herbalist warmth)
- Sculptural (art-object first, product second)

PRODUCT FAMILY COHERENCE (if multiple products in reel):
- All products share at least 2 design elements (material / finish /
  cap shape / silhouette family / color story / typography)
- Hero product can have one elevated element vs. supporting products
- Family must read as designed BY ONE designer
```

### Y.3 — THE UNIQUENESS TEST

Before any product ships in a prompt, the engine runs:

```
[ ] Could this product be confused with a generic AI-stock bottle?
    If YES → REWRITE.
[ ] Does the silhouette have at least ONE distinctive feature?
    If NO → REWRITE.
[ ] Is the material specified beyond "glass" or "metal"?
    If NO → REWRITE.
[ ] Does the cap/closure have intentional design?
    If NO → REWRITE.
[ ] Is the label treatment specified (not just "label")?
    If NO → REWRITE.
[ ] Does the design carry a brand register?
    If NO → REWRITE.
[ ] Would an industrial designer recognize this brief as complete?
    If NO → REWRITE.
[ ] Does the product belong in this concept's color thread and register?
    If NO → REWRITE.

ALL 8 MUST PASS.
```

### Y.4 — NON-PRODUCT OBJECT EXTENSION

This protocol applies to ANY prominent object in frame:

JEWELRY: specific cut, setting, metal, stone, era of design influence
Example: not "earrings" but "sculptural twisted-gold drop earrings, hammered brass finish, asymmetric — left earring sits 1cm lower than right, kundan accent at the joint, designer-art-piece feel"

BAGS: specific shape, hardware, material, closure mechanism, era
Example: not "handbag" but "structured trapezoid leather bag in oxblood, brushed antique gold hardware, magnetic closure, hand-stitched edge, mid-century design influence"

ACCESSORIES (sunglasses, watches, hair clips): specific frame, material, color, period reference

PROPS (cups, books, candles, vases): specific material, era, register, story
Example: not "coffee cup" but "matte black hand-thrown ceramic mug with raw clay base ring, slightly imperfect lip — Japanese wabi-sabi influence"

BACKGROUND OBJECTS (visible but not held): even background objects need uniqueness if visible enough to register — vase, lamp, mirror frame, picture, throw — each gets a brief design note.

### Y.5 — SIGNATURE OBJECT ARCHETYPES (engine reference library)

Starting points the engine elaborates from. Never used as final spec.

PERFUME BOTTLE ARCHETYPES:
1. Sculpted-shoulder column — tall, narrow, carved-in waist, weighted base, magnetic stopper
2. Faceted prism — geometric multi-sided cut, refracts like a gem, minimal label
3. Hand-blown bulb — organic asymmetric form, no two identical, raw stopper
4. Architectural cube — brutalist block, embossed logo only, weighted base
5. Inverted teardrop — apex-down balance, sits in matched stand, stopper at top
6. Apothecary heritage — amber glass, hand-applied paper label, cork stopper, antique-feel
7. Indo-modern — minimal silhouette with heritage motif (paisley, jaali) etched into glass

LIPSTICK ARCHETYPES:
1. Magnetic-snap heavy bullet — full metal weight, satisfying click
2. Sculpted twist — non-cylindrical body, ergonomic curve, brand-mark engraved
3. Faceted prism — multi-sided body catching light at every angle
4. Eco-luxe — biodegradable bamboo or recycled aluminum with refill mechanism
5. Heritage carved — engraved metal sleeve with Mughal or Art Deco pattern
6. Architectural slim — thinner than standard, engineering-minimal

SERUM / DROPPER ARCHETYPES:
1. Frosted-glass column — soft-touch frosted, gold dropper cap, weighted base
2. Apothecary amber — UV-protective amber, paper-label heritage, ceramic dropper bulb
3. Lab-tech clear — scientific-clarity glass, chrome dropper, minimalist sans-serif
4. Sculpted ceramic — hand-thrown ceramic body, glass dropper

JAR ARCHETYPES:
1. Hand-thrown ceramic with stone lid — wabi-sabi imperfect, matte glaze, river-stone lid
2. Faceted glass with brass screw-top — multi-sided body, brushed brass cap, embossed mark
3. Frosted minimal — clean cylinder, frosted finish, magnetic flush lid
4. Heritage cut-crystal — Indo-luxury, weighted, faceted, gold-rimmed lid with insignia

COMPACT / PALETTE ARCHETYPES:
1. Magnetic minimal — slim profile, satisfying snap-close, mirror inside
2. Sculpted clamshell — organic curved form, weighted, brushed metal
3. Heritage carved metal — engraved exterior pattern, vintage compact-mirror feel
4. Architectural square — sharp corners, embossed logo, weighted hinge

### Y.6 — INTEGRATION INTO THE ENGINE

STAGE 08 amendment: when a frame contains a product or hero object, the engine MUST insert an OBJECT DESIGN BLOCK before completing the frame's PRODUCT field.

```
PRODUCT (if applicable):
- PRODUCT NAME: [exact descriptor]
- OBJECT DESIGN BLOCK: [full Y.2 spec]
- HOW HELD: [grip detail]
- LABEL VISIBILITY: [readable Y/N — duration]
- INTERACTION: [exact technique]
- PRODUCT PERFORMANCE MOVE: [if hero, one only]
```

STAGE 11 amendment — adds to pre-flight:
[ ] Every product/hero object has a complete OBJECT DESIGN BLOCK
[ ] Uniqueness Test (Y.3) passed for every product
[ ] Product family coherence verified if multiple products
[ ] Background objects with visible presence have brief design notes

ENFORCEMENT RULE 21 (added to Part X.15):
21. NO PRODUCT OR HERO OBJECT SHIPS WITHOUT A COMPLETE OBJECT DESIGN BLOCK. Generic descriptors ("a bottle," "a lipstick," "earrings") are forbidden.

### Y.7 — GUARANTEE EXTENDED

✓ Every product is uniquely designed with full industrial-design specification
✓ Every accessory is specifically described (cut, material, era, hardware)
✓ Every prop has design intent (material, finish, story)
✓ No object on screen reads as generic AI-stock
✓ Product families show coherent design language across reel
✓ Background objects with visible presence carry brief design notes

Every object on screen now looks like it was designed, not generated.

## CHECKPOINT 3.2 — UNIQUE OBJECT DESIGN ENFORCED
(Continued — object/product uniqueness now mandatory per Part Y)
