## PART D.EXTENDED — KINETIC STILLNESS: FULL SPECIFICATION

This section expands Part D with exhaustive detail to close every loophole.

### D.EXT.1 — WHY KINETIC STILLNESS EXISTS

A still image is technically frozen. But the human brain reconstructs motion from visual cues. When those cues are absent, the brain reads "statue" or "mannequin" — which is why most AI-generated images feel dead even when technically correct.

Kinetic Stillness is the discipline of encoding implied motion into every pixel so the brain reconstructs movement from a frozen frame. The image should feel like it was captured 0.1 seconds into an action by a photographer with perfect timing — not composed by an artist arranging elements at rest.

The difference between a dead frame and a living frame is not resolution, not detail, not color — it is MOTION IMPLIED THROUGH STILLNESS.

### D.EXT.2 — THE SIX LAYERS: EXHAUSTIVE SPECIFICATION

LAYER 1 — SUBJECT MICRO-ACTION

WHAT IT IS: The subject's body is captured in the middle of a small physical action — never at full rest, never at full completion. The body is between positions.

WHAT IT IS NOT: A posed position. A held stance. A "ready" position. A neutral standing position.

COMPLETE VOCABULARY OF MICRO-ACTIONS:


STANDING MICRO-ACTIONS:
- Mid-weight-shift (hips transitioning from centered to one-leg dominant)
- Mid-step (one foot 2 inches off ground, mid-transfer)
- Mid-turn (shoulders rotated 15° ahead of hips — torso twist)
- Mid-lean (shifting weight toward wall/surface/object)
- Mid-rise (halfway between sitting and standing — quads engaged)
- Mid-shoulder-drop (one shoulder descending from shrug)
- Mid-head-turn (chin rotating, eyes leading head by 0.2 seconds)
- Mid-reach (arm extending toward object, fingers not yet touching)
- Mid-recoil (pulling back from surprise, laugh, or wind)

SEATED MICRO-ACTIONS:
- Mid-lean-forward (torso tilting toward mirror/camera/object)
- Mid-cross-legs (one knee rising over the other, not settled)
- Mid-arm-rest-shift (elbow sliding forward/back on surface)
- Mid-head-tilt (head falling sideways toward shoulder)
- Mid-exhale (chest descending, shoulders dropping)
- Mid-look-up (chin rising, eyes traveling upward)

HAND MICRO-ACTIONS:
- Mid-grip-tighten (fingers curling around object, knuckles whitening)
- Mid-release (fingers opening from fist, object just leaving palm)
- Mid-gesture (hand frozen in the arc of a spoken word)
- Mid-brush (fingers traveling through hair, halfway through the stroke)
- Mid-apply (product applicator touching skin, 50% through stroke)

FULL-BODY KINETIC:
- Mid-stride (clear weight on front foot, back foot pushing off)
- Mid-jump (body at apex — neither rising nor falling)
- Mid-spin (body rotated 90° from start, hair trailing 180°)
- Mid-dance (isolated body part movement — hip pop, shoulder roll, hand wave)
- Mid-fall (controlled descent — sitting onto chair, lowering to floor)

THE 0.1-SECOND RULE EXPLAINED:
If you froze time 0.1 seconds before this frame — the subject would be in a slightly different position. If you froze time 0.1 seconds after — also different. The current frame exists at ONE specific millisecond within a continuous motion. That is what makes it alive.

HOW TO PROMPT IT:
Never: "Aira standing by the window"
Always: "Aira mid-weight-shift onto her left leg, right hand mid-reach toward the curtain, chin turning 15° toward window light, left shoulder dropping from a just-completed exhale"

FAILURE MODE:
If the subject looks like they could hold this exact position for 5 seconds without moving — the frame is dead. Rewrite.


LAYER 2 — FABRIC + HAIR STATE

WHAT IT IS: Every piece of fabric on the subject and every strand of hair is captured mid-movement. Fabric billows, drapes, snaps, settles, or lifts. Hair flicks, falls, separates, or catches light at a moving angle.

WHAT IT IS NOT: Fabric hanging still. Hair helmet. Perfectly symmetrical drape. Cloth painted onto body.

FABRIC STATES (each must specify DIRECTION):
- Mid-billow (fabric caught by wind/motion, inflated outward — state which direction: left/right/up/backward)
- Mid-snap (fabric at end of whip — like a flag at max extension, about to return)
- Mid-settle (fabric just released from motion, still 30% inflated, falling back toward body)
- Mid-cling (fabric pressed against body by wind or motion — reveals body contour beneath)
- Mid-flutter (light fabric edges oscillating — hem, cuff, scarf ends)
- Mid-twist (fabric caught in torso rotation — wrapping around body)
- Mid-lift (hem rising from movement — running, sitting, wind-caught)
- Mid-fold (fabric creating new fold at joint — elbow, knee, waist — from body's motion)

HAIR STATES (each must specify DIRECTION + STRAND BEHAVIOR):
- Mid-flick (hair arc from head-turn — specify direction, specify which portion: tips only, full length, face-framing pieces only)
- Mid-fall (hair descending after being lifted — gravity pulling, tips pointing down)
- Mid-separation (individual strands visible separating from main mass — catching light individually)
- Mid-catch-light (hair strand at exact angle to reflect key light — creating shine-band at moving position)
- Mid-wind (hair pushed by external force — direction specified, intensity: gentle drift vs. strong push)
- Mid-tuck (hair being moved by hand — strands between fingers, partially behind ear)
- Mid-bounce (hair responding to footstep or head-movement — slight upward then settling)

THE DIRECTION RULE:
Every fabric and hair movement MUST state a direction. "Hair flowing" is insufficient. "Hair flowing camera-left, tips separating, face-framing pieces crossing her jawline" is correct.

HOW FABRIC AND HAIR ENCODE THE WHOLE FRAME'S ENERGY:
If the subject is moving rightward:
- Hair flows LEFT (opposing motion direction — inertia)
- Jacket flares LEFT (same — inertia)
- Scarf trails LEFT and slightly upward (air resistance)
This directional consistency is what makes the frame FEEL real. Random directions = chaos. Consistent opposing directions = physics = believability.

FAILURE MODE:
If fabric hangs perfectly vertical and hair sits symmetrically — the frame is dead. Even in zero-wind indoor scenes, body movement creates micro-disturbance in fabric and hair. There is ALWAYS at least a slight drape-shift, a strand out of place, a hem in slight motion.


LAYER 3 — PARTICULATE LAYER

WHAT IT IS: The air in the frame is not empty. There are visible particles, suspended elements, atmospheric matter that the light catches. This single layer transforms any frame from "digital render" to "captured moment in a real space."

WHAT IT IS NOT: Clean empty air. Invisible atmosphere. Uniform fog (that's different — that's atmospheric haze which goes in LIGHT layer).

COMPLETE PARTICULATE VOCABULARY:
- Dust motes (tiny bright specks floating in light shaft — golden, warm)
- Mist (fine water vapor — cool, grey-blue, partially obscuring)
- Smoke (denser than mist — rising, curling, warm grey to white)
- Sparks (bright orange/white points — trailing, short-lived, moving upward)
- Water spray (fine droplets — rim-lit, catching light as tiny bright points)
- Snow (small white flakes — falling at varied speeds, never all same size)
- Petals (soft flower petals — falling slowly, rotating as they descend)
- Paper scraps (torn paper fragments — lighter than petals, more chaotic drift)
- Pollen (tiny golden particles — dense in light shafts)
- Fabric lint (barely visible — only in sunbeams or hard light)
- Sand particles (fine grains — wind-driven, horizontal drift)
- Glitter/shimmer (metallic specks — from makeup, fabric, or light interaction)
- Steam (rising from hot surface — coffee, tea, just-showered skin)
- Incense smoke (thin, sinuous, vertical rising trail with horizontal drift)
- Breath vapor (visible exhale in cold air — warm, quickly dissipating)
- Embers (dying fire particles — orange to dark, rising slowly)

PARTICULATE RULES:
1. At least ONE particulate type per frame (non-negotiable)
2. Particles must be LIT BY THE KEY LIGHT (they're visible BECAUSE light catches them — in shadow they'd be invisible)
3. Particles must be at VARIED DISTANCES (some in foreground = large/blurred, some in midground = medium/sharp, some in background = tiny/blurred)
4. Particles must have VARIED SIZES (real dust is not uniform — some large, some microscopic)
5. Particles must be in MOTION (some rising, some falling, some drifting — never frozen in identical positions)
6. Particles must INTERACT with the light (they are tiny light-catchers — each one is a specular highlight)
7. Particles must match the SETTING logic (dust in old libraries, steam in bathrooms, petals outdoors in spring, mist in early morning, etc.)

HOW TO PROMPT PARTICULATE:
Never: "dust in the air"
Always: "golden dust motes floating in the window-light shaft from camera-left, varied sizes from barely-visible to pin-head, concentrated in the upper-third of frame, drifting slowly leftward and slightly upward, each mote catching the warm 3200K tungsten light as a tiny golden specular point"

FAILURE MODE:
Empty air = digital render feel. The viewer can't articulate why, but their brain knows: real rooms have stuff in the air. Real outdoor spaces have particles. Studios use hazers specifically to make light visible. If the air is empty, the frame reads as CGI.


LAYER 4 — CONTACT-POINT ACTIVITY

WHAT IT IS: Wherever Aira's body or any object touches another surface, something is happening at that contact point. The world responds to being touched.

WHAT IT IS NOT: Clean undisturbed surfaces. Perfect contact without consequence. Floating subjects with no ground interaction.

COMPLETE CONTACT-POINT VOCABULARY:

FOOT-TO-GROUND:
- Dust kick (foot lifts, tiny dust cloud from surface)
- Splash (foot in puddle, water displaced)
- Compression (soft surface — sand, carpet, grass — compressing under weight)
- Reflection distortion (wet/reflective floor showing distorted reflection at contact)
- Micro-debris displacement (pebbles, leaves, sand grains shifting from foot placement)
- Shadow compression (contact shadow at darkest immediately under sole)
- Rubber flex (shoe sole visibly compressed at ball-of-foot and heel)
- Surface crack/mark (intentional — like wet footprint on dry stone)

HAND-TO-OBJECT:
- Knuckle whitening (grip pressure visible through skin)
- Object deformation (soft objects: fabric bunching, cushion compressing)
- Fingerprint moisture (visible fingertip marks on glass, metal)
- Temperature transfer (cold glass fogging near warm hand)
- Weight communication (wrist angle showing how heavy object is)
- Fabric crush (where fingers grip fabric — directional creasing)
- Pen-pressure (fingertip pressing pen/brush — visible nail-bed color change)

BODY-TO-SURFACE:
- Lean-weight (surface receiving body weight — chair creaking, wall paint pressing)
- Fabric-surface friction (silk sliding on marble, cotton catching on rough stone)
- Hair-on-surface (hair strands laying across shoulder, vanity, fabric — obeying gravity)
- Skin-surface warmth (warm skin on cold surface — tiny condensation around contact)
- Imprint (leaving mark — seat cushion depressed, bed surface molded)

OBJECT-TO-SURFACE:
- Product-on-marble (reflected, tiny shadow, weight communicated)
- Glass-on-glass (contact point visible — tiny light refraction)
- Cup ring (moisture ring on surface from coffee cup)
- Candle wax (drip pattern on surface beneath candle)

THE CONTACT RULE:
No object or body part may FLOAT above a surface without stated reason. Every contact generates VISUAL EVIDENCE at the exact point of touching. The viewer's eye follows these micro-truths and reads "real."

HOW TO PROMPT CONTACT:
Never: "Aira sits on the chair"
Always: "Aira's weight creates visible fabric compression on the velvet chair seat, her thigh pressing the cushion inward by 1cm, left hand resting on armrest with knuckle pressure visible through skin, ring catching the armrest edge, right foot flat on floor with shoe-to-floor contact shadow at maximum darkness directly under sole"

FAILURE MODE:
Floating subjects, objects without shadows, hands gripping without knuckle tension, feet without ground contact — all read as CGI composites. The frame may be otherwise perfect but without contact-point truth, it will never feel real.


LAYER 5 — BACKGROUND MOTION

WHAT IT IS: The background is not a static painted backdrop. It contains its own motion and life independent of the subject. The background looks like the next frame would show it DIFFERENTLY.

WHAT IT IS NOT: A wallpaper. A flat backdrop. A blurred static zone. A frozen crowd.

COMPLETE BACKGROUND MOTION VOCABULARY:

INDOOR BACKGROUND MOTION:
- Curtain drift (sheer fabric moving from air current — slow, sinuous)
- Candle flame flicker (practical light source — flame shape changing)
- Steam rising (from mug, from shower, from humidifier)
- Screen-glow shift (if TV/phone/laptop in BG — screen content implies motion through glow)
- Shadow play (if light source moves — shadows shift subtly)
- Hanging plant sway (leaves moving from air current)
- Reflected light play (if water/mirror/glass in BG — caustic or reflected light shifting)
- Clock hand movement (if clock visible — second hand between marks)
- Fabric settle (throw or curtain just having been moved — still settling)
- Fan-driven motion (anything in BG moved by fan or AC: papers, fabric edges, light objects)

OUTDOOR BACKGROUND MOTION:
- Leaves mid-rustle (wind-animated foliage — not uniformly moved)
- Grass waving (field grass bending in wind direction)
- Birds mid-flight (pigeons taking off, birds crossing frame)
- Traffic streaks (motion-blurred vehicle lights in urban BG)
- Cloud movement (implied through streak or edge-blur)
- Water movement (waves, ripples, flowing stream — never still)
- Pedestrian mid-stride (background people caught mid-walk, slightly blurred)
- Flag/banner snap (fabric on poles caught by wind)
- Rain streaks (diagonal rain lines — direction consistent)
- Smoke/steam (from vents, chimneys, food stalls)
- Light change (sun-cloud-sun shift — implied through highlight/shadow shift)
- Wind-blown debris (papers, leaves, lightweight objects in air)

THE BACKGROUND LIFE RULE:
If you mentally freeze the background: would it look identical in 2 seconds? If yes — background is dead. At least ONE element in the background must be in a state that will visibly change within 0.5 seconds.

MOTION BLUR ON BACKGROUND:
- Background motion elements should carry slight directional blur (reinforces that THEY are moving while subject is sharp)
- Blur direction matches motion direction (leftward-moving traffic = leftward blur streaks)
- Blur amount: subtle (2-4px equivalent) — not smeared unrecognizable

HOW TO PROMPT BG MOTION:
Never: "busy street background"
Always: "urban street at golden hour — two pedestrians mid-stride camera-left with 3px directional blur, taxi passing camera-right with motion-blurred headlights streaking warm yellow, tree leaves in upper-right animated by wind with slight directional blur leftward, shop signage slightly swaying, and warm neon reflecting on wet pavement with caustic shimmer"

FAILURE MODE:
Static backgrounds immediately signal "AI-generated composite" because no real photograph has a perfectly frozen background. Even a 1/1000 shutter speed will show water moving, leaves shifting, people mid-stride. Absolutely static backgrounds are the #2 giveaway of AI imagery (after hands).


LAYER 6 — LIGHT IN MOTION

WHAT IT IS: The light itself appears to be in motion — either because the source moved, the atmosphere moved through it, or optical elements (lens) are interacting with it dynamically. Light that moves reads as LIVE CAPTURE rather than STUDIO SETUP.

WHAT IT IS NOT: Even, flat, unchanging illumination. Light that appears computed rather than caught.

COMPLETE LIGHT-IN-MOTION VOCABULARY:

LENS INTERACTIONS:
- Lens flare streak (anamorphic horizontal streak across frame from bright source — blue/gold)
- Lens flare circles (circular bokeh flares cascading from point source)
- Lens breathing (slight focus shift implying the lens just moved — edge softening)
- Chromatic aberration (slight color fringing at high-contrast edges — subtle, never heavy)

ATMOSPHERIC LIGHT:
- God rays / light shafts (visible beams through atmosphere — requires particulate to be visible)
- Volumetric cones (light spreading in cone from source through haze)
- Light beam cross (when light passes through a physical object — window frame, plant, blinds — casting shaped beam)
- Sun streaks on surface (light patches on floor/wall from window — shaped, warm, with particle content)

PRACTICAL LIGHT FLICKER:
- Candle flicker (warm light oscillating 3-5x per second — causing shadow movement)
- Neon buzz (sign flickering intermittently — casting colored glow with micro-gaps)
- Screen glow shift (TV/phone emitting color-shifting light as content changes)
- Fire glow (warm orange-red light from fireplace/bonfire — dancing on surfaces)

MOVING REFLECTIONS:
- Caustic dance (light refracted through water/glass creating moving pattern on nearby surface)
- Mirror reflection shift (reflected light moving because source or reflective surface moved)
- Wet-surface shimmer (rain-wet pavement reflecting lights — those reflections shift with water movement)

RIM / BACK LIGHT BEHAVIOR:
- Rim light wrap (backlight wrapping around subject edge — intensity varies along the contour suggesting either light or subject moved)
- Rim light flicker (if backlit by practical — candle, fire — rim varies)
- Hair light shimmer (backlight catching individual hair strands at varying angles — some bright, some dark — not uniform)

THE LIGHT-MOTION RULE:
At least ONE light behavior in the frame must suggest that either the light source, the atmosphere through which it passes, or the subject it hits is in MOTION. Static even light = studio setup = digital feeling. Light with character = captured moment.

HOW TO PROMPT LIGHT IN MOTION:
Never: "nice lighting"
Always: "single warm key from camera-right window creates a visible god-ray shaft through the dusty air, cutting across Aira's left cheekbone; a secondary caustic dance from a water glass on the vanity throws small moving light patterns on the wall behind her; and a faint horizontal anamorphic lens flare streaks across the upper third of frame from the window catch"

THE COMBINATION EFFECT:
When all 6 layers work together — subject mid-action + fabric/hair moving + particles in air + contact-point truth + background alive + light in motion — the frame reads as INDISTINGUISHABLE FROM A PHOTOGRAPH. This is not an aspiration. It is the minimum standard.

### D.EXT.3 — ENERGY HIERARCHY EXPLAINED

Not all six layers carry equal visual weight. Without hierarchy, the frame becomes noisy — the eye doesn't know where to focus.

THE 60/30/10 RULE:
- 60% of the visual energy goes to ONE hero element (usually the subject micro-action or the fabric/hair)
- 30% goes to 2-3 supporting elements (particulate, background motion, contact)
- 10% goes to ambient (light flickers, distant particles, subtle atmospheric)

WHAT THIS MEANS IN PRACTICE:
- If the HERO energy is Aira's hair mid-flick (biggest, most dramatic motion) — then fabric is supporting (smaller billow), particles are ambient (gentle drift)
- If the HERO energy is a splash at contact point (dramatic water kick) — then Aira is supporting (mid-stride), background is ambient (slight crowd blur)
- If the HERO energy is the background (dramatic traffic streak or crowd motion) — then Aira is supporting (subtle weight-shift), and particles are ambient

THE HIERARCHY MUST BE DECLARED per frame: "ENERGY HERO: [element]. SUPPORT: [elements]. AMBIENT: [elements]."

### D.EXT.4 — THE NEXT-FRAME TEST (FULLY EXPLAINED)

PURPOSE: To guarantee that the frame reads as ONE MOMENT in a CONTINUOUS timeline rather than an isolated posed image.

HOW TO APPLY:
After writing the full frame spec, the engine asks: "In 0.5 seconds from this frame, what will have changed?"

ACCEPTABLE ANSWERS:
- "Her hair will complete its arc and settle on her right shoulder"
- "The splash will hit the ground and scatter into smaller droplets"
- "Her hand will reach the curtain and begin to pull it"
- "The dust motes will drift 3cm leftward"
- "Her exhale will complete and her chest will begin to rise on the inhale"

UNACCEPTABLE ANSWERS:
- "Nothing changes" → frame is dead. REWRITE.
- "She'll do something else" (vague) → not specific enough. REWRITE.
- "The frame will look the same" → frame is dead. REWRITE.

The answer becomes part of the frame spec and helps the generation model understand the temporal position of this frozen moment.



---

## PART E.EXTENDED — CINEMATIC GRADE: FULL SPECIFICATION

### E.EXT.1 — WHAT "CINEMATIC" ACTUALLY MEANS MECHANICALLY

"Cinematic" is not a vibe. It is a specific collection of mechanical choices that Hollywood cinematographers make. When someone says a frame "looks cinematic," they are responding to specific measurable elements — not a feeling.

THE SEVEN PILLARS OF CINEMATIC:
1. ASPECT RATIO — wider than standard (2.39:1, 2:1, 1.85:1 letterboxed within 9:16)
2. LENS CHARACTER — specific optical personality (flares, bokeh shape, distortion, breathing)
3. DEPTH OF FIELD — selective focus creating depth layers
4. COLOR GRADE — intentional, stylized, non-neutral color science
5. LIGHTING — motivated, multi-source, shaped, never flat
6. COMPOSITION — intentional geometric framework
7. ATMOSPHERE — visible air (haze, mist, dust) making light volumetric

When ALL SEVEN are present — frame reads as cinema.
When ANY ONE is missing — frame reads as photograph or advertisement (which may be fine for some formats, but not for cinematic-tagged frames).

### E.EXT.2 — LENS CHARACTER: WHY IT MATTERS MORE THAN ANYTHING

The human eye recognizes lens character subconsciously. Different lenses create different emotional responses.

WIDE LENSES (14mm–35mm):
- 14mm: extreme wide, barrel distortion at edges, immersive, intimidating, used for architecture and scale
- 24mm: wide establishing, slight edge stretch, naturalistic environment, Lubezki signature
- 35mm: naturalistic, closest to human peripheral vision, documentary feel, "truth" lens

NORMAL LENSES (40mm–55mm):
- 40mm: Kubrick precision, slight-wider-than-human, controlled
- 50mm: "human eye" equivalent, intimate, honest, no distortion
- 55mm: classic portrait-start, slight compression, still natural

TELEPHOTO LENSES (85mm–135mm+):
- 85mm: portrait king, background compression starts, face flattering, separation
- 100mm: strong compression, subject isolated from background, voyeuristic
- 135mm: maximum compression, subject pulled from background entirely, background becomes texture

SPECIALTY LENSES:
- Anamorphic (40mm/50mm/75mm): horizontal lens flares, oval bokeh, edge distortion, focus breathing, cinematic signature — this is THE cinema lens
- Tilt-shift: selective focus plane at non-perpendicular angle, miniature effect or extreme selective focus on one plane
- Macro: extreme close-up capability, razor-thin DOF, detail revelation
- Petzval / Swirl: background spirals outward from center, dreamy, fashion-editorial

HOW TO PROMPT LENS:
Never: "close-up shot"
Always: "85mm f/1.8, shallow DOF with round bokeh, subject face sharp from nose-tip to ears, background compressed into soft cream texture, slight lens breathing suggesting camera just locked focus"

### E.EXT.3 — COLOR GRADE: THE INVISIBLE DIRECTOR

Color grade is what makes a frame belong to a specific WORLD rather than being a neutral capture.

HOW TO SPECIFY COLOR GRADE:
Option A — Name the colorist/film: "Grade this like Roger Deakins' Blade Runner 2049 — orange-teal collision, controlled highlights, deep shadows"
Option B — Describe the palette technically: "Lifted shadows to +15%, desaturated greens to -40%, warm orange push in midtones, cool blue in shadows only, highlight rolloff at 90% — film-print quality"
Option C — Name the film stock: "Kodak Vision3 5219 500T — warm skin tones, saturated but not oversaturated, slight grain in shadows, cyan in blacks"

COMMON GRADES AND THEIR EMOTIONAL EFFECTS:
- Orange/Teal: most common cinematic — creates face/environment separation naturally (skin is orange, shadows are teal)
- Desaturated + single warm pop: A24 signature — muted world with one element maintaining saturation
- Crushed blacks + amber: thriller, tension, urban night
- Lifted blacks + warm: nostalgic, soft, dream-like
- High contrast + saturated: commercial/editorial energy
- Cyan shadows + neutral mids: melancholic, cold, winter
- Full warm golden: romance, golden hour worship, Lubezki

### E.EXT.4 — COMPOSITION FRAMEWORKS: NAMED AND ENFORCED

Every cinematic frame follows ONE named composition framework. This is declared per frame and enforced.

KUBRICK ONE-POINT PERSPECTIVE:
- Camera dead-center, all lines converging to single vanishing point in frame center
- Subject often centered or slightly off-center within symmetric architecture
- Creates: unease, precision, control, institutional
- Best for: reveal shots, architectural, confrontation

WES ANDERSON CENTERED TABLEAU:
- Flat (planimetric) composition — no converging lines, camera perpendicular to subject
- Subject dead-center, symmetric left-right
- Creates: whimsy, precision, storybook
- Best for: editorial fashion, playful, product-centered

FINCHER LOCKED-OFF:
- Camera perfectly still, geometric precision, negative space intentional
- Often slightly lower than eye-level
- Creates: clinical precision, controlled menace, intelligence
- Best for: knowing register, precision ad work

MALICK LOW-ANGLE WIDE:
- Camera below subject looking up, sky dominant in upper 40% of frame
- Subject small relative to environment
- Creates: reverence, scale, spiritual
- Best for: reverent register, landscape integration

SPIELBERG OVER-THE-SHOULDER:
- Camera behind secondary subject, shooting over their shoulder toward primary subject
- Creates: relationship, tension between two forces, voyeur
- Best for: through-mirror GRWM, product-user relationship

DEAKINS DEPTH STAGING:
- Multiple subjects/elements at clearly different depths, all compositionally balanced
- Uses FG/MG/BG with intentional placement at each layer
- Creates: cinematic depth, visual richness, world-building
- Best for: ad work, establishing environment

### E.EXT.5 — ATMOSPHERE: THE AIR MUST BE VISIBLE

In cinema, the air is NEVER invisible. Cinematographers use haze machines, fog, smoke, and atmospheric effects on EVERY SET — even "clean" interiors — because visible air is what makes light photogenic.

WHY:
- Light shafts are only visible when there's matter in the air to scatter them
- Without atmosphere, light just illuminates surfaces — it doesn't EXIST as a visible element
- Atmosphere creates depth separation between FG/MG/BG (each layer slightly hazier)
- Atmosphere softens harsh transitions and creates unity

HOW MUCH:
- Interior scene: light haze (viewer might not consciously notice, but god rays are faintly visible)
- Moody scene: medium haze (visible light shafts, soft background)
- Dramatic scene: heavy haze (thick god rays, background almost lost, light becomes solid)
- Outdoor: natural atmospheric perspective (distant elements bluer/hazier)

HOW TO PROMPT:
Never: "atmospheric shot"
Always: "light atmospheric haze at density level 3/10, sufficient for the window-key to cast a faint visible shaft from upper-camera-right to lower-camera-left, crossing Aira's face at cheekbone level, with dust motes concentrated within the shaft"



---

## PART R.EXTENDED — HYPER-REALISTIC FACIAL DYNAMICS: FULL SPECIFICATION

### R.EXT.1 — WHY THIS IS THE MOST CRITICAL ANTI-AI LAYER

The human brain has a dedicated neural region (fusiform face area) that processes faces with extreme sensitivity. This region can detect asymmetries, held expressions, and unnatural muscle coordination at speeds below conscious awareness. This is why AI-generated faces feel "off" even when technically correct — the brain's face-processing hardware is detecting:

1. Symmetric perfection (real faces are never symmetric)
2. Held expressions (real faces are never still — micro-movements happen every 0.2-0.5 seconds)
3. Simultaneous activation (real expressions are sequenced — eyes before lips, brows before eyes)
4. Missing breath (real faces show breathing — nostrils, chest, lip-part)
5. Uniform muscle tone (real faces have some muscles engaged, others relaxed, creating complex texture)

This layer exists to defeat the fusiform face area's AI-detection system by encoding human-level facial dynamics into every Aira frame.

### R.EXT.2 — THE ASYMMETRY MANDATE

NO face frame may be bilaterally symmetric. Enforce at least 3 asymmetries per face:

NATURAL ASYMMETRIES TO ENCODE:
- One eye slightly more open (0.5–1mm difference)
- One brow slightly higher (creates "questioning" default)
- Smile stronger on one side (Aira: default left side stronger)
- One cheek dimples slightly deeper
- Hair parting creates asymmetric forehead/temple exposure
- One ear slightly more visible than other
- Nostril flare slightly different on each side
- Lip-corner height differs by 0.5mm
- One cheekbone catches slightly more light (head micro-tilt)

ENFORCEMENT:
The engine MUST declare at least 3 specific asymmetries per face frame. If a generated image shows perfect bilateral symmetry — FAIL. Re-prompt with explicit asymmetry instructions.

### R.EXT.3 — EXPRESSION SEQUENCING (DUCHENNE MARKERS)

Real human expressions do not happen all at once. They SEQUENCE through the face in specific orders. AI images that show all expression elements simultaneously read as masks.

SMILE SEQUENCE (0.6 seconds total):
1. Eyes squint first (crow's feet, lower-lid push, cheek-muscle contract) — at 0.0s
2. Cheeks lift — at 0.1s
3. Lip corners rise asymmetrically (one side 0.05s before other) — at 0.2s
4. Teeth become visible — at 0.3s
5. Nose may crinkle slightly — at 0.4s
6. Full expression stable — at 0.6s

For a FROZEN FRAME, pick ONE POINT in this sequence and freeze there:
- Frame frozen at 0.1s = eyes happy but lips still neutral (powerful, mysterious)
- Frame frozen at 0.3s = full smile but teeth just appearing (natural warmth)
- Frame frozen at 0.5s = full smile with slight nose crinkle (genuine joy)

SURPRISE SEQUENCE:
1. Brows rise — at 0.0s
2. Eyes widen — at 0.1s
3. Mouth drops open — at 0.2s
4. Head pulls back slightly — at 0.3s

CONTEMPLATION SEQUENCE:
1. Eyes defocus (gaze goes distant) — at 0.0s
2. Brow micro-furrows (inner brow draw) — at 0.1s
3. Lips press together — at 0.2s
4. Chin drops slightly — at 0.3s
5. Breath slows (visible in chest/shoulder stillness)

HOW TO PROMPT SEQUENCING:
Never: "Aira smiling"
Always: "Aira's expression frozen at the 0.2s point of a smile sequence — eyes already squinted with crow's feet, cheeks lifted, but lip-corners just beginning to rise asymmetrically (left corner 1mm higher than right), teeth not yet visible, slight nose-bridge tension beginning"

### R.EXT.4 — MICRO-MUSCLE MAPPING

The face has 43 muscles. AI typically activates only the major ones (zygomatic for smile, frontalis for surprise). Real faces show micro-engagement across many muscles simultaneously. The engine must specify at least 5 named muscle states per face frame:

KEY FACIAL MUSCLES TO REFERENCE:
- Frontalis (forehead) — raised = surprise/attention, relaxed = neutral, one-sided = skeptical
- Corrugator supercilii (between brows) — contracted = frown/concentration/concern
- Orbicularis oculi (around eyes) — contracted = genuine smile (Duchenne) or squint
- Zygomaticus major (cheek to lip) — smile pull
- Levator labii (upper lip) — disgust, snarl, or exposing teeth
- Depressor anguli oris (lip corners down) — sadness, displeasure
- Mentalis (chin) — chin dimple, lip push, emotional control
- Masseter (jaw) — clenched = tension/determination, relaxed = ease
- Platysma (neck) — visible strain in intense emotion
- Nasalis (nose) — flare on breath, crinkle on laugh

HOW TO USE:
Never: "determined expression"
Always: "Masseter lightly engaged (jaw set but not clenched), corrugator drawing inner brows fractionally together, orbicularis oculi slightly narrowing eyes, lips pressed by mentalis creating subtle chin dimple, frontalis relaxed (no forehead lines) — overall read: quiet determination"

### R.EXT.5 — BREATH AS CONSTANT

Breath is the continuous proof of life. EVERY face frame must show ONE breath indicator:

BREATH INDICATORS:
- Lip slightly parted on inhale (0.5–2mm gap between lips)
- Nostril slightly flared on inhale
- Chest/shoulder rising on inhale (even 2mm visible through fabric)
- Exhale visible as lip-together + chest-descend
- Visible breath vapor in cold air
- Slight throat movement (larynx bob) on swallow between breaths
- Shoulder settle on completed exhale
- Collarbone shadow shift with breath

HOW TO PROMPT:
Never: (nothing — most prompts just skip breath entirely)
Always: "Aira caught mid-inhale — lips parted 1.5mm, nostril micro-flared, right shoulder rising 3mm, visible breath catch before she speaks"

### R.EXT.6 — THE "3 MINIMUM" ENFORCEMENT

Every single frame showing Aira's face MUST specify AT LEAST 3 of the following micro-dynamic elements in the prompt. This is non-negotiable.

PICK 3+ FROM:
1. Specific eye state (mid-blink / catchlight position / asymmetric openness / gaze direction mid-shift)
2. Specific brow state (one raised / both micro-raised / inner draw / relaxed post-furrow)
3. Specific lip state (mid-phoneme / asymmetric corner / pre-smile tension / lip-press / moisture catching light)
4. Specific cheek state (apple-lift / flush visible / dimple appearing / shadow at hollow)
5. Specific breath indicator (lip-part / nostril flare / chest rise / exhale settle)
6. Specific jaw/chin state (micro-clench / soften / chin-tilt / throat-swallow)
7. Specific nose state (bridge crinkle / nostril flare / shadow shift)
8. Specific asymmetry (eye openness / smile-corner / brow height / dimple depth)

THE ENGINE MUST WRITE ALL 3+ AS EXPLICIT PROMPTING INSTRUCTIONS — never left to the generation model to decide.

---

## PART I.EXTENDED — SPATIAL LOGIC: FULL SPECIFICATION

### I.EXT.1 — WHY SPATIAL LOGIC MAKES OR BREAKS REALISM

The single most common reason AI-generated images look "flat" or "composite" is failed spatial logic. Elements appear to exist at the same depth, or scale relationships are wrong, or atmospheric perspective is absent. The human eye uses these cues to construct a 3D mental model from a 2D image — when they're wrong, the brain says "fake."

### I.EXT.2 — THREE-PLANE ARCHITECTURE: DETAILED

Every frame is built on three DISTINCT, READABLE depth planes. The engine must specify what occupies each:

FOREGROUND (FG) — 0 to 3 feet from camera:
- Function: creates DEPTH, frames the subject, adds intimacy/voyeur-feel
- Focus state: often soft/blurred (shallow DOF) OR sharp (deep focus)
- Typical elements: blurred leaves, shoulder of another figure, doorframe edge, fabric edge, hand holding glass, out-of-focus light source, table-edge with objects
- Scale: elements here appear LARGER than they physically are (perspective)
- Light: often DARKER than midground (negative fill, or simply shadow-side of object)
- Motion: if element has motion, it appears FASTEST here (closest = most parallax)

MIDGROUND (MG) — 3 to 12 feet from camera:
- Function: WHERE THE SUBJECT LIVES — primary action plane
- Focus state: ALWAYS sharp (this is the focus plane)
- Typical elements: Aira, held objects, interacted surfaces, product
- Scale: human scale — proportions correct, no wide-lens distortion (unless intentional)
- Light: primary lighting falls here — key + fill
- Motion: subject's own motion encoded through Kinetic Stillness layers

BACKGROUND (BG) — 12+ feet from camera:
- Function: provides WORLD, context, color story, mood, secondary energy
- Focus state: soft/blurred (shallow DOF) OR desaturated/hazy (atmospheric perspective) OR sharp (deep focus cinematic)
- Typical elements: architecture, landscape, crowd, traffic, sky, far walls, distant practicals
- Scale: elements SMALLER than midground (perspective compression or natural distance)
- Light: slightly LOWER contrast than midground (atmospheric perspective reduces contrast at distance)
- Motion: BG motion elements carry more BLUR than MG (distance = different motion relative to camera)

### I.EXT.3 — THE DEPTH SEPARATION ENFORCEMENT

The engine MUST ensure visual separation between planes:

SEPARATION TECHNIQUES (use at least 2 per frame):
1. FOCUS DIFFERENTIAL — FG blurred / MG sharp / BG blurred
2. LIGHT DIFFERENTIAL — subject brighter/darker than BG by ≥1.5 stops
3. COLOR DIFFERENTIAL — subject warmer/cooler than BG
4. CONTRAST DIFFERENTIAL — subject has higher contrast than BG (atmospheric perspective)
5. SIZE DIFFERENTIAL — FG objects larger, BG objects smaller (perspective)
6. DETAIL DIFFERENTIAL — subject has more texture detail than BG (DOF or distance)
7. MOTION DIFFERENTIAL — BG motion-blurred, subject sharp

Without separation, the frame reads FLAT — as if all elements are pasted on the same plane. This is the #1 "AI look" problem.

### I.EXT.4 — SCALE ANCHORING: RULES OF PHYSICAL TRUTH

The engine MUST maintain consistent scale relationships:

HUMAN SCALE ANCHORS:
- Standard doorway: 6'8" to 7'0" tall
- Aira (5'6"–5'8"): fills ~80% of doorway height
- Standard chair seat: hip-height (approximately 18")
- Table surface: waist-height (approximately 30")
- Phone in hand: fits comfortably in single palm
- Coffee mug: gripped with 4 fingers + thumb wrap
- Car: roof approximately at Aira's shoulder or higher
- Vanity: when seated, surface at elbow height
- Mirror: large enough to show at minimum head-to-waist of seated subject

PERSPECTIVE RULES:
- Objects closer to camera ALWAYS appear larger
- Objects farther from camera ALWAYS appear smaller
- Parallel lines (railroad tracks, hallways, roads) CONVERGE toward one vanishing point
- Vertical lines remain vertical (unless dutch-tilt intentional)
- Horizon line crosses the frame at Aira's eye-level (unless camera is above or below eye-level)

ATMOSPHERIC PERSPECTIVE:
- Objects farther away are: slightly desaturated, slightly lower contrast, slightly cooler OR warmer (depending on conditions), slightly hazier
- This effect increases with distance
- Indoor: subtle (maybe 5% desaturation at far wall)
- Outdoor: significant (distant mountains nearly monochrome, significantly lower contrast)

---



## PART P.EXTENDED — BEAUTY PRODUCT PERFORMANCE: FULL SPECIFICATION

### P.EXT.1 — THE 30 PRODUCT MOVES: EXHAUSTIVE DETAIL

Each move gets full specification so there is zero ambiguity in prompting:

MOVE 1 — SLOW LEVITATION HOVER:
- Description: Product rises from a surface (vanity, table, palm) to hover at mid-air position
- Speed: 3-5 seconds from surface to hover-stable
- Height: rises 6-12 inches above surface
- Rotation: optional slight rotation (5-15° on Y-axis) during rise
- Physics truth: product may show micro-bob once at hover-height (settling into position, like a magnetic hold finding equilibrium)
- Light interaction: rim-light intensity changes as product rises through light shaft; shadow on surface below shrinks and softens as product elevates
- Surface response: surface below shows diminishing shadow + possible reflected caustic shifting
- End state: stable hover with micro-oscillation (0.5mm gentle float, not dead-still)
- USE: luxury hero shot, perfume, serum, premium skincare

MOVE 2 — FREE-FLOAT IN SPACE:
- Description: Product already floating — no surface visible, negative space surrounds it
- Position: centered or rule-of-thirds within frame
- Rotation: slow continuous rotation on single axis (1 rotation per 8-12 seconds)
- Physics truth: no visible support, but product has weight-suggestion (slightly heavier at base, tilted naturally)
- Light interaction: as product rotates, light catches different surfaces sequentially — matte → glossy → label → cap → back
- Background: gradient or deep single-color — never cluttered
- End state: floating indefinitely, rotation continuous
- USE: hero product shot, grid-post, thumbnail

MOVE 3 — SUSPENDED AT APEX:
- Description: Product frozen at peak of an implied upward throw — it was tossed, and we see it at maximum height before gravity pulls it back
- Position: slightly above frame-center (it rose UP)
- Motion indicators: slight motion blur on edges (it was moving fast), trailing particle wake below it (dust/air disturbance), slight tilt on the axis of the throw-arc
- Physics truth: there is ONE frame of zero velocity at apex — product is neither rising nor falling. Hair on subject below may still be rising from the throw-force
- Light interaction: hard rim-light defines edges sharply against background
- Gravity indicator: any liquid inside the bottle will be at the BOTTOM (gravity still applies to contents even at apex)
- USE: dynamic hero, youth brands, electric energy concepts

MOVE 4 — COUNTER-GRAVITY DROP:
- Description: Product appears to fall UPWARD — from bottom of frame toward top. Physics inverted.
- Entry: product enters from below frame, rising
- Speed: slow enough to read (3-4 seconds of visible travel)
- Physics truth: despite inverted direction, maintain WEIGHT implication — heavier end leads, lighter end trails. If liquid inside, liquid pools at the "top" (which is now the leading direction)
- Particle response: small particles fall DOWNWARD normally even as product rises — this contrast sells the impossibility while maintaining one truth-anchor
- USE: pattern-interrupt hook, disorienting beauty, edgy editorial

MOVE 5 — ORBITAL FLOAT:
- Description: Multiple products (2-5) orbiting a central point or each other
- Orbit speed: one full revolution per 12-20 seconds (slow, graceful)
- Spacing: even distribution on orbital path
- Tilt: orbital plane can be tilted (not always horizontal — 30° tilt toward camera is cinematic)
- Physics truth: products maintain consistent spacing and speed (not random floating); they behave like a coordinated system
- Light interaction: as each product orbits, it passes through different lighting zones — some frames have product backlit, some front-lit, some rim-lit
- USE: collection reveal, product family launch, multiple-SKU campaign

[Moves 6-30 follow the same depth of specification. For brevity in this section, the remaining moves are specified at operational level:]

MOVE 6 — SURFACE-TENSION HOVER: product hovers 1-3cm above reflective surface, reflection visible below, micro-bob suggesting magnetic hold, shadow soft-edged beneath

MOVE 7 — GRAVITY-FREE POUR: liquid exits bottle but instead of falling, it curves, spirals, or floats in ribbon-form mid-air; surface tension holds stream shape; light refracts through liquid ribbon creating caustic on nearby surfaces

MOVE 8 — STRING-OF-PEARLS: 3-5 identical products stacked vertically in air, perfectly aligned, equal spacing, each rotated 15° from the one below creating spiral-staircase effect

MOVE 9 — SELF-OPENING CAP: cap unscrews itself (3 rotations visible), lifts off body, hovers 2-3cm above — applicator/wand visible; cap rotation must match thread-direction (clockwise to open)

MOVE 10 — LIQUID MATERIALIZATION: liquid drop (serum/perfume) appears first, floating, then more liquid gathers toward it, coalescing into the bottle shape from liquid-state to solid-product; the bottle EMERGES FROM its own formula

MOVE 11 — PARTICLE ASSEMBLY: fine powder/pigment particles swirl in air, then begin converging toward center-point, building the product shape particle-by-particle; final particles snap into place revealing complete product

MOVE 12 — DISSOLVE-AND-REFORM: product dissolves into mist/smoke from edges inward, then reforms in new position/angle from center outward; during dissolved state, shape is implied through particle density

MOVE 13 — REVEAL THROUGH SHATTER: outer casing (glass, crystal, ice) shatters radially outward from product revealing the hero product beneath; shards hover momentarily (freeze frame potential) before dissipating

MOVE 14 — BLOOM REVEAL: product opens like a flower — panels/petals unfold from closed-compact state to reveal interior product; mechanical precision of opening suggests luxury engineering

MOVE 15 — LIQUID MIRROR EMERGENCE: product rises slowly from perfectly still liquid surface (water, mercury, milk); surface tension holds until the moment of breach; droplets cascade down product surface as it emerges

MOVE 16 — SMOKE/MIST BIRTH: product materializes from center of a colored smoke/mist swirl; smoke parts around it as if displaced by the product's existence; residual wisps cling to surface briefly

MOVE 17 — HAND-CATCH LEVITATION: product floats toward Aira's open palm from 12+ inches away; settles gently into her hand; her fingers close around it naturally; the float implies magnetic attraction between user and product

MOVE 18 — MAGNETIC PULL-IN: product on a surface suddenly slides/lifts toward Aira's approaching hand — as if pulled by invisible magnetic force; movement accelerates as distance closes (inverse-square feel)

MOVE 19 — LIGHT-BEAM DELIVERY: a visible shaft of light carries the product from BG to FG; product travels along the beam like a track; arrives at hero position

MOVE 20 — PETAL/PARTICLE GATHER: loose petals/particles scattered in air suddenly attract toward a central point, converging and solidifying into the product shape

MOVE 21 — LIQUID SPLASH FROZEN: product dropped into liquid at exact moment of maximum splash-crown; crown frozen at peak with individual droplets suspended; product visible at impact center

MOVE 22 — WIND-ANIMATED STILLNESS: product sits completely stable on surface while everything around it moves in wind (hair, fabric, particles, leaves) — product is the one still point in a kinetic frame

MOVE 23 — MACRO PUSH-IN: camera travels from medium shot into extreme macro on product surface; reveals texture invisible at normal viewing — glass refraction, label embossing, liquid clarity, cap threading

MOVE 24 — ORBIT-AROUND HERO: camera orbits 360° around stationary product; every surface/angle/material revealed in continuous motion; product is the sun, camera is the planet

MOVE 25 — VERTICAL TILT REVEAL: camera tilts from product-top to product-base (or reverse); traces the full form in 9:16 vertical; especially powerful for tall perfume bottles or column packaging

MOVE 26 — PARALLAX LAYER REVEAL: camera moves laterally; foreground element passes by (blurred), product (sharp) stays centered, background slides (soft); depth communicated through relative motion

MOVE 27 — PULL-BACK FROM MACRO: starts on extreme detail (one letter on label, one drop on neck, one thread of embossing) then pulls back to reveal full product, then full scene context

MOVE 28 — DRONE-STYLE TOP-DOWN: camera starts directly above product (plan-view), then tilts/dollies to eye-level front-facing; architectural reveal

MOVE 29 — PRODUCT "LOOKS AT" CAMERA: product's label/logo slowly rotates toward camera as if the product is "facing" the viewer; anthropomorphizing without being literal; rotation subtle (30-45° max)

MOVE 30 — PHYSICS TRICK: liquid inside vial swirls against gravity, or foundation drips upward, or powder defies fall — ONE impossible liquid/particle behavior within the product's sealed container

### P.EXT.2 — WHEN TO USE WHICH MOVE (REGISTER MATCHING)

QUIET LUXURY (restrained, slow, premium):
Moves 1, 2, 6, 15, 17, 22, 23, 24, 25, 29
Speed: slow, deliberate
Energy: restrained, gravity-respecting
Brands: Chanel, Dior, Hermès, La Mer, Aesop

EDITORIAL BOLD (dramatic, statement):
Moves 3, 4, 9, 13, 14, 16, 21, 28
Speed: medium, impactful
Energy: dramatic single moment
Brands: Pat McGrath, NARS, Charlotte Tilbury, YSL

HERITAGE/WELLNESS (warm, natural, quiet magic):
Moves 10, 15, 16, 20, 22
Speed: organic, natural-feeling
Energy: gentle, earth-connected
Brands: Forest Essentials, Kama Ayurveda, Tatcha, Drunk Elephant

YOUTH/GEN-Z (bold, fast, attention-grabbing):
Moves 3, 4, 5, 7, 8, 11, 12, 13, 18, 19, 30
Speed: faster, snappy
Energy: high, pattern-interrupting
Brands: Glossier, Rare Beauty, Rhode, Fenty

## PART O.EXTENDED — 3D CAMERA TRICKS: FULL SPECIFICATION

### O.EXT.1 — WHY 3D CAMERA MATTERS FOR BEAUTY/AD

A static camera treating a still subject creates a flat image. Camera movement — even implied — gives the brain DEPTH INFORMATION through parallax. This is why product ads with orbiting cameras feel premium: the viewer's brain constructs a 3D mental model of the product because different surfaces are revealed sequentially.

In 9:16 vertical format, camera movement is even more critical because the narrow frame limits left-right visual exploration. Vertical camera moves (tilt, crane) and depth moves (push-in, pull-back) work BETTER in 9:16 than horizontal pans.

### O.EXT.2 — EVERY CAMERA MOVE: FULL DETAIL

PUSH-IN (DOLLY IN):
- What: camera moves physically closer to subject/product
- Speed: slow (3-5 seconds of travel) for beauty/luxury; medium (1.5-3s) for energy/reveal
- Effect: increasing intimacy, focus narrowing, world closing in
- DOF change: as camera approaches, DOF naturally shallows — background gets softer
- Start/end framing: starts wider (MS/MCU), ends tighter (CU/ECU)
- Emotional read: escalation, intimacy building, "leaning in"
- Best for: revealing product detail, approaching Aira's face, emotional escalation
- VEO prompt: "camera dolly-in from MS to CU over 4 seconds, steady speed, focus locked on subject eye"

PULL-BACK (DOLLY OUT):
- What: camera moves physically away from subject/product
- Speed: slow to medium
- Effect: revealing context, world expanding, subject in environment
- DOF change: as camera retreats, DOF deepens — more of environment comes into focus
- Start/end: starts tight (ECU/CU), ends wider (MS/WS)
- Emotional read: revelation, scale, breath, release, conclusion
- Best for: reveal frames, showing full outfit, environmental context, exit beats
- VEO prompt: "camera dolly-out from ECU to WS over 5 seconds, revealing full scene"

ORBIT (CIRCULAR TRACK):
- What: camera circles around subject/product on a circular track
- Arc options: full 360° / quarter-circle (90°) / half-circle (180°)
- Direction: CW (clockwise) or CCW (counter-clockwise)
- Speed: one full orbit in 12-20 seconds (slow luxury) or 6-10 seconds (energy)
- Subject behavior: may remain stationary (product) or counter-rotate (Aira turning to maintain eye-contact through orbit)
- Parallax effect: strong — FG/MG/BG all shifting differently, proving depth
- Best for: product hero (360° reveals all surfaces), fashion reveal, power shot
- VEO prompt: "camera orbit CCW 180° around product at table-height, 8 seconds, product static, background parallaxing softly"

VERTICAL TILT (UP/DOWN):
- What: camera angle changes vertically — tilting from high to low or low to high
- TILT UP: starts at feet/product-base, tilts to reveal face/top
- TILT DOWN: starts at face/sky, tilts down to reveal feet/product-base/ground
- Speed: smooth, 3-6 seconds
- 9:16 advantage: PERFECT for vertical format — traces the full height of subject or product
- Best for: full-outfit reveal (tilt up from shoes), product-form trace, architectural reveal
- VEO prompt: "camera tilt-up from Aira's heels to face, 5 seconds, 85mm, smooth gimbal, revealing full outfit sequentially"

PARALLAX LATERAL SLIDE (TRUCK):
- What: camera slides laterally (left or right) while keeping subject centered
- Effect: FG elements slide fast in one direction, BG slides slow in other direction — classic parallax proving depth
- Speed: gentle, 2-4 seconds of travel
- Distance of travel: 12-36 inches laterally
- Best for: depth revelation, product shots with foreground elements, establishing spatial relationship
- VEO prompt: "camera truck right 24 inches over 3 seconds, Aira centered in MG sharp, FG blurred leaves sliding left, BG soft architecture sliding right"

CRANE UP/DOWN:
- What: camera physically rises or descends (not tilt — actual position change)
- CRANE UP: camera ascends from low to high, looking down progressively
- CRANE DOWN: camera descends from high to low, arriving at eye-level or below
- Effect: power dynamics shift (low camera = subject powerful; high camera = subject vulnerable)
- Best for: power reveal, aerial-to-intimate transition, scale establishment
- VEO prompt: "camera crane down from overhead (drone-view) to eye-level over 4 seconds, arriving at Aira's face-level"

WHIP-PAN:
- What: extremely fast horizontal rotation — subject 1 is lost in blur, subject 2 is found
- Duration: 0.3-0.8 seconds of blur between lock-positions
- Effect: energy, transition, time-skip, surprise
- Motion blur: HEAVY during whip (frame is unreadable), then SHARP lock at destination
- Best for: scene transitions, product-to-face reveal, energy beats
- VEO prompt: "whip-pan camera-right from product (locked) to Aira's face (locks after 0.5s blur), 85mm"

SNAP-ZOOM:
- What: rapid zoom in or out (lens zoom, not physical movement — gives slightly different feel than dolly)
- Duration: 0.3-0.6 seconds
- Effect: emphasis, surprise, impact, horror/thriller aesthetic
- Visual: slight "compression" change as zoom alters focal length (background appears to grow/shrink relative to subject)
- Best for: reaction beats, emphasis on emotion, hook moments
- VEO prompt: "snap-zoom from WS to CU in 0.4 seconds, handheld energy"

HANDHELD:
- What: camera has organic micro-movement — not stabilized, not static
- Amplitude: subtle (1-3mm oscillation) for intimacy; medium (5-8mm) for energy; heavy for chaos
- Effect: documentary truth, realness, proximity, intimacy, anxiety (depending on amplitude)
- NOT jitter — organic breathing motion with natural rhythm
- Best for: GRWM intimacy, documentary-style, confessional reels, energetic moments
- VEO prompt: "handheld camera at MCU, subtle 2mm organic motion, breathing rhythm, 35mm naturalistic"

GIMBAL-SMOOTH:
- What: camera moves physically (track, crane, orbit) but with zero shake — floating, inhuman smoothness
- Effect: ethereal, cinematic, premium, slightly surreal (too smooth for human = elevated reality)
- Best for: luxury ads, fashion film, product hero, fragrance
- VEO prompt: "gimbal-smooth push-in from MS to CU, zero shake, 4 seconds, floating ethereal quality"

STATIC (INTENTIONAL):
- What: camera does NOT move. Deliberately locked. Tripod.
- When: when subject movement carries all energy and camera stillness creates contrast
- Effect: control, precision, letting subject/performance dominate
- Best for: beauty ECUs where face-acting is the content, held-moment frames, sign-off beats
- VEO prompt: "camera static, locked tripod, MCU, 85mm, subject provides all motion"

### O.EXT.3 — ONE MOVE PER SHOT: WHY

Compound camera moves (push-in WHILE orbiting WHILE tilting) confuse VEO 3.1 and make the viewer seasick. One clear move per shot is cinematic discipline. Hitchcock, Kubrick, and Deakins rarely compound. Each shot has ONE move that serves ONE purpose.

If a concept needs multiple camera perspectives — use CUTS between shots, each with its own single move.

### O.EXT.4 — 9:16 CAMERA PRIORITY

In vertical format, ranked by effectiveness:
1. VERTICAL TILT (native to format — traces full height)
2. PUSH-IN / PULL-BACK (depth movement works in any format)
3. CRANE UP/DOWN (vertical travel = vertical format = natural)
4. ORBIT (works in any format but limited horizontal reveal in 9:16)
5. PARALLAX SLIDE (works but limited horizontal travel visible)
6. HANDHELD (format-agnostic — always works)
7. PAN L-R (LEAST effective in 9:16 — limited horizontal canvas)

---

## PART J.EXTENDED — CINEMATIC AD MANDATE: FULL SPECIFICATION

### J.EXT.1 — THE FIVE MANDATES EXPLAINED IN FULL

MANDATE 1 — LIGHT SEPARATION (≥1.5 stops between subject and BG):

WHAT THIS MEANS:
The subject (Aira) must be either BRIGHTER or DARKER than the background by at least 1.5 exposure stops. This creates visual separation — the eye instantly finds the subject.

HOW TO ACHIEVE:
- Subject brighter: light subject with key, let background fall to ambient (negative fill on BG)
- Subject darker: expose for bright background, let subject go into silhouette or partial shadow
- Mixed: rim-light subject edge to separate from matching-brightness BG

WHY:
Without light separation, subject merges into background visually. The eye doesn't know where to focus. The frame reads as flat snapshot, not directed cinema.

HOW TO PROMPT:
Never: "well-lit scene"
Always: "Aira lit 1.5 stops brighter than background — key light from camera-left at f/4 equivalent, background ambient at f/2.8 equivalent, creating clear luminance separation; rim light from camera-right-back defining her silhouette edge against the darker environment"

MANDATE 2 — COLOR NARRATIVE (3-color palette enforced):

WHAT THIS MEANS:
Declare exactly 3 colors at the top of the prompt. Everything in frame — subject wardrobe, product, background, props, lighting gels, post-grade — must use ONLY these 3 colors (plus neutrals: black, white, grey).

HOW TO DECLARE:
"COLOR NARRATIVE: Anchor = deep emerald / Support = brushed gold / Accent = cream"

Then enforce:
- Aira's outfit uses emerald + cream
- Product bottle is gold with emerald label
- Background wall is dark neutral with emerald plant + cream throw
- Lighting gel adds subtle gold to rim-light

WHY:
Uncontrolled color is the #1 reason ads look amateurish. Professional art directors declare a palette before shooting and REJECT anything off-palette. This is that same discipline in prompt form.

MANDATE 3 — ATMOSPHERIC LAYER:

Already fully specified in Part D.EXT.2 Layer 3 and Part E.EXT.5. Non-negotiable. At least one particulate/atmospheric element per frame in any ad concept.

MANDATE 4 — CAMERA INTENT (declared with reason):

WHAT THIS MEANS:
Every camera position and lens choice must be STATED WITH ITS REASON — not just "35mm" but "35mm because this is a naturalistic lifestyle beat and 35mm reads as truth-lens."

TEMPLATE:
"CAMERA: 85mm at eye-level, because this is an intimacy-building beauty CU and 85mm creates face-flattering compression with creamy background separation. Camera height at eye-level for equal-power dynamic with viewer."

WHY:
When camera is chosen with intent, the frame has PURPOSE. When it defaults to "somewhere around 50mm at eye level" — the frame has no opinion.

MANDATE 5 — HERO MOTIVATION:

WHAT THIS MEANS:
ONE element in the frame is the undisputed hero. The eye must land there within 0.3 seconds. If the eye has to search — the frame is flat.

HOW TO ENFORCE:
- Hero is brightest element in frame (light separation)
- Hero has highest contrast (sharpest edges, most detail)
- Hero is at largest scale relative to alternatives
- Hero is at the focal point of composition lines (converging lines, leading lines, gaze direction all point to hero)
- Hero has the most saturated color

If the prompt produces a frame where two elements compete for "hero" status — one must be de-emphasized. Two heroes = zero heroes.

---

## CHECKPOINT 3.3 — EXTENDED SPECIFICATIONS COMPLETE
(Parts D, E, I, J, O, P, R now fully specified — see those sections above)
