## PART Z — SUBJECT & BACKDROP PERFORMANCE PROTOCOL

### Z.1 — THE PRINCIPLE

A beauty reel has THREE PERFORMERS in every frame:
1. THE PRODUCT (already covered in Part P with 30 named moves)
2. THE SUBJECT — Aira (now fully covered here)
3. THE BACKDROP — the environment itself (now fully covered here)

Each of these three performs in coordination with the others. A frame where only the product performs is incomplete. A frame where the subject is static and the backdrop is dead reads as flat advertising. Every frame must have all three layers actively performing — at one of three energy levels (HERO / SUPPORT / AMBIENT) — so the eye experiences a frame that is alive on every plane.

### Z.2 — THE 30 SUBJECT PERFORMANCE MOVES (AIRA)

These are named, choreographed, beauty-grade behaviors for Aira. Each is specified at the same depth as the 30 product moves.

#### MOVEMENT MOVES (1–10):

MOVE 1 — SLOW-REVEAL TURN
- Aira faces away from camera at start
- Slowly rotates toward camera over 2-4 seconds
- Hair sweeps across her face mid-turn, then settles
- Final position: 3/4 turn or full frontal with eye contact
- Speed: deliberate, never rushed
- USE: hero reveal, fragrance, evening editorial
- Motion vector: rotational — clockwise or counter-clockwise specified

MOVE 2 — HAIR CASCADE
- Aira tilts her head sharply to one side then slowly returns
- Hair on the dropped side falls fully over shoulder to chest
- Hair on the lifted side reveals the neck, ear, jewelry
- The cascade moment captures hair mid-fall (frozen still option) or mid-flow (motion option)
- USE: shampoo, hair-care, beauty hero, jewelry reveal (ear shot)

MOVE 3 — LIGHT-CATCH PROFILE TURN
- Aira faces straight to camera, then turns to perfect profile (90°)
- At the profile moment, key light catches cheekbone, brow ridge, jaw line creating defined sculpted shadow
- Held for 1-2 seconds at profile peak
- USE: skincare, foundation hero, jaw line reveal, beauty editorial

MOVE 4 — DOWN-UP-EYE-CONTACT
- Aira's chin starts dropped, eyes downcast (vulnerable opening)
- Slow rise of chin
- Eyes lift LAST (head tilt completes 0.3 seconds before eye contact lands)
- Lock eye contact with camera
- Single slow blink seals the moment
- USE: beauty hero opener, fragrance, intimate ad, GRWM frame 1

MOVE 5 — HAND-MEET-FACE
- Aira's hand approaches her own face from below frame
- Fingertip makes contact at specific point (cheekbone, jaw, lip, temple)
- Contact creates skin compression visible at touch point
- Hand may continue motion (tracing along face) or hold at contact
- USE: skincare application, beauty hero, contemplation beat

MOVE 6 — WALK-INTO-FRAME
- Aira enters frame from left, right, or behind camera
- 2-4 strides visible
- Settles into hero position centered or rule-of-thirds
- Hair, fabric all in motion from walk, settle as she stops
- USE: full reveal, fashion editorial, hero entrance, ad opener

MOVE 7 — MIRROR APPROACH
- Aira approaches a mirror (visible or implied = camera)
- Pace slows as she nears
- Face becomes more visible as proximity increases
- Final beat: face at near-touch distance to mirror/lens
- USE: GRWM, beauty intimacy, fragrance "looking at oneself" beat

MOVE 8 — SEATED DESCENT
- Aira lowers herself slowly into seated position (chair, bed, floor, vanity stool)
- Knees bend, weight transfers, posture composes once seated
- Outfit settles around her in the seated position
- USE: vanity opener, intimate frame, GRWM transition

MOVE 9 — RISE-FROM-SEATED
- Aira begins seated, rises slowly to standing
- Posture engages, weight transfers, outfit drapes settle
- Final hero beat: standing in full reveal
- USE: GRWM reveal frame, ad transformation moment

MOVE 10 — STILL-AT-WINDOW
- Aira at window in profile or 3/4 turn
- Body completely still (only breath visible)
- Window light defining her silhouette
- All motion comes from light, atmosphere, hair-strand-drift
- USE: contemplative beat, mood piece, reverent register

#### EXPRESSION MOVES (11–18):

MOVE 11 — DUCHENNE BLOOM
- Expression progresses through full Duchenne smile sequence over 0.6 seconds
- Frozen frame captured at specific point (0.1s eyes-only / 0.3s teeth-appearing / 0.5s full bloom)
- One half of face leads (asymmetry preserved)
- USE: joy moment, hero beauty, ad warmth

MOVE 12 — REVEAL-EYE-OPEN
- Aira's eyes start closed (eyelash detail visible)
- Slow opening — eyelashes lift, iris reveals progressively
- Catchlight appears as iris fully exposed
- Pupils adjust dilation visible in 0.3 seconds
- USE: skincare reveal, mascara, eye product hero, beauty wake-up

MOVE 13 — SUSPENDED LAUGH
- Mid-laugh frozen at peak
- Eyes squinted, cheeks fully apple-lifted, teeth visible, mouth open at maximum
- Hair displaced backward from head-tilt
- Genuine micro-asymmetry preserved
- USE: lifestyle joy, casual ad, electric register

MOVE 14 — KNOWING HALF-SMILE
- One lip corner rises, the other stays neutral
- Single brow micro-raises on the smile-side (matched asymmetry)
- Eyes narrow slightly with held intent
- Held for 1-2 seconds — the moment communicates "I know"
- USE: knowing register, mischievous, cultural commentary, confident ad

MOVE 15 — CONTEMPLATIVE-DRIFT
- Eyes defocus — gaze travels off-camera as if remembering or thinking
- Brow softens (corrugator releases)
- Lips part fractionally on slow exhale
- 2-3 seconds of held drift before any other movement
- USE: contemplative register, mood piece, fragrance, evening reels

MOVE 16 — SHARP-EYE-RETURN
- Eyes start looking off-camera (any direction)
- Snap back to camera in under 0.3 seconds
- Brows micro-raise on return (suggesting "caught attention")
- Hold eye contact for 1-2 seconds after return
- USE: electric register, energy beats, hook moments, trend deconstruction

MOVE 17 — SLOW-BLINK-LOCK
- Direct eye contact with camera held
- Single deliberate blink (slower than involuntary — about 0.4s)
- Eyes reopen with intentional gaze re-lock
- Tiny smile may follow
- USE: intimate beauty, GRWM hook, fragrance, reverent register

MOVE 18 — LIP-PRESS-RELEASE
- Lips press together briefly (mentalis engaged, slight chin dimple)
- Held for 0.3-0.5 seconds (gathering thought)
- Lips release with slight separation, glossy lower lip catching light
- Often pairs with single brow raise post-release
- USE: beauty hero, lipstick reveal, contemplative moment

#### INTERACTION MOVES (19–25):

MOVE 19 — PRODUCT-RECEIVE
- Aira's hand opens or extends toward incoming product (often paired with Product Move #17 Hand-Catch Levitation)
- Product lands in palm
- Fingers close gently around it
- Aira looks down at the product as it settles
- USE: product hero, brand-collab moment

MOVE 20 — PRODUCT-PRESENT
- Aira holds product at deliberate framing distance
- Product positioned with label readable to camera
- Aira's other hand may gesture toward it (open palm presentation)
- Eye contact split between product and camera
- USE: product reveal beat, ad mid-section

MOVE 21 — APPLY-WITH-EYES-CLOSED
- Aira closes eyes during product application
- Application proceeds (skincare, perfume, eye product)
- Eyes remain closed during the full application beat
- Eyes open AFTER application complete (often paired with Move 12)
- USE: skincare reverence, fragrance, intimate beauty

MOVE 22 — CAMERA-INTERACTION
- Aira physically engages with camera/lens (any move from Performance Library: tap, sway, lean, cover, push, beckon, fingerprint, whisper, blow)
- 0.4-1.2 second duration
- Returns to non-interaction immediately after
- USE: intimacy beats, transition moments, fourth-wall winks

MOVE 23 — GAZE-FOLLOW-PRODUCT
- Aira's eyes track a moving product (levitating, falling, orbiting)
- Head may follow or stay still while only eyes track
- Tracking ends with eye-contact return to camera OR hand-catch
- USE: paired with product moves where product is in motion

MOVE 24 — TURN-AND-SETTLE
- Aira rotates body 90-180° (away from camera, then back, OR vice versa)
- Hair, fabric all in motion during turn
- Settles into new framing
- Final beat: held composed in new position
- USE: outfit reveal (back of dress / front of dress), GRWM reveal

MOVE 25 — POSE-AND-MOVE
- Aira holds a deliberate pose (hand on hip, arms crossed, leaning)
- Single small movement breaks the held pose (hand drops, head tilts, weight shifts)
- New micro-position becomes the held frame
- USE: fashion editorial, pillar 2/7/9 reels

#### INTIMATE MOVES (26–30):

MOVE 26 — BREATH-VISIBLE
- Aira inhales deeply enough that chest/shoulder rise is visible
- Or exhales with visible cold-air vapor (winter/cold setting)
- Or held breath caught at peak (chest still, lips parted)
- Body language reflects breath state
- USE: reverent, contemplative, intimate moments

MOVE 27 — HAIR-TUCK-BEHIND-EAR
- Aira lifts a strand of hair from beside her face
- Tucks it behind her ear
- Fingertips graze cheek/temple during the motion
- Movement reveals ear, jewelry, or jaw line
- USE: signature feminine beat, GRWM, beauty intimacy

MOVE 28 — JEWELRY-TOUCH
- Aira touches her own jewelry (earring, necklace, ring)
- Often unconscious, contemplative gesture
- Reveals the jewelry detail through the touching motion
- USE: jewelry collab, accessory hero

MOVE 29 — FABRIC-ADJUST
- Aira touches her own clothing — adjusts a strap, smooths a hem, tucks fabric
- Reveals fabric texture, drape, fit
- Often an unconscious gesture mid-thought
- USE: fashion ad, wardrobe reveal, GRWM

MOVE 30 — STILLNESS-WITH-MICRO-LIFE
- Aira appears completely still
- Only micro-movements visible: breath, blink, single hair strand drift, micro-cheek-flush, single eyelash settle
- Held for 2-3 seconds of total apparent stillness
- USE: reverent register, fragrance, mood piece, peak emotional moments

### Z.3 — THE 30 BACKDROP PERFORMANCE MOVES

These are named, choreographed environmental behaviors. The backdrop is a third performer — never wallpaper.

#### LIGHT-DRIVEN BACKDROP MOVES (1–10):

MOVE 1 — GOD-RAY SWEEP
- Visible light shaft enters frame from window/source
- Shaft moves slowly across the space (sun moves OR camera moves OR atmosphere shifts)
- Dust motes within shaft become visible
- Speed: 4-8 seconds for shaft to traverse
- USE: reverent register, hero ad, fragrance, contemplative

MOVE 2 — PRACTICAL FLICKER WASH
- Practical light source (candle, neon, fire, broken bulb) flickers in BG
- Flicker rhythm causes BG light to oscillate
- Subject lighting may pick up subtle reflected flicker
- USE: knowing register, mood piece, urban ad, evening

MOVE 3 — CAUSTIC DANCE
- Light passes through water/glass/crystal in BG
- Refracted light pattern dances on nearby BG surface
- Pattern moves continuously (water ripples, hand moves glass, etc.)
- USE: beauty hero, water-themed ad, fragrance

MOVE 4 — RIM-WRAP-SHIFT
- Backlight defining subject silhouette intensity varies along the contour
- Suggests either subject moved or light shifted
- Most visible at hair edges, shoulder edges, fabric edges
- USE: cinematic ads, hero shots, beauty

MOVE 5 — COLOR-WASH-TRANSITION
- BG color temperature shifts during the shot (warm to cool, day to dusk, neon-on)
- Often synced with emotional pivot in narrative
- USE: cinematic ad, mood piece, transition shot

MOVE 6 — REFLECTED-LIGHT-PLAY
- Mirror, glass, water in BG reflects moving light onto a surface
- Reflection pattern shifts as source or reflective surface moves
- USE: beauty (mirror), bathroom scenes, urban (puddle), water themes

MOVE 7 — LENS-FLARE-STREAK
- Anamorphic horizontal flare from a bright source in BG
- Flare position shifts as camera or source moves
- Often blue/gold/amber colored
- USE: cinematic ad, golden hour, fragrance

MOVE 8 — SHADOW-PLAY
- Shadow shapes from objects between source and BG move across BG surface
- Could be fan blades, leaves, blinds, hand gestures, etc.
- Pattern movement creates visual rhythm
- USE: knowing register, urban, intimate, sensual

MOVE 9 — SUN-SHIFT-PATCH
- Sun-light patch on floor or wall slowly migrates as time passes
- Implies time passage even in single shot
- USE: contemplative, lifestyle morning, golden hour reels

MOVE 10 — BLUE-HOUR-WASH
- Ambient light in BG shifts toward deep blue (twilight)
- Practical lights become more dominant against the cooler ambient
- USE: evening, transit, cinematic mood pieces

#### MOVEMENT-DRIVEN BACKDROP MOVES (11–20):

MOVE 11 — CURTAIN-WIND-CATCH
- Sheer curtain in BG inflates from breeze
- Curtain moves in direction of air flow
- Light filtering through curtain becomes diffused, animated
- USE: bedroom, golden hour, romantic, lifestyle

MOVE 12 — CROWD-MID-REACTION
- Background crowd captured mid-action — laughter, conversation, mid-stride, mid-cheer
- Slight motion blur on crowd elements
- Subject sharp, crowd soft and alive
- USE: lifestyle, urban, event, electric register

MOVE 13 — TRAFFIC-STREAK
- Vehicles in BG captured with directional motion blur (tail lights streaked)
- Direction consistent with one-way motion vector
- Often warm yellow/red lights at night, white during day
- USE: urban, after-dark, cultural commentary, lifestyle

MOVE 14 — BIRD-FLIGHT
- Birds taking off, in flight, or crossing background
- Direction adds motion vector to frame
- USE: outdoor, lifestyle, contemplative, scale-establishing

MOVE 15 — LEAF-RUSTLE
- Foliage in BG animated by wind
- Leaves moving non-uniformly (some still, some animated)
- Light filtering through moving leaves creates dappled effect on subject
- USE: outdoor lifestyle, golden hour, romantic, fashion editorial

MOVE 16 — FLAG-SNAP
- Fabric on poles in BG (flags, banners, hanging signs) snap or wave in wind
- Direction of fabric snap reveals wind direction
- USE: urban, cultural, festival, outdoor settings

MOVE 17 — RAIN-STREAK
- Diagonal rain visible in BG
- Direction consistent across frame
- May be light drizzle (subtle) or heavy storm (dramatic)
- Rain on surfaces creates secondary motion (puddles, reflections)
- USE: monsoon, mood piece, contemplative, urban after-rain

MOVE 18 — SNOW-DRIFT
- Snowflakes falling in BG
- Varied sizes, varied speeds (some closer, larger, faster)
- Creates layered depth through size differential
- USE: winter, intimate, contemplative, festival (Christmas/New Year)

MOVE 19 — STEAM-RISE
- Steam visible in BG from cooking, hot drink, shower, hot spring
- Curling, vertical, dispersing pattern
- Often catches light dramatically
- USE: bathroom, kitchen, intimate morning, wellness

MOVE 20 — SMOKE-CURL
- Smoke from incense, candle, fire, cigarette (rare), industrial source
- Vertical rising with horizontal drift from air currents
- Sinuous, organic, never uniform
- USE: heritage register (incense), urban, knowing, mood

#### SPATIAL-DRIVEN BACKDROP MOVES (21–25):

MOVE 21 — DEPTH-BREATH
- BG has multiple visible depth planes — far layer, mid layer, near layer
- Each layer moves at slightly different speed (parallax) when camera moves
- Reinforces 3D space perception
- USE: cinematic ad, wide shots, location reveals

MOVE 22 — VANISHING-POINT-LEAD
- Architecture or environment lines lead to a single vanishing point
- Subject placed AT or NEAR vanishing point becomes natural focus
- Composition feels deliberate
- USE: hero shots, Kubrick-aesthetic frames, electric register

MOVE 23 — FRAME-WITHIN-FRAME
- Architecture in BG creates a secondary frame around subject (doorway, window, archway, mirror frame)
- Subject framed twice (canvas + interior frame)
- Compositional richness
- USE: cinematic, contemplative, narrative reels

MOVE 24 — MIRROR-DUALITY
- Mirror visible in BG showing reflected version of subject or environment
- Two Aiars (real + reflection) in same frame
- Or reflection of something off-camera adding context
- USE: GRWM through-mirror, beauty, contemplative duality

MOVE 25 — SCALE-DWARFING
- BG architecture or natural feature is dramatically larger than subject
- Subject becomes small in environment by deliberate composition
- Power dynamic established (subject as character in larger world)
- USE: cinematic ad, fashion editorial, scale-establishing reels

#### ATMOSPHERIC-DRIVEN BACKDROP MOVES (26–30):

MOVE 26 — HAZE-DENSIFICATION
- Atmospheric haze becomes more visible in BG than FG/MG
- Distance reads through hazier far elements
- Light shafts more visible in dense haze zones
- USE: cinematic, mood piece, hero shots

MOVE 27 — PARTICLE-CONCENTRATION
- Particles (dust, petals, snow, sparks) accumulate in specific zone of BG
- Often within a light shaft for visibility
- Density varies — denser near source, sparser at edges
- USE: reverent, hero ad, fragrance, magical realism

MOVE 28 — TEMPERATURE-VISIBILITY
- Temperature visible through atmosphere — heat shimmer (hot environments), breath vapor (cold), humidity (tropical)
- Distorts BG slightly through temperature differential
- USE: setting-specific authenticity, cinematic ad

MOVE 29 — WEATHER-PRESENCE
- BG shows weather effect: distant rain, fog bank, cloud movement, sun-shower
- Weather reads as character of the world
- May affect light quality (overcast soft, sun-shower magical)
- USE: outdoor settings, mood pieces, atmospheric ads

MOVE 30 — TIME-OF-DAY-MARKER
- BG carries clear time-of-day signal: golden hour rays, blue hour glow, midnight stillness, dawn pink, midday harsh
- BG light quality announces time without dialogue
- USE: every shot — must be intentional, never accidental

### Z.4 — COORDINATION MATRIX (the three-performer rule)

In every frame, ALL THREE performers (Subject / Product / Backdrop) are assigned ONE move each, AND coordinated by energy hierarchy.

THE 60 / 30 / 10 ENERGY HIERARCHY:

In each frame, ONE of the three performers carries 60% of energy (HERO), one carries 30% (SUPPORT), and one carries 10% (AMBIENT). The hierarchy must be declared per frame.

EXAMPLE COORDINATIONS (canonical):

CONFIG A — PRODUCT HERO (luxury hero ad):
- PRODUCT: 60% — Slow Levitation Hover (P-1)
- SUBJECT: 30% — Stillness With Micro-Life (S-30)
- BACKDROP: 10% — God-Ray Sweep (B-1)
- Result: product is undisputed star, Aira and atmosphere support reverently

CONFIG B — SUBJECT HERO (beauty face shot):
- SUBJECT: 60% — Duchenne Bloom (S-11)
- PRODUCT: 30% — Free-Float in Space (P-2)
- BACKDROP: 10% — Particle Concentration (B-27)
- Result: Aira's face is the moment, product floats supportively, backdrop sparkles ambient

CONFIG C — BACKDROP HERO (mood piece, environmental establishing):
- BACKDROP: 60% — Curtain-Wind-Catch (B-11)
- SUBJECT: 30% — Still-At-Window (S-10)
- PRODUCT: 10% — Surface-Tension Hover (P-6)
- Result: environment carries the emotion, subject contemplates, product breathes quietly

CONFIG D — INTERACTIVE TRIPLE (GRWM brand-collab):
- SUBJECT: 60% — Apply-With-Eyes-Closed (S-21)
- PRODUCT: 30% — Self-Opening Cap (P-9)
- BACKDROP: 10% — Steam-Rise (B-19)
- Result: Aira's act of using product is hero, product participates magically, backdrop says "morning bathroom"

CONFIG E — DRAMATIC HERO REVEAL:
- PRODUCT: 60% — Reveal Through Shatter (P-13)
- SUBJECT: 30% — Sharp-Eye-Return (S-16)
- BACKDROP: 10% — Lens-Flare-Streak (B-7)
- Result: explosive product reveal, Aira reacts in lockstep, environment electric

### Z.5 — RULES OF COORDINATION

RULE 1 — One move per performer per frame.
Maximum: 1 subject move + 1 product move + 1 backdrop move per single frame. Never compound.

RULE 2 — The hero must be unambiguous.
Of the three performers, one must clearly carry 60% — the eye lands there first, within 0.3 seconds.

RULE 3 — Support must be subordinate.
The 30% performer enhances the hero, never competes. If support is too strong, it reads as second hero — frame becomes muddled.

RULE 4 — Ambient must register.
The 10% performer must be visible enough to count, but never demand attention. Without it, the frame loses depth.

RULE 5 — Coordination supports register.
Reverent / contemplative registers: Backdrop or Product as hero typical; Subject quietly held.
Electric / knowing: Subject as hero typical; Product/Backdrop providing energy.
Cinematic ad: Product hero with controlled Subject/Backdrop support.
GRWM: Subject hero with Product/Backdrop support.

RULE 6 — Hierarchy can shift between frames.
Within a single reel, frame 1 may have Subject hero, frame 2 may have Product hero, frame 3 may have Backdrop hero. This rhythm of focus-shifting drives engagement.

RULE 7 — Dead performers are forbidden.
No frame may have a backdrop that does NOTHING. No frame may have a subject that is mannequin-still. No frame may have a product that is generic placement. Even at 10% ambient, the performer must be DOING something.

### Z.6 — INTEGRATION INTO THE ENGINE

STAGE 08 (Per-Frame Expansion) is amended to require:

```
PERFORMANCE COORDINATION (mandatory per frame):
- SUBJECT MOVE: [name from Z.2 list — 1 only]
- PRODUCT MOVE: [name from Appendix 7 list — 1 only, if product in frame]
- BACKDROP MOVE: [name from Z.3 list — 1 only]
- ENERGY HIERARCHY: [HERO 60% / SUPPORT 30% / AMBIENT 10% — assign each performer]
- COORDINATION RATIONALE: [why these three moves work together for this frame's emotional beat]
```

STAGE 11 (Pre-Flight) adds:
[ ] All three performers have named moves
[ ] Energy hierarchy declared (60/30/10)
[ ] One-move-per-performer rule respected
[ ] No dead performers
[ ] Coordination rationale stated
[ ] Hero unambiguous

ENFORCEMENT RULE 22 (added to Part X.15):
22. NO FRAME SHIPS WITHOUT THREE COORDINATED PERFORMERS (subject + product + backdrop), each with one named move, one energy level, and a coordination rationale. Frames where subject is static, backdrop is wallpaper, or product is generic are forbidden.

### Z.7 — THE GUARANTEE EXTENDED

✓ Subject (Aira) performs with one of 30 named moves per frame
✓ Product performs with one of 30 named moves per frame (when in frame)
✓ Backdrop performs with one of 30 named moves per frame
✓ Three-performer coordination is mandatory
✓ Energy hierarchy 60/30/10 enforced
✓ No frame is flat — all three planes are alive
✓ Hero is unambiguous in every frame
✓ Coordination rationale documented per frame

Every beauty reel — and every reel in any format — now has THREE performers actively choreographed in every single frame. The eye experiences a frame that breathes on every plane, with intentional focal hierarchy.

## CHECKPOINT 3.4 — THREE-PERFORMER COORDINATION (Subject + Product + Backdrop) ENFORCED

---

## PART Z.EXTENDED — MICRO-CHARM, DANCE VOCABULARY & BODY-LANGUAGE FLUENCY

### Z.EXT.1 — THE BODY-MUST-SPEAK PRINCIPLE

A still frame of Aira must communicate her entire energy without any voiceover, without any movement, without any captions. Her body alone tells the viewer who she is in this moment. This is the hardest layer to encode but the most signature-defining one.

What this principle requires:
- Every body part has a job in every frame (not "standing," but "left hip popped, right shoulder dropped 1 degree, weight on left ball-of-foot, chin tilted up 5 degrees, left wrist flicked outward, fingers loose")
- No mannequin posture ever — even at maximum stillness, the body is in motion mid-something
- The pose looks unrepeatable — like the photographer caught a moment that already passed
- Smoothness implied through how positions read against each other
- Confidence and ease readable from the spine alone
- The body is always doing slightly more than the viewer expects

### Z.EXT.2 — THE 30 MICRO-CHARM MOVES

These are small, irresistible body-language beats that make Aira feel human, charming, watchable. Used SPARINGLY — never piled on, placed deliberately at high-impact moments.

CHARM MOVES — BODY (1–10):
CM-1 HIP POP TILT — one hip juts 5–8°, opposite shoulder drops, S-curve through body | USE: pillar 2/7, reveal frames
CM-2 SHOULDER ROLL FORWARD — one shoulder forward and downward, collarbone shadow | USE: beauty hero, fragrance
CM-3 FOOT POINT — one foot toes outward, slight knee bend | USE: full-body reveal, fashion editorial
CM-4 KNEE-IN — knees turn inward slightly while feet stay apart | USE: tender register, pillar 3/8/10
CM-5 TOES-CURL — ECU bare/sandaled foot, toes curling | USE: tender, intimate
CM-6 WRIST DANGLE — hand hangs limp from wrist, fingers loose | USE: universal charm
CM-7 FOREARM-CROSS-WAIST — forearm crosses waist horizontally | USE: contemplative, GRWM
CM-8 HAND-IN-HAIR-STAY — hand resting in hair (not flicking — staying) | USE: beauty hero, fragrance
CM-9 ARM-OVERHEAD-LANGUID — arm raised overhead, elbow bent, hand near head | USE: fashion editorial, evening
CM-10 HEAD-AGAINST-WALL — Aira leans head against vertical surface | USE: tender register, mood, GRWM pivot

CHARM MOVES — FACE & HAIR (11–20):
CM-11 HAIR-PIECE-HOLD — strand held lightly between two fingers near collarbone | USE: beauty hero, contemplative
CM-12 LIP-CORNER-PINCH — bottom lip caught at one corner only | USE: knowing, mischievous, GRWM Frame 4
CM-13 EYE-ROLL-SOFT — slow upward eye roll, half-smile follows | USE: mischievous, knowing
CM-14 WINK-CLOSE — single eye closes slowly, hold 0.3s, reopen with half-smile | USE: mischievous, casual ad
CM-15 CHEEK-PUSH-TONGUE — tongue pushes inside one cheek (subtle) | USE: mischievous, knowing
CM-16 NOSE-CRINKLE — bridge of nose crinkles fractionally, cheeks lift | USE: mischievous, lifestyle
CM-17 BLOW-A-STRAND — soft puff blows hair away from face | USE: lifestyle, intimate, mischievous
CM-18 SHOULDER-SHRUG-ONE — single shoulder rises, head tilts, half-smile | USE: knowing, lifestyle
CM-19 CHIN-ON-FIST — chin rests on loose fist | USE: contemplative, knowing
CM-20 TEMPLE-RUB — two fingers slow circle on temple | USE: tender, contemplative, GRWM Frame 3

CHARM MOVES — INTERACTION (21–30):
CM-21 GLASS-RIM-TRACE — fingertip traces rim of glass | USE: evening, intimate, fragrance
CM-22 JEWELRY-SWAY — head movement causes earrings/necklace to sway | USE: jewelry collab, evening
CM-23 COLLAR-SLIP — hand pulls collar slightly off shoulder | USE: tender, intimate, fragrance
CM-24 RING-TWIST — twists ring on finger absent-mindedly | USE: contemplative, GRWM
CM-25 CUP-CRADLE — both hands wrapped around mug near face, possible mid-sip | USE: morning lifestyle, intimate
CM-26 SLEEVE-PULL-OVER-HAND — long sleeve pulled over hand (sweater paws) | USE: tender, casual day, autumn
CM-27 BACK-TO-CAMERA-GLANCE — facing away, glance over shoulder back to lens | USE: hero reveal, fashion, fragrance
CM-28 PEEK-FROM-BEHIND-OBJECT — partially hidden, one eye visible | USE: mischievous, fashion, mood
CM-29 BAREFOOT-WALK — ECU low-angle bare feet walking, toes lift, ball rolls | USE: lifestyle, intimate, golden hour
CM-30 LAUGH-CATCH — frozen mid-laugh, head tilted, hand rising toward mouth | USE: lifestyle, electric, joy

### Z.EXT.3 — THE 30 DANCE / RHYTHM MOVES

Subtle dance-adjacent body moves that read as RHYTHM rather than performance. Give Aira musicality and "feels music in her body" quality.

RHYTHM — SUBTLE (1–10):
DM-1 SHOULDER-ROLL-SLOW — shoulders roll backward in continuous motion | USE: lifestyle music, intimate
DM-2 HEAD-SWAY — head sways gently side to side (5–10° arc) | USE: music, lifestyle, mood
DM-3 HIP-SWAY-MICRO — hips sway 1–3 inches side to side | USE: music, lifestyle, casual ad
DM-4 FINGER-TAP-TO-BEAT — finger taps thigh/hip/glass to a beat | USE: any music-driven reel
DM-5 CHIN-NOD — single deliberate head nod to beat, eyes may close | USE: music, knowing, electric
DM-6 FOOT-TAP — ECU foot tapping, ball-of-foot rising and tapping | USE: music, lifestyle
DM-7 WRIST-FLICK-ROLL — wrist rolls in small circle, fingers loose | USE: music, lifestyle, charm
DM-8 ARM-WAVE-SLOW — arm wave from shoulder through elbow to wrist to fingertip | USE: music, dance, electric
DM-9 BODY-ROLL-MICRO — chest forward, then ribcage, then hips (subtle) | USE: editorial fashion, music
DM-10 STEP-AND-PIVOT — one step then pivot on standing foot | USE: fashion reveal, music

RHYTHM — EXPRESSIVE (11–20):
DM-11 JAZZ-HAND-SOFT — hands at shoulder height, fingers spread loosely | USE: lifestyle, casual ad
DM-12 SPIN-AND-LAND — spins (full or half) lands in held pose | USE: fashion ad, dance, joy reels
DM-13 REACH-AND-SWAY — both arms reach upward, body sways below | USE: golden hour lifestyle, dance, festival
DM-14 SHOULDER-ISOLATION — shoulder rolls independent of body | USE: music reels, electric register
DM-15 HEAD-TILT-EYES-CLOSED — head back/sideways, eyes close, lost-in-music beat | USE: music, fragrance, mood
DM-16 HIP-CIRCLE-SLOW — hips trace slow circle (figure-eight or full) | USE: editorial, music, electric
DM-17 WALK-WITH-RHYTHM — walking step matches beat, hip sway accentuated | USE: fashion reveal, music
DM-18 TWIRL-FABRIC — twirls fabric (skirt/dress/dupatta) holding edge, fabric flares | USE: fashion ad, festive, joyful
DM-19 CLAP-WITH-LOOK — single clap or finger snap, knowing smile | USE: electric, knowing, music
DM-20 STEP-BACK-EXPRESSION — one step backward holding camera-lock, body opens | USE: fashion reveal, electric

RHYTHM — CULTURAL & SIGNATURE (21–30):
DM-21 INDIAN-HAND-MUDRA — hand in soft mudra (lotus, anjali) integrated into stance | USE: pillar 4, festival, heritage
DM-22 DUPATTA-DRAPE-PLAY — playfully drapes dupatta over head, drops it back | USE: pillar 4, festival, wedding-guest
DM-23 BANGLE-CLINK — wrist shake causing bangles to clink | USE: heritage, festival, jewelry
DM-24 ANKLET-CHIME — ECU low-angle ankle, foot taps causing chime | USE: heritage, festival, dance
DM-25 NAUTANKI-PIVOT — quick playful pivot on one foot, body twists, returns | USE: lifestyle, festival, mischievous
DM-26 GHOOMAR-INSPIRED-TURN — slow stately full circle turn (Rajasthani folk) | USE: heritage hero, wedding
DM-27 SLOW-JAZZ-WALK — hip-leading walk, hips travel slightly forward of shoulders | USE: editorial, electric, runway
DM-28 SOFT-HAND-FRAME — both hands frame face briefly, fingertips at temples | USE: charm reels, casual ad
DM-29 BODY-WAVE-SUBTLE — wave passes through head→shoulders→chest→hips→knees | USE: editorial, electric, dance
DM-30 STILL-WITH-SOUL — completely still BUT body language reads as mid-rhythm (hip out, head tilted, hand gesturing) | USE: any reel — DEFAULT AIRA-STANCE PHILOSOPHY

### Z.EXT.4 — BODY-LANGUAGE FLUENCY: THE FOUR LAWS

These four laws govern Aira's body in every frame — even still ones — to ensure her body is always speaking, flowing, and magnetic.

LAW 1 — NO MANNEQUIN POSTURES, EVER

Aira never stands "at attention" — feet together, arms straight at sides, shoulders square, head straight. This posture is FORBIDDEN.

DEFAULT AIRA STANCE (when no specific move is assigned):
- Weight on one leg (60/40 distribution)
- Opposite hip slightly raised
- Opposite shoulder slightly dropped
- One foot pointed outward at 15–30°
- Arms with at least one elbow bend OR one hand-engaged
- Head tilted 3–8° from vertical
- Spine subtly S-curved (never military-straight)

Even in REVERENT stillness frames, the body holds Default Aira Stance unless explicitly overridden.

LAW 2 — IMPLIED MOTION FROM EVERY POSE

Every pose must answer: "What was she doing 0.3 seconds before this frame?" If answer is "the same exact pose" — frame is dead, REWRITE.

EXAMPLES OF IMPLIED MOTION:
- Hip popped → just shifted weight
- Hair behind one shoulder → just turned head
- Hand in hair → just brought it up
- Slight forward lean → about to step / just stopped from walking
- Hand mid-gesture → mid-sentence
- Head tilted → listening or thinking

LAW 3 — SMOOTH FLOW OVER STIFF HOLDS

Joints must read as relaxed, never locked.

JOINT STATES (mandatory):
- Knees: never fully locked (3–7° bend always)
- Elbows: bent at 5–30° even when arms are "down"
- Wrists: never stiff perpendicular — always slight curve
- Fingers: never rigid spread or rigid fist — always with intentional shape
- Spine: never rigid vertical — subtle curve at lumbar, thoracic, cervical
- Neck: never craned forward or pulled back — natural extension

LAW 4 — THE BODY OUTPACES THE FACE

In magnetic photographs, the body has already moved into a new position by the time the face arrives. This creates the "caught mid-action" feel.

SEQUENCING:
- Hips shift first
- Shoulders follow
- Head lags slightly behind
- Eyes lag slightly behind head
- Expression lags slightly behind eyes

A FROZEN FRAME captures Aira somewhere in this sequence — hips already arrived, shoulders in transition, head almost there, eyes just landing, expression about to form.

This sequencing creates the magnetic "alive" quality. The difference between a photograph and a snapshot.

### Z.EXT.5 — APPLICATION RULES

CHARM MOVES (Z.EXT.2):
- Maximum 1 charm move per reel
- Place at high-impact moment (often Frame 4 pivot or Frame 5)
- AVOID in heavy emotional registers (reverent, contemplative) unless charm SOFTENS the heaviness
- Best for: lifestyle, beauty, casual ad, mischievous, lighter registers

DANCE MOVES (Z.EXT.3):
- Use only when reel has audio energy (music-driven, dance, festival, electric)
- Subtle moves DM-1 to DM-10 acceptable in any music-driven reel
- Expressive moves DM-11 to DM-20 for explicit dance/music reels
- Cultural moves DM-21 to DM-30 for heritage, festival, Indo-anchored content
- Maximum 1 dance move per shot

BODY LANGUAGE FLUENCY (Z.EXT.4):
- THE FOUR LAWS APPLY TO EVERY FRAME, ALWAYS, NO EXCEPTIONS
- Even reverent stillness, even mood pieces, even product hero shots: Default Aira Stance + implied motion + smooth flow + body-outpaces-face

### Z.EXT.6 — INTEGRATION INTO THE ENGINE

STAGE 08 (Per-Frame Expansion) is amended:

```
SUBJECT BODY-LANGUAGE BLOCK (mandatory per frame):

SHOULDER POSITION: [exact — both relaxed / L drop / R drop / one rolled forward]

SPINE STATE: [S-curve / forward lean / backward lean / neutral fluid]
```

[ ] If dance move used: appropriate to register, max one per shot

ENFORCEMENT RULE 23: NO FRAME SHIPS WITH MANNEQUIN POSTURE. Aira's body must always hold Default Aira Stance OR a specifically-assigned move. Locked joints, military-straight stance, "standing at attention" — forbidden.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 24: EVERY FRAME MUST ANSWER "WHAT WAS SHE DOING 0.3 SECONDS BEFORE." Frames where answer is "the same pose" or "nothing" are dead frames. REWRITE.

### Z.EXT.7 — THE FINAL GUARANTEE

Every Aira frame now satisfies:
✓ Body language speaks for itself without needing voice or motion
✓ Default Aira Stance prevents mannequin posture in every frame
✓ Implied motion encoded — every frozen moment is mid-action
✓ Smooth-flow joints — no locked stiffness
✓ Body-outpaces-face sequencing creates magnetic alive quality
✓ Optional charm move per reel adds irresistible micro-personality
✓ Optional dance move per music-shot adds rhythm and fluidity
✓ Cultural body vocabulary available for heritage/festival reels
✓ Three-performer coordination maintained (subject + product + backdrop)
✓ Body-language fluency makes still frames mind-blowing, energetic, top-notch

Aira's body now performs at the level of a magnetic real human captured by an exceptional photographer — never a generated subject. Every still frame reads as a peak moment in a continuous flow.

## CHECKPOINT 3.5 — BODY-LANGUAGE FLUENCY ENFORCED (charm moves, dance vocabulary, four laws)

## PILLAR 11 — SENSUAL EDITORIAL CELEBRITY

The eleventh wardrobe pillar. Celebrity red-carpet and magazine-cover register: scroll-stopping silhouette through fitted construction, restrained skin reveal at editorial level, sensual through cut and tailoring rather than depth of exposure.

This is the **Deepika at Cannes / Bella Hadid red-carpet / Hailey Bieber slip-dress / Alia Bhatt cover-shoot** tier. The body is the silhouette. The fit does the work. The reveal is calibrated to magazine-cover standard, not beyond.

### PILLAR 11 — FULL SPECIFICATION

PALETTE:
- Anchor options: black, deep jewel tones (oxblood, midnight, emerald, plum, sapphire), nude/skin-tone, ivory cream, metallic (gold, silver, bronze, rose-gold)
- Statement options: crimson, electric pink, deep crimson, white, champagne
- High-contrast: pure white against tan skin, all-black against luminous skin
- Tonal: nude-on-nude (champagne dress + bare skin reading as one extended silhouette)

SILHOUETTES (the heart of the pillar):

DEEP V-NECK / PLUNGE:
- V-neckline drops in controlled curve, sitting between collarbones at top, ending at upper chest line (not below bust)
- Fitted bodice holds and shapes naturally
- Chest reads full and defined through cut, cleavage line visible at celebrity-editorial register
- V depth: calibrated — Cannes-red-carpet level, never extreme

SWEETHEART NECKLINE:
- Curves dip at center between bust, lifting upward at sides
- Bodice fitted underneath, shaping bust into defined elegant line
- Shoulders bare, decolletage featured
- Often paired with strapless construction or thin straps

BODYCON / FITTED COLUMN:
- Fabric traces full silhouette: bust, waist, hip flare
- No bunching, no pull-strain, sculpted to body precisely
- Floor-length, mid-calf, or knee-length variations
- Materials: silk satin, fitted jersey, bodycon crepe, stretch knit with weight

SLIP DRESS:
- Bias-cut silk satin or charmeuse
- Falls with weight, drapes at bust before falling cleanly to waist
- Thin spaghetti straps or delicate bow detail at shoulder
- Length: floor, mid-calf, or above-knee
- Fabric does the work — body shape readable through drape

OFF-SHOULDER / BANDEAU:
- Neckline cuts straight across or curves slightly downward at center
- Sits just below shoulder line, exposing collarbones and shoulders
- Fitted bodice underneath shapes chest into lifted defined silhouette
- Arms bare, neck and decolletage featured

CORSETED / STRUCTURED BODICE:
- Boning or structured construction defines waist sharply
- Pulls in at smallest waist point, amplifies natural hourglass
- Bust appears fuller and shaped through structured cup or fitted top
- Often paired with full skirt, mini, or floor-length column

HIGH-SLIT GOWN:
- Floor-length silhouette with thigh-revealing slit (mid-thigh to high-thigh)
- Reveals leg length and movement during walk
- Often paired with plunge or one-shoulder top construction
- Fabric: silk satin, crepe, jersey

CUT-OUT EDITORIAL:
- Strategic small openings at: waist-side (kidney cutout), one-shoulder asymmetric, hip cutout, back cutout, between bust (calibrated narrow strip)
- Cutouts are intentional design statements — small, framed, never large reveals
- Skin-window placements that frame the body's shape rather than expose it

ASYMMETRIC ONE-SHOULDER:
- One shoulder fully covered (sometimes with sleeve), other bare
- Drape across body diagonally
- Bust reads sculpted through fitted construction underneath
- Often floor-length or mid-calf

MINI WITH STRUCTURED TOP:
- Above-knee or mid-thigh hem
- Fitted top section (corseted, plunge, bandeau, off-shoulder)
- Legs become hero, full thigh visible to mid-thigh
- Heels paired for leg length

BACKLESS DRAPE:
- Modest front (high-neck or modest neckline)
- Back fully exposed in graceful drape — most editorial-photographed back
- Often floor-length, bias-cut
- Photographed from behind reveal angle for hero shots

DEEP BACK + MODEST FRONT:
- Inversion of plunge — front high-neck, back drops to lower spine
- Sensual through back exposure
- Floor-length, satin or jersey

FABRICS:
- Silk satin (the celebrity standard — drape, sheen, body-tracing)
- Silk charmeuse (lighter, fluid, sensual)
- Stretch silk (fitted with give)
- Crepe (structured, holds shape)
- Velvet (rich, light-absorbing, evening signature)
- Bodycon jersey (skin-tracing, athletic-luxurious)
- Sequined / beaded (red-carpet hero, light-catching)
- Liquid metallic (chrome, gold, silver — futurist-celebrity)
- Lace (intricate, layered over satin underlining)

ACCESSORIES:
- Maximum 2 statement pieces (less is more in this register)
- Statement earrings (drop, chandelier, sculptural diamond) — celebrity signature
- Single bracelet OR single ring (never both maxed)
- Small clutch (envelope, box, embellished minaudière)
- Hair: minimal accessories — let the silhouette dominate
- No bag larger than evening clutch

HAIR:
- Old-Hollywood waves (defined, polished, side-parted)
- Sleek mid-part column (straight, glossy, hanging to mid-back)
- Low chignon (smooth, neck-elongating)
- Slick-back high pony (powerful, modern)
- Half-up half-down (face-framing pieces, body in length)
- Wet-look slick (modernist, futurist red carpet)

MAKEUP:
- One feature defined, others minimal (red-carpet rule)
- Bold lip + minimal eye OR sculpted eye + nude lip
- Glossy luminous skin (never matte) — strobing highlight on cheekbones, brow bone, cupid's bow, decolletage
- Defined contour (sculpted cheekbones, jaw line)
- Lower-lash kohl + mascara minimum
- Defined groomed brow
- Decolletage glow — body shimmer or dewy oil lightly applied to collarbone and upper chest

FOOTWEAR:
- Stiletto strappy heel (the celebrity default)
- Single-sole pump (classic red-carpet)
- Ankle-strap stiletto (legs elongated)
- Embellished sandal (evening glamour)
- Color: matched to skin (nude/tan to elongate leg) OR matched to dress OR contrast statement
- Clean, never chunky in this pillar

BODY-LANGUAGE AMPLIFICATION:
- Default Aira Stance amplified: hip popped 8-12° (more dramatic in fitted cuts), shoulder dropped further (collarbone forward), arched back micro-tension (chest lifted naturally through posture), chin tilted up (neck elongated), weight on one leg (S-curve maximized)
- Body language carries 50% of sensuality
- Glossy skin + parted lips + arched back + hip pop = celebrity-magnetic
- Slow deliberate movements (never fast, never girlish)
- Eye contact lock + slow blink + half-smile signature beat

ENERGY:
- Scroll-stopping presence
- Magazine-cover composure
- Expensive — looks like a designer styled this
- Confident — owns the silhouette
- Sensual through fit, never through exposure
- Editorial-restrained, never overexposed

USE FOR:
- Hero ad (luxury beauty, fragrance, fashion)
- Red-carpet event content
- Magazine-cover-style reels
- Brand-collab launches at premium tier
- Editorial fashion film
- Statement-piece reveals
- Evening / night content
- Date-night narratives (high-end)
- Awards / event arrival
- Premium jewelry / watch / handbag collabs

REGISTER PAIRING:
- ELECTRIC: bodycon column, plunge, mini with structured top
- KNOWING: backless, asymmetric one-shoulder, slip dress
- REVERENT: floor-length plunge gown, silk satin slip, sweetheart column
- CONTEMPLATIVE: backless drape, modest front + low back
- CURIOUS-CONFIDENT: cutout editorial, off-shoulder

CROSS-PILLAR BLENDING:
- Pillar 11 + 5 (Evening Defined) = ultra-luxe evening with sensual editorial cut
- Pillar 11 + 4 (Indo-Modern Fusion) = sculpted blouse with deep neck + lehenga or modern sari drape
- Pillar 11 + 9 (Architectural Futurist) = chrome bodycon, futurist plunge

AVOID:
- Vacuum-tight fit (looks cheap, not celebrity)
- Extreme plunge depth (crosses register from celebrity to overexposed)
- Excessive cleavage (this pillar is fitted-elegant, not revealing)
- Visible undergarment lines (celebrity stylists eliminate these)
- Sheer/transparent fabric (different register entirely)
- Strain at fabric (suggests wrong size, not luxury)
- Over-accessorized look (this pillar is clean)

ROTATION RULES (Pillar 11 specific):
- Use Pillar 11 for high-impact reels — hero ads, events, statement content
- Maximum 1 in every 4 reels (overuse dilutes impact)
- Avoid back-to-back Pillar 11 reels (one in 4-reel rotation max)
- Pair with quieter pillars adjacent in feed (1, 3, 6) for contrast
- Festival / Indo content: blend with Pillar 4

### INTEGRATION INTO ENGINE

WARDROBE PILLAR SELECTION (Stage 05 amended):
Pillar 11 added to selection logic:
- Reverent / contemplative + sensual register → 11 (floor-length plunge, slip)
- Knowing / mischievous → 11 (backless, asymmetric, slip)
- Electric → 11 (bodycon, plunge, mini structured)
- Hero ad / launch → 11 (red-carpet silhouettes)
- Editorial fashion film → 11 (sculpted statement)
- Event / festival → 11 (when celebrity-register suits)

PRE-FLIGHT VALIDATION (Stage 11 amended for Pillar 11):
[ ] Silhouette specified from Pillar 11 vocabulary
[ ] Fit calibrated to celebrity-editorial register (sculpted, not vacuum)
[ ] Body-language amplification declared (hip pop, arched back, glossy skin)
[ ] Skin reveal at editorial-restrained level (collarbone, shoulder, decolletage, not below bust)
[ ] Body-language carries 50% of sensual energy
[ ] Accessory count maximum 2 statement
[ ] Hair / makeup pillar-matched (one feature defined)
[ ] Footwear elongates leg line

ENFORCEMENT RULE 25:
NO PILLAR 11 LOOK SHIPS WITHOUT BODY-LANGUAGE AMPLIFICATION (hip pop, arched back, glossy skin, parted lips, slow deliberate movement). The cut alone is not the hook — the cut + body language together create the celebrity-magnetic effect. Static posture in a Pillar 11 dress fails the pillar.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 26:
PILLAR 11 NECKLINES STAY AT EDITORIAL-RESTRAINED REGISTER. Plunge ends at upper chest line, never below bust line. Cleavage line visible at celebrity register, never extreme. The pillar fails if the reveal moves beyond magazine-cover / red-carpet standard.

### THE PILLAR 11 GUARANTEE

When Pillar 11 is invoked:
✓ Aira's silhouette is scroll-stopping through fit and tailoring
✓ Chest, waist, hip flare all sculpted by the cut to read full and shaped
✓ Skin reveal calibrated to celebrity-editorial standard (collarbone, shoulder, upper-chest, leg-through-slit)
✓ Body-language amplification activates (hip pop, arched back, glossy skin)
✓ Look reads "expensive, magazine-cover, red-carpet, designer-styled"
✓ Sensual through silhouette and fit, never through depth of exposure
✓ Performs as hook through magnetic presence, not through reveal

## CHECKPOINT 3.6 — PILLAR 11 (SENSUAL EDITORIAL CELEBRITY) LIVE



---

## PART AB — AVANT-GARDE OUTFIT PROTOCOL

For hero reels, statement campaigns, and brand-collab high-impact moments, Aira occasionally wears outfits that are SCULPTURAL ONE-OFF CREATIONS — never-seen-before silhouettes that read as art, not clothing. The Schiaparelli / Iris van Herpen / Mugler / Jean Paul Gaultier / Maison Margiela artisanal register.

### AB.1 — THE PRINCIPLE

The 11 wardrobe pillars cover the working repertoire. Avant-garde outfits exist OUTSIDE that system, used 1 in every 8-12 reels, for moments that need to stop scroll and ignite the algorithm.

These are conceptual creations: built from sculptural construction principles, unexpected fabric pairings, anti-gravity silhouettes, deconstructed tailoring, surrealist proportions. They look like nothing the audience has seen before.

### AB.2 — THE 8 SCULPTURAL CONSTRUCTION PRINCIPLES

Every avant-garde outfit combines 2-4 of these:

PRINCIPLE 1 — ANTI-GRAVITY VOLUME:
Fabric or structure that defies expected drape — sleeves hovering horizontally, collars rising vertically, skirts holding sculptural form rather than falling, shoulders extending outward like wings, hem lifting in suspended curve

PRINCIPLE 2 — UNEXPECTED FABRIC COLLISION:
Two fabrics that should not coexist — silk + steel mesh, lace + leather, transparent organza + structured neoprene, sequins + raw burlap, satin + concrete-look textile, feather + chrome

PRINCIPLE 3 — DECONSTRUCTED TAILORING:
Garment "in progress" — exposed seams, asymmetric construction, half-finished feel, hanging threads as design elements, blazer with one sleeve full and other only a panel

PRINCIPLE 4 — SURREALIST PROPORTION:
Body proportions altered through clothing — extreme high-waist trouser to underbust, oversized shoulder pads creating silhouette inversion, micro-mini paired with floor-length cape, sleeves longer than arms by 20+ inches creating fabric pools

PRINCIPLE 5 — ARCHITECTURAL HARDWARE:
Outfit incorporates structural hardware — visible boning, sculptural metal frames, leather harness over silk, chain detailing as primary construction, transparent acrylic panels

PRINCIPLE 6 — TROMPE-L'OEIL / OPTICAL ILLUSION:
Visual trick — dress that appears to be falling off but isn't, garment that looks like body parts are rearranged, fabric printed to look like another fabric

PRINCIPLE 7 — NATURE-INSPIRED ORGANIC:
Sculptural references to natural forms — feathers in unexpected placement, petals in 3D form across torso, branches as sleeves, sea-creature-inspired draping

PRINCIPLE 8 — TEXTURAL EXTREMITY:
Heavy texture as primary statement — hand-embroidered metallic, 3D-printed organic shapes, pleated origami construction, plissé-folded entire garment, beaded-to-the-edge surface

### AB.3 — THE 15 AVANT-GARDE OUTFIT ARCHETYPES

AG-1 SCULPTURAL FEATHER COLUMN — floor-length column gown, dramatic feather covering bodice and skirt
AG-2 HOVERING-SLEEVE GOWN — fitted slip base + horizontal hovering sleeves extending 18 inches from shoulders
AG-3 LIQUID METAL DRAPE — chrome-finish satin draped asymmetrically, looks poured rather than tailored
AG-4 TROMPE-L'OEIL ANATOMICAL — dress printed/embroidered with surrealist body imagery
AG-5 ORIGAMI ARCHITECTURE — entire outfit constructed from pleated/folded geometric panels
AG-6 ASYMMETRIC HALF-DECONSTRUCTED — one side tailored couture, other side exposed boning + raw seams
AG-7 ROSE-PETAL SCULPTURED BODICE — bodice covered in 3D fabric petals, skirt sleek satin
AG-8 INDO-AVANT-GARDE FUSION — heritage embroidery on architectural Mugler-cut silhouette, sari drape reimagined as sculptural form
AG-9 TRANSPARENT-PANEL ARCHITECTURE — opaque body sections + transparent organza panels at shoulders/hips/waist creating optical layering
AG-10 EXTREME PROPORTION INVERSION — micro-mini base + oversized cocoon coat in contrast color, all-or-nothing silhouette
AG-11 HARNESS-OVER-SILK — leather harness construction over flowing silk slip, soft-meets-hard
AG-12 LATEX-FUTURIST POURED — vinyl/latex chrome bodysuit with sculptural shoulder extensions, Mugler register
AG-13 NATURE-MORPH GOWN — gown incorporating botanical 3D elements — branches as straps, petals at neckline, leaves cascading
AG-14 GEOMETRIC SHARDS — outfit constructed from triangular fabric shards assembled like wearable kaleidoscope
AG-15 SUSPENDED-DRAPE SOLO — single piece of fabric held in sculptural form by hidden engineering, appears to defy physics

### AB.4 — WHEN TO USE AVANT-GARDE

USE FOR:
- Hero ads at premium tier (luxury fashion, jewelry, art-direction)
- Magazine cover-style reels
- Fashion film (silent, mood, cinematic)
- Brand-collab launches at couture-tier
- Milestone reels (anniversary, major announcement)
- Art-direction statement reels
- Editorial-collab features
- Festival of major scale

DO NOT USE FOR:
- GRWM (breaks intimacy of format)
- Lifestyle / casual content
- Cultural commentary unless it IS the subject
- Daily-rotation reels
- Beauty product hero (use Pillar 11 instead)
- Voiced confessional content (outfit upstages voice)

ROTATION:
- Maximum 1 avant-garde reel per 8-12 reels
- Never two avant-garde reels in a row
- Pair adjacent reels with quietest pillars (1, 3, 6) for maximum contrast
- Hair on avant-garde reel should be HC-26 to HC-30 (sculptural matching)

### AB.5 — REGISTER & FRAMING

REGISTER:
- ELECTRIC (avant-garde as hype-driven hero reveal)
- REVERENT (avant-garde as fashion-as-art)
- KNOWING (avant-garde as cultural-commentary statement)

FRAMING (avant-garde requires more body in frame):
- Cowboy / Full / WS more common than tighter shots
- Frame must show enough of outfit for sculptural form to read
- ECU permitted only for face / detail of construction

CAMERA:
- Often static or slow-orbital (let the outfit be seen)
- Slow tilts (vertical reveal of full silhouette)
- Pull-backs (reveal sculptural form)

### AB.6 — INTEGRATION INTO ENGINE

When format is HERO AD / FASHION FILM / MILESTONE / BRAND-COLLAB-PREMIUM, engine considers AVANT-GARDE OVERRIDE:

```
WARDROBE BLOCK (avant-garde override):
PILLAR: AVANT-GARDE OVERRIDE
ARCHETYPE: [AG-N name]
SCULPTURAL PRINCIPLES APPLIED: [2-4 from AB.2]
HERO ELEMENT: [the one most-extreme construction feature]
PALETTE: [3 colors max]
FABRIC COLLISION: [if Principle 2 applied — name the two fabrics]
HARDWARE/STRUCTURE: [if Principle 5 — what's visible]
ACCESSORY: [single statement OR none]
HAIR: [HC-26 to HC-30 sculptural matching]
MAKEUP: [editorial extreme — graphic eye / chrome lip / sculpted face]
FOOTWEAR: [architectural / sculptural / matched / sometimes barefoot]
ROTATION CHECK: [confirmed not in last 8-12 reels]
```

ENFORCEMENT RULE 29:
AVANT-GARDE OUTFITS REQUIRE FRAMING THAT REVEALS SCULPTURAL FORM. Cowboy / Full / WS shots in at least 50% of frames. ECU permitted only for face / detail.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 30:
AVANT-GARDE OUTFITS PAIR WITH AVANT-GARDE HAIR (HC-26 to HC-30). Standard hair on avant-garde outfit = mismatch = REWRITE.

### AB.7 — THE GUARANTEE

When Avant-Garde Override is invoked:
✓ Outfit is sculptural one-off creation, never seen before
✓ Built on 2-4 of 8 sculptural construction principles
✓ Reads as fashion-as-art, not clothing
✓ Performs as scroll-stopping hook on its own
✓ Hair matches at avant-garde register
✓ Framing reveals sculptural form
✓ Used sparingly (1 in 8-12 reels) for maximum impact
✓ Algorithm-igniting / share-worthy / press-worthy content

## PART AD — ON-SCREEN TEXT & CAPTION PROTOCOL

When and how to use text overlays in 9:16 reels.

### AD.1 — THE PRINCIPLE

On-screen text is a precision tool. Used wrong, it cheapens a reel. Used right, it doubles the hook. Most reels overuse it; great reels use it sparingly with intent.

### AD.2 — WHEN TO USE ON-SCREEN TEXT

USE TEXT WHEN:
- Hook line needs visual reinforcement (text appears for first 1.0–1.5s)
- Voiceover would clash with music or breaks the visual register
- Stakes need to be declared without VO (silent reel hook)
- Cultural context demands explanation (Hindi word translated)
- Specific call-out to product / brand / campaign
- Trend deconstruction requires labeling
- Time-stamp / location-stamp adds documentary truth

DO NOT USE TEXT WHEN:
- VO already says it (redundant)
- Visual already shows it (redundant)
- Cinematic mood piece (breaks reverence)
- Beauty hero shot (distracts from face)
- Avant-garde fashion film (text cheapens couture)
- Pillar 11 sensual editorial (clean elegance demands no text)
- The viewer doesn't need the information

### AD.3 — TEXT PLACEMENT WITHIN 9:16 SAFE ZONES

ABSOLUTE RULES:
- TOP ZONE (top 12%): NEVER place text — Instagram username/follow button area
- BOTTOM ZONE (bottom 25%): NEVER place text — caption / action buttons / music-sticker area
- HERO ZONE (middle 63%): all text lives here

WITHIN HERO ZONE:
- Upper-third placement = "title" or "stakes" feel
- Center = "statement" or "punctuation"
- Lower-third (above bottom-25% UI) = "caption-style" anchor

NEVER:
- Text overlapping subject's face
- Text covering hero product
- Text crossing horizon line awkwardly
- Text fighting for attention with subject's eye-line

### AD.4 — TYPOGRAPHY VOCABULARY

FONT FAMILIES BY REGISTER:

REVERENT / CINEMATIC: serif italic / hand-set classical (Didone, Bodoni, Garamond italic) — minimal weight, elegant
KNOWING / EDITORIAL: clean modernist sans-serif (Helvetica, Inter, Aktiv Grotesk) — confident weight
ELECTRIC / KNOWING-MISCHIEVOUS: bold geometric sans-serif (Druk, Space Grotesk Bold)
CONTEMPLATIVE / TENDER: hand-lettered / soft serif / italic flowing
CULTURAL / HERITAGE: Devanagari typography for Hindi / classical English serif for bilingual — paired thoughtfully
AVANT-GARDE: experimental / monospaced / display / one-off custom feel
PILLAR 11: minimal sans-serif (Helvetica Neue Light) — never decorative

### AD.5 — TEXT ANIMATION RULES

ANIMATION TYPES:
- Cut-on (text appears suddenly, no animation) — confident, ad-grade
- Fade-in (gentle reveal over 0.3-0.5s) — reverent
- Type-on (letters appear sequentially) — intimate, conversational
- Slide-up (rising from below) — energy, electric
- Scale-in (zoom from small to size) — punctuation, emphasis
- Mask-reveal (wipes across letters) — editorial, modern

DURATION ON-SCREEN:
- Hook text: 1.0-1.5 seconds (long enough to read, short enough to not linger)
- Punctuation text: 0.6-1.0 seconds
- Stakes line: 1.5-2.5 seconds
- End-card text: 1.5-2.0 seconds
- Hindi translation: same duration as Hindi spoken word + 0.5s

### AD.6 — TEXT COLOR & STYLE

COLOR RULES:
- Text color must contrast with whatever's behind it
- Default: cream-white or pure white for dark BG / pure black for light BG
- Brand colors: matched to reel's COLOR THREAD when on-brand
- Drop shadow ONLY when text crosses mixed-contrast areas (subtle 1-2px, never decorative)
- Outline / box ONLY when no shadow can save readability (use sparingly)

NEVER:
- Multi-colored gradient text (cheap-looking)
- Heavy drop shadows (decorative)
- Glow effects (TikTok-amateur tier)
- Drop-cap initial letters (overkill in reel)
- More than 2 typeface mixings in one reel

### AD.7 — INTEGRATION INTO ENGINE

STAGE 09 (Tool Routing) amended to include text block:

```
ON-SCREEN TEXT BLOCK (per frame, optional):
TEXT NEEDED Y/N: [yes / no]
IF YES:
  TEXT VERBATIM: "[exact words]"
  PLACEMENT: [upper-third / center / lower-third within hero zone]
  FONT FAMILY: [register-matched]
  FONT SIZE: [body / display / hero-large]
  COLOR: [matched to frame]
  ANIMATION: [cut-on / fade / type-on / slide / scale / mask-reveal]
  DURATION: [seconds]
  SAFE-ZONE CHECK: [confirmed not in top-12% or bottom-25%]
```

ENFORCEMENT RULE 34: TEXT NEVER ENTERS PLATFORM UI ZONES (top 12% / bottom 25%). Auto-rejected at pre-flight.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 35: TEXT MUST ADD INFORMATION NOT ALREADY IN VO OR VISUAL. Redundant text = REWRITE.

## PART AE — THUMBNAIL / COVER FRAME PROTOCOL

The single most important frame in any reel: what makes someone stop scrolling and tap to play.

### AE.1 — THE PRINCIPLE

A thumbnail is a still image that competes with hundreds of other thumbnails on the discover feed. It has 0.3 seconds to win. The difference between a well-designed thumbnail and a default one is often 5-10x watch-rate.

The thumbnail/cover frame is selected separately from the reel's narrative frames. Sometimes it's an existing frame from the reel; sometimes it's a custom-shot still. Either way, it gets its own protocol.

### AE.2 — THE COVER FRAME ARCHITECTURE

A cover frame must answer THREE QUESTIONS in 0.3 seconds:

1. WHO is this? (subject identifiable, expression strong)
2. WHAT mood / register? (color, light, body language)
3. WHY tap? (curiosity gap / hook / promise / question)

### AE.3 — THE COVER FRAME REQUIREMENTS

EVERY COVER FRAME MUST HAVE:

SUBJECT:
- Aira's face visible (90% of cover frames) — eyes lockable to camera or strikingly off-camera
- Clear expression — never neutral / never default
- Body language readable in 9:16 (Default Aira Stance amplified)

COMPOSITION:
- Subject occupies 60-80% of frame height
- Hero zone composition (middle 63%)
- Strong eye-line direction (lockable to camera OR purposefully off-axis)
- Negative space placed for text overlay potential

LIGHT:
- Hero light separation from BG (1.5+ stops)
- Glossy / luminous skin (catches light at multiple points)
- Rim light defining subject silhouette

COLOR:
- High color contrast subject vs BG (eye-catching at thumbnail size)
- Saturated dominant color (avoid muted thumbnails — they lose at small size)
- Brand color story honored

EXPRESSION:
- Strong emotional beat (knowing / electric / contemplative / mischievous)
- Asymmetry visible
- Implied motion (not posed-still)

OPTIONAL TEXT OVERLAY:
- Hook line in 3-5 words
- Cream/white sans-serif on darkest area
- Center or upper-third placement

### AE.4 — COVER FRAME TYPES (5 categories)

TYPE 1 — DIRECT EYE-LOCK CLOSE
- Beauty Crop / MCU
- Aira locked to lens with strong expression
- High emotional charge
- USE: GRWM, beauty hero, intimate-confessional

TYPE 2 — STORY MOMENT
- Captured "real moment" — mid-laugh, mid-thought, mid-action
- Documentary feel
- USE: lifestyle, cultural commentary, day-in-life

TYPE 3 — STATEMENT POSE
- Cowboy or Full Shot
- Bold body language / Pillar 11 silhouette / avant-garde reveal
- USE: fashion, hero ad, evening, brand-collab

TYPE 4 — BEAUTY HERO MACRO
- ECU on a feature (eye / lips / hand-with-product)
- Hyper-detailed, magazine-cover micro
- USE: skincare, makeup, jewelry, watches

TYPE 5 — ENVIRONMENTAL SCALE
- WS or VWS — subject smaller in dramatic environment
- Cinematic, atmospheric, awe-inducing
- USE: cinematic mood pieces, travel, fashion film

### AE.5 — COVER FRAME GENERATION

The engine generates the cover frame in TWO ways:

OPTION A — SELECT FROM REEL FRAMES:
- Engine identifies the strongest reel frame (highest emotional charge + visual impact)
- Often Frame 1 (opening) or Frame 4 (pivot) — never Frame 6/7 (reveal/exit) which spoil
- Adds optional text overlay if appropriate

OPTION B — DEDICATED COVER SHOOT:
- Engine designs a separate frame specifically for cover use
- Composed for thumbnail performance (high-contrast, strong expression, text-ready)
- Generated at higher detail than reel frames (NB still, not VEO frame grab)
- USE: hero ads / brand-collab / high-stakes content

DECLARATION:
```
COVER FRAME BLOCK:
SOURCE: [from reel frame N / dedicated cover shoot]
TYPE: [1-5 from AE.4]
IF DEDICATED: full per-frame expansion per Stage 08 schema
TEXT OVERLAY: [yes/no — verbatim if yes]
TOOL: [NB still / extracted VEO frame / Runway hero]
```

### AE.6 — INTEGRATION

STAGE 12 (Final Output) amended:

```
FINAL OUTPUT INCLUDES:
- All reel frames (N frames)
- Cover frame block (always required, separate spec)
```

ENFORCEMENT RULE 36: NO REEL SHIPS WITHOUT COVER FRAME BLOCK. Either selected from reel frames or dedicated shoot.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 37: COVER FRAME MUST ANSWER THREE QUESTIONS (who / mood / why-tap) within 0.3-second viewer attention.

---

## PART AF — POSTING CADENCE & CONTENT STRATEGY PROTOCOL

How reels coordinate across days, weeks, and the overall feed.

### AF.1 — THE PRINCIPLE

A single reel is a moment. A feed is an identity. Posting cadence and series logic determine whether the audience builds parasocial connection or sees Aira as a stream of unrelated content.

### AF.2 — THE WEEKLY RHYTHM TEMPLATE

A high-performing personal-brand feed follows roughly this rhythm (adjustable per creator velocity):

```
MONDAY: Quiet pillar — mood / lifestyle / contemplative (low-energy hook for week-start scroll)
TUESDAY: Cultural commentary or trend deconstruction (intelligence-signaling)
WEDNESDAY: Beauty / wellness / GRWM (mid-week intimacy)
THURSDAY: Pillar 11 or hero ad (build energy toward weekend peak)
FRIDAY: Avant-garde or major statement (peak attention day)
SATURDAY: Indo-modern / cultural / festive (cultural anchor)
SUNDAY: Tender / reverent / closing the week (emotional resonance)
```

NOT mandatory — adapts per creator strategy. But the principle is: rotate registers across the week so audience never gets the same emotional flavor two days running.

### AF.3 — CONTENT PILLARS (FEED STRATEGY)

A creator's overall feed is anchored in 4-6 ongoing content pillars (different from wardrobe pillars):

CREATOR CONTENT PILLARS (recommended for Aira):
1. CULTURAL COMMENTARY (deep-research, trend deconstruction, "what's actually inside the trend")
2. PERSONAL POV (confessional, day-in-life, "what I'm thinking about")
3. BEAUTY & WELLNESS (skincare, fragrance, hair, ritual)
4. FASHION & STYLE (outfits, GRWM, fashion film)
5. CULTURAL HERITAGE (festivals, Indo-modern, family, traditions)
6. BRAND COLLAB / SPONSORED (clearly marked when applicable)

Across any 30-reel set: balance content pillars roughly 5-5-5-5-5-5 (avoid one pillar dominating).

### AF.4 — SERIES LOGIC

Some concepts span multiple reels — series. Series must follow:

SERIES RULES:
- Series declared explicitly at top of prompt: "SERIES: [name] — Episode N of M"
- Each episode self-contained but with shared CONCEPT BIBLE anchors
- Series anchored by: same color thread / same setting type / same emotional question across episodes
- Audience can enter at any episode without confusion
- Minimum 3 reels for a series, maximum 8 (longer loses audience)
- Episode 1 = strongest hook, Episode 3-4 = depth, final = payoff
- Series releases over 1-3 weeks (not all in one day)

### AF.5 — CONTENT-COLLAB STRATEGY

When brand collabs are scheduled:

COLLAB PLACEMENT RULES:
- Never two paid collabs back-to-back (alienates audience)
- Quiet pillar / personal POV reel between collabs
- Collab register matched to brand register (Pillar 11 for luxury / Pillar 3 for accessible)
- Disclosure ("Paid Partnership") never reduces creative quality

### AF.6 — INTEGRATION

The engine's batch generation (Stage X.14) amended to consider weekly rhythm and content pillar balance:

```
BATCH STRATEGY BLOCK (when generating multi-reel batches):
WEEKLY PLACEMENT: [Monday / Tuesday / Wednesday / etc. — informs register]
CONTENT PILLAR: [1-6 from AF.3]
SERIES STATUS: [standalone / Series Name Episode N of M]
COLLAB STATUS: [organic / paid partnership]
ADJACENCY CHECK: [verify previous and next reel registers contrast appropriately]
```

ENFORCEMENT RULE 38: BATCH GENERATION ENFORCES CONTENT PILLAR DIVERSITY. No single content pillar dominates more than 30% of any 10-reel set.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 39: SERIES REELS DECLARE EPISODE STATUS. Standalone vs. series flagged at top of prompt.

## PART AJ — THE COMPLETE ENFORCEMENT RULES (Master List)

For clarity, all enforcement rules consolidated:

01. No prompt skips the 12-stage pipeline.
02. No field in any block is left blank.
03. No pre-flight checkbox is forgiven.
04. No frame exists without full expansion.
05. No concept ships without fresh-generated opener + sign-off (if signature flag = FULL).
06. No batch ships without diversity check.
07. No prompt ships without negative block.
08. No wardrobe piece described vaguely.
09. No lighting described vaguely.
10. No voice line described vaguely.
11. No facial expression described vaguely.
12. No product performance move duplicated in one reel.
13. No camera move duplicated in one frame.
14. No stakes generic.
15. No GRWM ships without through-mirror frame.
16. No beauty ad ships without 3D camera move on hero product.
17. No mood piece ships without at least one silent frame.
18. No cinematic ad ships without named colorist/film reference.
19. No reel ships without 4-Voice Test passing.
20. No reel ships without Kinetic Stillness / Micro-Life layers.
21. No product or hero object ships without Complete Object Design Block.
22. No frame ships without three coordinated performers.
23. No frame ships with mannequin posture.
24. Every frame must answer "what was she doing 0.3 seconds before."
25. No Pillar 11 look ships without body-language amplification.
26. Pillar 11 necklines stay at editorial-restrained register.
27. No reel ships with undefined hair.
28. No hair concept repeats within 10-reel rotation window.
29. Avant-garde outfits require framing that reveals sculptural form.
30. Avant-garde outfits pair with avant-garde hair (HC-26 to HC-30).
31. No reel ships without Audio Block filled.
32. Audio mix levels declared per frame.
33. Silence is always deliberate.
34. Text never enters platform UI zones.
35. Text must add information not in VO or visual.
36. No reel ships without Cover Frame Block.
37. Cover frame must answer three questions in 0.3 seconds.
38. Batch generation enforces content pillar diversity.
39. Series reels declare episode status.
40. No reel ships without Color Grade Block.
41. No makeup look repeats within 10-reel window.

ALL 41 RULES ARE ABSOLUTE. No override.
