## PART Q.EXTENDED.II — GRWM 101% COMPLETENESS & FULL INTEGRATION

NOTE: Hair references now use Part AP library. Makeup references now use Part AQ library.


This part closes every gap in GRWM by integrating it with all post-v3.4 protocol additions: Hair (Part AA), Makeup (Part AH), Audio (Part AC), Color Grade (Part AG), Cover Frame (Part AE), Three-Performer Coordination (Part Z), Body-Language Fluency (Part Z.EXT), Object Design (Part Y), Hyper-Realistic Facial Dynamics (Part R.EXT). After this part, GRWM is fully production-complete with no remaining loopholes.

### Q.EXT.II.1 — GRWM × HAIR PROTOCOL (Part AA Integration)

GRWM hair has a unique trajectory: it CHANGES across the reel as part of the transformation arc. This is unlike any other format.

GRWM HAIR ARC (mandatory per GRWM reel):

FRAME 1 (Opening State) — UNDONE HAIR STATES (pick one):
- Wet from shower (towel-just-removed)
- Air-dried mess (overnight bedhead-styled)
- Towel-wrapped turban (white or cream, classic)
- Silk-towel hair wrap (heritage / luxury indoor)
- Damp from face-wash (slightly water-droplet)
- Loose low pony for prep (held back during skincare)
- Bedhead second-day (slept on, slightly flat one side)
- Wrapped in silk scarf at temples (heritage prep)

FRAMES 2-3 (Skincare/Base) — TRANSITIONAL HAIR STATES:
- Pulled back into claw-clip (working hands-free)
- Tucked behind both ears
- Center-parted and held back
- Half-clipped half-loose (one side worked already)

FRAME 4 (Pivot — when hair styling happens):
- MID-WORK HAIR STATE (hot tool / brush / clip in hand):
  * Sectioned with visible clips
  * Mid-curl on barrel
  * Mid-flat-iron stroke
  * Mid-blow-dry with brush
  * Mid-twist into final form

FRAMES 5-6 (Near-Complete / Reveal) — FINAL HAIR CONCEPT:
- Hair concept (HC-N) from Part AA library
- ROTATION RULE applies — not used in last 10 reels
- Pillar-matched to closing-state outfit pillar

FRAME 7 (Exit Beat):
- Hair settled, possibly hair-flip or hair-tuck signature beat

GRWM HAIR PRE-FLIGHT (added):
[ ] Hair Arc declared (opening state → transitional → mid-work → final concept)
[ ] Final hair concept (HC-N) selected per Part AA
[ ] Final hair concept matches closing-state pillar (per AA.4 matching)
[ ] Hair concept passes 10-reel rotation check
[ ] Mid-work hair state in Frame 4 specifies tool + technique
[ ] Hair behavior coordinated with Part Z subject performance moves

ENFORCEMENT RULE 42: GRWM REQUIRES FULL HAIR ARC (opening undone → mid-work → final concept). Static hair across all frames = FAIL. Same hair in Frame 1 as Frame 6 = FAIL.

### Q.EXT.II.2 — GRWM × MAKEUP PROTOCOL (Part AH Integration)

GRWM makeup also follows an arc — bare to complete — across frames.

GRWM MAKEUP ARC (mandatory per GRWM reel):

FRAME 1 (Opening State) — BARE-FACE STATE:
- Truly bare: no foundation, no concealer, no shaped brow, no mascara
- Real skin texture visible (pores readable, refined)
- Natural lash (no curl, no mascara)
- Bare lip (slight chap or natural pink, no liner, no color)
- Brow groomed but unfilled (natural shape, slight asymmetry)
- Skin condition: visible texture, possible under-eye softness, slight tired-fresh look
- NEVER glam-fake-bare (no contouring disguised as no-makeup)

FRAMES 2-3 (Skincare / Base) — BUILDING:
- Skincare visible on skin (toner sheen, serum droplet absorbing, moisturizer slight gloss)
- Then primer / SPF (slight sheen)
- Then foundation in early stages (partial coverage visible)
- Concealer dots visible at this point

FRAMES 3-5 (Build through Pivot) — PROGRESSION:
- Each frame shows visible delta in makeup completion
- Eyes done before lips (or vice versa, declare order)
- Cheek color appears
- Defined brow appears
- Mascara appears
- Highlight appears

FRAMES 5-6 (Near-Complete / Reveal) — FINAL MAKEUP LOOK:
- Makeup look (ML-N) from Part AH library
- ROTATION RULE applies — not used in last 10 reels
- Pillar-matched to closing-state outfit pillar

FRAME 7 (Exit Beat):
- Makeup fully set, possibly fragrance application visible (atomizer to neck)

GRWM MAKEUP PRE-FLIGHT (added):
[ ] Makeup Arc declared (bare → building → progression → final look)
[ ] Final makeup look (ML-N) selected per Part AH
[ ] Makeup look matches closing-state pillar (per AH.2 matching)
[ ] Makeup look passes 10-reel rotation check
[ ] Bare-face state in Frame 1 is REAL bare, not glam-fake-bare
[ ] Each frame shows visible makeup progression delta

ENFORCEMENT RULE 43: GRWM REQUIRES TRUE BARE-FACE FRAME 1. No foundation, no contour, no mascara, no shaped brow. Glam-fake-bare = FAIL.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 44: GRWM REQUIRES VISIBLE MAKEUP DELTA per progression frame. Frame 3 must show visibly more makeup than Frame 2.

### Q.EXT.II.3 — GRWM × IDENTITY LOCK (Bare-Face Frame 1 Specifics)

When Aira's face is bare in Frame 1, identity drift risk increases (no makeup means no shape-anchors). Lock these:

BARE-FACE IDENTITY ANCHORS:
- Same face geometry as makeup-on frames (jaw, eye spacing, nose bridge, lip shape, ear shape)
- Same skin tone (warm honey-to-caramel, golden undertone)
- Same hairline (no drift)
- Same brow shape (natural, ungroomed-yet)
- Same lip shape (defined cupid's bow, full)
- Eyes: same color, same size, same shape (almond, dark brown iris with amber flecks)
- Skin texture: real pores, slight under-eye softness, no blur
- Slight natural flush at apple-of-cheek (warm undertone visible)

BARE-FACE ANTI-DRIFT NEGATIVES:
"NEGATIVE: identity drift, different person, age drift younger, age drift older, plastic skin, doll-face, generic-bare-skin, oversmoothed, photoshopped, AI-bare, glam-fake-bare, contoured-as-bare"

ENFORCEMENT RULE 45: BARE-FACE FRAME 1 USES STRICTEST IDENTITY LOCK. Must read as the same Aira from any other reel — just bare. Identity must be lockable across thousands of reels even when bare-faced.

### Q.EXT.II.4 — GRWM × THREE-PERFORMER COORDINATION (Part Z Integration)

GRWM has all three performers in every frame — but the energy hierarchy is GRWM-specific.

GRWM ENERGY HIERARCHY DEFAULT (subject = HERO):
- SUBJECT 60% (HERO): Aira's body / face / story / hands
- PRODUCT 30% (SUPPORT): the products being applied
- BACKDROP 10% (AMBIENT): the setting (vanity / bathroom / bedroom)

This is the inverted hierarchy from beauty hero ads (where product is HERO). In GRWM, Aira is always hero — even in brand-collab reels.

GRWM SUBJECT MOVES PER FRAME (from Part Z.2):

FRAME 1 (Opening): S-7 Mirror Approach OR S-4 Down-Up-Eye-Contact OR S-8 Seated Descent OR S-10 Still-At-Window
FRAME 2 (First Application): S-5 Hand-Meet-Face OR S-21 Apply-With-Eyes-Closed OR S-20 Product-Present
FRAME 3 (Build): S-12 Reveal-Eye-Open OR S-15 Contemplative-Drift OR S-11 Duchenne Bloom (small) OR S-22 Camera-Interaction (lens-tap)
FRAME 4 (Pivot): S-14 Knowing Half-Smile OR S-17 Slow-Blink-Lock OR S-18 Lip-Press-Release OR S-26 Breath-Visible
FRAME 5 (Near-Complete): S-13 Suspended Laugh OR S-29 Fabric-Adjust OR S-27 Hair-Tuck-Behind-Ear OR S-28 Jewelry-Touch
FRAME 6 (Reveal): S-1 Slow-Reveal Turn OR S-9 Rise-From-Seated OR S-24 Turn-And-Settle
FRAME 7 (Exit Beat): S-6 Walk-Into-Frame (in reverse — walk-OUT-of-frame) OR S-30 Stillness-With-Micro-Life

GRWM PRODUCT MOVES PER FRAME:
- Frame 2-5 may include product performance moves (P-9 Self-Opening Cap, P-17 Hand-Catch Levitation, P-1 Slow Levitation Hover, etc.)
- Maximum ONE product performance move per reel (per existing rules)
- Reserved for HERO product (only one of the 3 max products gets the magical beat)

GRWM BACKDROP MOVES PER FRAME (from Part Z.3):
- B-1 God-Ray Sweep (all GRWM settings — light shaft from window)
- B-19 Steam-Rise (bathroom GRWM specifically)
- B-9 Sun-Shift-Patch (bedroom golden hour)
- B-27 Particle Concentration (any setting with key light)
- B-11 Curtain-Wind-Catch (bedroom / heritage settings)
- B-3 Caustic Dance (water glass on vanity)
- Backdrop always at 10% AMBIENT energy in GRWM

GRWM CHARM MOVE PLACEMENT:
- Maximum 1 charm move per GRWM reel
- Placed at Frame 4 (pivot) or Frame 5 (near-complete)
- Ideal charm moves for GRWM: CM-11 Hair-Piece-Hold, CM-19 Chin-On-Fist, CM-20 Temple-Rub, CM-23 Collar-Slip, CM-24 Ring-Twist, CM-25 Cup-Cradle, CM-28 Soft-Hand-Frame

ENFORCEMENT RULE 46: GRWM ENERGY HIERARCHY IS SUBJECT-HERO. Aira is always 60%. Product 30% max. Backdrop 10%. Inverting this for GRWM = format failure.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 47: GRWM SUBJECT MOVES MUST BE FROM PART Z.2 OR APPROVED FOR GRWM (per Q.EXT.II.4 mapping). Random posing without named move = FAIL.

### Q.EXT.II.5 — GRWM × BODY-LANGUAGE FLUENCY (Part Z.EXT Integration)

The 4 Body-Language Laws (Part Z.EXT.4) apply to EVERY GRWM frame:

LAW 1 — DEFAULT AIRA STANCE: Even when seated at vanity, weight distribution, hip position, shoulder drop apply. When seated: weight slightly to one hip, opposite shoulder dropped, spine S-curved (forward lean toward mirror common in GRWM), arms with elbow bend.

LAW 2 — IMPLIED MOTION: Every GRWM frame answers "what was she doing 0.3 seconds before."
- Frame 1: "She was looking down at her hand / she just exhaled / she just sat down at the vanity"
- Frame 2: "She just opened the bottle / she just dipped fingertip into product"
- Frame 3: "She just released the brush from skin / she just blinked"
- Frame 4: "She just spoke the pivot line / she just lowered her hand"
- Frame 5: "She just blotted lips / she just touched cheek for blush check"
- Frame 6: "She just stood up from vanity / she just adjusted strap"

LAW 3 — SMOOTH FLOW: All joints loose. Knees bent (3-7°). Elbows bent (5-30°). Wrists soft. Fingers in natural curve. No stiff product-grip.

LAW 4 — BODY OUTPACES FACE: Hands have already started moving toward face / product, head still arriving, eyes still landing, expression still forming.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 48: GRWM FRAMES OBEY ALL 4 BODY-LANGUAGE LAWS. Mannequin posture in any GRWM frame = FAIL.

### Q.EXT.II.6 — GRWM × HYPER-REALISTIC FACIAL DYNAMICS (Part R.EXT Integration)

GRWM is the most face-revealing format. Facial dynamics standards are the strictest here.

GRWM FACIAL DYNAMICS PER FRAME (mandatory minimum):

FRAME 1 (Bare face, intimate):
- Asymmetry: minimum 3 (eye openness, brow height, lip-corner pre-tension)
- Eyes: mid-blink OR catchlight at 10/2 o'clock OR slow-blink-recovery
- Lips: parted 1.5mm on inhale OR pre-smile tension
- Breath: visible chest rise / nostril micro-flare
- Skin: subsurface scattering visible (light penetrating ear, nose tip)

FRAMES 2-5 (Application):
- Eye state shifts per frame (closed during application / open during result-check / mid-blink during beat)
- Cheek apple-lift varies (pre-smile, mid-smile, post-smile)
- Lip state changes (pressed during concentration, parted during speech, mid-phoneme during VO)
- Brow micro-movements per frame (concentration furrow during application, relaxed post-completion)

FRAME 6 (Reveal):
- Confident expression with all sequencing intact (Duchenne smile from eyes-first OR knowing-half-smile asymmetric)
- Catchlight in iris from key light
- Glossy lower lip catching light at 10/2 position

FRAME 7 (Exit):
- Held expression OR fade-to-neutral (with breath still visible)

ENFORCEMENT RULE 49: GRWM FACIAL DYNAMICS MUST INCLUDE ALL OF: minimum 3 asymmetries per face frame / Duchenne sequencing on smile beats / breath visible in at least 4 of 6 frames / catchlight position declared per frame.

### Q.EXT.II.7 — GRWM × OBJECT DESIGN (Part Y Integration)

Every product Aira touches in GRWM gets a complete OBJECT DESIGN BLOCK (per Part Y).

For brand-collab GRWM:
- Maximum 3 hero products
- Each gets full Object Design Block specification
- Brand register matches GRWM intimacy (apothecary-warm, modern-minimalist, heritage-luxe)
- AVOID architectural-futurist register in GRWM (clashes with intimacy)
- AVOID extreme avant-garde packaging in GRWM (breaks lived-in feel)

For non-collab GRWM:
- Hero product can still be uniquely designed
- Or generic-brand-neutral acceptable (her own products, no specific brand emphasis)
- If brand-neutral: Object Design Block still specifies silhouette/material/finish to ensure uniqueness

ENFORCEMENT RULE 50: GRWM HERO PRODUCTS REQUIRE OBJECT DESIGN BLOCK. No generic "a bottle" or "a tube" in GRWM either.

### Q.EXT.II.8 — GRWM × AUDIO PROTOCOL (Part AC Integration)

GRWM audio is distinct from other formats. Key rules:

MUSIC SELECTION FOR GRWM:
- Slower tempo than other formats (90-115 BPM typical)
- Low-key, intimate, non-distracting
- Genre matched to GRWM register: lo-fi indie / soft electronic / acoustic / minimalist piano / R&B-slow / trending-audio-but-mellow
- NEVER big-drop EDM / aggressive bass / hyper-pop in GRWM (kills intimacy)
- Music plays at -12dB during VO frames, -6dB during VO-LESS frames (e.g., Frame 6 reveal)
- Music can build subtly through reel — same track, slight intensity ramp from Frame 1 to Frame 4 pivot

AMBIENT BED FOR GRWM (always present at -24 to -30dB):
- Indoor settings: room tone, faint AC hum, distant traffic, water-running (bathroom)
- Vanity: subtle metal-on-marble (jewelry shifting), product-against-surface tap
- Bathroom: water dripping, distant fan, steam-hiss
- Bedroom: window-air, fabric-rustle, distant city or birds

SFX FOR GRWM:
- Cap unscrew (P-9 product move pairs with this SFX)
- Brush stroke on skin (subtle)
- Pump click (foundation, serum)
- Atomizer hiss (perfume)
- Tissue rustle (blotting)
- Heel click on tile (Frame 7 exit on hard floor)
- Door click (Frame 7 exit)
- Single breath-catch (intimate moments)
- Hair clip snap-close (Frame 4 pivot if styling)

SILENCE BEATS IN GRWM:
- Hero visual frame — Frame 6 reveal often has 0.5s silence as music holds breath
- Pivot frame — Frame 4 sometimes has music ducked to silence for the line landing
- Exit beat — Frame 7 may end on silence + ambient only

ENFORCEMENT RULE 51: GRWM AUDIO BLOCK SPECIFIES: music genre / BPM / duck levels / ambient bed type / SFX per frame / silence frames declared.

### Q.EXT.II.9 — GRWM × COVER FRAME (Part AE Integration)

GRWM cover frame rules:

GRWM COVER FRAME SOURCE:
- USUALLY Frame 1 (vulnerability + intimacy = strongest hook for GRWM)
- OR Frame 4 pivot (most-quoted moment, expression peak)
- NEVER Frame 6 reveal (spoils the payoff)
- NEVER Frame 7 exit (no hook value)

GRWM COVER FRAME REQUIREMENTS:
- Aira's face dominant (60-80% of frame)
- Vulnerability or pivot moment
- Eye contact OR purposeful off-axis gaze
- Expression strong (knowing / pre-smile / mid-thought)
- Setting visible enough to register (vanity / bedroom / bathroom)
- Optional text overlay: stakes line in 3-5 words

GRWM COVER FRAME TEXT OVERLAY (when used):
- Stakes line snippet ("getting ready to confront her" / "the night I should have had last week")
- Question that hooks ("would you go alone?")
- Bilingual hook ("dekho... I'm going anyway")
- Placement: upper-third within hero zone
- Font: register-matched (Helvetica Light for clean / Italic Serif for editorial / hand-set for tender)

ENFORCEMENT RULE 52: GRWM COVER FRAME IS FRAME 1 OR FRAME 4. Never reveal-frame, never exit-frame. Spoils format.

### Q.EXT.II.10 — GRWM × COLOR GRADE (Part AG Integration)

GRWM color grade is intimate and unified across frames.

GRWM COLOR GRADE PRESET:
- Warm-toned overall (skin-priority warm-shift)
- Slight golden-hour warm in midtones
- Lifted blacks (intimate, never crushed)
- Skin protection on (no over-saturation of subject)
- Slight grain (Kodak Portra 400 reference) — never digital-clean
- Atmospheric haze rendered with slight bloom in highlights (golden-hour or window-light glow)
- Setting accent color (vanity wood / bathroom marble / bedroom curtain) slightly desaturated to keep skin priority

CROSS-FRAME COLOR CONSISTENCY:
- Same grade across all GRWM frames
- Slight intensity build (Frame 1 slightly cooler-vulnerable, Frame 6 slightly warmer-confident)
- Never color-grade-shift mid-reel (breaks continuity)

ENFORCEMENT RULE 53: GRWM COLOR GRADE IS UNIFIED across all frames. Skin-priority warm-shift mandatory. Crushed shadows = FAIL (kills intimacy).

### Q.EXT.II.11 — GRWM × PILLAR 11 (Sensual Editorial Celebrity Use)

Standard GRWM uses Pillars 1, 3, 4, 5, 8, 10 for closing state (intimate / lifestyle / heritage / evening / romantic / heritage).

PILLAR 11 IN GRWM — SPECIFIC USE CASES:
- "Getting ready for a red carpet event" GRWM
- "Getting ready for the Cannes-after-party I'm going alone to" GRWM
- "Getting ready for the hero brand-event premiere" GRWM
- "Getting ready for the cover-shoot" GRWM (meta-cover-shoot content)

When Pillar 11 used in GRWM:
- Closing-state outfit reveals are MORE DRAMATIC (Frame 6 reveal carries extra weight)
- Stakes must justify the elevation
- Body-language amplification (Pillar 11 rules) activates only at Frame 6 reveal — not during routine frames
- During routine frames, Aira is still in robe / slip / prep clothing
- Reveal frame transformation feels MORE earned because the elevation is dramatic

ENFORCEMENT RULE 54: PILLAR 11 IN GRWM REQUIRES STAKES JUSTIFICATION. "Getting ready for a regular evening" with Pillar 11 outfit = mismatch. Stakes must support the elevation.

### Q.EXT.II.12 — GRWM × AVANT-GARDE (Part AB Integration — EXCLUSION RULE)

GRWM NEVER uses Avant-Garde Override (Part AB). The format requires intimacy and lived-in realness; sculptural one-off fashion-as-art clothing breaks this.

EXCEPTION — META-GRWM: A reel where the concept IS "Aira getting ready in avant-garde for an editorial photoshoot" — but this is rare and must be flagged explicitly.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 55: GRWM FORBIDS AVANT-GARDE OVERRIDE except for meta-photoshoot concepts. Default GRWM uses Pillars 1-11 only.

### Q.EXT.II.13 — GRWM HINDI PLACEMENT (Specific Locations)

Per voice rules, GRWM uses 70% English / 30% Hindi (more Hindi-anchored than other formats due to intimacy).

EXACT HINDI PLACEMENTS (declared per GRWM reel):

PLACEMENT 1 — OPENING CONFESSION (Frame 1):
- Hindi anchor in opener line
- Examples: "Dekho... I'm going anyway." / "Suno, ek baat batati hoon." / "Bas, this is happening."

PLACEMENT 2 — PIVOT REALIZATION (Frame 4):
- Hindi anchor in pivot/decision line
- Examples: "Bas, decision ho gaya." / "Asli baat yeh hai..." / "Soch lo, samajh gaye?"

PLACEMENT 3 — SIGN-OFF (Frame 6 or 7):
- Hindi closer
- Examples: "Chalo." / "Theek hai." / "Yeh tha asli moment." / "Bas yahi."

ENFORCEMENT RULE 56: GRWM HINDI USAGE LANDS AT 3 EXACT PLACEMENTS (opening confession / pivot realization / sign-off). Random Hindi sprinkling = FAIL. No Hindi at any of the 3 = format failure (intimacy register weakened).

### Q.EXT.II.14 — GRWM SELECTIVE VOICE MODE

When GRWM uses SELECTIVE voice mode (some frames silent, some VO):

USE CASE: When the visual itself is doing all the talking — dramatic transformation reveal, peak emotional moment, post-pivot release.

CHOREOGRAPHY:
- Frames 1-3: VO present (story building)
- Frame 4 (pivot): VO present (pivot line lands)
- Frame 5: VO drops, only ambient + music (tension release through silence)
- Frame 6 (reveal): VO returns OR remains silent (depends on register)
- Frame 7: silent (visual seals it)

ENFORCEMENT RULE 57: GRWM SELECTIVE VOICE MODE DECLARES WHICH FRAMES ARE VO-LESS. Random silence = FAIL.

## CHECKPOINT 3.9 — GRWM 101% INTEGRATED (Q.EXT.II added)

## PART AK — STATE PERSISTENCE & CUMULATIVE CONTINUITY PROTOCOL

The single most failure-prone aspect of multi-frame AI generation: previously-applied state resetting between frames. If lipstick is on in Frame 3, it must still be on in Frame 4. If hair was towel-dried in Frame 2, it cannot revert to wet in Frame 3. This part enforces strict cumulative continuity — making every reel a single continuous timeline rather than a slideshow of related-but-independent images.

### AK.1 — THE PRINCIPLE

A reel is ONE continuous timeline. Every frame is a moment within that timeline. Once an element changes state (skin, hair, makeup, wardrobe, environmental position, prop placement), the new state PERSISTS forward — it cannot reset, cannot regress, cannot disappear unless an explicit reverse-change is shown.

This is how real continuity works. This is how the eye reads "same world, same moment, time passing." Without this protocol, AI generators reset elements between frames and the reel reads as discontinuous — multiple short scenes rather than one unfolding moment.

### AK.2 — THE STATE TRACKER

Every reel maintains a STATE TRACKER — a running ledger of every element's state at every frame. The engine declares this at Stage 08 and validates it at Stage 11.

STATE TRACKER STRUCTURE:

```
STATE TRACKER — [REEL CONCEPT NAME]

ELEMENT                  | F1 | F2 | F3 | F4 | F5 | F6 | F7
=========================|=====|=====|=====|=====|=====|=====|=====
SKIN STATE               | bare | toner | toner+ serum | + foundation | + concealer + blush | + highlight + setting | full
EYES STATE               | bare | bare | bare | primer | + shadow | + liner + mascara | full
LIPS STATE               | bare | bare | bare | bare | bare | + lipstick | + gloss
BROW STATE               | natural | natural | natural | natural | filled | filled + groomed | filled + groomed
HAIR STATE               | wet/towel | wet/towel | towel-dried | sectioned + heat tool | mostly styled | fully styled | fully styled
WARDROBE STATE           | robe | robe | robe | robe + earrings | + dress underlayer | + dress + heels | + dress + heels + bag
JEWELRY STATE            | none | none | none | earrings on | earrings + ring | full set | full set
FRAGRANCE STATE          | none | none | none | none | none | sprayed | sprayed
SETTING - VANITY ITEMS   | products closed | toner open | + serum open | + foundation open | + brushes scattered | + lipstick open | partially packed up
SETTING - LIGHTING       | morning soft | morning soft | morning soft | morning soft | golden afternoon | golden afternoon | golden afternoon (door open)
AIRA POSTURE             | seated leaning | seated forward | seated 3/4 turn | seated frontal | seated frontal | standing | walking
PROP - HEATED TOOL       | not visible | not visible | not visible | curling iron in hand active | iron set down warm | tool cooled | tool gone
PROP - PHONE             | face-down | face-down | face-down | face-down | face-down | screen up | in bag
```

EVERY ELEMENT IN FRAME GETS A ROW. Engine maintains the table internally.

### AK.3 — THE FORWARD-ONLY MOVEMENT RULE

Once an element changes state in any direction, it can only move FORWARD on the timeline:

PERMITTED:
- bare → toner (forward step)
- bare → toner → serum (cumulative forward)
- wet hair → towel-dried → fully styled (forward progression)
- robe → robe + earrings → robe + earrings + dress (additive)
- products closed → first product open → multiple products open (progressive)

FORBIDDEN:
- toner → bare (reset — illegal)
- foundation → no foundation (reset — illegal)
- styled hair → wet hair (reverse — illegal unless reverse-change is shown explicitly)
- earring on → earring off (regress — illegal unless removal beat is shown)
- product open → product closed (snap-back — illegal)

EXPLICIT REVERSE-CHANGE EXCEPTIONS (rare, declared):
- "Aira removes earring at Frame 5 to inspect" — earring state legitimately moves with the action shown
- "Aira blots lip with tissue" — lipstick state moves from "applied glossy" to "applied matte-blotted" (this is forward in finishing, not a reset)

ALL STATE CHANGES MUST HAVE A SHOWN MOTIVATION. No element changes off-screen.

### AK.4 — FRAME-TO-FRAME DIFF DECLARATION

Engine MUST declare per-frame, in the prompt itself:

```
FRAME N — STATE DIFF

PERSISTING FROM FRAME N-1 (must remain visible):
- [list every state element from previous frame that carries forward]
Example:
  - Skin: still has toner from Frame 2
  - Lips: still bare
  - Hair: still towel-wrapped
  - Wardrobe: still in robe
  - Setting: window light still 4 PM golden

NEW IN FRAME N (the change/delta):
- [the one or two visible additions/changes]
Example:
  - Skin: serum droplet added on cheekbone (newly applied)
  - Setting: serum bottle now open on vanity (was closed)

NOT-YET-IN-FRAME (will appear in later frames):
- [forward elements not yet introduced]
Example:
  - Foundation (Frame 4)
  - Lipstick (Frame 5)
  - Hair styling (Frame 4)
```

This DIFF DECLARATION goes into the actual generated prompt for the AI tool, so the model has explicit instructions to preserve previous-frame state.

### AK.5 — CONTINUITY NEGATIVES (per frame)

Every routine frame from Frame 2 onward gets continuity negatives auto-injected:

```
CONTINUITY NEGATIVE BLOCK (per frame N>=2):

NEGATIVE: skin reset to bare, makeup disappearance, hair reverting to wet,
hair reverting to undone, wardrobe disappearing, jewelry disappearing,
products closing back up off-screen, lipstick wiping off, foundation
vanishing, setting changing impossibly, lighting changing impossibly
without time-passage cue, props teleporting, identity drift between frames,
posture teleporting, wardrobe color change, hair length change, jewelry
substitution.
```

This is appended IN ADDITION TO the standard image/video negatives.

### AK.6 — THE SINGLE-TIMELINE PRINCIPLE

Every multi-frame reel is ONE continuous timeline. Rules:

1. TIME ALWAYS MOVES FORWARD between frames (chronological order)
2. NO FLASHBACKS unless explicitly framed (rare, requires visual cue)
3. EACH FRAME IS A MOMENT, NOT AN INDEPENDENT IMAGE
4. THE VIEWER CAN PAUSE BETWEEN FRAMES — but cannot rewind
5. WHAT WAS DONE STAYS DONE
6. WHAT WASN'T YET INTRODUCED STAYS NOT-YET-INTRODUCED
7. CONTINUITY OF STATE > CONTINUITY OF MOOD (mood can shift; state cannot regress)

### AK.7 — STATE PERSISTENCE PRE-FLIGHT CHECKS

Added to every multi-frame reel pre-flight:

```
[ ] State Tracker constructed for every element in reel
[ ] Forward-only movement verified per element across frames
[ ] Frame-to-Frame Diff declared per frame N>=2
[ ] Continuity Negatives appended per frame
[ ] No state regressions present
[ ] All state changes have shown motivation (no off-screen changes)
[ ] Identity locked across all frames
[ ] Posture transitions logical (no teleporting)
[ ] Setting elements track consistently (props don't appear/disappear)
[ ] Lighting transitions logical (golden hour stays golden, doesn't reset to morning)
```

### AK.8 — THE GRWM-SPECIFIC STATE LAWS

GRWM is the highest-stakes format for state persistence because of the visible transformation arc.

LAW 1 — ANY MAKEUP APPLIED IN FRAME N MUST PERSIST FOREVER FORWARD
- Concealer applied Frame 2 = visible in Frames 3, 4, 5, 6, 7
- Lipstick applied Frame 5 = visible in Frames 6, 7
- Mascara applied Frame 4 = visible in Frames 5, 6, 7

LAW 2 — HAIR ARC PROGRESSES STRICTLY FORWARD
- Frame 1: wet/towel-wrapped/undone
- Frame 2-3: transitional (clipped, sectioned, partial dry)
- Frame 4: mid-styling (heat tool active, sections released)
- Frame 5: mostly styled, finishing
- Frame 6: fully styled
- Frame 7: fully styled (slight movement from walking, never resetting)

LAW 3 — WARDROBE BUILDS ADDITIVELY
- Frame 1: robe / towel / slip
- Robe stays until wardrobe change beat is shown
- New garments added cumulatively
- Final outfit complete by Frame 6

LAW 4 — PRODUCTS PROGRESS FROM CLOSED TO OPEN TO USED
- Each product introduced ONCE
- Once opened, stays open until reel ends or close-it beat shown
- Used products accumulate on vanity surface
- By Frame 5-6: vanity should look LIVED IN, not pristine

LAW 5 — LIGHTING SHIFTS WITH TIME
- If reel implies time passing (morning → afternoon), light naturally shifts
- Golden hour deepening across frames is acceptable (forward time)
- Random light changes between frames = FAIL

LAW 6 — IDENTITY ABSOLUTELY PERSISTS
- Same face across all frames (no drift)
- Same body proportions (no drift)
- Same skin tone, freckles, moles, asymmetries
- Bare-face Frame 1 must be recognizably the SAME PERSON as Frame 6 made-up

ENFORCEMENT RULE 58: STATE PERSISTENCE IS ABSOLUTE. Any element shown in Frame N must persist through Frame N+1, N+2... unless an explicit reverse-change beat is shown. Reset = FAIL = REWRITE.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 59: FRAME-TO-FRAME DIFF MUST BE DECLARED per frame N>=2 in the actual generation prompt.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 60: CONTINUITY NEGATIVES APPENDED to every routine frame.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 61: GRWM STATE TRACKER IS MANDATORY. Skin / Eyes / Lips / Brow / Hair / Wardrobe / Jewelry / Fragrance / Setting / Posture / Props all tracked across all frames.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 62: NO MAKEUP APPLIED IN ANY GRWM FRAME MAY DISAPPEAR IN A SUBSEQUENT FRAME. Once on, always on.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 63: HAIR STATE PROGRESSES STRICTLY FORWARD. Wet cannot become dry without a shown drying beat. Styled cannot become unstyled.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 64: WARDROBE BUILDS ADDITIVELY. Garments do not vanish or substitute between frames.

### AK.9 — STATE PERSISTENCE GUARANTEE

When the engine generates a multi-frame reel with State Persistence Protocol active:

✓ Every element in every frame is tracked across the reel
✓ Forward-only state movement enforced
✓ Frame-to-Frame Diff declared per frame in actual prompt
✓ Continuity negatives appended per frame
✓ Identity locked across all frames
✓ Makeup applied in Frame N is visible in Frame N+1, N+2, N+3...
✓ Hair arc progresses strictly forward
✓ Wardrobe builds additively
✓ Products track from closed → open → used cumulatively
✓ Lighting transitions logically with time-passage cues
✓ Setting elements maintain continuous physical placement
✓ Reel reads as ONE continuous timeline rather than slideshow

The reel becomes literal storytelling — every frame is a moment within a continuous flow, every state visible to the viewer is a result of what happened in earlier frames, and the audience experiences the transformation as a real lived sequence rather than disconnected images.

## PART AL — FRAME HANDOFF CONTINUITY PROTOCOL

State persistence (Part AK) ensures elements don't disappear between frames. This part goes one critical step further: every frame begins EXACTLY where the previous frame ended. Frame 2 starts at the precise physical position Frame 1 closed on. Frame 3 starts at the precise position Frame 2 closed on. The reel reads as one continuous performance, stitched together at the cut points.

This is action continuity — what cinematography calls "matching action" at the edit point. Without it, multi-frame reels read as a slideshow even when state persists.

### AL.1 — THE PRINCIPLE

Frame N+1 begins where Frame N ends.

If Frame N closes with:
- Aira's right hand raised toward her cheek
- Eyes mid-blink at 70% closed
- Lip parted on a held breath
- Body in 3/4 turn, weight on left leg, hip popped
- Curling iron in left hand, mid-section curl
- Light in shaft from camera-left at golden hour
- Dust motes drifting upward leftward

Then Frame N+1 must open with EXACTLY THESE SAME STATES — same hand position, same blink phase (or completing it within the first 0.2s), same breath continuing, same body posture, same tool in same hand, same light, same particle drift. Then the action continues forward from there.

The viewer should not be able to tell where the cut happened. The reel should feel like one breath, one continuous motion, broken only by deliberate camera moves or angle changes.

### AL.2 — THE CLOSING-FRAME SPECIFICATION

Every frame DECLARES its CLOSING STATE — what the final 0.5 seconds of the frame contains. This is then the OPENING STATE of the next frame.

CLOSING STATE BLOCK (mandatory per frame N where N is not the last frame):

```
FRAME N — CLOSING STATE (final 0.5 seconds — handoff to Frame N+1)

POSITION:
- Body posture: [exact — seated 3/4 turn, weight 60/40 on left leg, etc.]
- Hand positions: [left hand exact / right hand exact]
- Head position: [tilt angle / direction faced]
- Eye state: [open / mid-blink at X% / closed / mid-shift to direction]
- Lip state: [closed / parted N mm / mid-phoneme of word X / smile partial]

OBJECTS IN HAND:
- Right hand: [exact object held, exact grip]
- Left hand: [exact object held, exact grip]

OBJECTS IN MOTION:
- [any moving element and its direction/state at the close moment]

ATMOSPHERIC STATE:
- Light position: [shaft direction, intensity]
- Particles: [drift direction at close]
- Hair state: [position/motion at close]
- Fabric state: [drape/motion at close]

VOICE STATE:
- VO: [completed line / mid-word / silent / breath]
- Music: [playing at -X dB / ducked / silent]
- Ambient: [continuing]

THE CLOSING ACTION:
- The micro-action being completed at this exact moment
- What happens NEXT (immediately into Frame N+1)
```

### AL.3 — THE OPENING-FRAME SPECIFICATION

Every frame N+1 DECLARES its OPENING STATE — which must MATCH Frame N's CLOSING STATE exactly in the first 0.2 seconds, then proceed forward.

OPENING STATE BLOCK (mandatory per frame N+1):

```
FRAME N+1 — OPENING STATE (first 0.2 seconds — handoff from Frame N)

INHERITED FROM FRAME N CLOSING STATE:
- Body posture: [identical to Frame N close]
- Hand positions: [identical]
- Head position: [identical]
- Eye state: [identical, completing from Frame N close phase]
- Lip state: [identical, continuing]
- Objects in hand: [identical]
- Objects in motion: [continuing motion]
- Light position: [identical]
- Particles: [continuing drift]
- Hair state: [continuing motion if mid-flick, settled if held]
- Fabric state: [continuing]

ACTION CONTINUES FROM HERE:
- Frame N+1's action begins at 0.2s, building forward from the inherited state
```

### AL.4 — ACCEPTABLE DISCONTINUITIES (rare, deliberate)

Some discontinuities ARE acceptable — but they must be deliberate cinematic choices, declared explicitly:

ACCEPTABLE 1 — DELIBERATE CUT (camera angle change, time-passage suggestion):
- Frame closes mid-action
- Frame N+1 opens at slightly later moment with logical time-skip
- Time-skip must be small (1-3 seconds) and CONSISTENT WITH STATE PROGRESSION
- Example: Frame 3 closes with mascara wand approaching lash; Frame 4 opens with mascara now applied to lashes (1-2 seconds skipped, continuity preserved through state)

ACCEPTABLE 2 — MATCH CUT:
- Frame closes on one matching shape/motion
- Frame N+1 opens on a different element with the same visual shape/motion
- Used for poetic transitions

ACCEPTABLE 3 — ANGLE CUT WITH SAME-TIME:
- Frame N is over-shoulder shot
- Frame N+1 is reverse angle showing same instant from different camera position
- Hand positions, posture, eye-line all match — only camera moved

ACCEPTABLE 4 — MAJOR SCENE TRANSITION (only at Frame 6 → Frame 7 in GRWM):
- Frame 6: Aira in vanity reveal, full transformation visible
- Frame 7: Aira at door, walking out
- Time has passed — she has left vanity and crossed room
- This is the only acceptable major time-skip in GRWM, because the exit beat IS a scene change

### AL.5 — UNACCEPTABLE DISCONTINUITIES

UNACCEPTABLE — STATE TELEPORT:
- Frame closes with hand raised; next frame opens with hand at side (no transition shown)
- Frame closes mid-blink; next frame opens with eyes wide open (no completion shown)
- Frame closes with subject seated; next frame opens with subject standing (no rise shown)
- Frame closes with mascara wand approaching lash; next frame opens with lipstick already on lips (skipping the in-between)

UNACCEPTABLE — POSTURE RESET:
- Frame closes with body in dramatic 3/4 turn; next frame opens with body frontal (no turn motivation)
- Frame closes with hip popped; next frame opens square stance

UNACCEPTABLE — OBJECT TELEPORT:
- Curling iron in hand at frame close; gone in next frame's open without set-down shown
- Lipstick on vanity Frame N; in hand Frame N+1 without pickup motion

UNACCEPTABLE — LIGHTING SNAP:
- Golden hour at Frame N close; afternoon white light at Frame N+1 open
- Practical lit at Frame N close; dark at Frame N+1 open

UNACCEPTABLE — PARTICLE FREEZE:
- Dust motes drifting upward at Frame N close; same exact mote positions at Frame N+1 open (frozen) instead of continuing drift

### AL.6 — THE HANDOFF DECLARATION FORMAT

Engine writes the handoff specifically into the prompt for adjacent frames:

```
HANDOFF: FRAME N → FRAME N+1

FRAME N (closing 0.5s):
- Right hand mid-rise toward face, fingertip 2cm from cheekbone
- Eyes 30% closed in slow-blink phase
- Body seated, 3/4 turn camera-left, weight on left hip
- Lip parted 1.5mm on inhale
- Music at -12dB, ambient continuing
- Light: golden window-key from camera-left, shaft visible with dust motes drifting upward
- Hair: damp tendrils settled on right shoulder, slight motion continuing

FRAME N+1 (opening 0.2s — INHERITED):
- Right hand at exact 2cm from cheekbone (continuing rise)
- Eyes completing slow-blink (closing the remaining 70% within 0.2s)
- Body identical 3/4 turn, weight identical
- Lip identical parted 1.5mm
- Music continues at -12dB
- Light continues from camera-left
- Hair continues settling

THEN at 0.2s+ the new frame's action begins:
- Fingertip lands on cheekbone (skin compression visible at touch)
- Eyes complete blink, reopen
- New beat begins
```

This handoff declaration is appended directly into the generation prompt for both frames so the AI tool has explicit instructions to maintain continuity at the cut.

### AL.7 — VOICE/AUDIO HANDOFF

Audio also has handoff continuity:

VOICE HANDOFF:
- If Aira is mid-sentence at Frame N close: Frame N+1 picks up the sentence
- If Aira is between sentences: silence carries across, then next thought begins
- If Aira is mid-word (rare): word completes within first 0.3s of Frame N+1
- VO never restarts

MUSIC HANDOFF:
- Music level at Frame N close = music level at Frame N+1 open
- Musical phrase continues (not restarts) across the cut
- If music ducked at Frame N close: stays ducked at Frame N+1 open until VO ends
- BPM and key continue without break

AMBIENT HANDOFF:
- Ambient bed continues unchanged across all cuts
- Room tone level remains consistent
- Specific ambient elements (water dripping, traffic distant) maintain rhythm

SFX HANDOFF:
- If an SFX is mid-play at Frame N close: continues into Frame N+1
- If new SFX hits in Frame N+1: lands at appropriate beat, never random

### AL.8 — THE CONTINUOUS-PERFORMANCE TEST

Before any reel ships, the engine runs the CONTINUOUS-PERFORMANCE TEST:

Read all frames as one continuous timeline. Check:
- Could this be played as one unbroken video? Yes / No
- Are there any teleports? Any state resets? Any unexplained changes?
- If you removed all frame-cut markers, would the action still flow? Yes / No

If any answer fails — REWRITE the failing handoff.

### AL.9 — HANDOFF PRE-FLIGHT (additional checks)

Added to the master pre-flight:

```
[ ] CLOSING STATE declared per frame N (where N is not last frame)
[ ] OPENING STATE declared per frame N+1 (matches closing state)
[ ] All position/posture/object/eye/lip/light states match across handoffs
[ ] Voice continues without restarts
[ ] Music continues without restarts
[ ] Ambient bed continues
[ ] No teleports detected
[ ] No state regressions detected
[ ] Continuous-Performance Test passed
[ ] Major scene transitions (if any) explicitly justified
```

### AL.10 — GRWM-SPECIFIC HANDOFFS

GRWM cuts are particularly sensitive because intimacy depends on continuity.

GRWM HANDOFF EXAMPLES:

FRAME 1 → FRAME 2 (opening to first application):
- Frame 1 closes: Aira's right hand has just tucked hair behind right ear, eyes locked to camera, breath held
- Frame 2 opens: same hand still near ear (releasing strand), eyes still locked, breath releasing, then hand begins reaching for serum bottle

FRAME 2 → FRAME 3 (first application to build):
- Frame 2 closes: Aira's fingertip just released from cheekbone after pressing serum, eyes returning to mirror
- Frame 3 opens: fingertip still descending, eyes completing return to mirror, then new product picked up

FRAME 3 → FRAME 4 (build to pivot):
- Frame 3 closes: Aira mid-application of foundation with sponge, head turning slightly toward mirror, eyes drifting
- Frame 4 opens: head completing the turn, sponge moving away from face, eyes locking onto camera mid-rotation, then she sets down sponge, picks up lipstick (the pivot beat begins)

FRAME 4 → FRAME 5 (pivot to near-complete):
- Frame 4 closes: lipstick application complete, lips pressed together to set color, breath held
- Frame 5 opens: lips releasing the press, breath releasing, hand setting down lipstick, then new product (mascara) reached for

FRAME 5 → FRAME 6 (near-complete to reveal):
- Frame 5 closes: mascara wand pulling away from upper lashes, eyes opening
- Frame 6 opens: eyes fully opened, wand setting down on vanity, then Aira begins to rise from vanity (this is where the camera pulls back)

FRAME 6 → FRAME 7 (reveal to exit — major scene transition allowed):
- Frame 6 closes: Aira fully composed, slow turn complete, looking at camera with half-smile
- Frame 7 opens: Aira mid-stride toward door (acceptable scene transition — small time skip implicit, she walked from vanity to door)

ENFORCEMENT RULE 65: EVERY ADJACENT FRAME PAIR DECLARES HANDOFF — Frame N closing state matches Frame N+1 opening state.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 66: NO TELEPORTS BETWEEN FRAMES — body position, hand position, head position, eye state, lip state, objects, light, hair, fabric all flow continuously.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 67: VOICE/MUSIC/AMBIENT CONTINUE WITHOUT RESTARTS at frame cuts.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 68: MAJOR SCENE TRANSITIONS REQUIRE EXPLICIT JUSTIFICATION (typically only Frame 6 → Frame 7 in GRWM).

ENFORCEMENT RULE 69: CONTINUOUS-PERFORMANCE TEST MUST PASS — reel reads as one unbroken performance when frames are played sequentially.

### AL.11 — THE LITERAL STORYTELLING GUARANTEE

Combined with State Persistence (Part AK), this protocol delivers:

✓ Every state persists forward (Part AK)
✓ Every position/motion handoffs across cuts (Part AL)
✓ Frame N+1 begins exactly where Frame N ends
✓ Body, hands, eyes, lips, breath all continue without reset
✓ Objects in hand carry across cuts unless visibly set down
✓ Voice continues without restart
✓ Music continues without restart
✓ Ambient continues without break
✓ Light continues without snap-change
✓ Particles continue drifting
✓ Hair continues motion
✓ Fabric continues motion
✓ Reel reads as ONE continuous performance — frame cuts are invisible

The reel becomes literal storytelling at the highest level — not just state persistence (lipstick stays on) but motion-and-position continuity (the action that ended Frame 1 IS the action that begins Frame 2). The viewer experiences the reel as a single breath, a single performance, never broken.

This is what cinematography calls **invisible editing** — the highest form of multi-frame craft.

## PART Q.EXTENDED.III — GRWM DURATION STANDARDS

The strategic length range for GRWM reels, locked to maximize completion rate, save rate, and algorithmic distribution while preserving the format's intimacy and narrative integrity.

### Q.EXT.III.1 — THE STRATEGIC DURATION RANGE

```
GRWM CANONICAL DURATION:    40-56 seconds (DEFAULT — 80% of GRWM output)
GRWM WORKING BAND:          32-64 seconds (full operational range)
GRWM HARD FLOOR:            32 seconds (below this, format breaks)
GRWM HARD CEILING:          64 seconds (above without exceptional cause = REWRITE)
GRWM ABSOLUTE MAXIMUM:      90 seconds (only milestone/festival/once-a-quarter)
ENGINE DEFAULT:             48 seconds = 6-8 frames × 8 seconds each
```

### Q.EXT.III.2 — WHY THIS RANGE

THE 40-56s ZONE IS WHERE:
- Algorithm completion rate stays above 70% (peak distribution)
- Save rate is highest (viewers archive to re-watch)
- Re-watch rate is highest (viewers loop the reel)
- Top-performing creator GRWMs cluster (Hailey Bieber, Alix Earle, Diipa Khosla, Komal Pandey)
- Indian and Western audiences both behave well (no regional drop-off)

BELOW 32 SECONDS:
- Transformation arc visibly compressed (skips beats)
- Stakes don't have time to land
- Format reads as teaser, not GRWM
- Parasocial intimacy not built

ABOVE 64 SECONDS WITHOUT JUSTIFICATION:
- Completion rate drops below 50% (algorithm penalty)
- Viewer feels reel "should have ended"
- Save-rate doesn't compensate for completion-rate loss

### Q.EXT.III.3 — STAKES-TIER DURATION MAPPING

LIGHT STAKES TIER — 32-40s (4-5 frames):
Examples: "Getting ready for casual brunch" / "Getting ready while overthinking a text" / "Getting ready for a regular Wednesday meeting"
Charm-driven, lighter emotional arc, faster cadence
Use: 25% of GRWM output

MEDIUM STAKES TIER — 40-48s (5-6 frames) — DEFAULT:
Examples: "Getting ready for the dinner where I'll see him" / "Getting ready for the launch event" / "Getting ready for first dinner with his parents"
Standard transformation arc with full pivot beat
Use: 50% of GRWM output (THE STANDARD)

HEAVY STAKES TIER — 48-56s (6-7 frames):
Examples: "Getting ready to confront her" / "Getting ready for the first event after the breakup" / "Getting ready for the family dinner where I have to tell them"
Full arc with extended pivot, longer pivot-line beats, exit beat
Use: 20% of GRWM output

EMOTIONAL / HERITAGE / MILESTONE TIER — 56-64s (7-8 frames):
Examples: "Getting ready for Karwa Chauth alone this year" / "Getting ready for the wedding I almost didn't attend" / "Getting ready for the Cannes after-party walking in alone"
Reverent register, deeper silences, extended reveal
Use: 5% of GRWM output (special occasions)

### Q.EXT.III.4 — FRAME BUDGET TABLE (8s frames)

```
| Frames | Duration | Stakes Tier              |
|========|==========|==========================|
| 4      | 32s      | LIGHT                    |
| 5      | 40s      | LIGHT-MEDIUM             |
| 6      | 48s      | MEDIUM (DEFAULT)         |
| 7      | 56s      | MEDIUM-HEAVY             |
| 8      | 64s      | HEAVY-EMOTIONAL          |
```

ABOVE 8 FRAMES (>64s) — RARE EXCEPTION with explicit justification only.
Maximum 90 seconds. Never exceeded.

### Q.EXT.III.5 — INTERNAL PACING WITHIN DEFAULT ZONE

OPENING (Frame 1) — 8 seconds — 17% of reel
- 0-2s: opener + breath
- 2-5s: stakes line
- 5-8s: held eye contact / settle

MIDDLE FRAMES (Frames 2-4 or 5) — 24-32 seconds — 50-58% of reel
- Routine + voice continuation each
- Pivot frame (Frame 4) extended internal pause (1-2s held silence)

REVEAL + EXIT (Frames 5-6 or 6-7) — 8-16 seconds — 17-29% of reel
- Reveal frame: composed beat + payoff
- Exit beat: walk-out + sign-off + silence

### Q.EXT.III.6 — DURATION-AUDIO COORDINATION

32-40s GRWM: track hook within first 8s, one full vocal phrase, quick fade-out
40-48s GRWM: two phrase cycles, build-up implied, standard duck-and-lift
48-56s GRWM: emotional build (intensity ramp Frame 1 → Frame 4), pivot may have music-drop-to-silence, reveal lands on musical peak
56-64s GRWM: extended ducks during VO, longer silence beats, exit fades over 4-5s

### Q.EXT.III.7 — ENGINE INTEGRATION

STAGE 04 amended:
```
DURATION BLOCK (mandatory per GRWM):
STAKES TIER: [LIGHT / MEDIUM / HEAVY / EMOTIONAL-MILESTONE]
TOTAL DURATION: [N seconds]
FRAME COUNT: [4-8]
FRAME DURATION: [default 8s]
JUSTIFICATION (if outside default): [explicit reason]
```

PRE-FLIGHT additions:
[ ] Stakes tier declared
[ ] Duration matches tier per Q.EXT.III.3
[ ] Frame count within 4-8 (or justified for >8)
[ ] Duration within 32-64s band (or justified for >64s)
[ ] Pacing rhythm correctly distributed

ENFORCEMENT RULE 70: GRWM DURATION STAYS WITHIN 32-64 SECOND WORKING BAND. Outside without justification = REWRITE.
ENFORCEMENT RULE 71: GRWM STAKES TIER MUST MATCH DURATION. Heavy stakes in 32s = fails. Light stakes in 64s = fails.
ENFORCEMENT RULE 72: GRWM DEFAULT IS 48 SECONDS (6-8 frames × 8s). Engine selects this when no specific tier signal given.

### Q.EXT.III.8 — DURATION GUARANTEE

Every GRWM produced now satisfies:
✓ Within 32-64s working band (40-56s default)
✓ Frame count 4-8 (5-7 default)
✓ Duration matched to stakes tier
✓ 8-second frames as engine preference
✓ Pacing distributed correctly
✓ Audio coordinated with duration
✓ Algorithm performance optimized (>70% completion rate target)
✓ Save-rate and re-watch-rate maximized
✓ Top-creator length-tier alignment

GRWM duration is strategically locked.

## PART AM — ACCESSORIES LOCK PROTOCOL

Accessories carry signature weight. They appear, disappear, and persist across reels at a level demanding explicit tracking, parallel to the wardrobe and identity locks.

### AM.1 — THE PRINCIPLE

Accessories fail in four specific ways across AI generation: appearing out of thin air mid-reel, changing between frames, mismatching register (heritage jhumkas with futurist outfit), and lacking design specificity. The Accessories Lock fixes all four through structured tracking, design specification, and rotation enforcement.

### AM.2 — THE ACCESSORIES INVENTORY

Every reel declares an ACCESSORIES INVENTORY at Stage 05. Every accessory is named, designed, placed:

```
ACCESSORIES INVENTORY (mandatory per reel):

EARRINGS:
- TYPE: [stud / hoop / drop / chandelier / threader / cuff / jhumka / bali / huggies]
- SIZE: [micro 2-4mm / small 6-10mm / medium 12-20mm / statement 25mm+]
- METAL: [gold yellow / gold rose / gold antique / silver / chrome / platinum / brass / mixed]
- STONE/DETAIL: [diamond / pearl / ruby / emerald / kundan / meenakari / no stone / enameled]
- ASYMMETRY: [matched pair / asymmetric pair / single (one ear only)]
- DESIGN ERA: [classical / Art Deco / 70s / contemporary / heritage Indian / modernist]

NECKLACE:
- TYPE: [delicate chain / collar / pendant / choker / multi-strand / lariat / heritage / bib / Y-chain / no necklace]
- LENGTH: [16" / 18" / 20" / 24" / longer]
- METAL: [matched-or-contrast to earrings]
- PENDANT/DETAIL: [exact piece — single diamond / locket / charm / heritage motif]

BRACELET / BANGLE:
- TYPE: [tennis / cuff / chain / charm / bangle stack / heritage / single / paired wrist / no bracelet]
- SIZE: [thin / medium / chunky]
- METAL: [matched]
- WRIST: [left / right / both]

RING(S):
- COUNT: [0 / 1 / 2 / stack of 3-4 / multiple stacked]
- FINGERS: [exact fingers — index L / middle L / ring R / etc.]
- TYPES: [solitaire / signet / band / cocktail / heritage / charm]
- METAL: [matched]

WATCH:
- TYPE: [no watch / classic dress watch / sport / heritage / smart-watch styled]
- BRAND-NEUTRAL OR NAMED: [generic-luxury / branded for collab]
- METAL/STRAP: [leather / metal bracelet / mesh / fabric]
- WRIST: [left typically; right if signature beat]

BAG / CLUTCH:
- TYPE: [clutch envelope / box clutch / minaudière / shoulder / tote / crossbody / no bag]
- SIZE: [evening / day / oversized]
- MATERIAL: [leather / satin / sequined / embellished / metallic]
- COLOR: [matched / hero contrast]

EYEWEAR:
- TYPE: [no eyewear / sunglasses / optical glasses]
- FRAME: [aviator / cat-eye / oversized / round / geometric / wireframe / no frame]
- LENS: [tinted / clear / mirrored / gradient]
- COLOR: [tortoise / black / metal / clear acetate / colored]

HAIR ACCESSORY:
- TYPE: [no hair accessory / silk scarf / pearl pin / fresh flower / vintage barrette / claw clip / maang tikka / hair chain / metallic cuff / sculptural pin]
- PLACEMENT: [exact location — temple / crown / nape / tucked behind ear]

BELT (if pillar requires):
- TYPE: [thin metal-buckle / wide statement / heritage embroidered / corset]
- METAL/MATERIAL: [leather / silk / metallic / fabric]

OTHER:
- Brooch / Anklet / Toe ring / Body chain — specify only if culturally significant
```

### AM.3 — ACCESSORIES PILLAR MATCHING

EVERY ACCESSORY MATCHES OUTFIT PILLAR REGISTER:

PILLAR 1 (Modern Minimalist Luxe): delicate gold (16-18" chain, small studs, signet ring); max 2 statement; no heritage motifs
PILLAR 2 (Editorial Bold): architectural sculptural earrings OR oversized statement; one bold ring OR one bold cuff (never both)
PILLAR 3 (Effortless Day): layered delicate gold, dainty rings stack, canvas/raffia bag, simple watch
PILLAR 4 (Indo-Modern Fusion): heritage reimagined — jhumkas / kundan layered, maang tikka, statement nath, bangles, embroidered juttis, potli/modern clutch
PILLAR 5 (Evening Defined): statement earrings OR statement bracelet (one hero); small embellished clutch; one bold ring
PILLAR 6 (Sculpted Active): minimal — small studs, delicate chain, sleek smartwatch, cap, small leather sling
PILLAR 7 (Street Edge): layered chains (silver-toned), oversized shades, multiple ear piercings, statement watch, structured backpack
PILLAR 8 (Romantic Ethereal): delicate gold/rose-gold, small pearl studs, fresh florals; soft metals only
PILLAR 9 (Architectural Futurist): SINGULAR sculptural piece — one geometric earring OR bold cuff OR futuristic shades
PILLAR 10 (Warm Heritage): vintage gold (signet rings, charm bracelets, antique chains), silk neckscarf, tortoiseshell sunglasses, leather-strap watch
PILLAR 11 (Sensual Editorial Celebrity): statement earrings OR statement bracelet (ONE hero — celebrity rule); small clutch; one bold ring max; minimal hair accessories
AVANT-GARDE: singular sculptural piece OR none

### AM.4 — ACCESSORIES STATE PERSISTENCE (Part AK Integration)

Accessories obey State Persistence:
- Worn in Frame N must persist through Frame N+1, N+2... unless removal beat shown
- Cannot substitute (same earrings throughout, never different next frame)
- New accessories appear only via shown wearing-on beat
- Earrings put on Frame 4 = visible Frames 5, 6, 7

### AM.5 — ACCESSORIES IN GRWM CONTEXT

GRWM has accessories APPEARING during reel — not on at Frame 1, fully on by Frame 6.

GRWM ACCESSORY ARC:
- FRAME 1: No jewelry on body; visible on vanity/tray (laid out, sparkles in light)
- FRAMES 2-3: Some pieces start appearing (one earring slipping in, ring slipped on)
- FRAME 4: Earrings being put in (mirror-check beat)
- FRAME 5: Full set appearing on body
- FRAME 6 (Reveal): All accessories complete on body
- FRAME 7 (Exit): Bag added, fragrance applied (last beats)

Engine declares WHICH frame each accessory enters body.

### AM.6 — ACCESSORIES PRE-FLIGHT

[ ] Accessories Inventory complete for reel
[ ] All accessories pillar-matched
[ ] Asymmetry/matched-pair specified per accessory
[ ] Design fields filled (type, size, metal, stone, era)
[ ] State Persistence applied (no teleporting between frames)
[ ] GRWM-specific: accessory arc declared (which frame each piece enters body)
[ ] Maximum 3 statement pieces per look (Pillar 11 max 2)
[ ] Hero accessory category declared

ENFORCEMENT RULE 73: ACCESSORIES INVENTORY MANDATORY. Generic accessories ("earrings") forbidden. Each piece designed.
ENFORCEMENT RULE 74: ACCESSORIES PILLAR-MATCHED. Cross-register accessories forbidden unless intentional Indo-fusion.
ENFORCEMENT RULE 75: ACCESSORIES PERSIST FORWARD. Once worn, visible in all subsequent frames.
ENFORCEMENT RULE 76: ASYMMETRIC vs MATCHED PAIR DECLARED. Mismatched left/right without intent = FAIL.
ENFORCEMENT RULE 77: GRWM ACCESSORY ARC TRACKED. Each accessory's "frame of entry" specified.

## PART AN — GRWM SUBCONSCIOUS MOVEMENTS LIBRARY

The small unconscious-feeling beats that make Aira read as a real person being filmed rather than a subject performing. These live BETWEEN named subject moves and charm moves — connective tissue of being-alive-and-getting-ready.

### AN.1 — THE PRINCIPLE

A GRWM is intimate because the viewer feels they're catching real behavior, not staged content. Real behavior has unconscious moments — leaning to check the mirror, glancing down to grab a tool, adjusting a slipped strap, tapping the side of a product. These are micro-gestures that happen WITHOUT thought — and when included, they elevate GRWM from "made for camera" to "captured by camera."

### AN.2 — THE 30 SUBCONSCIOUS MOVEMENTS (SCM Library)

CAMERA / MIRROR INTERACTIONS (1-8):

SCM-1 LEAN-IN-TO-MIRROR-CHECK
Aira leans face fractionally closer to mirror (1-3cm) to inspect specific detail (mascara, blush, lip line). Eyes narrow with focus. Returns to position. Never acknowledges camera consciously — she's checking herself.

SCM-2 CHIN-TILT-FOR-LIGHT-ANGLE
Tilts chin slightly up or down to catch light better while applying. Functional, not performative. Light visibly catches cheekbone or forehead at new angle.

SCM-3 SIDE-PROFILE-CHECK
Turns head briefly to side-profile to verify symmetry. 0.3-0.5s glance. Returns. Common during cheek/jaw application.

SCM-4 EYEBROW-LIFT-FOR-ACCESS
While applying eye product, eyebrow lifts subtly to give better access to lid. Functional anatomy.

SCM-5 LEAN-BACK-TO-EVALUATE
After applying something, leans back from mirror briefly (3-5cm) to see overall effect. Eyes scan reflection. Returns to continue.

SCM-6 FACE-TILT-LEFT-RIGHT
Tilts entire head left then right slightly while looking at mirror — comparing both sides of face symmetry.

SCM-7 SQUINT-OF-FOCUS
Eyes narrow slightly during precision moments (eyeliner, lip line). Not posed concentration — actual focus tension.

SCM-8 GLANCE-TO-PRODUCT-AND-BACK
Eyes flick down to product label/brush briefly to check, then back to face. Quick reference glance, 0.4-0.6s.

OBJECT/PRODUCT BEATS (9-18):

SCM-9 LEAN-OVER-TO-PICK-UP
Body leans slightly forward and to one side to grab product on vanity. Hip and torso shift, return upright. Real reach physics.

SCM-10 PRODUCT-TAP-TO-SETTLE
Taps bottom of product (foundation, sprayer) to settle formula before opening. 2-3 quick taps. Functional.

SCM-11 BRUSH-FLICK-OFF-EXCESS
Holds brush, taps it on side of palette/jar/wrist to remove excess. Quick functional motion, dust visible briefly.

SCM-12 SHAKE-BOTTLE-BEFORE-USE
Single quick shake of nail polish or foundation bottle before opening. Wrist motion.

SCM-13 DROP-AND-CATCH-FUMBLE
Almost-drops a product, catches it with second hand or against thigh. Brief recovery beat. Real-life clumsy moment.

SCM-14 SIDE-EYE-TO-PRODUCT-LINEUP
Glance sideways at products laid out, scanning for next one needed. Doesn't move head, just eyes.

SCM-15 CAP-TWIRL-IN-FINGERS
While speaking, twirls a small cap or applicator between thumb and finger. Idle hand movement during VO.

SCM-16 PRODUCT-TO-CHEEK-WARMTH
Briefly holds product (lip balm, cream) against cheek/wrist to warm it before applying. Real beauty technique.

SCM-17 RUB-FINGERTIPS-TOGETHER
After dispensing serum/cream onto fingertips, rubs them together to warm and emulsify. 1-2 quick rubs.

SCM-18 BLOW-ON-NAIL-OR-BRUSH
Soft puff of breath onto wet nail polish, freshly-loaded brush, or warm tool to cool. Small natural beat.

BODY/POSTURE BEATS (19-25):

SCM-19 SHOULDER-ROLL-TO-RELEASE-TENSION
Single shoulder rolls back, releasing held tension. Often after focused application beat. Functional release.

SCM-20 NECK-ROLL-SIDE
Tilts head to one side, holds for a beat, returns. Releasing neck tension during routine.

SCM-21 STRAP-ADJUST
If wearing slip/robe with strap — slipped strap pulled back up unconsciously without breaking eye-contact-with-mirror. Functional.

SCM-22 ROBE-CINCH-TIGHTEN
Re-cinches robe belt during reel, tightens around waist. Quick functional motion.

SCM-23 LEG-CROSS-OR-UNCROSS
While seated, recrosses legs or shifts weight. Subtle posture reset.

SCM-24 STRETCH-FINGERS
Hand stretches or splays briefly between products — releasing micro-tension.

SCM-25 SCRATCH-OR-RUB-ITCH
Quick scratch at neck or behind ear — completely real-human moment. Use sparingly (once per reel max).

JEWELRY/ACCESSORY BEATS (26-30):

SCM-26 EARRING-PUT-IN-WITH-MIRROR-CHECK
Tilts head to one side, hand finds earlobe, slides earring through, secures back, glances at mirror to verify. Common Frame 4-5 beat.

SCM-27 EARRING-TOUCH-CHECK
After earrings on, fingertip briefly touches one earring to verify it's secure. Real human anxiety beat.

SCM-28 NECKLACE-CLASP-BEHIND-NECK
Both hands rise behind neck to fasten necklace clasp. Brief lean back, lifted chin. Functional.

SCM-29 BANGLE-SLIDE-DOWN-WRIST
Slides bangles down wrist to settle them, or up to push out of way of routine.

SCM-30 RING-TWIST-WHILE-SPEAKING
Idle ring-twist between thumb and finger during VO. Common in pivot frame when she's thinking out loud.

### AN.3 — RULES OF SCM USE

RULE 1 — PER-REEL COUNT: Use 2-4 SCMs across a GRWM reel. More than 4 = busy. Fewer than 2 = clinical.
RULE 2 — DISTRIBUTION: Spread across multiple frames. Never two SCMs in same frame.
RULE 3 — INVISIBILITY: Viewer should NOT register these as "moves" — read as natural behavior. If viewer thinks "she just did a beat" — over-performed.
RULE 4 — AUTHENTICITY HIERARCHY: SCMs are MORE intimate than charm moves. They suggest "she forgot the camera was on" — highest GRWM intimacy.
RULE 5 — DURATION: Each SCM 0.3-1.0 seconds. Quick. Subtle. Folded into other actions.
RULE 6 — CHARM vs SCM:
- Charm moves (CM): aware, slightly performative, "knowing wink"
- SCMs: unaware, functional, "real human"
- A GRWM reel may have ONE charm move PLUS 2-4 SCMs. Different functions.

### AN.4 — SCM-FRAME PLACEMENT GUIDE

FRAME 1 (Opening): SCM-7 squint-of-focus / SCM-8 glance-to-product / SCM-22 robe-cinch
FRAME 2 (First Application): SCM-9 lean-over-to-pick-up / SCM-10 product-tap / SCM-17 rub-fingertips / SCM-21 strap-adjust
FRAME 3 (Build): SCM-1 lean-in-mirror / SCM-2 chin-tilt-for-light / SCM-11 brush-flick / SCM-14 side-eye-to-products
FRAME 4 (Pivot): SCM-15 cap-twirl / SCM-30 ring-twist-while-speaking / SCM-19 shoulder-roll
FRAME 5 (Near-Complete): SCM-26 earring-put-in / SCM-27 earring-touch-check / SCM-28 necklace-clasp / SCM-3 side-profile-check
FRAME 6 (Reveal): SCM-5 lean-back-to-evaluate / SCM-6 face-tilt-left-right
FRAME 7 (Exit): SCM-21 strap-adjust / SCM-22 robe-cinch / SCM-29 bangle-slide-down

### AN.5 — INTEGRATION

STAGE 08 (Per-Frame Expansion) amended:

```
SUBCONSCIOUS MOVEMENT BLOCK (per frame, optional):
SCM USED: [name from AN.2 or "none"]
TIMING: [seconds within frame]
DURATION: [0.3-1.0s]
FUNCTIONAL CONTEXT: [what real-world reason motivates beat]
INTEGRATION: [folded into which other action]
```

Engine selects 2-4 SCMs across reel based on stakes register and frame structure.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 78: GRWM USES 2-4 SUBCONSCIOUS MOVEMENTS ACROSS REEL. Zero = clinical. More than 4 = over-performed.
ENFORCEMENT RULE 79: SCMs MUST READ AS UNCONSCIOUS, not performed. Visible-as-moves = wrong.
ENFORCEMENT RULE 80: SCM PLACEMENT FOLLOWS AN.4 FRAME GUIDE.

### AN.6 — THE INTIMACY GUARANTEE

When the engine uses SCMs correctly, GRWM achieves the highest intimacy register:
✓ Real-human texture in every frame
✓ Body alive, functional, not posed
✓ Viewer feels they're watching something not made for them — deepest engagement state
✓ Functional motivations underneath every beat
✓ Layered movement: named moves + charm moves + SCMs + body-language laws together

GRWM becomes highest-craft version of format — feels caught, not made.

## PART Q.EXTENDED.IV — GRWM WARDROBE TRANSFORMATION PROTOCOL

The exact mechanics of how Aira transitions from her opening attire (robe / slip / camisole / towel) to her final composed outfit. Locked as the Hybrid Approach — visible single dressing beat with implied major changes, modeled on how Hailey Bieber / Diipa Khosla / Komal Pandey / top fashion-editorial GRWMs actually execute.

### Q.EXT.IV.1 — THE HYBRID APPROACH (DEFAULT)

```
FRAMES 1–5: OPENING ATTIRE PERSISTS
- Aira remains in robe / silk slip / cotton tee / camisole / towel-wrapped throughout makeup + hair routine
- Opening attire is comfortable, intimate, real
- Skin / face / hair transformation happens WHILE wardrobe stays simple

FRAME 5b (MINI-BEAT) OR END OF FRAME 5: THE DRESSING BEAT
- ONE visible "becoming" moment
- Tasteful framing — over-shoulder / profile silhouette / through-mirror / cropped at chest
- What's shown: garment going ON (slip pull-down, dress slip-over-head, zipper closing, button fastening)
- What's NEVER shown: undressing / removal footage

FRAME 6: THE REVEAL
- Fully dressed, fully composed
- All major outfit complete
- Hair finished, makeup finished, primary outfit on

FRAME 7: FINAL ACCESSORIES + EXIT
- Bag picked up
- Fragrance applied (2 sprays — collarbone + wrist)
- Final mirror check
- Walks out
```

### Q.EXT.IV.2 — THE DRESSING BEAT — DETAILED

The single visible wardrobe beat is choreographed precisely:

DURATION: 2-4 seconds (within Frame 5b or final 4s of Frame 5)

VISIBLE GARMENT-ON ACTIONS (pick ONE per reel):
1. SILK SLIP OVER-HEAD — Aira lifts dress overhead with both hands, pulls down through, fabric cascades over body, hands smooth at waist. Body always covered by underlayer or by descending dress.
2. STEP-INTO-DRESS — Aira stepping into dress from floor, pulling up to waist. Shot waist-up only.
3. ZIPPER CLOSING (BACK) — reaches behind to pull side or back zipper. Side-profile, hair lifted forward.
4. FRONT-CLOSURE FASTENING — buttons / hooks / wrap ties fastened in front. Over-shoulder or close-up on hands.
5. WRAP-DRESS TIE — wrap-style fabric tied at waist or hip. Quick precise motion.
6. STRAP-PULL-UP — slip dress already half-on; both straps pulled up onto shoulders. Front view, intimate.
7. SARI/DUPATTA-DRAPE — Pillar 4 — final drape of pallu over shoulder, or dupatta arrangement.
8. CORSET-CLOSURE — Pillar 5/11 — front hooks closing, brief shot. Decolletage covered by garment edge.
9. TROUSER-PULL-UP — Pillars 1/2/7 — trousers pulled up, button at waist closing. Cropped shot.
10. BLAZER-SHRUG-ON — Aira shrugs into blazer — arms slipping into sleeves, lapels straightening. Pillars 1/2/7/10.

FRAMING RULES FOR DRESSING BEAT:
- Over-the-shoulder (camera behind Aira, fabric/dress visible going on from her POV implied)
- Profile silhouette (side angle, fabric dropping)
- Through-mirror (camera shoots reflection, Aira's back to camera)
- Cropped (chest-up, waist-up, ECU on hands fastening — body hidden by frame edge)
- Soft-focus or shallow DOF (movement softened, never sharp full-body)

### Q.EXT.IV.3 — WHAT'S NEVER SHOWN

FORBIDDEN in any GRWM dressing beat:
- Undressing footage (removal of robe, slip, any garment)
- Body without underlayer between layers
- Lingerie / undergarment focus shots
- Bare back below shoulder line
- Bare front of body
- Frame composition emphasizing uncovered skin during transition
- Long lingering on undergarment-only state

The dressing beat is about THE GARMENT GOING ON — never about what's underneath.

### Q.EXT.IV.4 — STATE PERSISTENCE INTEGRATION

WARDROBE STATE TRACKER FOR GRWM:

```
| Frame | Wardrobe State                                       |
|=======|======================================================|
| 1     | Robe / Silk Slip / Cotton Tee / Camisole / Towel    |
| 2     | Same as Frame 1                                      |
| 3     | Same as Frame 1                                      |
| 4     | Same as Frame 1 (+ possibly first jewelry pieces)    |
| 5     | Opening attire transitioning → main outfit (DRESSING BEAT) |
| 6     | Full main outfit + jewelry + heels                   |
| 7     | Full outfit + bag + fragrance just applied + walking |
```

Each frame's wardrobe persists from the previous unless visible change beat shown.

### Q.EXT.IV.5 — TIER-SPECIFIC WARDROBE ARCS

LIGHT STAKES TIER (32-40s, 4-5 frames):
- Opening attire: cotton tee + comfy bottoms / casual robe
- Single dressing beat (often blazer-shrug-on or slip-into-jeans + change-top)
- Outfit: Pillar 3 (Effortless Day) typical
- Less dressing complexity

MEDIUM STAKES TIER (40-48s, 5-6 frames) — DEFAULT:
- Opening attire: silk slip / cream robe
- Single dressing beat at Frame 5b
- Outfit: Pillar 1, 5, 8, 10 typical

HEAVY STAKES TIER (48-56s, 6-7 frames):
- Opening attire: silk slip / robe (often with story-significance)
- Dressing beat at Frame 5 or 5b — slightly more elaborate
- Outfit: Pillar 5 / Pillar 7 / Pillar 11 typical
- Possible extended Frame 5 to include zipper close + accessory layering

EMOTIONAL/HERITAGE/MILESTONE TIER (56-64s, 7-8 frames):
- Opening attire: silk slip / heritage robe / kurta-base
- Extended dressing arc — multiple wardrobe stages may be shown:
  - Stage 1: Underlayer (already on)
  - Stage 2: Main garment going on (Frame 5)
  - Stage 3: Drape/dupatta arrangement (Frame 5b)
  - Stage 4: Heritage jewelry layering (Frame 6)
  - Stage 5: Final composition (Frame 6 or 7)
- Outfit: Pillar 4 / Pillar 5 / Pillar 11

### Q.EXT.IV.6 — PILLAR-SPECIFIC DRESSING BEATS

- PILLAR 1 (Modern Minimalist Luxe): Slip dress over-head OR blazer-shrug-on
- PILLAR 2 (Editorial Bold): Sculptural gown step-in OR architectural top pull-down
- PILLAR 3 (Effortless Day): Trouser pull-up + tank tucking, OR linen shirt button-up
- PILLAR 4 (Indo-Modern): Sari/dupatta drape OR kurta slip-over OR lehenga ties
- PILLAR 5 (Evening Defined): Silk slip over-head OR back-zipper close OR strap-pull-up
- PILLAR 6 (Sculpted Active): Matched-set top pull-down (rare — usually casual already)
- PILLAR 7 (Street Edge): Leather jacket shrug + denim button + chain layer
- PILLAR 8 (Romantic Ethereal): Floral midi over-head + ribbon tie at waist
- PILLAR 9 (Architectural Futurist): Sculptural one-piece step-in + sleek closure
- PILLAR 10 (Warm Heritage): Tweed blazer shrug-on + scarf tie at neck
- PILLAR 11 (Sensual Editorial Celebrity): Slip dress over-head OR strap-pull-up OR back-zipper close — extra care for tasteful framing

### Q.EXT.IV.7 — FRAME 7 FINAL ACCESSORIES + FRAGRANCE BEATS

EXIT BEAT SEQUENCE (Frame 7):
- 0.0-1.0s: Aira at vanity completing final accessories (statement earring final adjustment, bracelet sliding on, ring twist)
- 1.0-2.0s: Bag picked up from vanity / chair / floor
- 2.0-3.5s: Fragrance bottle picked up, 2 sprays applied (collarbone, wrist) — atomizer hiss SFX
- 3.5-5.0s: Final mirror check / chin-tilt / half-smile
- 5.0-6.5s: Walks toward door, hem catches air
- 6.5-8.0s: Hand on door, glance back (or not), Hindi sign-off OR silence, exits

### Q.EXT.IV.8 — INTEGRATION

STAGE 05 amended:

```
WARDROBE TRANSFORMATION BLOCK (mandatory per GRWM):
OPENING ATTIRE: [exact — robe / silk slip / cotton tee / camisole / towel]
DRESSING BEAT: [chosen from 10 actions Q.EXT.IV.2]
DRESSING BEAT FRAMING: [over-shoulder / profile silhouette / through-mirror / cropped / soft-focus]
DRESSING BEAT FRAME PLACEMENT: [Frame 5b / final 4s of Frame 5 / extended into Frame 6 for emotional tier]
CLOSING OUTFIT PILLAR: [N from Part M / Pillar 11]
WARDROBE STATE TRACKER: [per-frame persistence per Q.EXT.IV.4]
TIER-SPECIFIC ARC: [LIGHT / MEDIUM / HEAVY / EMOTIONAL]
ACCESSORIES TIMING: [which frame each piece enters body — per Part AM]
FRAGRANCE TIMING: [Frame 7, 2 sprays declared]
```

PRE-FLIGHT additions:
[ ] Opening attire declared
[ ] Dressing beat selected from 10 options
[ ] Dressing beat framing tasteful (cropped/silhouette/over-shoulder/through-mirror)
[ ] No undressing footage
[ ] No bare-body emphasis between layers
[ ] Wardrobe state tracker per frame
[ ] Closing pillar matches stakes tier
[ ] Accessory arc tracked through frames
[ ] Frame 7 fragrance + bag beats declared

ENFORCEMENT RULE 81: GRWM REQUIRES VISIBLE DRESSING BEAT in Frame 5/5b unless emotional tier explicitly extends arc into Frame 6. No magical wardrobe-teleport.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 82: DRESSING BEAT FRAMING IS TASTEFUL. Cropped / silhouette / over-shoulder / through-mirror / soft-focus mandatory. Never full-body bare-skin focus during transition.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 83: NO UNDRESSING FOOTAGE in any GRWM. Garment GOING ON only — never coming off.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 84: WARDROBE STATE PERSISTS forward (per Part AK). Once garment is on, stays on.

ENFORCEMENT RULE 85: FRAME 7 INCLUDES FRAGRANCE BEAT (2 sprays — collarbone + wrist) + bag pickup + final mirror check before exit.

### Q.EXT.IV.9 — THE WARDROBE TRANSFORMATION GUARANTEE

When the engine generates a GRWM with this protocol active:
- Aira begins in opening attire (robe/slip/camisole/towel)
- Wardrobe persists as opening attire through Frames 1-5
- Single tasteful dressing beat at Frame 5/5b shows ONE garment going on
- Frame 6 reveals full composed outfit
- Frame 7 layers final accessories + fragrance + bag, then exit
- Tasteful framing throughout — cropped / silhouette / over-shoulder / through-mirror
- State Persistence ensures wardrobe builds additively
- Tier-appropriate arc complexity (Light = simple, Heavy/Emotional = extended)
- Pillar-matched dressing beat type
- Platform-safe imagery throughout — never undressing, never bare-body focus

The wardrobe transformation reads as ritual, narrative satisfaction, and editorial sophistication — modeled on top-creator GRWM execution.
