## PART P.EXTENDED.II — BEAUTY 101% COMPLETENESS & FULL INTEGRATION

This part closes every remaining gap in Beauty (non-GRWM) reels by integrating it with all post-v3.4 protocol additions and giving Beauty the same depth of bit-by-bit specification that GRWM received in Q.EXTENDED.II.

After this part, Beauty reels are fully production-complete with no remaining loopholes — parallel in rigor to GRWM.

### P.EXT.II.1 — THE FIVE BEAUTY FORMAT SUB-TYPES

Beauty is not one format — it's five distinct sub-formats with different conventions, durations, and registers:

SUB-TYPE 1 — CINEMATIC BEAUTY HERO
- Single hero product or single hero feature
- Duration: 8-15 seconds (short, dense)
- Register: REVERENT or ELECTRIC
- Voice: usually SILENT or single tagline
- Frame count: 3-5
- USE: launch reveal, hero shot of product or face

SUB-TYPE 2 — FRAGRANCE MOOD PIECE
- Pure visual poetry, narrative-light
- Duration: 15-30 seconds
- Register: REVERENT, CONTEMPLATIVE, or TENDER
- Voice: SILENT (default) or single whispered line
- Frame count: 4-6
- USE: fragrance launches, perfume editorials

SUB-TYPE 3 — PRODUCT LAUNCH AD
- Multi-product or product-family showcase
- Duration: 15-30 seconds
- Register: ELECTRIC or REVERENT
- Voice: SELECTIVE (tagline + 1-2 lines of product mention)
- Frame count: 5-7
- USE: full collection launches, brand campaigns

SUB-TYPE 4 — SENSORY BEAUTY TUTORIAL
- Quick technique or look reveal (NOT a GRWM — this is short-form how-to)
- Duration: 12-25 seconds
- Register: KNOWING or CURIOUS-CONFIDENT
- Voice: SPOKEN (lower volume, instructional but not lecture-tone)
- Frame count: 4-6
- USE: technique demos, quick tutorials, product application reveals

SUB-TYPE 5 — BEAUTY EDITORIAL FILM
- High-fashion-magazine aesthetic, narrative implied not stated
- Duration: 20-45 seconds
- Register: REVERENT, CONTEMPLATIVE, or KNOWING
- Voice: SILENT or VO with poetry-fragment quality
- Frame count: 5-8
- USE: brand collab editorial, fashion-house beauty crossover

EVERY BEAUTY REEL DECLARES SUB-TYPE AT TOP — non-negotiable.

### P.EXT.II.2 — THE 30 MOOD ARCHETYPES (Beauty equivalent of stakes)

GRWM uses STAKES (real specific reasons). Beauty uses MOOD ARCHETYPES — sensory atmospheres that organize the entire reel.

WARMTH FAMILY (1-6):
MA-1 "the weight of golden light on slow afternoons"
MA-2 "honey on skin"
MA-3 "amber ritual at dusk"
MA-4 "warmth of held breath in cold air"
MA-5 "fire and crystal — opposites touching"
MA-6 "saffron threads dissolving in milk"

WATER/LIQUID FAMILY (7-12):
MA-7 "blue-hour stillness on the surface"
MA-8 "rain-glass intimacy"
MA-9 "the moment before a drop falls"
MA-10 "silk poured slow"
MA-11 "dewdrop on petal at dawn"
MA-12 "ocean caught in a vial"

LIGHT FAMILY (13-18):
MA-13 "first light on the back of the neck"
MA-14 "moon on glass"
MA-15 "cathedral light through dust"
MA-16 "neon held in palm"
MA-17 "the gleam beneath polished surfaces"
MA-18 "shadow tracing the cheekbone"

INTIMACY FAMILY (19-24):
MA-19 "skin remembering the day"
MA-20 "fragrance unfolding on bare collarbone"
MA-21 "fingertip at the inner wrist"
MA-22 "lips parting before words"
MA-23 "pulse beneath thin skin"
MA-24 "breath on cold mirror"

ARTISANAL FAMILY (25-30):
MA-25 "hand-thrown clay still warm"
MA-26 "ink bleeding into rice paper"
MA-27 "antique gold catching afternoon"
MA-28 "embroidered thread under magnifying glass"
MA-29 "pressed flower preserved in resin"
MA-30 "marble veined with stories"

EVERY BEAUTY REEL DECLARES ONE MOOD ARCHETYPE. Concept Bible (Part G) builds outward from the archetype.

### P.EXT.II.3 — THE BEAUTY SENSORY ARC

GRWM has the emotional arc (vulnerable → processing → decision → ready → loose). Beauty has the SENSORY ARC:

BEAT 1 — OPENING SENSATION (10-15% of reel):
- First sensory element introduces — droplet, light shaft, breath, particle, surface
- Slow pace, never rushed
- Viewer's senses tune in

BEAT 2 — BUILDING INTENSITY (30-40% of reel):
- Sensory elements layer — light deepens, particles densify, product enters
- Subject begins engagement (closes eyes / breathes in / tilts head)
- Pace slightly quickens but stays controlled

BEAT 3 — PEAK INTIMACY (20-30% of reel):
- Subject + product + atmosphere fuse — peak fragrance moment, peak skin glow, peak product transformation
- Held silence often dominant
- Time slows to suspended

BEAT 4 — AFTERGLOW / SETTLE (15-25% of reel):
- Sensory release — settling, breath out, product complete
- Light may shift slightly (sun moved, candle settled)
- Viewer's senses release

BEAT 5 — RESONANCE (5-15% of reel):
- Held final visual or product hero shot
- Tagline lands (if voiced) or silence holds
- Resonance lingers

Every beauty reel traces this arc. Without it = flat product showcase.

### P.EXT.II.4 — THE 8 BEAUTY SETTING PILLARS

B-1 MIRROR-WALL STUDIO — polished concrete or seamless paper, single hard colored key (pink/gold/blue/magenta), mirror wall behind subject, theatrical, controlled negative space, clean haze. USE: hero ad, editorial, electric register.

B-2 WET-LIGHT BATHROOM — marble or terrazzo counter, large mirror, fogged shower glass BG, water droplets on surfaces, steam rising, slight humidity haze, reflected wet-surface light play. USE: skincare hero, fragrance freshness, intimate beauty.

B-3 GOLDEN-HOUR BEDROOM — bed-edge or floor cushion + mirror, window light at 4-6 PM golden, soft fabric BG (curtains, throws), wardrobe in BG, golden particles drifting, warm haze. USE: tender, evening, romantic beauty, fragrance.

B-4 DAWN BALCONY / WINDOW — window light at 6-8 AM cool warm, open vista BG (city/garden/sky), atmospheric haze, dew on surfaces, cool-warm temperature collision. USE: morning skincare, fresh beauty, contemplative.

B-5 ATELIER / WORKSHOP — wooden surface, artisan tools, plants in clay pots, natural daylight from large window, slight dust in air, lived-in feel, hand-thrown ceramic, leather, raw materials in BG. USE: artisanal beauty, heritage, wellness, slow-luxury.

B-6 BOTANICAL / GARDEN — outdoor — golden hour or overcast soft, foliage BG with selective focus, petals or particles in air, natural sunlight + reflector fill. USE: floral beauty, fresh skincare, fragrance with nature notes.

B-7 MINIMALIST GALLERY — clean architectural BG (stone, concrete, white plaster), single hard light or skylight, negative space dominant, particles minimal, atmosphere clean. USE: avant-garde beauty, sculptural product, futurist fragrance.

B-8 POOLSIDE / WATER-EDGE — water as primary visual element, caustic light dancing on surfaces, reflective surfaces (water, tile, glass), sun overhead or sunset. USE: summer beauty, body care, sun-care, oceanic fragrance.

EVERY BEAUTY REEL SELECTS FROM THESE 8 SETTINGS. Setting matched to mood archetype + sub-type + register.

### P.EXT.II.5 — FRAME-BY-FRAME VOICE / SILENCE MAP FOR BEAUTY

CINEMATIC BEAUTY HERO (3-5 frames):
- Frame 1: SILENT (atmospheric establish)
- Frame 2: SILENT (build)
- Frame 3: SILENT or single whispered word (peak)
- Frame 4: SILENT (afterglow)
- Frame 5 (if used): tagline lands OR silence

FRAGRANCE MOOD PIECE (4-6 frames):
- All frames default SILENT
- One frame may carry a poetic line (rarely more than 4-6 words)
- Music carries the emotional load
- Ambient (breath, fabric, water-drop) fills silence

PRODUCT LAUNCH AD (5-7 frames):
- Frame 1: SILENT (hook visual)
- Frames 2-3: SELECTIVE — one line introduces product
- Frame 4: SILENT (peak demonstration)
- Frame 5: tagline OR product name
- Frame 6: SILENT (afterglow)
- Frame 7: brand mark visible, optional sign-off

SENSORY BEAUTY TUTORIAL (4-6 frames):
- Frames 1-5: SPOKEN at intimate volume
- Voice is conversational instructional, not lecture-tone
- VO ducks during peak visual moments

BEAUTY EDITORIAL FILM (5-8 frames):
- Mixed — VO may carry poetry-fragment lines
- Lines are sentence-fragments, not full sentences ("breath held," "the wait," "almost gold")
- Music dominant, VO punctuates

VOICE-FREE FRAMES IN BEAUTY ARE THE STRENGTH OF THE FORMAT. Silence is not absence — it is directive.

### P.EXT.II.6 — THE 20 BEAUTY SUBCONSCIOUS MOVEMENTS (BSCM)

SKIN/FACE BSCMs (1-7):
BSCM-1 SKIN-LIGHT-CATCH-WHILE-BREATHING — light catches subject's collarbone/cheekbone as she inhales
BSCM-2 EYELASHES-SETTLING-ON-CLOSED-EYE — eyes close softly, lashes finding rest position
BSCM-3 SLOW-CHIN-TILT-TO-FEEL-SCENT — chin tilts upward 5-10° as she breathes in fragrance
BSCM-4 LIP-PART-ON-INHALE — lips part fractionally as breath comes in
BSCM-5 NOSE-BRIDGE-RELAXATION — micro-relaxation of nose-bridge muscle (post-tension release)
BSCM-6 PULSE-VISIBLE-AT-INNER-WRIST — vein/pulse barely visible, real life-sign
BSCM-7 FACE-SOFTENING-INTO-LIGHT — facial muscles release as warm light hits

HAND/FINGER BSCMs (8-13):
BSCM-8 FINGERTIP-TRACE-COLLARBONE — fingertip slowly traces along collarbone
BSCM-9 FINGER-PAUSE-AT-INNER-WRIST — fingertip rests at inner wrist briefly
BSCM-10 PALM-OPEN-TO-LIGHT — opens palm to catch falling light/particle/droplet
BSCM-11 FINGER-CIRCLES-ON-PRODUCT-EDGE — fingertip slowly circles the rim/edge of a product
BSCM-12 FINGER-TIP-TO-LIP-CORNER — fingertip touches lip corner (checking moisture/setting)
BSCM-13 HAND-RESTING-AT-NECK-HOLLOW — palm rests at suprasternal notch (between collarbones)

HAIR/SHOULDER BSCMs (14-17):
BSCM-14 SINGLE-STRAND-FALLING-INTO-FRAME — one hair strand drifts loose, stays
BSCM-15 SHOULDER-SOFT-DROP-ON-EXHALE — shoulder visibly drops as breath releases
BSCM-16 NECK-EXTENSION-INTO-LIGHT — neck slightly elongates, catching light along jaw line
BSCM-17 HAIR-SHIFT-WITH-HEAD-MOVEMENT — head turns slowly, hair follows with delay

EYE BSCMs (18-20):
BSCM-18 SLOW-EYE-OPENING-AFTER-INHALE — eyes opening after a held-breath beat, pupils adjusting
BSCM-19 EYE-DRIFT-OFF-CAMERA — gaze drifts off-frame (looking at scent, light, or invisible thought)
BSCM-20 EYELID-MICRO-FLUTTER — fast involuntary lid flutter (real human eye reflex)

USAGE: 2-3 BSCMs per Beauty reel, distributed across frames, read as unconscious not performed.

### P.EXT.II.7 — BEAUTY BRAND-COLLAB RESTRAINT RULES

Product count by sub-type:
- Cinematic Beauty Hero: 1 hero product only
- Fragrance Mood Piece: 1 hero product only
- Product Launch Ad: maximum 3 hero products
- Sensory Beauty Tutorial: 1-2 hero products
- Beauty Editorial Film: 1 hero product

Each hero product gets:
- Minimum 2-3 dedicated frames
- Logo/wordmark readable in at least 2 frames
- Held label-clear shot for at least 1.0 second
- Maximum 1 product performance move per reel (hero product only)
- Brand name in VO max once if voiced
- Visual dominance: product hero shots ≥40% of frame time

### P.EXT.II.8 — BEAUTY DURATION STANDARDS

```
SUB-TYPE                  | RANGE   | DEFAULT | FRAMES
Cinematic Beauty Hero     | 8-15s   | 12s     | 3-5 (default 4)
Fragrance Mood Piece      | 15-30s  | 24s     | 4-6 (default 5)
Product Launch Ad         | 15-30s  | 24s     | 5-7 (default 6)
Sensory Beauty Tutorial   | 12-25s  | 20s     | 4-6 (default 5)
Beauty Editorial Film     | 20-45s  | 32s     | 5-8 (default 6)

ABSOLUTE BEAUTY RANGE: 8-45s
HARD CEILING: 60s (only milestone editorial)
```

### P.EXT.II.9 — BEAUTY PERFORMANCE BEATS (Cinematic Beauty Hero default 4 frames × 3s)

FRAME 1 — OPENING SENSATION (0-3s):
- Visual: ECU on sensory element (droplet about to fall / light shaft / breath-vapor)
- Subject: not yet visible OR silhouette
- Audio: ambient + music low (-18dB)
- Camera: slow push-in (VEO 3.1 on NB still)

FRAME 2 — BUILDING (3-6s):
- Visual: subject appears — face profile, partial CU, OR hands entering frame
- Subject: closes eyes slowly, breath visible (BSCM-1 or BSCM-4)
- Audio: music builds, ambient continues
- Camera: orbital quarter-turn OR vertical tilt
- Performance: subject move (S-15 contemplative-drift OR S-12 reveal-eye-open OR S-26 breath-visible)

FRAME 3 — PEAK INTIMACY (6-9s):
- Visual: product hero moment — fragrance bottle hovers / drop materializes / light catches product
- Subject: opens eyes / lips part / chin tilts (BSCM-3 OR BSCM-18)
- Audio: music peak OR sudden silence for 0.5s
- Camera: macro push-in OR pull-back to reveal subject + product
- Performance: product performance move (P-1 slow levitation OR P-10 liquid materialization)

FRAME 4 — AFTERGLOW + RESONANCE (9-12s):
- Visual: held composition — subject + product in resolved frame
- Subject: half-smile OR slow-blink-lock (S-17) OR stillness-with-micro-life (S-30)
- Audio: music settles to resonance, ambient holds
- Camera: static OR very slow continued push
- Performance: held visual, optional tagline

### P.EXT.II.10 — BEAUTY WARDROBE / SKIN-VISIBILITY PROTOCOL

WARDROBE OPTIONS (pick one per reel):
1. Silk slip dress (cream/black/nude/champagne)
2. White or cream cotton robe
3. Bare shoulders with draped fabric (towel/silk scarf/linen across shoulder)
4. Minimalist couture top (silk shell/cashmere mock-neck/cream camisole)
5. Embroidered Indo-modern blouse
6. Wet-hair-only with bare shoulders, draped towel below frame edge — for B-2 setting
7. Sheer wrap with structured undergarment (Editorial only — Pillar 11 register)
8. Architectural sculpted top (futurist beauty — Pillar 9)

SKIN-VISIBILITY:
- Collarbones, shoulders, upper-chest at decolletage level — celebrated
- Side of neck, jaw line, ear — featured for fragrance/skincare
- Inner wrist — featured for fragrance application (BSCM-9)
- Lower body — typically not featured (reel is upper-body focused)
- Always tasteful — beauty editorial register, never beyond magazine-cover standard
- No undergarment focus, no bare midsection focus

### P.EXT.II.11 — BEAUTY × HAIR (Part AA Integration)

Hair in Beauty is STATIC — one defined concept from first frame to last.
- Hair concept (HC-N) selected at Stage 05
- Same final-styled state throughout all frames
- May have micro-motion (BSCM-14 or BSCM-17) but no structural change
- Wet-hair beauty: hair stays wet throughout
- Editorial avant-garde: HC-26 to HC-30 sculptural concepts
- 10-reel rotation rule applies

### P.EXT.II.12 — BEAUTY × MAKEUP (Part AH Integration)

- Makeup look (ML-N) declared at Stage 05
- Cinematic Hero / Fragrance / Editorial: makeup arrives complete in Frame 1
- Sensory Tutorial: makeup builds across frames (compressed compared to GRWM)
- Product Launch: depends on product (lipstick = visible application; foundation = clean skin reveal)

### P.EXT.II.13 — BEAUTY × BARE-FACE PROTOCOL

If reel features bare-face / no-makeup state:
- Same Bare-Face Identity Lock from Q.EXT.II.3 applies
- Real skin texture, real pores, identity locked
- Never glam-fake-bare
- Bare-face anti-drift negatives applied

### P.EXT.II.14 — BEAUTY × THREE-PERFORMER COORDINATION

HERO ASSIGNMENT BY SUB-TYPE:

Cinematic Beauty Hero: PRODUCT 60% / SUBJECT 30% / BACKDROP 10%
Fragrance Mood Piece: BACKDROP 60% / PRODUCT 30% / SUBJECT 10%
Product Launch Ad: PRODUCT 50% / SUBJECT 30% / BACKDROP 20%
Sensory Beauty Tutorial: SUBJECT 50% / PRODUCT 35% / BACKDROP 15%
Beauty Editorial Film: SUBJECT 50% / BACKDROP 30% / PRODUCT 20%

### P.EXT.II.15 — BEAUTY × COVER FRAME

COVER FRAME SOURCE:
- Cinematic Beauty Hero: Frame 3 (peak intimacy) — NOT Frame 4
- Fragrance Mood: Frame 2 or 3 (subject + atmosphere together)
- Product Launch: Frame 3 or 4 (product hero with subject reaction)
- Sensory Tutorial: Frame 1 (hook) OR Frame 4 (result)
- Beauty Editorial: Frame 2 or 3 (most striking single image)

NEVER as cover: pure product still without subject, subject without sensory atmosphere, mid-blink unflattering moment.

OPTIONAL TEXT OVERLAY: minimal, register-matched — usually let visual carry.

### P.EXT.II.16 — BEAUTY × COLOR GRADE

Color grade follows mood archetype family:
- WARMTH FAMILY → warm-shift, golden highlights, lifted blacks, Kodak Portra reference
- WATER/LIQUID → cool-shift, controlled highlights, slight cyan in shadows
- LIGHT → high-key whites, controlled rolloff, minimal saturation
- INTIMACY → skin-priority warm, soft shadows, glossy highlights
- ARTISANAL → warm with grain, vintage-leaning, slight desaturation

UNIFIED ACROSS ALL FRAMES — no mid-reel grade shifts.

### P.EXT.II.17 — BEAUTY 101% PRE-FLIGHT CHECKLIST (FULL)


### P.EXT.II.18 — ENFORCEMENT RULES (86-95)

ENFORCEMENT RULE 86: BEAUTY SUB-TYPE DECLARED PER REEL. One of 5. Generic "beauty reel" = FAIL.
ENFORCEMENT RULE 87: BEAUTY MOOD ARCHETYPE DECLARED. One MA-N from P.EXT.II.2. Concept Bible builds outward.
ENFORCEMENT RULE 88: BEAUTY SENSORY ARC TRACED. All 5 beats distributed across frames.
ENFORCEMENT RULE 89: BEAUTY SETTING FROM 8 PILLARS (B-1 to B-8). Atmospheric details mandatory.
ENFORCEMENT RULE 90: BEAUTY DURATION WITHIN SUB-TYPE RANGE.
ENFORCEMENT RULE 91: BEAUTY BSCMs — 2-3 per reel, read as unconscious.
ENFORCEMENT RULE 92: BEAUTY THREE-PERFORMER HIERARCHY MATCHES SUB-TYPE.
ENFORCEMENT RULE 93: BEAUTY HAIR STATIC THROUGHOUT REEL (not arc — unlike GRWM).
ENFORCEMENT RULE 94: BEAUTY WARDROBE FROM P.EXT.II.10 LIST. Tasteful skin-visibility.
ENFORCEMENT RULE 95: BEAUTY COVER FRAME PER SUB-TYPE GUIDE. Never pure product still, never unflattering.

### P.EXT.II.19 — THE BEAUTY 101% GUARANTEE

When the engine generates a Beauty concept:
✓ Sub-type declared and structurally followed
✓ Mood archetype anchors the concept
✓ Sensory arc traced across all frames
✓ Setting from 8 dedicated beauty pillars
✓ Duration within sub-type range
✓ Voice/silence map appropriate
✓ Three-performer hierarchy matches sub-type
✓ 2-3 BSCMs distributed
✓ Hair static with rotation enforced
✓ Makeup matched to register
✓ Wardrobe tasteful, register-appropriate
✓ Object Design Block for hero products
✓ Brand-collab restraint rules satisfied
✓ Cover frame strategically chosen
✓ Color grade matched to mood archetype
✓ State Persistence + Frame Handoff active
✓ All facial dynamics, body-language laws, kinetic stillness layers maintained
✓ All 95 enforcement rules pass
✓ Sensory arc reads as captured-real-moment

BEAUTY IS NOW 101% PRODUCTION-COMPLETE — parallel in rigor to GRWM.

# Sys Directive 3 — Vibrance Patch (Commercial Beauty Energy + Hair Library)

<aside>
🎯

**What this is.** An override layer that sits on top of Sys Directive 3. It does not delete the existing engine — the identity lock, three-performer system, anti-drift negatives, 12-stage prompt engine and tool routing all stay. It fixes the one real problem: the directive's *aesthetic defaults* pull toward muted prestige cinema, which reads dull and vibe-less on Instagram / Facebook / YouTube. These parts flip the defaults for beauty, GRWM and social content while keeping the cinematic mode available when you actually want it.

</aside>

## Part 00 — Upgrades, Fixes & Replacements (Keep vs. Replace)

<aside>
📌

This is the **changelog layer** of the patch: everything we agreed to **keep** and everything that **replaces** the old Sys Directive 3. Apply these deltas to the original base directive. The net-new sections they reference (Parts AO–BF) follow in full below — so this single page is the complete record: *what changed* plus *all the new material*.

</aside>

### 00.1 — Tooling: replace the old stack

| Old (remove) | New (keep) |
| --- | --- |
| Nano Banana (Gemini 2.5 Flash Image), VEO 3.1, Runway Gen-3, Kling 2.0, Pika 2.0 | **Nano Banana Pro** (stills) + **VEO 3.1** (all video). No other tools. |
- **Stills → Nano Banana Pro only.** Best legible in-image text; supports ≈14 reference images / 5 subjects; outputs 1K / 2K / 4K.
- **Video → VEO 3.1 only.** Text-to-video + image-to-video; Frames-to-Video; Extend (→≈148s, chain ≤20×); Ingredients (≤3 refs); native synced audio; 4 / 6 / 8s clips; 9:16 + 16:9; 720p / 1080p (+4K); 24fps; English.
- All other generators (Runway, Kling, Pika, old Nano Banana) are **removed** from the directive.

### 00.2 — Fixes & replacements (old → new)

These edits modify existing Parts of the base directive:

1. **Header tooling block** → replace the old 5-tool list with **Nano Banana Pro + VEO 3.1** (see 00.1).
2. **Part B — Tool Routing** → add explicit routing: stills route to Nano Banana Pro, all motion routes to VEO 3.1.
3. **Age** → set to **25** everywhere (Part C clause 15 and the Part M age line).
4. **Part M — Identity Lock (BUILD)** → **neutralize the explicit body-size enumeration.** Do not spell out body proportions; likeness is carried by the reference sheet only. Keep identity as canon (internal reference), never in prompts.
5. **Part E** → keep the **vibrance** callout (the brighter, more saturated, contemporary look).
6. **Part O + Appendix 9** → update all tool references to **VEO 3.1 + Nano Banana Pro**.
7. **Part K — Voice** → keep the **voice-override** rule + GRWM voice guidance.
8. **Default aspect ratio** → **9:16 locked** as the default for everything.

### 00.3 — Guardrails to keep (new rules)

- **AO-X — no physical enumeration in prompts.** Never spell out Aira's age, ethnicity, skin, hair, eyes or face shape in prompt text. Use `Aira [placeholder]` + the reference sheet for likeness; describe only styling, wardrobe, pose and mood.
- **Subject line format** → `SUBJECT: Aira [placeholder] (per identity lock, Part M)`.
- **Body-safety rule** → never reproduce sexualized or size/shape body enumeration; never graft a real person's face/body. Describe pose and position, not body parts by shape.
- **9:16** is the default ratio unless explicitly overridden.
- **VEO 3.1 = the only video tool; Nano Banana Pro = the only stills tool.**
- **Always ask before generating** any concept / reel / image / video.

### 00.4 — New additions index (Parts AO–BF, full text below)

- **AO (AO.0–AO.8 + AO-G/S/R/X/H/N)** — Vibrance operating block: global look, scale, social-native, GRWM reset, subject-consistency guardrail, hero rule, aesthetic exclusions.
- **AP** — 30 hair styling library. **AQ** — 24 makeup/glam library.
- **AR** — audio & sound design (incl. AR-MASTER + Fast Audio checklist).
- **AS** — product-hero spec. **AT** — camera & motion (AT-V, AT.0, AT.0-K, AT.1 18-move table — all VEO 3.1, AT.2–AT.6).
- **AU** — anti-hallucination lock (AU.1–AU.6). **AV** — frame count (6–8). **AW** — 30 outfit library.
- **AX** — concept category library 26 (AX.0–AX.5, incl. 3a/b/c). **AY** — studios & environments (AY.0–AY.4, incl. AY.3-C).
- **AZ** — visual elevation (AZ.0–AZ.7). **BA** — GRWM environment system (BA.0–BA.6). **BB** — composition / negative space.
- **BC** — Anti-Sameness log. **BD** — GRWM Captivation Kit (BD.0–BD.10, incl. BD.4-G). **BE** — BE.0–BE.3. **BF** — BF.0–BF.3.

- Convert bare `[ ]` checkboxes → proper `- [ ]` to-do items.

## Part AO — Commercial Beauty Energy & Color Override

### AO.0 — When this mode is ON

- **Default ON** for: beauty/cosmetic ads, GRWM, product reels, festive glam, and *anything destined for Instagram Reels, Facebook, or YouTube Shorts*.
- **Default OFF** (fall back to the original cinematic engine) only for: deliberate moody editorial, narrative/short-film pieces, or an explicit "quiet luxury / muted" brief.
- When ON, the rules below **override** any conflicting colorist, grade, register or palette instruction in the base directive.

### AO.1 — Color (the biggest lever)

- **Vibrance floor:** every frame must read as saturated, glossy and bright on a phone screen in daylight. No desaturation, no muddy mids.
- **Hero color world per reel:** commit to a vivid color identity — color-drenched seamless, gel-lit backdrops, gradient washes, or bold brand-color blocking.
- **Retire the muted colorist references** (A24 muted saturation, lifted blacks, crushed shadows, film-grain Portra/Cinestill) for this mode. They desaturate and lower contrast — the opposite of beauty-feed grammar.
- **Replace them with bright commercial-beauty references:** Fenty, Rare Beauty, Rhode, Charlotte Tilbury, Maybelline, Lakmé, Nykaa — glossy, punchy, saturated, high-key.

### AO.2 — Lighting

- Swap chiaroscuro / crushed-shadow setups for **high-key glossy beauty light**: clamshell, ring or beauty-dish, lifted shadows, clean bright base.
- Keep controlled **glossy specular highlights** on skin and product — luminous, not flat.
- Idealized-luminous over documentary-realistic. Beauty skin = glass-glow, not literal texture.

### AO.3 — Grade

- **No film grain. No lifted blacks. No "faded" looks** in this mode.
- Use a clean, punchy, high-saturation digital grade with crisp whites and rich (not crushed) blacks.

### AO.4 — Energy & motion

- **Unlimited real-physics energy.** Beauty/GRWM is maximalist: stack as many *real-world-physics* kinetic elements as you want — powder bursts, splashes, confetti, fabric whips, hair swing, product explosions, sparkle. They obey physics, so they read believable no matter how many you pile on. **These never count against the cap below.**
- **Max ONE physics-breaking move per shot.** The original cap stays — but scoped *only* to **impossible / physics-breaking miracles** (levitation, liquid materialization, self-opening cap, teleport, particle assembly). One per shot keeps it premium-magic instead of fake-CGI, and renders cleaner — multiple impossible motions in one clip = morphing/warping artifacts. This directly serves AO.7.
- **Faster cut rhythm, beat-synced.** Cuts land on the music.
- Three-performer 60/30/10 stays, but the energy ceiling goes up.

### AO.5 — Register & palette rebalance

- Default registers flip from reverent/contemplative to **electric / curious-confident / mischievous**.
- Default wardrobe pillars flip from neutral (Pillar 1) toward **Editorial Bold (2)** and other bright palettes. Neutrals become a deliberate choice, not the baseline.

### AO.6 — MUST-POP positive mandates

The base directive is ~90% "don't." Add these "must":

- ≥ 1 saturated color element in every frame.
- ≥ 2 moving elements per hero frame.
- Glossy specular highlight on skin **and** product in every hero frame.
- Beat-locked cuts.

### AO.7 — "Don't Overcook" realism guardrail

Counterweight to the brightness push: vivid **but believable**.

- **Skin stays real:** keep natural texture/pores; no plastic, waxy or over-smoothed skin. Glow comes from light, not blur.
- **Saturation rich, not clipping:** push vibrance to commercial level but stop before neon, banding or blown channels.
- **Gloss, not grease:** highlights read luminous/wet, never oily-plastic.
- **Kill the AI tells:** no over-sharpening, halo edges, uncanny symmetry or too-perfect everything.
- **Whites clean, blacks rich (not crushed)** — keep detail in both highlights and shadows.
- **Litmus test:** if a frame looks like a 3D render or a filter, pull the effect back ~20%.

### AO.8 — Subject energy & performance (always alive, never robotic)

The subject is a living performer in *every* concept — only the **intensity** of her energy changes, never her aliveness.

- **Universal baseline (all concepts):** Aira always moves like a real human — natural hand gestures, body language, weight shifts, head tilts, real blinks, breath, and genuine micro-expressions. **Never** robotic, stiff or AI-stilted movement; **never** a frozen / static smile, a blank dead-eyed stare, or mannequin stillness. Static or robotic performance instantly breaks realism and throws away all the detail work — treat it as a hard fail.
- **Fluid body motion — everywhere, always.** Aira's body moves like liquid: every motion smooth, continuous and flowing, one beat melting into the next — never stiff, jerky, snappy or robotic. Motion travels *through* the body like a wave (hips → spine → shoulders → hands → fingertips) instead of isolated rigid limbs; hair, clothing and jewelry lag and trail with natural follow-through and weight. Even at high speed she stays graceful and controlled — a dancer's fluency, never twitchy. This applies in every concept and every frame.
- **Living stillness — never frozen, even when standing still.** When Aira simply stands or holds in one place, her body must still read as a real human at rest, not a paused mannequin: soft breathing that moves the chest and shoulders, tiny natural weight shifts and sways, small head / hand micro-adjustments, real blinks and subtle eye movement, a gentle settle rather than a hard lock. Standing still does not mean a still body — there is always quiet, believable life. A perfectly motionless, breathless hold instantly reads as unreal / AI; treat it as a hard fail.
- **High-energy concepts** (electric / mischievous / curious-confident — Product Demo, Transformation, Hair Reel, Dance, Trend, Fitness, Empowerment): she is dynamic and in motion — expressive gestures, real movement, confident performance energy; a *moving performer*, not a posed model. This sits on top of the scene's kinetic elements (AO.4) and the moving-elements mandate (AO.6).
- **Calmer concepts** (Wellness / self-care, contemplative / tender, ASMR-led, quiet-luxury): lower the *amplitude*, not the life. These are **not** low-energy or static — they must be **equally captivating in their own register**: slow, graceful, deliberate, intimate motion — soft natural hand movement, gentle gestures, real breathing, and present, expressive eyes. Serene, never sleepy, frozen or flat.
- **In stills (AT.3):** capture this as a *frozen / suspended instant* of real motion — mid-gesture, the peak of a hair swing, a genuine in-between expression — not a posed, static, smile-at-camera frame. The movement itself plays out in the video.

---

## Part AO-G — Scale & Grandeur (Beauty Hero)

Beauty ads should feel **vast, unimaginably beautiful and stunning** — but channeled, not generic spectacle.

- Build **grand, surreal worlds**: impossible skies, oceanic scale, floating fabric, light that doesn't exist in reality, dreamlike sets.
- **The face and product always stay the hero.** Scale serves the beauty moment; it never swallows it. Grand world → intimate, flawless, luminous face/product anchor.
- Rule of thumb: *scale up the world and the lighting; keep the beauty hero tight and pristine.* If the spectacle buries the product, pull back.
- **Out-of-this-world bar (beauty & editorial):** beauty and editorial concepts should look *unreal-beautiful* — flawless, luminous, jaw-dropping. Push set design, scale and light to gallery / campaign quality (use the vast studios in Part AY), but hold AO.7 believability and keep the face/product the pristine hero.

---

## Part AO-S — Platform-Native Social Engagement (IG / FB / YT)

The directive's **scroll-stopper checklist** already handles the mechanics (first-1.5s hook, cut rhythm, audio hook, subject staging, loop point / payoff) — keep using it. This part only adds the feed-energy layer it's missing:

- **Phone-bright:** high contrast and saturation so it pops on a small screen in daylight (per AO.1).
- **9:16 native** with caption/UI **safe zones** kept clear top and bottom.
- **Lead with faces + emotion + energy** on the cover / first frame.
- **Carousels are a real reach lever, not just video** — strong concepts (especially Listicle / Countdown, Before & After, and tutorials) can also be cut as multi-image carousels; carousels currently out-engage standalone reels on a per-post basis, so repurpose key concepts into both formats rather than only video.
- **Shoppable / product tagging:** when a real product is featured (AS / Part P), tag it natively so the reel is shoppable — keep the product hero-locked and the tags out of the safe zones (BA.6).

---

## Part AO-R — GRWM Default Reset (Contemporary Vivid)

The base directive's GRWM defaults to rooted, traditional, emotionally heavy and muted — a sad-girl short film. Reset the default:

- **Colorful, beautiful, outstanding, contemporary.** A stylish modern woman in a bright, beautiful space — upbeat and aspirational.
- **"Normal Indian," not rooted.** This is a *styling/setting* default, **not** an identity change. Aira stays Indian — her face, features and skin (identity lock unchanged). What changes is the aesthetic: contemporary/global-modern wardrobe (Pillars 1/2/3) and bright, stylish interiors instead of temple-festive-gajra territory.
- **Lighter stakes, brighter mood.** Keep the relatability and the specific moment, drop the melancholy-by-default.
- **Rooted / festive styling is opt-in only** — heritage looks, embellished braids, floral buns, traditional settings are available for explicitly festive reels, never the baseline.
- Voice ratio stays GRWM-friendly; tone shifts to fun/confident over confessional.
- **Make the single-location get-ready captivating** — GRWM is shot in one place, so run every GRWM concept through the **GRWM Captivation Kit (Part BD)** to keep it catchy, scroll-stopping and rewatch-worthy.

---

## Part AO-X — Subject Consistency (Aira)

### Subject line

> Aira [placeholder]
> 

### Guardrails (non-negotiable)

- Adult and non-sexualized: any build reference stays neutral and only for wardrobe fit — never enumerate or emphasize individual body parts.
- Identity consistency comes from a reusable generated character sheet, not photographs of a real person.
- Build the character sheet with multiple locked angles (front, three-quarter, profile) so any anchor angle stays on-model. Nano Banana Pro stills accept many reference images (up to about 14, or 5 consistent subjects), so don't cap the sheet at a few; for video, VEO 3.1 Ingredients to Video uses up to 3 references per clip — feed it the 3 best angles for each shot.

## Part AO-H — Aira Is the Hero (she elevates the look, not the reverse)

In every regular concept Aira herself is the hero — her charm, presence and expression are what make the frame work. The outfit, makeup, hair and product are *supporting cast*: she makes **them** look good, not the other way around. A look should never be carrying her; her magnetism carries the look.

- **Charisma is the constant — preserve it everywhere.** Across every concept, register and frame, Aira reads as warm, magnetic and alive — an irresistibly likable, screen-owning presence (charm and charisma, always adult and non-sexualized — AO-X). This never switches off; only its *amplitude* shifts with the register (playful and electric in high-energy reels, soft and luminous in calm ones — AO.8).
- **She elevates the styling, not the reverse.** Pick wardrobe (AW), makeup (AQ) and hair (AP) that *suit and flatter* her — but the frame must land because *she* sells it. If a look only works because the garment or makeup is loud, the concept is upside-down: dial the styling back and let her presence lead.
- **The litmus test:** strip the look down to a plain outfit and bare-ish makeup — does she *still* own the frame on charm and expression alone? She should. The styling then adds to an already-magnetic hero; it never props up a flat one.
- **Reinforces the hierarchy (three-performer 60/30/10 + hero-lock AO-G):** subject first, product second, world third. Scale, wardrobe and spectacle all *serve* Aira; none of them upstage her face and presence.
- **It lives in the performance (AO.8) and the eyes — not the clothes.** The charm reads through genuine expression, a warm gaze to camera, real micro-reactions and living motion. A gorgeous outfit on a dead, blank performance fails this rule; a magnetic, alive Aira makes even a simple look shine.
- **Cute, not childish.** When a concept calls for it, Aira can read as charming, playful and adorable — but always as an adult woman: cuteness comes from expression, warmth and styling, never from childlike or infantilized cues (no baby-voice, no juvenile posing, no little-girl wardrobe). Keep wardrobe and makeup age-appropriate for a 25-year-old — sweet and playful is welcome; childish is not (ties to the AO-X adult / non-sexualized lock and AW wardrobe).

---

## Part AO-N — Aesthetic exclusions (no festival-kitsch lighting · reinvented color-powder)

Two hard aesthetic bans that hold across **every** concept, on top of the "not rooted by default" reset (AO-R). These are about *kitsch*, not about Aira's identity — her Indian identity lock is untouched (AO-X).

- **No Diwali-like "bad lights" — anywhere, ever.** Never light a concept with cheap festival-kitsch lighting: strings of fairy / twinkle lights, diya / oil-lamp clusters, marigold-and-light decor, gaudy multicolor blinking or rope lights, or any "festival decoration" lighting scheme. They read tacky and instantly cheapen the frame. Light every concept with clean, motivated, cinematic light instead — high-key glossy beauty light (AO.2), sculpted dimensional light (AZ.2), window daylight, warm practicals, ring-light or vanity-bulb glow. This holds *even for festive concepts*: a festive reel still uses elevated, tasteful light, never string-light kitsch.
- **Reinvent any Holi-like color-powder beat — never the Indian festival.** The color-powder / pigment-burst visual stays in the toolkit (it's a gorgeous medium — AT.5 Spin-Transform, AX.3a Chaotic-Beautiful), but it must be rendered as an **abstract, editorial, surreal color event** — clouds of pigment blooming in a clean studio or dreamworld, fashion-film color smoke, paint-in-water — **not** the Indian festival Holi: no festival crowd, no religious / cultural festival framing, no rooted Holi iconography or setting. Strip the "festival" read entirely and keep only the pure, beautiful color-in-motion as a styled visual.
- **Why:** the brand look is contemporary, global-modern and premium (AO-R). Festival-kitsch lighting and literal-festival staging pull it back toward the rooted, dated look we're deliberately moving away from. Keep the *beauty* of color and light; drop the festival-kitsch read.

- **Curated random, not pure random:** roll within the styles tagged for the reel's pillar/register so the pull always fits. (Use the # column as a d30 roll, re-roll if best-fit clashes.)
- **Motion matters:** each style carries a motion behavior that plugs into the 60/30/10 energy.
