## Part AR — Audio & Sound Design (incl. Beauty ASMR)

On Reels / Shorts, sound *is* retention — design it as deliberately as the visuals.

- **Spoken line — applies to GRWM *and* beauty ads:** at some point Aira *says* a few words — a question, a bold claim, a secret/tease, or a relatable "POV" line, on-camera or as VO. **Language: English always, in a natural, authentic Indian accent** (never exaggerated or caricatured); sprinkle in **at most one or two Hindi words, and only occasionally** — a light anchor like *arre, suno, haan, na, sach* — **never a full Hindi phrase or sentence** (many lines can run 100% English). This is deliberate: the voice models sound most natural and human in English, while heavy or formal Hindi is what pushed yesterday's delivery into stiff, robotic 'news-anchor' territory. Examples of intent: a question ("the one step everyone skips?"), a tease ("nobody tells you this…"), a claim ("this changed my whole base"), a POV setup.
- **Tone & substance — bold, confident, meaningful:** every phrase is delivered with conviction — punchy, self-assured, magnetic; never filler, hedging or hesitant. It must *mean something specific to that reel* (tied to the product, the look, or the GRWM moment) — not a generic line that could be pasted onto any video. Short, declarative, quotable.
- **Human delivery — never robotic:** the voice must sound like a real person talking, not TTS. Natural speaking rhythm and pacing, conversational cadence, real micro-pauses and breaths, subtle pitch/emphasis shifts and a warm human timbre. Allow tiny natural imperfections — a breath, a soft laugh, a quick *"haan"/"umm"*, a trailing word — so it feels spontaneous and in-the-moment. Match emotion to the words; avoid flat, monotone, evenly-stressed or over-enunciated TTS delivery. When on-camera, lip-sync must align cleanly and mouth movement must look natural.
- **Randomize WHERE she speaks — never a fixed slot.** Her spoken moment must land at a *different* point from concept to concept — sometimes the opener, sometimes mid-build, sometimes on the reveal/payoff, sometimes a throwaway aside. Do **not** default it to the start (nor always the middle or end); vary it reel to reel so it never feels templated. Roll the placement like a hairstyle.
- **Hook still gets covered either way:** when the line lands at the open it doubles as the verbal hook; when it lands later, the first-second hook is carried by the visual frame + audio beat (AO-S) instead.
- **Trending audio:** pick a current platform-trending track where it fits; lock the hook/drop to the first beat.
- **Beat-map:** map cuts and reveals to the beats — the biggest visual moment lands on the biggest beat/drop.
- **Beauty ASMR layer:** foreground tactile product sound — cap clicks, pump/spray, brush sweeps, cream squish, tap-tap on glass, fabric rustle. Clean, close, satisfying.
- **Voice (AIRA PRIME)** sits above the music; duck music under VO; **English-always, Indian-accented delivery with only an occasional one- or two-word Hindi accent** (per the language rule above).
- **SFX accents:** whoosh on snappy transitions; sparkle/shimmer on glow and reveal beats.
- **Mix discipline:** VO clear, music supportive, SFX crisp, nothing clipping; design the audio to loop seamlessly.
- **Captions on by default** for sound-off viewing — but the sound design rewards sound-on.
- **Per-frame SFX — itemize precisely in every video prompt's audio section.** For each frame, the video prompt's audio section must list *every* diegetic sound the frame needs — never a vague "add sound." For each one: **name the source** (petals fluttering, cap click, fabric whip, footstep on marble — never "a magical noise"); **tie it to its action and moment** (what triggers it, and when in the clip); **give it a full envelope** (attack → body → tail, so it never sounds cut off — e.g. "a whoosh that swells, then snaps off clean"); and **match the space's acoustics** (bright reverb in a glass hall, dry and airy outdoors). Layer simultaneous sounds for fullness (petals + wind + her breath). Goal: the clip arrives sonically *complete*, so nothing has to be added in post.
- **Time accent SFX to the action — never to dead air.** Punchy accent sounds (whoosh, snap, swish, sparkle, impact) must land *exactly* on the moment the move happens — the frame of the hair flip, the cap click, the petal swirl, the reveal hit, the camera whip — synced tight, never floating loosely before or after it, and never dropped onto a static beat where nothing moves to justify it. The rule: **a move earns a sound; no move, no accent.** A misplaced whoosh reads as fake instantly. Lock each accent to its AT.4 timeline timestamp and the AR beat-map.
- **But never let a frame go empty — keep a subtle ambient bed under every frame.** Between the accents, every frame still carries a low, continuous layer of quiet ambient sound — soft room tone, gentle air / breeze, distant texture, faint fabric / skin / breath — so no frame ever feels dead, silent or hollow. This bed stays subtle and sits *under* both the accents and the post master track; it fills the in-clip silence the way the music fills the overall reel. Itemize it in the audio section too (e.g. "low room tone + soft air throughout") so VEO always generates a base of presence rather than dead air.
- **Include the subject's own Foley — the sounds Aira herself makes.** Don't only sound the product and the magic — itemize the sounds *her body and actions* generate too: footsteps (heel clicks on marble, a soft pad on a rug), a door opening or closing, a hand clap, a finger snap, the rustle of her clothing as she moves or turns, a bracelet/jewelry tinkle, picking up or setting down the product, a chair scrape, the swish of her hair on a flip. Run each through the same discipline — **source · action · moment · envelope · acoustics** — and sync it to the exact frame the action happens (per the timing rule above). When she *does* something, you should *hear* it: this is what makes her presence feel physically real instead of a silent mime floating over a music bed.
- **Diegetic SFX only inside the clip — no in-clip music.** Tell VEO to generate *only* the real-world action sounds plus Aira's reaction vocals/breaths, and explicitly request **no background music** in the generation — the one master track is added later in the edit (see Master Track Brief below), and any clip-baked music would fight it.
- **Reaction vocals are non-verbal & universal** — breaths, a soft "whoa", a small gasp, a quiet laugh as she reacts to a beat (e.g. being swept into a transformation). These read human in *any* language and sidestep the spoken-language rule; keep them small and real, never theatrical, and sync them in the dedicated voice layer when consistency matters.
- **Regenerate, don't post-patch.** Native clip audio varies, so QC each clip's sound; if an SFX is missing, incomplete or wrong, **regenerate that clip** rather than fixing sound in post. Precise SFX prompt + regenerate-don't-patch = clips that arrive finished.

### AR-MASTER — Per-concept master background track (Gemini Music brief)

End **every concept** with a precise, detailed **Master Track Brief** — the spec to paste into the Gemini app's music-generation feature (with the finished reel uploaded) so it generates one continuous instrumental bed for the whole stitched reel. Background music stays **subtle**: it fills the silence and the void, and never competes with VO, reactions or SFX. The brief must specify:

- **Genre / style** — e.g. dreamy cinematic electronica with a soft pulse.
- **Mood + emotional arc** — how it feels and how it travels (e.g. curious & airy → building wonder → euphoric peak → warm resolve).
- **Instrument palette** — e.g. soft piano, airy synth pad, light hand percussion, sub-bass.
- **Tempo + key** — e.g. ~90 BPM, A minor (for coherence and beat-matching).
- **Energy arc with hit-point timecodes** — where it builds and where the peak/drop lands, tied to the actual reel timecodes (e.g. "soft to 0:15, build to a drop at 0:18 on the swirl, peak on the reveal at 0:21, resolve by 0:30").
- **Reference vibe** — "feels like" a named score, artist or mood, to steer it fast.
- **Length** — the exact reel runtime.
- **Instrumental only** — no lyrics or vocals (never fight Aira's VO); leave **mid-range headroom** so the voice sits on top and the music ducks cleanly.
- **Avoid** — no genre shifts or sudden tonal jumps mid-track.
- **Volume — keep it LOW, a background bed only (never full).** The master track is *never* at full 100% volume. It sits well under the voice, reaction vocals and SFX — just loud enough to fill the silence and the quiet/empty stretches so the reel never feels bare or hollow. Mix it as an ambient under-layer (rough guide: clearly below the VO level), and **duck it down further** under any spoken line, reaction sound or key SFX so those always sit cleanly on top. It should be *felt* more than *heard*: if a viewer notices the music competing with the voice or the action, it's too loud — pull it back. State this in the brief too ("subtle background bed, low volume, sits under VO/SFX") so Gemini doesn't generate something that wants to dominate.

**Workflow:** stitch the reel (picture + diegetic SFX + Aira's voice/reactions) → upload to Gemini → paste this brief → generate one instrumental master at the reel's length → lay it under the whole reel, ducked low. Give each concept its *own* distinct track identity — consistency within a concept, variety across the set.

### AR — Fast Audio Finishing (10-minute checklist)

A quick, repeatable pass to finish a reel's sound without overproducing:

1. **QC each clip's diegetic audio** — every itemized SFX present, complete and synced; regenerate any clip that's wrong rather than post-patching.
2. **Stitch the picture** with beat-locked cuts (AO.4 / AR beat-map).
3. **Check the ambient bed** carries under every frame — no dead silence anywhere.
4. **Generate the master track** from the AR-MASTER brief (Gemini, finished reel uploaded).
5. **Lay it under, low** — ducked below VO, reaction vocals and key SFX (AR-MASTER volume rule).
6. **Place the spoken line** at its rolled position; confirm clean lip-sync.
7. **Confirm the loop** — does the end audio flow back into the open (AX.5 perfect loop)?
8. **Final mix pass** — VO clear, music supportive, SFX crisp, nothing clipping; captions on.

---

## Part AS — Product-Hero Spec (Beauty Ads)

The base directive's **Part P — Beauty Product Performance Protocol** already covers product rendering (performance move, label readability, build-up vs. payoff, hyper-real texture, believability, three-performer fit). **Use Part P as-is — just re-lit bright per AO.1–AO.2.** This part only adds the beauty-makeup beats Part P doesn't spell out:

- **Swatch moment:** product swatched on skin showing true color and finish.
- **Application beat:** Aira applying it — the satisfying tactile moment (pairs with ASMR, Part AR).
- **Payoff / before → after:** the visible result on skin (glow, color, coverage).
- Everything else (hero glamour shot, texture macro, label-lock, three-performer fit) → defer to Part P; don't restate it.

---

## Part AT — Camera Tricks & Motion (Video Prompts)

Every video prompt should name a deliberate camera move (the directive's CAMERA INTENT rule: declared height/angle/lens *with reason* — never default eye-level 35mm). This part adds a beauty/GRWM/social move library built for the **frame-exact keyframe workflow**.

### AT-V — VEO 3.1 is the ONLY video generation tool (supersedes all other tool routing)

Standing rule: every video clip in this system is generated with **VEO 3.1 (or VEO 3.1 Fast) only**. No Kling, no Runway, no Luma, no Pika — VEO 3.1 is the single video tool. (Stills are still generated with Gemini / Nano Banana per AT.3; that image-vs-video split is unchanged.)

- **This is not a downgrade — VEO 3.1 already does every job the old multi-tool routing did:**
    - **Image-to-video animation** — animate a start still (the original image-to-video job).
    - **Start + end keyframes ("Frames to Video")** — supply a first AND a last frame and VEO 3.1 interpolates between them. This is exactly the locked-keyframe workflow AT.0 / AT.0-K / AT.5-T depend on: hide-then-reveal end-lock, the precise non-negotiable last frame, and match-cut handoffs.
    - **Continuous-shot stitching ("Extend")** — VEO 3.1 extends a clip by continuing from the final second of the previous one, so the "stitch clips into one continuous one-shot" case is native: chain Extend (or set each clip's locked end frame as the next clip's start frame) down the whole shot.
    - **Native synced audio** — VEO 3.1 generates the diegetic SFX, Foley and spoken line in-clip; the entire Part AR audio workflow is built on this.
- **Read every legacy tool name as VEO 3.1.** Wherever this directive still says Kling, Runway, Luma or Pika — including the Tool column of the AT.1 move library and every "needs a tool that accepts a last frame" note — it now means **VEO 3.1**. All the move, transition, keyframe and transformation techniques stay exactly as written; only the tool consolidates.
- **Work to VEO 3.1's envelope:** clips are 4 / 6 / 8s (build the 6-8 frame reel as chained 8s clips per AV / AT.4); 9:16 portrait and 720p/1080p are supported (4K available via upscale); keep one camera move + one subject action per clip (AT.3) — even more important now that a single model does everything. For anything longer than 8s, use Extend rather than forcing one long generation.

### AT.0 — Exploit frame-exact control (start → end keyframes)

We generate the **start frame and the end frame as separate identity-locked stills**, composed so the *difference between them encodes the camera move*. The video model (VEO 3.1) then only has to interpolate the path — which is what makes the trick land cleanly.

- **The start still *is* the clip's opening frame — so fix its exact angle in the image prompt.** Whatever camera position, height, angle, lens / focal length, distance and framing you bake into the start image is *precisely* where the animation begins — the image-to-video model opens *from that exact frame* and moves on from there. So state the angle deliberately in **every** image prompt (e.g. "low three-quarter view from below, 35mm, product lower-left, face upper-right") — never leave it at a vague or default eye-level, or the clip starts in the wrong position. Compose each start still as the intended *first* frame of the move and each end still as its intended *last* frame, and the interpolation lands exactly as planned.
- **Encode the move in the delta:** push-in = wider start → tighter end; orbit = ¾-left start → ¾-right end; rack focus = product-sharp/face-soft start → face-sharp/product-soft end; reveal = occluded start (hand / petal / steam) → clear end.
- **Lock continuity across both keyframes:** identical lighting, color world, wardrobe, hair, makeup, product — *only* the camera/subject pose changes. Any other drift breaks the interpolation.
- **For transitions/match cuts across clips:** design clip A's **end** frame and clip B's **start** frame to share silhouette position / negative space so the cut is seamless.
- **One motion idea per clip.** Chain clips with beat-locked cuts (AO.4 / AR beat-map) rather than stuffing multiple moves into one shot.
- **VEO 3.1 only (AT-V).** One tool does it all: image-to-video animation, start+end keyframe interpolation (Frames to Video), continuous-shot stitching (Extend) and native synced audio / spoken line. No Kling / Runway / Luma / Pika.

### AT.0-K — Continuity-reel discipline + cross-frame object lock (build bit by bit)

Two failure modes break multi-image reels: (1) a **start → end keyframe pair** (AT.0) fed to an image-to-video model interpolates *messily* when the two frames aren't placed precisely; (2) any **object that recurs across frames** mutates — changes shape, color, position or count — when it isn't described identically each time. Both are fixed the same way: build every frame *bit by bit*, placed perfectly, described exactly, so generation is clean and you hit no problems when you generate.

- **Build keyframe pairs bit by bit — nothing messy, nothing confusing:**
    - **Change only what's meant to change.** Between the start and end frame, *only* the intended camera move + the one intended subject action / transformation may differ. Everything else — set, props, object positions, lighting, color world, wardrobe, hair, makeup — stays identical across the pair (AT.0 / AU.4). Any unintended drift is what makes the interpolation warp.
    - **Compose deliberately and cleanly.** Place the subject, product and every prop in clear, stable, non-overlapping positions; leave clean negative space for the motion to travel (BB). A cluttered or ambiguous frame is exactly what sends interpolation messy.
    - **Never set up a bridge the model can't cross.** Avoid a start→end delta that's too big or impossible to smoothly interpolate — huge pose jumps, objects appearing / vanishing, limbs crossing, a busy tangle. If the change is too large, split it into more frames / clips rather than forcing one messy clip (AT.0: one motion idea per clip).
    - **Spell out the exact difference.** State unambiguously what moves, how far and in which direction between start and end, so there's zero confusion; confirm it passes the first-time-viewer clarity test (BA.0). Bit-by-bit clarity in = clean motion out.
- **Cross-frame object lock — the "chair rule":**
    - **Describe every recurring object in precise, repeatable detail, then reuse that description verbatim.** Any object that appears in more than one frame — a chair, a vanity, a mug, a vase, a bottle, a rug, a plant, a painting — gets a detailed lock the first time and the *exact same wording* in every later frame. Not "a chair" but e.g. "a cream bouclé accent chair with tapered light-oak legs and a single vertical seam down the backrest." Vague = the model reinvents it and it won't match.
    - **Keep an object / set continuity sheet per concept** (the prop equivalent of Aira's character sheet, AO-X): list each recurring object *once* with its locked spec — material, color, shape, finish, size, distinguishing details — and paste that block into every frame prompt that includes it.
    - **Lock position, orientation and state, not just appearance.** A recurring object holds its placement, angle and condition across frames unless a beat intentionally moves it; props set down stay put; nothing changes color, shape or count between frames (BA.4 / AU.4).
    - **Reuse a reference image where possible.** Reuse the same generated reference for a recurring object / set the way we reuse Aira's, so frame 2's chair is frame 1's chair.
    - **This covers the whole set, not just single props.** The room, the wall, the window, the mirror and the light fixtures must read as the *same* space in every frame — same geography, same light direction (BA.1 / BA.2).
- **Identity must be carried by the keyframes — never *revealed by* the interpolation (the face-anchor rule).** A video tool only knows Aira's face from the frames you hand it — the start frame (and the end frame, if the tool accepts one). It cannot guess her correctly. Her identity has to live *in those frames*, never be discovered by the model mid-clip.
    - **Every clip that shows her face must START on her face — clearly recognizable and identity-locked (AO-X).** Never begin a clip with her face hidden, occluded, turned away or absent and then *reveal* it during the animation: if the start frame has no face, the model fabricates one when it appears and it will not match her. This holds for the start of **every** frame / clip across the 6–8 (frame 2, 3, 4 … 8), not just the first.
    - **"Recognizable" means a clear likeness at any flattering angle — NOT a flat full-front face every time.** A dead-on, passport-style frontal face on every clip looks amateur / beginner. Front, three-quarter and side profile are all valid anchors, as long as her actual identity-locked features read clearly as *her* — a **three-quarter** angle is often the sweet spot (most flattering *and* the most identity-rich). Vary the angle clip to clip for a premium, cinematic look. What's banned is only a start with **no usable likeness**: the back of her head, face fully turned away, fully occluded, a featureless skin macro, or an unlit silhouette — *that* gives the model nothing to anchor, so it invents her. A side profile still anchors her; an absent face does not.
        - **Lock multiple angles in her character sheet (AO-X) so any anchor angle stays on-model.** Build the sheet with front, three-quarter *and* profile references, so a side-profile start matches *her* rather than a guess the model infers from a front-only reference.
        - **A big angle *change* within one clip is itself a reveal.** If a clip *starts* in profile and turns toward full-front, the front of her face is being revealed mid-animation — handle it with the same care (start+end keyframes, or keep the turn within a modest range the sheet locks). A clip that holds roughly one angle is always safe.
    - **A face anchored at the start holds the whole clip; a face only at the end fixes only the end.** With her face in the start frame, every interpolated in-between stays her. If the face is missing at the start and correct only at the end keyframe, the middle is a guessy, drifting morph that snaps right only in the last moment — bad even when the final frame is correct. So lead with her face and keep the move's delta modest (identity is weakest in the middle of a clip).
    - **Brief turn-away → come back; a long turn-away should NOT turn back in that shot.** If her face leaves the frame for only 2–3 frames (a quick glance away, a short turn), it returns essentially intact — let her face the camera again. But if she stays turned away, or faces the other direction, for a long stretch, do NOT bring her face back to camera within that same clip — the returning face would be a drifting re-invention that no longer matches her. Make the turn-back its own fresh clip that STARTS on her locked face (cut), or supply both keyframes — never resolve a long hidden span back to her face through the interpolation.
    - **If a frame is meant to be face-free, say so explicitly in the prompt.** When a beat only needs her back, the back of her head, an over-the-shoulder, a silhouette, or any framing where her face isn't required, state it plainly in that frame's prompt — "back shot, face not visible," "shot from behind, no face," "over-the-shoulder, face turned away" — so the model doesn't try to render (and botch) a face that was never meant to be there. Lock her *non-face* identity instead — hair, outfit, body styling, posture — so the shot still reads unmistakably as Aira from behind, and never quietly drifts toward a half-turned face the tool has to invent.
    - **When a beat genuinely needs a hidden-face → reveal, don't animate across the gap — use one of these:**
        - **Reverse-a-push-in (easy cases only):** generate a clip that *starts* on her full, locked face and pushes IN to the macro — one clean camera move, identity anchored from frame one — then **reverse it** in the edit so it plays macro → pull-back to her face. Use only when the *only* motion is the camera: gentle breathing reverses fine, but a one-way blink, hair fall, falling droplet or product being set down reads wrong backward.
        - **Start + end keyframes, both locked:** supply the occluded / macro shot as the start *and* a correct, identity-locked face shot as the end, so the model interpolates *toward* a face you already defined (VEO 3.1 accepts a last frame — Frames to Video).
        - **Cut, don't interpolate:** make the hidden / macro / occluded shot its own clip, then **hard-cut** to a separate clip that *starts* on her locked face — the reveal lands on the cut, never through the interpolation (the AT.0-K bridge rule: a faceless-start → face delta is a bridge the model can't cross).
    - **Default = lead every face clip with her established face.** Most reels won't fit the reverse trick, so don't rely on it: reverse / start+end / cut are the tools for the *hard* cases, while the everyday rule is simply to never design a clip that has to *find* her face partway through. Keep an eye on this on every single frame.

### AT.1 — Camera move library

| # | Move | Use / beat | Frame-exact setup (start → end) | Tool |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 1 | Slow Push-In (dolly) | Build suspense toward hero | Wider → tight macro on product/eye | VEO 3.1 |
| 2 | Pull-Back Reveal | Reveal world / context | Tight on face/product → wide | VEO 3.1 |
| 3 | Orbital Arc / 360 | Premium hero spin | ¾-left → ¾-right (or full turn) | VEO 3.1 |
| 4 | Crash / Snap Zoom | Punch hook on a beat | Wide → extreme close, motion blur | VEO 3.1 |
| 5 | Whip Pan transition | Energetic cut between looks | Clip A end blur L→R ≈ clip B start blur | VEO 3.1 |
| 6 | Match Cut | Seamless transform (bare→glam, product→result) | Align silhouette/negative space: A-end = B-start | VEO 3.1 (frame-exact) |
| 7 | Speed Ramp | Slow-mo → real-time on the drop | Keyframe the freeze/peak moment | VEO 3.1 |
| 8 | Rack Focus (focus pull) | Shift attention product ↔ face | Product sharp/face soft → reverse | VEO 3.1 |
| 9 | Dolly Zoom (vertigo) | Surreal hero emphasis — use sparingly | Push in while widening FOV | VEO 3.1 |
| 10 | Parallax 2.5D | Depth on a near-flat hero | Separate foreground/background layers | VEO 3.1 |
| 11 | Tilt Reveal | Pan product → up to face (or reverse) | Start on product → end on eyes | VEO 3.1 |
| 12 | Overhead Flatlay Rotate | Top-down product/tools spin | 0° → rotated | VEO 3.1 |
| 13 | Through-Mirror Move | GRWM signature (directive: ≥1×) | Camera moves to/through reflection | VEO 3.1 |
| 14 | Macro Slider (lateral) | Glide across texture / swatch | Left of swatch → right, slow-mo | VEO 3.1 |
| 15 | Floating Orbit (levitation) | IMPOSSIBLE — counts as the one (AO.4) | Product floats; camera orbits it | VEO 3.1 |
| 16 | Hyperlapse / Time-warp | Fast transformation montage | Keyframe each stage | VEO 3.1 |
| 17 | Handheld Micro-Move | UGC authenticity (research-backed) | Subtle sway, not locked-off | VEO 3.1 (low motion) |
| 18 | FPV Swoop | Grand-world entrance (AO-G hero only) | Wide swoop into hero anchor | VEO 3.1 |

### AT.2 — Rules

- **Camera moves are real-physics → unlimited** (AO.4). But a camera doing something *physically impossible* (passing through a solid bottle, teleporting) counts as the **one impossible move** for that shot.
- **Match move to beat:** hook = snap/whip/crash-in or fast push; build = orbit / slider / rack focus; reveal/payoff = speed-ramp + push-in or pull-back on the drop (AR beat-map).
- **Slow-mo on texture moments** (foundation drop, brush sweep, cream squish) — the premium cue real beauty ads use.
- **Stay motivated & believable (AO.7):** smooth, intentional moves; if interpolation morphs or warps, simplify the start→end delta rather than pushing harder.

### AT.3 — Keep the tools from getting confused (Gemini image vs VEO video)

The two tools do opposite jobs. **Split the labor and never mix motion language into a still prompt** — this is the #1 cause of confused/struggling output.

#### Gemini image (Nano Banana) — stills ONLY

- **Prompt-length cap — never exceed the image tool's input limit, and stay FAR below it for quality.** Gemini's image models accept enormous text inputs, so the hard token ceiling is *never* the real constraint: Gemini 2.5 Flash Image (original Nano Banana) ≈ 32,768 input tokens; Gemini 3 Pro Image (Nano Banana Pro) ≈ 65,536; Gemini 3.1 Flash Image (Nano Banana 2) ≈ 131,072. (≈ 100 tokens ≈ 60-80 English words, so even the *smallest* ceiling is roughly 20,000+ words — no sane still prompt comes close.) The limit that actually bites is **quality**: the image model drops details, garbles and reinvents the frame the moment a prompt gets bloated. So the working rule is a tight practical cap, not the technical one — keep every still prompt to a focused, structured block (rough target **≈ 150-250 words, hard stop well under ~350**), one clear subject + product + background, no run-ons. If a prompt is creeping past that, it's doing too much — split the scene into more keyframes/clips (AT.0) or push detail into the reference image / character sheet (AO-X) instead of piling on words. Short, declarative, lead with the most important element beats a long wall of text every time.
- **Describe the FRAME, not the movement.** Translate every camera move into a *static* composition: framing + lens/focal length + angle + focus plane + depth of field. Push-in → "wide framing" still vs "tight macro" still; orbit → two fixed angles; rack focus → state which plane is sharp in each still; whip pan → render directional motion-blur as a static effect; speed-ramp → the single frozen peak moment.
- **No motion verbs** (dolly, orbit, pan, zoom, track, push, swoop) — a still model can't act on them and they muddy the frame.
- **One clear subject + product + background.** Don't overload; Gemini degrades when juggling many objects, precise counts, or complex spatial relationships.
- **Positive description beats negatives** — it tends to ignore "no X." Describe what you *do* want in frame. Keep any negatives short.
- **Hold identity via the reference image + a consistent short character description**, not a wall of adjectives.
- **Text rendering is now a STRENGTH — use it (Nano Banana Pro).** Gemini 3 Pro Image (Nano Banana Pro) is best-in-class at legible in-image text, including long passages and multiple languages — so you *may* render taglines, on-screen hook copy, and even product-label / poster text directly in the still. Spell-check every rendered word in the AU.6 QC pass and regenerate if a glyph is off. Only two cases still belong in the edit, not the generation: *guaranteed-perfect* legal / claim / brand copy, and any *animated* text. (Render text on **Pro** — the original Nano Banana and Nano Banana 2 are weaker at text.)
- **Match-cut / transition keyframes:** just compose the two stills to align (silhouette / negative space). No transition or "cut to" wording in the image prompt.

#### VEO 3.1 — motion + audio

- **This is where the camera move lives.** ONE camera move + ONE subject action per clip (AT.0). Stacking moves causes morphing/warping.
- **Max one physics-breaking move** (AO.4); unlimited real-physics energy is fine.
- **State move, subject action, and audio separately and clearly** — music/SFX/ASMR, plus the spoken line in quotes and kept short. Don't bury them in one run-on sentence.
- **Keep clips short**; don't choreograph multiple subjects or many simultaneous events in one generation.
- **Trim the negative prompt** — don't dump all of Part U; keep the few negatives that matter for this shot.
- **When feeding start+end keyframes to VEO 3.1 (Frames to Video)**, the prompt should only *name the move* connecting them and stay minimal, so the model follows the frames instead of fighting them.

#### Both tools

- **Short, declarative, structured prompts** beat long run-ons; lead with the most important element.
- **No contradictions in one prompt** (bright vs moody, sharp vs blurred, calm vs frantic).
- **One idea per prompt.** Let the keyframe workflow and beat-locked cuts chain the complexity — never a single overloaded prompt.

### AT.4 — Timed beat sequencing (so VEO doesn't crush every command at once)

VEO's #1 failure mode: given several actions in one prompt, it tries to do them **all simultaneously** — collapsing the shot into a chaotic, morphing mess. Fix it by handing VEO an explicit **timeline string** so it runs the beats **in sequence**.

- **Always include a timeline in the VEO prompt.** Break the clip into **2–4 timestamped segments** and assign one beat to each. Template:
    
    `Timeline (8s): 0.0–2.0s — [subject action + camera move]; 2.0–5.0s — [next action]; 5.0–8.0s — [payoff + camera move]. Audio: [music bed] throughout; spoken line at 3.5s: "…"; SFX [whoosh] at 5.0s.`
    
- **One action per segment** — never list two simultaneous actions inside the same time block.
- **Put camera + subject + audio on the same clock** so the move, the action and the beat land exactly where intended (ties to AR beat-map + randomized spoken-line placement).
- **Match segments to clip length** (per-clip ≈ 8s; AV / runtime) — keep it 2–4 beats; more overloads one generation.
- **Biggest visual moment lands on the biggest beat / drop timestamp** (AR).
- **With start → end keyframes (VEO 3.1 Frames to Video):** keep the timeline minimal — the keyframes already encode the move; the timeline just paces the in-between (e.g. `0.0–8.0s: smooth push-in from start frame to end frame`).
- **Chronological order only** — write segments in the order they happen; don't scatter them.
- Still obey AT.3: one camera move + one subject action in focus, max one impossible move (AO.4), trimmed negatives.

### AT.5 — Signature Surreal Shot: the Spin-Transform Reveal

Aira's flagship transformation mechanic — a magical fast spin that transforms her look, outfit or world in a single move. It's the signature beat for Transformation (#2), Hair Reels (#4), GRWM reveals and Cinematic / Surreal films (AX.3).

- **The mechanic:** Aira turns / spins; the transformation happens *during* the blur of the turn; she emerges mid-spin in the new state and settles into a hero pose. The spin is the cover for the change — the single impossible move (AO.4).
- **The performance arc (7 beats):** Notice → swept-up → Spin → Stop + burst → Stumble → Recover → Hero. Keep it human: a tiny stumble / recover on the landing sells weight and realism (AO.8), then she lands the confident hero beat.
- **Physics rules:** the *transformation* is the one impossible move; the spin itself, hair, fabric and any particles still obey real physics (BA.3). The medium (petals, light, fabric, color) flows believably; identity stays locked through and after the spin (AU.4); the product, if present, ends as the hero.
- **Worked example ("Fragrance Realm"):** close on Aira mid-thought → a ribbon of light sweeps in → she spins → on the stop, a burst of petals and the new gown / world materialize → a half-step stumble → she recovers → lands the hero pose as the master track drops.
- **15-variant bench (rotate the *medium*, then the *destination*):** petals · light-ribbons · color-powder (abstract pigment — not festival Holi, AO-N) · water / splash · silk / fabric swirl · sparks / embers · falling flowers · paint / ink bloom · glass shards reassembling · autumn leaves · snow / frost · sand → gold · feathers · butterflies · stardust. Pair each with a destination (new outfit · new hair · new makeup · new world · product reveal).
- **Rotation rule:** never repeat the same medium back-to-back; log it (Anti-Sameness, Part BC). Roll **mechanic × deployment × medium × destination × register** (AT.5-T) so each transformation feels distinct — vary the *mechanic and deployment*, not just the medium.
- **Concept arcs already scoped:** A "Fragrance Realm" · B "Blooming Garden" · C "Glass Rain" · D "Color Storm" · E "Silk Spin" — plus a "Still Center" variant where the world spins around a calm, still Aira.

### AT.5-T — Transformation / Transition Engine (vary the *grammar*, not just the medium)

The catchy media stay — petals, ribbons, water, ripples, light streaks, color, glitter, the whole AT.5 bench. They're gorgeous and we keep leaning on them. The repetition risk was never the *medium*; it's the *grammar* — every transform so far is "she spins and the medium swirls around her." Fix it by treating any transformation as **three independent dials — Mechanic × Deployment × Medium — and rotating all three.** The same beautiful petals can rain, sweep, ripple, bloom or trail instead of only swirling, and the change can be carried by a camera move, an action or a burst of light instead of only a spin. Same catchy ingredients, endlessly different shots.

#### Dial 1 — Mechanic (what hides or drives the change)

- **Spin-Transform (the original):** she spins; the change happens in the blur of the turn (AT.5).
- **Action match-cut:** an action *is* the cut — eyes close → open changed, a finger snap, a hair toss across frame, sit down bare → stand up done.
- **Camera-hidden:** the move hides the change — whip-pan and back, tilt down-and-up, crash-zoom into the eye and out, a pass behind a pillar / plant / doorway.
- **Occlusion / wipe:** something crosses the frame and reveals — hands, a compact, a fan, a swept coat or dupatta, a passing curtain or person.
- **Light-hidden:** the change rides a light shift — a flash or bloom, lights off → on, a beam or shadow sweeping across her.
- **Threshold / walk-through:** she walks through a doorway, a beaded curtain, a wall of mist / steam, or behind a screen and exits changed.
- **Touch-radiate:** she touches the mirror / a flower / the product, and the change ripples *outward from the contact point* rather than around her whole body.
- **World-morph (Still Center):** she stays calm and still while the room / world transforms around her — ideal for calm registers.
- **Dissolve-and-travel:** she disperses into the medium and reforms in a new pose or place.
- **No-magic real cut:** sometimes just a clean beat-drop cut or a genuine match-cut — over-using *any* magic is itself repetition, so not every reel gets a transformation.

#### Dial 2 — Deployment (how the medium behaves — the real key to "differently")

Any medium can be deployed in any of these, so the same petals / water / light never read the same twice:

- **Swirl-around** — orbits her body (the original).
- **Rain / fall** — drifts or pours down; she stands under it or steps through it.
- **Rise / float-up** — lifts upward, reverse-gravity.
- **Sweep-across (wipe)** — a wave / sheet / streak crosses the frame and clears on the new look.
- **Burst-from-point** — explodes outward from a spot (her hand, the product, the floor).
- **Ripple-out** — concentric rings spread from a touch, impact or footstep.
- **Trail / trace** — follows her hand or movement like a comet tail.
- **Curtain / wall** — forms a vertical sheet she walks through (pairs with Threshold).
- **Settle / disperse** — gathers onto her, or scatters off her.
- **Bloom-from-touch** — grows outward from a fingertip contact.
- **Suspended / frozen** — hangs motionless in the air; she or the camera moves through it.

#### Dial 3 — Medium (the catchy ingredient — keep all of them)

The full AT.5 bench, none retired: petals · light-ribbons · color-powder (abstract pigment, not festival Holi — AO-N) · water / splash · ripples · light streaks · silk / fabric · sparks / embers · falling flowers · paint / ink bloom · glass shards · autumn leaves · snow / frost · sand → gold · feathers · butterflies · stardust · glitter / shimmer.

#### Worked proof — one medium (petals), five non-repeating shots

- **Petals + Spin-Transform + swirl-around** → the classic reveal.
- **Petals + Threshold + curtain** → she walks through a falling-petal curtain and exits in the new look.
- **Petals + Touch-radiate + bloom-from-touch** → she touches the mirror and petals bloom outward, the look changing in their wake.
- **Petals + Camera-hidden + sweep-across** → a gust of petals wipes the frame on a whip-pan and clears on the reveal.
- **Petals + World-morph + settle** → she stands still, petals drift in, and the room transforms around her.

#### Rules

- **Rotate the mechanic AND the deployment, never just the medium (BC).** Never the same mechanic or deployment back-to-back; change at least the mechanic + deployment between concepts even when the medium repeats.
- **Match it to the register (fit-gate, AX.0):** energetic → spin / whip / burst; calm → world-morph / light-bloom / settle; grounded or relatable → an action match-cut or a real no-magic cut.
- **Still one impossible move per shot (AO.4 / BA.3):** whatever mechanic you pick, only the transformation breaks reality — the medium and everything else obey real physics.
- **Catchiness is preserved, not traded away:** every one of these still uses the gorgeous media; we're varying *how* they move and *what role* they play, so the feed stays just as stunning without repeating the same shot.
- **Log mechanic × deployment × medium per concept (BC)** so the grammar never repeats across the feed.

#### Keyframe decision — lock the END frame wherever a transform HIDES her then brings her back

A transformation that works by *hiding* her and then bringing her back is the single highest hallucination risk in the whole system: the swirl / blur / occlusion covers the change beautifully, but the moment she **emerges**, the model invents whatever face it likes unless you have handed it a locked end frame. The **petal-swirl is the textbook case** — petals swirl around her, the spin-blur hides the change, and the instant she comes out is a *reveal* the interpolation will guess wrong. So decide this per beat when you build the keyframes (BB) and log it.

- **The rule:** wherever a beat OBSCURES her face (or a transforming look) for more than a brief moment and then has to resolve back to a recognizable, identity-locked her, you MUST either lock BOTH keyframes or cut — never let her emerge as a free interpolation. The obscured middle is the magic cover; both ends carry her identity. This is the sanctioned "supply both keyframes" exception to the long-turn-away rule (AT.0-K): a transform is allowed to bring her face back *because* you lock the end frame.
- **Needs start + end keyframes (lock both) — the "hide-then-reveal" mechanics:**
    - **Spin-Transform (AT.5) — the petal-swirl beat:** start frame = pre-spin recognizable face; end frame = post-spin emerged hero (new look AND clearly her). The swirl covers the middle; both ends are locked. Lock the end here, always.
    - **Occlusion / wipe** — something crosses the frame and clears on the new look: start (pre, locked) + end (post, locked face).
    - **Dissolve-and-travel** — she disperses into the medium and reforms: the reformed end MUST be a locked hero frame, or she reforms as a stranger.
    - **Continuous camera-hidden (whip-pan / crash-zoom away and back) or a continuous push *through* a threshold** — if you keep it one unbroken shot, lock the landing frame.
    - Needs a tool that accepts a last frame — VEO 3.1 (Frames to Video).
- **Also lock start + end for a precise, non-negotiable LAST frame (nothing to do with hiding her).** Any beat where the *ending* must land on an exact composition — a specific hero pose, a perfect-loop closing frame that has to rhyme with the open (AX.5), a match-cut handoff where clip A's end must line up precisely with clip B's start (AT.0 / AT #6), a label-locked product payoff, or a screenshot-worthy final beat — supply that exact frame as the locked end so the model resolves *to* it rather than approximating it. Never leave a frame that *must* land precisely to free interpolation; if you know what the last frame has to be, lock it.
- **Also lock start + end to STITCH clips into one continuous shot (seamless long one-take).** When a reel is meant to read as a single unbroken take across all its frames — clip after clip chained with no visible cut, the whole thing flowing as one long continuous shot — join them at the seams: clip A's locked END frame *becomes* clip B's START frame, clip B's end becomes clip C's start, and so on down the chain. Each internal handoff is a single shared, locked keyframe, so every clip begins exactly where the previous one ended and the joins are invisible; only the true opening frame and the final closing frame are unshared. (VEO 3.1 accepts a last frame — Frames to Video — and pair it with the AT.0-K continuity / object lock so nothing drifts across the seam.)
- **Cut instead (cleaner, cheaper — the default wherever it fits):**
    - **Action match-cut** (eyes close → open, finger snap, hair-toss) — by definition two locked stills hard-cut; no interpolation crosses the gap.
    - **Threshold / doorway / curtain** — the threshold IS the cut (Portal section): cut on the moment of passage and land on a locked face.
    - Any hide-reveal where a continuous morph isn't worth the cost or risk — cut on the peak-blur and START the next clip on her locked face.
- **Reverse-a-push-in (the narrow camera-only case):**
    - Faceless macro → pull-back-to-face where the ONLY motion is the camera: generate face → push in → reverse it in the edit (AT.0-K). NOT for transforms carrying one-way physics (falling petals, a real spin) — those don't reverse cleanly.
- **Start-anchor alone is enough — no end-lock needed for identity — the "stays-visible" beats:**
    - **World-morph / Still Center** — she stays still and recognizable while the WORLD changes around her; her face is never hidden, so the start anchor holds her. (Build the world swap as cut frames, and lock the OBJECTS / set per AT.0-K, not her face.)
    - **Touch-radiate / bloom-from-touch** — the change ripples outward while her face stays in view.
    - **AT.6 micro-moves and simple visible camera moves** (push-in, pull-back, orbit, rack focus) where her face stays in frame throughout — the brief 2-3 frame turn-away rule (AT.0-K) already covers a quick glance away; only a *long* turn needs a cut.
- **Net:** lock the end frame wherever she is hidden then revealed (spin / swirl / occlusion / dissolve / continuous threshold), wherever the ending must land on a precise final frame (hero pose, perfect loop, match-cut handoff, label-locked payoff), and wherever clips must stitch into one continuous one-shot (each seam = one shared locked keyframe); cut wherever a clean break is cleaner (match-cut, doorway); reverse only the camera-only macro; and rely on the start anchor wherever she stays visible (world-morph, touch-radiate, micro-moves).

#### Cut frames vs continuity reels (you do NOT need one continuous shot)

World-builds-around-her, seasons-change and world-morph (Still Center) concepts can be built **either** way — and **cut frames are the better default**, not a compromise. You almost never *have* to render a single unbroken continuity morph.

- **Cut-frame / match-cut (preferred default):** generate each state as its own identity-locked keyframe pair (AT.0), keep **Aira locked** — same pose, position, eye-line and framing (AT.0-K object/pose lock) — and let the **world swap state on the cut** while she holds. Spring → summer → autumn → winter snapping around a still Aira reads *more* striking than a morph, and it's cheaper, sharper and far more reliable (no morph-warping, no identity drift). Mask each cut with a micro-move (AT.6), a whip-pan or a beat-drop (AT.4 / AR). This is the "World-morph / Still Center" mechanic executed as clean cuts.
- **Continuity reel (optional upgrade — use sparingly):** one continuous shot where the world visibly grows / melts / blooms around her with no cut (VEO 3.1 — a single continuous generation, or Extend for a longer one; Extend continues from each clip's final second and can chain to roughly a minute-plus, about 148s total). Use it only for a *single* seamless hero beat where watching the change happen in real time is the whole point — it's harder, costlier and more artifact-prone, so don't build an entire reel on it.
- **Best of both — the usual answer:** chain mostly cut frames and spend *one* continuity micro-clip on the single most magical morph. Whichever you pick, only the change breaks reality (one impossible move — AO.4 / BA.3) and the cross-frame object / set continuity lock holds across every frame (AT.0-K).

#### Portal / threshold travel — one structure, endlessly different reels

A whole format where Aira moves through a series of thresholds — doors, mirrors, curtains — and each one opens on a *different world* (the "endless doors" world, AX.3a). It's the **Threshold mechanic** (Dial 1) chained across several worlds.

- **Build it as cut / sequential frames — the threshold *is* the cut.** You do not need a continuous morph: the doorway physically hides the change, so it's the cleanest, most reliable transition there is. Per world: approach the threshold → (optional short continuity push *through* it to sell the travel) → CUT on the moment of passage → land in the new world, let her react (AX.3a trigger → surprise → smile) → move to the next threshold. Keep Aira identity-locked across every cut (AT.0-K); *only* the world changes. Bridge each cut on the threshold itself (the door swinging, her body passing, a hand on the handle, the dark of the gap) or a beat-drop / whip-pan.
- **Reserve continuity for one beat only** — e.g. a single dreamy push through the most magical doorway; everything else cuts.
- **Vary the method into totally different reels (rotate these dials, BC):**
    - **The portal** — not just a door: a mirror, a wardrobe, an elevator opening on a new floor-world, a curtain, a wall of water / mist, a turning page of a giant book, a painting frame, a ring of light, falling backward into the next world.
    - **What the worlds represent** — seasons · color worlds · eras / decades · moods / registers · elements (sky / water / fire / bloom) · or each world a different *look*.
    - **The purpose (category)** — the *same* portal spine becomes a pure Cinematic / Surreal film (AX.3), an **OOTD** (each door = a new outfit, AW), a **Hair Reel** (each door = a new style, AP), a **makeup transformation** (each door = a new look, AQ), or a **product reel** (each door = a different benefit / result).
    - **The arc** — searching for "the one" world (best saved for last) · cumulative build (each door upgrades her look toward a final glam) · escalation (worlds get more fantastical each time) · **perfect loop** (the last door opens back onto the first — AX.5).
    - **Render style** (AX.3b) and the transition deployment (slam-on-beat · slow dreamy push · whip-pan · fall-through).
- **Camera grammar — change the angle on the *cut*, not inside the shot (controlled, never chaotic).** Within a single passage clip the camera does **one** controlled thing: *either* a locked, steady angle as she moves through, *or* one smooth motivated move (a follow-push toward / through the doorway). **Never swing through several angles inside one clip** — that's exactly what makes the interpolation warp and go messy (AT.0 / AT.3: one camera move + one subject action per clip). Get your variety **across** clips instead: give each new world its own angle, lens and height to match its mood, so the reel still feels dynamic. Best practice — keep a *consistent passage move* through every threshold (so the cuts stay rhythmic and the match-cut bridges cleanly, AT #6), then let the camera **open onto a fresh angle once she lands** in each new world. Dynamic across worlds, controlled within each shot.
- **Net:** one "doors" idea spawns many reels that read as completely different — a seasons-portal, a decades-portal, an outfit-portal, a color-storm-portal, a product-benefit-portal — because the portal, the worlds, the purpose and the arc all rotate. Same spine, totally different reels.

### AT.6 — Signature Micro-Moves (mini swirls, little dance beats, playful flourishes)

The small-scale companion to AT.5. Where the Spin-Transform is the big magical reveal, these are the *little* charming movements that keep a reel alive and scroll-stopping — with **no** transformation and **no** impossible move. A mini twirl, a beat bounce, a quick step-touch, a hair flick. Sprinkle one or two into almost any concept (GRWM, Demo, OOTD, Trend, Dance, even a calm reel at low amplitude).

**Bench — roll & rotate (never the same one back-to-back; log via Part BC):**

- **Mini swirl / half-twirl** — a small graceful spin or skirt-swish that settles back to camera (pure charm, no transform).
- **Shoulder shimmy / body bounce** — a quick playful bounce on the beat.
- **Hip sway / step-touch** — a small two-step or side-to-side sway, casual and rhythmic.
- **Hair flick / tuck** — a light flip or tuck that puts motion in the hair (pairs with AP motion).
- **Hand framing / playful gesture** — framing the face, a little point, a wave, a finger-snap on the beat.
- **Pivot-and-settle** — a quick quarter / half turn into a confident pose (a mini hero-land).
- **Fabric play** — a small twirl of a hem, a sleeve flourish, a coat-swish.
- **Head tilt + smile pop** — a tiny tilt into a genuine smile, timed to a beat.
- **Bounce-walk / approach** — a light rhythmic walk toward camera.
- **Product flourish** — a small graceful hand-spin or pass of the product into frame.

**Rules:**

- **Small and fluid (AO.8):** subtle, smooth, human — a flourish, not a full routine; never stiff, jerky or robotic. Even calm reels get a low-amplitude version (a gentle sway, a soft hair tuck), never frozen.
- **Beat-synced (AR / AT.4):** land the move on a beat — bounce on the drop, twirl on the music swirl; place it on the AT.4 timeline and earn its own accent SFX (AR: no move, no accent).
- **Real physics, not the impossible move (AO.4 / BA.3):** ordinary real-world motion — it does **not** use up the one-impossible-move budget.
- **One or two per reel, not a constant fidget** — they punctuate (hook, transition, payoff); they don't fill every frame.
- **Rotate them (BC):** vary the micro-move concept to concept; don't default to the same twirl every time.
- **Great for:** hooks (a bounce-in), transitions (a pivot or hair-flick whip-cut), and payoffs (a mini twirl-and-settle on the reveal).
- **Fit-gate — only if it suits the concept (placement logic).** A micro-move goes in *only* when it fits the reel's category, register and mood — otherwise leave it out entirely. A bouncy dance step or playful twirl has no place in a calm Wellness / ASMR reel, a tender or solemn moment, or a serious Myth-bust / Tutorial; a swirl that breaks an intimate beat hurts more than it helps. The same logic governs every optional element (dance moves, swirls, surreal beats, SFX flourishes): **match it to the concept or drop it — an unsuitable flourish is worse than none. Fit beats inclusion.**

---

## Part AU — Anti-Hallucination & Accuracy Lock

Bright and energetic must **never** mean invented. Both models still hallucinate on **logos, hands, fine product details, and — on the weaker image models — text** — lock these down. (Nano Banana Pro now renders text reliably; see AU.2 — but always verify it.) This part works alongside AO.7 (believability) and AT.3 (tool hygiene).

### AU.1 — Product & brand truth

- **Match the real product exactly** — shape, cap, color, finish, proportions, logo — from the reference image. Never invent packaging, a different bottle, or a second product that isn't real.
- **Never fabricate brand names, logos, or label copy.** If the real label isn't available as a reference, keep the surface clean / minimal / out of focus rather than letting the model guess.
- One product identity per shot — don't let it morph, duplicate, or merge with another object across frames.

### AU.2 — Text rendering (now a strength on Nano Banana Pro — still verify)

- **You MAY render text on Nano Banana Pro (Gemini 3 Pro Image).** It is best-in-class at legible in-image text — taglines, on-screen hook copy, product-label and poster text, even long passages and multiple languages (AT.3). The old "never render text" rule was written for the weaker earlier models; drop it for Pro.
- **Still verify every rendered word letter-by-letter in the AU.6 QC pass** and regenerate if a glyph is off — legibility is strong, not guaranteed on every roll.
- **Two cases still belong in the editor, not the generator:** *guaranteed-perfect* legal / claim / brand-mandated copy (zero tolerance for a typo), and any *animated* text. For a real brand logo, still anchor it from the reference and keep it clean and in focus.
- **Animated captions / on-screen CTA copy (AO-S, AR)** are added in the editor for motion and timing control.

### AU.3 — Anatomy & objects

- **No anatomy errors:** correct hands/fingers (count them), teeth, eyes, ears, symmetry; no extra or fused limbs; jewelry and nails consistent and intact.
- Applicators / brushes / tools stay physically consistent; liquid and powder behave believably (ties to AO.4 real-physics + AO.7).
- **Mirror reflections must match** the subject and scene (GRWM through-mirror) — no mismatched or "extra person" reflection.

### AU.4 — Identity & continuity

- **Aira's identity lock is absolute** — same face, features and skin across every frame; no drift to a different person (relies on the character sheet, AO-X — not real photos).
- **Continuity across frames:** wardrobe, hair, makeup, product, set, lighting and color world stay consistent unless a beat is an *intentional* transformation. No props appearing/vanishing, no random color shifts.

### AU.5 — Claims & spoken/caption truth

- **No invented factual claims** in the spoken line or captions — no fake efficacy stats ("97% saw results"), made-up SPF / ingredient / "clinically proven" claims, fake awards or fabricated reviews.
- Keep it benefit-style and honest (AR tone) — confident, not counterfeit. If a real claim isn't supplied, don't manufacture one.

### AU.6 — QC verify pass (before publish)

Quick human check on every render: product/label correct · any text spelled right · hands/anatomy clean · reflection matches · Aira on-model · continuity holds · no invented claims. If any fails, regenerate or fix — don't ship the hallucination.

---

## Part AV — Frame Count (per concept)

Every concept runs on a **randomized frame count of 6 to 8 frames** (6, 7 or 8).

- **Roll it per concept** — pick 6, 7, or 8 fresh for each concept so the structure never feels templated.
- **Vary across a batch** — don't default every concept to the same number; mix 6 / 7 / 8 across the set (roll it like a hairstyle or the spoken-line placement).
- **Builds on the base 6-frame arc:** 6 = the core arc (Opening State → First Application → Build → Pivot → Near-Complete → Reveal). The +1 / +2 are *added* beats — an extra build/detail beat, a spoken aside, or an Exit/loop beat — never padding.
- **Each frame is still a designed start → end keyframe pair** (AT.0). More frames = more clips to chain via beat-locked cuts, **not** longer single clips.
- **Runtime scales with frame count** but stays feed-appropriate (≈ 30–60s); keep per-clip duration within the directive's range.

---

## Part AW — Outfit / Wardrobe Combo Library (30)

The 11 Wardrobe Pillars are *style families*; this gives concrete head-to-toe outfits so the look changes concept to concept (and reads modern, not templated).

### AW.0 — Rules

- **Identity lock unaffected:** outfit varies only — never Aira's face, features or skin.
- **Roll per concept** (use # as a d30) and **vary across a batch** — don't repeat the same outfit; mix pillars across the set (roll it like hair / makeup / frame count).
- **Match the pillar/register** to the reel, and let fabric/color fit the hero color world (AO.1) — bright, glossy, feed-ready.
- **Tasteful & non-sexualized (AO-X):** these are fashion-forward looks; describe the *garments*, never body parts. Keep coverage stylist-appropriate.
- **Festive / traditional looks (#19, #28)** are opt-in per AO-R — not the default.
- **Continuity (AU.4):** the outfit stays consistent within a concept unless a beat is an *intentional* wardrobe change.

## Part AX — Concept Category Library (26)

GRWM and Beauty Ad are no longer *the* two formats — they're two entries in this library. Pick the category that fits the goal; each runs the full engine (AO vibrance, AP hair, AQ makeup, AR audio, AS product, AT camera, AU accuracy, AV frame count, AW outfit) and pulls the libraries noted.

### AX.0 — Rules

- **Don't default to GRWM / Beauty Ad.** Choose the category by goal: convert, reach, save, share, build trust, or prestige.
- **Every category runs the same engine;** frame count still rolls 6–8 per AV (no fixed per-category count).
- **Mix categories across a batch** so the feed stays varied.
- **Match register, libraries and environment (Part AY)** to the category.
- **Suitability gate — place every element logically; drop what doesn't fit.** Only pull the moves and devices that suit the chosen category, register and mood. Micro-moves (AT.6), the Spin-Transform (AT.5), engagement structures (AX.5), surreal beats (AX.3), SFX flourishes (AR) and color arcs (AZ.7) are all *opt-in by fit*, never mandatory. If something doesn't belong in a given reel — a dance move or swirl in a calm / serious concept, a plot-twist gimmick in a sincere one, a loud flourish in an intimate beat — deliberately leave it out. **Fit beats inclusion: an unsuitable element hurts more than its absence.**
- GRWM (Part AO-R) and Beauty Ad (Parts P / AS) stay fully valid — just two options among many.

Aira's world beyond beauty / fashion. Same engine; lean on the noted environments (Part AY) + AR audio. Roll and mix these with the core 13 so the feed has real range.

### AX.3 — Signature lane: Cinematic / Surreal Aesthetic Film

Aira's flagship "watch-because-it's-mesmerizing" category — the true opposite of the utility content above. **No selling, no teaching, no talking** — pure visual mood carried entirely by the master track. It exists to build Aira as a *brand and a presence* (not a salesperson or teacher) and to bank saves and rewatches.

- **Why it's the signature lane:** it leans into the one thing only an AI persona can do — genuinely impossible, surreal imagery a human creator physically cannot film (levitation, dissolving into a swirl of petals, a dreamworld where the sky and light bend). It plays to every strength (AO-G grand worlds, AZ elevation, AO.8 motion, AT surreal shots, the one-impossible-move rule) and none of the weaknesses (no comedic timing, no long dialogue).
- **Spoken line OFF — the one deliberate exception to AR.** No VO and no competing captions; sound = the master track + the subtle ambient bed + soft diegetic SFX / Foley, with at most a non-lexical breath or sigh. The image does all the talking.
- **One impossible move still applies (AO.4 / BA.3):** the surreal beat is the hero, but still only one physics-break per shot — everything else obeys real physics so the magic reads as intentional, not a glitch.
- **Mood over message:** commit to one emotional arc and one color world; let it breathe — slower cuts, longer holds, suspended-motion stills (AO.8 / AT.3 / AZ).
- **Hero-locked (AO-G):** vast, surreal, out-of-this-world set, but Aira's face and the mood stay the anchor — spectacle serves the beauty moment, never swallows it.

| # | Category | Purpose · primary hook | Core beats | Pulls · register |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 22 | Cinematic / Surreal Aesthetic Film | Brand-building · saves & rewatch · stunning surreal visual hook (no sell, no talk) | World reveal → surreal hero moments → the one impossible beat → glow-out | AO-G · AZ · AO.8 · AT surreal · AR master-track-led (no VO) · reverent / electric / contemplative |

#### AX.3a — Surreal World Library (roll a world, then a mood)

A rollable bench of impossible worlds for this lane. Pick one (or blend two), then layer a Render-Style Mode (AX.3b) and a register. Build variety by rotating **world → what she does with it → mood**, and never repeat a world back-to-back (log it — Anti-Sameness). Every world must clear the catchy-or-cut bar (AX.3c) — vivid, luminous, never dull.

| Family | Rollable worlds (pick or blend) | Signature feel |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Sky & Cosmic | Cloud-walk at golden sunset · recline on a crescent moon trailing stars · leap between floating islands · conduct the aurora by hand · rain falling upward | Ethereal, vast, weightless |
| Water & Ocean | Underwater palace with fish of light · walking on the ocean surface, light blooming underfoot · glass-dome city on the seafloor, whales overhead | Serene, fluid, luminous |
| Nature & Elemental | Flowers bloom in her wake reviving a grey world · seasons change on a single turn · dancing with fire-ribbons that never burn · dunes rippling into liquid gold | Alive, organic, powerful |
| Chaotic-Beautiful | Slow-mo color-powder storm (abstract pigment, not festival Holi — AO-N) · ink blooming into shapes in water · a galaxy swirling like spilled paint · shattered glass freezing then reassembling | Dramatic, kinetic, slow-mo |
| Dreamlike / Impossible-Physics | Gravity tips sideways — she walks up the wall · endless doors, each a new world · her reflection steps out to join her · scale-flip (tiny in giant blooms, or giant over a tiny city) · time frozen, weaving through suspended raindrops | Surreal, mind-bending |
- **Massive, felt scale — make the bigness *land* on screen (the signature of this lane).** These worlds only hit if the viewer can *feel* how huge they are, so build scale deliberately into every frame: place Aira as a small figure against a towering, endless environment (a tiny silhouette under colossal clouds, dwarfed by a vast ocean, lost among giant blooms) so the size contrast does the work; open on extreme-wide establishing shots; stack foreground → midground → background with atmospheric haze receding into the distance for depth; use low angles looking *up* at towering elements; and reveal the vastness with a slow crane-up or pull-back (AT #2 / #18). Scale you can *feel*, not just see — overwhelming, awe-inducing grandeur. Still **hero-locked (AO-G)**: go as vast as possible, but Aira's face and the mood stay the anchor — the scale frames her, never buries her.
- **Pair the scale with a close, recognizable shot of Aira — establish her, *then* the bigness (this is what makes it feel perfect).** A tiny silhouette against a vast world sells the scale but loses *who* she is — so the vastness must always be partnered with at least one clear, **close hero shot where Aira's face reads unmistakably** (AO-X identity lock + hero-lock AO-G): her beauty and presence land first, or land right alongside the scale. Use the interplay deliberately — open close on her face → pull back to unveil the colossal world around her (AT #2 pull-back / #1 reverse push-in), *or* cut between the intimate close and the epic wide so the viewer keeps re-anchoring on her. That rhythm — **recognize her, then feel the scale** — is exactly what reads as perfection; an epic wide with only an unrecognizable dot in it is a fail. Rule of thumb: every surreal film carries both registers — the *intimate close* (who she is) and the *epic wide* (where she is).
- **Let her *react* — genuine amazement, expression matched to the moment (the final touch toward perfection).** In that close hero shot Aira is never a blank model posing in front of the spectacle — she *reacts* to it like a real person witnessing something impossible and breathtaking: eyes widening and lighting up, lips parting on a soft gasp, a slow wondering smile, breath caught, head tilting up to take in the vastness, a hand rising in awe. Crucially, her emotion must **match the world and the beat** — wonder for a vast reveal, delight as flowers bloom, serene reverence in a cosmic calm, exhilaration in a color storm, stillness held in a frozen-time moment — and it must read on **her face and body**, not just in the environment. This is what bridges the close and the wide: she *sells* the scale by visibly feeling it, so the viewer feels it with her. Ties to AO.8 (living, expressive performance) and the chosen register — a stunning world with a dead, unreacting face breaks the spell; her genuine, matched reaction is what makes the moment land as perfect.
- **Stage the reaction as an *arc*, not a single held expression — trigger → surprise → smile.** Let it play out in cause-and-effect order, never a pre-loaded "wow" face: (1) **trigger** — the wonder or the scale reveals on screen; (2) **surprise** — eyes widen, breath catches, lips part, a tiny still beat or half-step back; (3) **smile bloom** — a slow, genuine smile blooms as the payoff lands (the screenshot frame). Time it to the reveal and the music beat — surprise on the build, smile on the drop — so the feeling reads as clearly *caused by* the spectacle. Keep it matched and proportional (AO.8), never theatrical or instant; the arc is what sells the moment as real.
- **Only one impossible move per shot still holds (AO.4 / BA.3)** — even in these worlds, isolate the single magic beat; everything else obeys real physics so it reads as intentional, not a glitch.
- **Endlessly extensible:** these are seeds, not a closed list — generate fresh worlds by rotating the **force** (sky / water / fire / gravity / time / bloom / color) × **what she does** (walks through / conducts / dissolves into / reverses) × **mood**.

#### AX.3b — Render-Style Modes (the "shot like…" skin)

The same world looks completely different depending on the visual language it's rendered in. Pick one per film and commit:

- **Dreamy / Ethereal** — soft glow, bloom, gentle slow-mo, pastel-to-jewel light; floaty and weightless. The natural default for serene cosmic / water worlds.
- **Editorial Fashion-Film** — high-fashion campaign energy: bold color, crisp styling, striking poses, gallery-grade composition. The most "beauty-brand" of the three.
- **AAA Game-Cinematic** — the look of a modern game's cutscene / trailer: epic scale, dramatic backlight and god-rays, sweeping camera arcs, hero slow-mo, lens flare, and a frozen hero-pose button at the end. Beats that fit it: a hero reveal, a magical gear-up (= the Spin-Transform in a game skin), the unbothered walk through chaos, a cliff-edge overlook, an "ability activation" where she raises a hand and the elements respond. **Stylized, not literal photoreal** — lean into a rich, rendered, cinematic look rather than chasing Unreal-Engine realism the tools can't consistently hold; here the slightly-rendered quality reads as *style*, not as an AI tell.

#### AX.3c — Catchy-or-cut (everything beautiful, never dull)

Non-negotiable across this whole lane (and really the whole directive): **every world, frame and light setup must be eye-catching enough to freeze a scrolling thumb.**

- **Beautiful by default, dull is banned** — no flat / grey / murky lighting, no drab or empty environments. Every world reads vivid, luminous and rich (vibrance floor AO.1, hero-lock AO-G, elevation AZ).
- **Hook on the very first frame** — the opening instant is already stunning, never a slow warm-up; the scroll-stopper has to land in the first ~1 second (AO-S).
- **If a frame isn't catchy, it doesn't ship** — treat "would this stop me mid-scroll?" as a pass/fail gate. If it's merely *nice*, push the light / color / scale / motion until it's genuinely arresting.

### AX.4 — Tier 3: Engagement & Trend Formats

High-reach, high-save formats proven across beauty / lifestyle creators. Same engine; roll and mix with the rest of the library so the feed keeps real range.

| # | Category | Purpose · primary hook | Core beats | Pulls · register |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 23 | Unboxing / PR Haul (ASMR-led) | Trust & reach · "look what just arrived" + tactile sound hook | Sealed package → tactile unwrap → first-look reactions → favorite pick | AR ASMR (foreground) · AT macro · curious-confident / mischievous |
| 24 | BTS / Process / "How it's made" / Satisfying-making | Saves & trust · oddly-satisfying process hook | Raw start → satisfying process steps → finished reveal | AR ASMR · AT macro slider · knowing / contemplative |
| 25 | Listicle / Countdown ("X things…") | Saves & rewatch · numbered-promise hook | Title promise → fast numbered beats → best-for-last payoff | AR voice · on-screen number captions · curious-confident |
| 26 | Myth-busting / "This vs That" / Comparison | Trust & shares · bold claim / side-by-side hook | Myth or A-vs-B setup → test / demo → verdict | AR voice · AT split / match-cut · knowing |

### AX.5 — Engagement Structures (cross-cutting devices)

Not categories — *structural devices* you layer onto any category to lift retention, rewatches and shares. Pick one per concept where it fits.

- **Plot-twist / delayed gratification:** withhold the payoff and tease it up front ("wait for the end"), then deliver a bigger-than-expected reveal on the last beat. Drives full watch-through and rewatches.
- **Hook-swap:** plan 2–3 alternate opening frames / lines for the same concept and A/B them; if a reel underperforms, re-cut it with a different hook rather than rebuilding it. The first second is the single biggest retention lever (AO-S).
- **Perfect loop:** design the last frame to flow seamlessly back into the first (matching composition, motion and audio phrase) so the reel replays invisibly — banks extra watch-time and plays. Especially strong for Cinematic / Surreal (AX.3) and Transformation (#2).
