## Part AY — Studios & Environments

### AY.0 — Rules

- Every environment must meet the **vibrance floor (AO.1)** and stay **hero-locked (AO-G)** — beautiful, never dull; the face/product always wins the frame.
- **Roll per concept and match to the category + register;** vary environments across a batch.
- **Beauty & Editorial** → vast indoor studios or vivid outdoors. **GRWM** → intimate-but-aspirational indoors (spectacle would break the "with me" intimacy).
- **Rooted / festive settings are opt-in** (AO-R), never the default.

### AY.1 — Beauty & Editorial · Indoor (vast first)

- **Grand soundstage cyclorama** — massive color-drenched infinity wall, scale you can feel
- **Cathedral / atrium hall** — soaring ceilings, huge light beams, marble
- **Infinity mirror hall** — vast reflective repetition
- **Giant gradient / neon-gel hall** — big bold color walls
- **Reflective water-floor stage** — mirror-glass floor, dramatic scale
- **Glass conservatory / botanical greenhouse** — huge, bright, blooming
- **LED volume / virtual-production stage** — any world, vivid and limitless
- **Crystal / ice palace set** — luminous surreal grandeur
- *Intimate subset (for closeness, never the only choice):* glossy luxury vanity, marble bathroom, sunlit minimalist loft

### AY.2 — Beauty & Editorial · Outdoor (vivid only)

- ❌ Excluded as dull: rooftop golden-hour, desert dunes.
- **Tropical turquoise beach / ocean** — bright saturated blue
- **Infinity pool / poolside** — vivid water, glossy
- **Lush blooming garden / flower field** — color-saturated florals
- **Waterfall lagoon** — vivid greens and blues
- **Santorini-style white + cobalt architecture** — crisp, high-contrast
- **Neon city night** — vibrant bokeh, electric color
- **Colorful mural / street-art wall** — punchy graphic color
- **Surreal dreamscape** — impossible vivid sky, floating elements (the out-of-this-world lane)

### AY.3 — GRWM · Indoors (intimate, aspirational, bright)

Real, lived-in but aspirational personal spaces — bright and contemporary (AO-R), sized for intimacy not spectacle, always able to support the through-mirror move (AT #13) and the transformation arc.

- **Luxury glam vanity** — Hollywood-bulb mirror, product-lined
- **Sunlit modern bedroom** — big windows, airy, plush
- **Marble spa bathroom** — glossy, bright
- **Walk-in closet / dressing room** — lit shelves, full-length mirror (pairs with AW)
- **Boutique hotel suite** — chic designer room, big mirror
- **Penthouse window nook** — daylight + soft skyline
- **Mirror-lined dressing studio** — built for the through-mirror move
- **Pastel / color-pop dressing room** — fun, saturated
- **Clean-girl minimalist room** — warm neutrals, plants, natural light
- **Content-creator vanity nook** — ring light + window, UGC feel
- **Warm-lamp evening get-ready** — golden glow for a night out (kept bright, not muddy)

### AY.3-C — Make the GRWM background catchy (rich, not vast)

The GRWM room must stop the scroll on its own — but the lever is **richness, not spectacle**. Scale breaks the "with me" intimacy (AY.0), so don't make it vast; make the *intimate* space gorgeous in every other way, so the background is captivating without ever upstaging the face or the get-ready.

- **Never a plain wall** — the room is styled, characterful and beautiful; it should read as a dream space people screenshot, not an empty backdrop.
- **One hero feature per room** — give the eye a single standout anchor: a Hollywood-bulb mirror, a blooming flower wall, a glowing neon accent, a stunning window / skyline, a statement vanity or headboard.
- **Carry the hero color world (AO.1)** — a pastel / color-pop dressing room, a saturated accent wall, colored-gel or LED-strip accents, so the background pops on a phone in daylight.
- **Build real depth (AZ.3)** — foreground (a styled vanity surface) → midground (Aira) → background (window, decor, soft bokeh lights) so it never looks flat or pasted-on.
- **Dynamic, motivated light (AZ.2)** — window daylight, warm practicals, ring-light glow, warm bulb / vanity bokeh (clean and modern, never Diwali-style string-light kitsch — AO-N); let it evolve cool-prep → warm-reveal (AZ.7) so the room itself changes across the arc.
- **Life & motion in the background** — drifting sheer curtains, a candle flicker, rising steam, plants, a rain-streaked window, a soft skyline — give the set its own quiet motion so it's alive, not dead (the AO.8 spirit applied to the room).
- **Beautiful, intentional styling — not mess** — product-styled surfaces, flowers, books, fabrics, arranged with care; tidy-but-lived-in, never cluttered or distracting (BA.6 / AZ.6).
- **Use the mirror for layers** — reflections add depth and a second angle (AT #13 through-mirror).
- **Stay believable & intimate (AO.7 / AY.0)** — gorgeous but a real personal space; the moment it starts feeling like a vast commercial studio, pull it back to intimate.
- **Vary it every concept (BC)** — roll a different GRWM room and a different hero feature each time; never the same background back-to-back.

### AY.4 — Lifestyle category environments (Tier 2)

For the Part AX.2 categories. Same rules: vibrance floor (AO.1), hero-locked, bright-not-dull.

- **Bright modern kitchen** — sunlit, glossy counters, colorful produce (Food / Recipe)
- **Sunlit gym / movement studio** — airy, mirrored, bright (Fitness)
- **Cozy reading-and-coffee nook** — warm, plants, soft daylight (Wellness, Storytime)
- **Chic café** — aesthetic, bright, lifestyle backdrop (Café moments, vlog)
- *Reuse:* Wellness also pulls the spa bathroom / sunlit bedroom (AY.3); the Vlog roams across any existing set.

---

## Part AZ — Visual Elevation ("more and more")

Treat the last good result as the *floor*, not the target — every concept should look more elevated than the one before. This part pushes raw visual quality up while holding AO.7 believability and AU accuracy.

### AZ.0 — Continuous-improvement intent

- "Good enough" is the baseline to beat. On every concept and every regenerate, push at least one thing further — bigger world, better light, finer texture, cleaner composition.
- Elevate *without* overcooking: richer ≠ more effects. Hold AO.7 (real skin, no plastic / CGI tells) and AU (no invented detail) as you push.

### AZ.1 — Render quality

- Ultra-crisp, high-resolution feel with fine micro-detail; no softness, mush, smearing or low-res patches.
- Material truth: skin reads as skin, glass as glass, metal as metal, liquid as liquid — correct reflectivity, refraction and weight.

### AZ.2 — Light is the #1 elevator

- Sculpt with motivated, dimensional light — multiple roles (key, fill, rim / kicker, practical, background separation), never a flat single source.
- Keep glossy specular life on skin and product (AO.2); use negative fill / shadow shaping for form and depth.

### AZ.3 — Depth & dimensionality

- Always build foreground / midground / background layers; stage for parallax (AT #10).
- Use restrained atmosphere (a touch of bokeh, light bloom, sparse lit particles) for depth — never enough to dull or haze the frame (AO.1).

### AZ.4 — Texture & the hero "wow" moment

- Foreground tactile micro-texture: fabric weave, dewy pores, liquid surface tension, glass facets, powder grain, brush bristles.
- Each concept gets one hero macro "wow texture" beat (pairs with AR ASMR + AT #14 macro slider).

### AZ.5 — Color richness & harmony

- Commit to a deliberate color world (complementary or analogous), saturated and glossy (AO.1) but controlled (AO.7) — gradients, color-rhyme between product and set, specular interest. No muddy or flat single-color frames.

### AZ.6 — Composition & finish

- Intentional framing — thirds, centered hero, or leading lines; clean negative space; balanced, campaign / magazine-grade polish.
- Kill amateur tells: accidental dead-center, tilted horizons (unless intended), cluttered frames, distracting background objects.

### AZ.7 — Optional color-story arc (opt-in)

A deliberate color *journey* across the reel — the palette shifts frame to frame to mirror the emotional arc (e.g. cool muted open → warm saturated payoff, or near-monochrome → full color on the reveal). **Opt-in, not the default.**

- **Best for:** Cinematic / Surreal films (AX.3), Before & After / Transformation (#2), and any "drab → vivid" reveal.
- **Reconcile with the one hero-color-world rule (AO.1 / AZ.5):** a color *arc* is a controlled progression *between* related hero worlds, not random color chaos — move along one coherent path (analogous shift, or a saturation / temperature ramp) so every frame still reads as a committed color world, just an evolving one.
- **Never break continuity within a beat (BA.2 / BA.4):** the arc evolves *across* frames, never flickers inside a single beat. Log it so it doesn't fight color continuity.
- **Default stays:** most concepts commit to a single hero color world start to finish (AO.1); the arc is a deliberate creative choice, not a free pass.

---

## Part BA — Logical Coherence & Continuity (nothing that confuses the viewer)

Everything in frame and across frames must make physical, spatial and narrative sense. Beauty and spectacle never excuse confusion.

### BA.0 — The viewer-clarity test (litmus)

- If a first-time viewer would think "wait — where did that come from / how is that possible / why did that change / what am I looking at," it fails. Fix it or cut it. Clarity beats cleverness.

### BA.1 — Spatial logic

- Objects, product, props and set occupy real, consistent space with a coherent geography; scale stays consistent shot to shot.
- Hands actually hold and contact what they appear to; eyelines and gaze land where they should; camera position makes spatial sense.

### BA.2 — Light & shadow logic

- Light direction, color and intensity stay consistent within a frame and evolve consistently across frames; shadows fall the correct way; highlights and reflections match the real light sources.
- Mirror reflections match the subject and scene and keep correct orientation (GRWM through-mirror, AU.3).

### BA.3 — Physical plausibility

- Gravity, liquid behavior, fabric drape and hair physics all read believable — except the single permitted impossible move (AO.4), which must be the *only* break and must look like intentional magic, not a glitch.
- **Cause-and-effect directional logic — source above/before its effect.** Place the producer of every action correctly relative to its result. A bottle dispensing serum sits *higher* and the drop falls *below* it, mid-air, downward (never level with or above the bottle). A pour goes downward into the vessel; spray emits outward *from* the nozzle in the direction it points; a brush / applicator meets the skin exactly where the color appears; steam rises, droplets and powder fall; splashes radiate *from* the point of impact; a shadow falls on the opposite side from its light source. If the spatial direction of a cause and its effect is reversed or mismatched, the viewer instantly reads it as wrong — get the geometry of the action right.
- **The one impossible move must still obey its own physics — and leave everything else intact.** When you use the single permitted magic beat (levitation, materialization, self-pour, particle assembly — AO.4), isolate it: *only* that one element breaks reality, and everything around it keeps obeying gravity and real physics. The magic itself must be internally consistent and precise — a levitating bottle or suspended drop still carries correct weight cues, lighting, shadow and reflection for exactly where it sits in space, moves along a clean, motivated path at a believable speed, and never clips, jitters, drifts or pops. It must read as deliberate, controlled magic — never as a glitch or as the scene's gravity randomly failing. And it still respects the directional logic above: e.g. a levitating serum drop holds or rises with intent, but if it then falls it falls *downward*, below its source.

### BA.4 — Continuity across frames

- Wardrobe, hair, makeup, product, props, set and time-of-day hold steady unless a beat is an *intentional* progression (cumulative makeup build, an explicit change). Props set down stay put; nothing appears, vanishes, teleports or shifts color without reason (AU.4).

### BA.5 — Action & sequence logic

- Each beat is a plausible next step in a real sequence (reach → open → apply → blend → result); no skipped or impossible steps.
- The product used matches the result shown; the applicator matches the product; the "before" and "after" are the same person and scene.

### BA.6 — Narrative & on-screen logic

- The concept tells one clear, followable story; spoken line and captions match what is on screen; no contradictory cues (e.g. morning light under a night caption).
- On-screen text sits in the UI safe zones (AO-S) and never covers the hero face / product.

---

## Part BB — Motion-Ready Power Frames (stills built to move)

Every still (the Gemini keyframe) should be composed so it *animates well* — a frame that's beautiful but motion-dead wastes the video step. Build motion potential into the still itself.

- **Leave room to move:** include negative space in the direction of the intended action (hair swing, camera push, product rise) so the motion has somewhere to go.
- **Pose mid-gesture, not at rest:** capture a frozen instant of motion — the peak of a turn, a hand lifting, fabric mid-lift (AO.8 / AT.3) — so the video starts already alive.
- **Stage moveable elements:** include things that *can* move — loose hair, flowing fabric, particles, liquid, light — at least two per hero frame (AO.6).
- **Encode the camera move in the start ↔ end delta** (AT.0) so the interpolation has a clear path to follow.
- **Keep identity and continuity locked** across the pair (AU.4) — only the intended motion changes between start and end.

---

## Part BC — Anti-Sameness Rotation Engine (never twice the same)

The libraries are big on purpose — this is the rule that *forces* variety so the feed never feels templated.

- **Log every roll:** track the category (AX), hair (AP), makeup (AQ), outfit (AW), environment (AY), register, frame count (AV), surreal world + render mode (AX.3a/b), transformation mechanic + deployment + medium (AT.5 / AT.5-T) and signature micro-move (AT.6) used per concept.
- **No back-to-back repeats:** never reuse the same category, surreal world, render mode, transformation mechanic / deployment / medium or dominant register in consecutive concepts.
- **Rotate the dials independently:** change at least 3–4 dials between any two concepts so even same-category reels look distinct.
- **Roll, don't default:** treat each dial as a fresh roll per concept (re-roll on best-fit clash), never a habit.
- **Combinatorial reality:** with 26 categories × 30 hair × 24 makeup × 30 outfits × ≈30 environments × 7 registers, the on-paper space is ≈100M+; curated best-fit narrows it, but disciplined rotation keeps thousands of genuinely distinct, premium concepts in play — effectively limitless non-repeating content.

---

## Part BD — GRWM Captivation Kit (single-location, scroll-stopping)

GRWM is shot in **one place**, in **one continuous get-ready arc** — which is exactly why it risks going flat and scroll-past. The fix is never "add another location"; it's to vary the *frame, pace, sound and story* inside the one room and make the *transformation* the engine. Run every GRWM concept through these levers so a one-room get-ready becomes impossible to scroll past — and worth a like, a save and a rewatch.

### BD.0 — The single-location problem (and the fix)

- One room + one activity = monotony risk. Don't solve it by leaving the room — solve it by changing **what the camera sees, how fast it moves, what we hear, and why we're watching**, while the bare → glam change carries the spine.

### BD.1 — Hook the first second (reveal-first / end-first)

- Open on a flash of the **finished look** (the payoff), then smash-cut back to the bare "let's get ready" start. The curiosity gap — *how did she get there?* — drives full watch-through (ties AO-S, AX.5).
- Alternatives: a bold spoken hook (AR), a striking macro (a pigment-loaded brush, a droplet on glass), or the single most dramatic beat shown out of order. The first ≈1s must already be arresting.

### BD.2 — Give it a reason (story spine + stakes)

- Get ready *for something specific* — a date, a shoot, an event, "20 minutes till he's here." A reason creates stakes and a finish line, so people stay for the reveal.
- A tiny narrative or relatable POV ("the text that started it") beats a context-free routine — it gives the reel a story, not just a process.

### BD.3 — Make the transformation the engine (visible momentum)

- Build a clear **bare → build → reveal** arc where every frame reads visibly more "done" than the last. The before↔after delta is the thing people actually watch for — protect it; don't show the finished face too early.
- **Withhold the payoff:** keep the full face / eyes partly hidden (hair down, an angle, a hand, a turned back) until the reveal beat so the finish truly lands.

### BD.4 — Never let one room feel static (vary the frame)

- Rotate framing inside the *same* space so it reads as many shots: through-mirror (AT #13), macro close-up (lash, lip, a brush sweep), overhead vanity flatlay, profile, over-the-shoulder, and a wide reaction shot.
- Shift **distance and lens** beat to beat; let the light **evolve** across the arc (cool prep → warm reveal — opt-in AZ.7).
- Treat the room as a styled "character" — depth layers, beautiful props, dynamic, motivated light (AY.3 / AZ.2). Use the mirror as a second camera.

### BD.4-G — Eye-line: mirror-gaze to *do*, camera-gaze to *talk*

A real GRWM has a built-in eye-line tension: while she's **applying** something she naturally looks at her own reflection or down at the product (away from the lens), but to **talk to the viewer** she has to look into the camera. Choreograph the two gazes deliberately instead of letting them fight.

- **Two clear gaze modes:**
    - **Doing-gaze (application beats):** eyes on her reflection in the mirror or down on the product / hands — absorbed, focused, authentic. This is correct and intimate; don't force her to stare at the lens while doing precise work (it looks unnatural, and she physically can't see what she's doing).
    - **Talking-gaze (address beats):** the instant she speaks to the viewer (AR spoken line, an aside, the hook, the reveal), she lifts her eyes and connects **directly with the camera** — the parasocial eye contact that earns the like / follow (BD.9).
- **Use the mirror as the bridge (the clean fix).** Shoot her reflection so one setup serves both: looking at her *own* face / hands in the mirror = doing; lifting her eyes to meet the *camera through the mirror* = talking to the viewer (eye contact via the reflection reads as looking right at them — AT #13 through-mirror). This lets her flip from doing to talking without breaking the scene or repositioning.
- **Switch on the beat, not randomly.** Tie the gaze change to the AR spoken-line placement and the AT.4 timeline: she drops the doing-gaze and looks to camera (or to camera-through-mirror) exactly as the line lands, then returns to her reflection / product after. The lift-and-connect is a deliberate, timed beat — never a constant stare at the lens, never a constant head-down.
- **Don't cross the wires.** Never have her *talk to the viewer while fixed on her own reflection as if it's herself*, and never have her *do delicate application while locked on the lens* — both read wrong. Match gaze to intent on every beat.
- **The reveal is the big camera-gaze (BD.6).** The payoff "turn" is when she finally turns from the mirror to meet the camera directly — save the strongest, fullest, most confident eye contact for that moment.
- **Eyeline logic holds (BA.1 / AU.3):** wherever she looks must be spatially correct for the room and camera, and the mirror reflection must match her and the scene (correct orientation, no mismatched or "extra person" reflection).

### BD.5 — Pace & beat (slow-luxe → fast-build → punch-reveal)

- Ramp the rhythm: a luxurious slow open, a faster beat-synced build, a punchy reveal on the drop (AO.4 / AR beat-map).
- Speed-ramp the satisfying texture moments — brush sweep, cream squish, spritz (AT #7) — the premium GRWM cue real beauty creators use.

### BD.6 — The reveal "turn" (the payoff beat)

- Land the finish on a signature move — a mirror turn-to-camera, a hair flip, a mini twirl-and-settle (AT.5 / AT.6) — beat-synced to the biggest moment, on the best light and best frame. The reveal must **over-deliver** on the hook's promise; an underwhelming "after" kills the whole reel.

### BD.7 — Sound is the secret weapon (ASMR + voice)

- A single location is carried by **sound**: foreground tactile ASMR (cap clicks, brush sweeps, spritz, tap-on-glass, cream squish) plus the bold spoken line placed *somewhere* in the arc — not always the open (AR).
- Trending track, beat-locked; design it to loop. On a one-room reel, sound is half the rewatch value.

### BD.8 — The one surprise (screenshot / share beat)

- Drop the single permitted impossible micro-moment — product floats into her hand, color blooms across the lid, or a full transformation reveal rolled from the mechanic bench — not always a swirl (AO.4 / AT.5 / AT.5-T / BA.3). It's the share / screenshot beat that makes an ordinary routine memorable. One per shot only.

### BD.9 — Engineer the reward (like · save · comment · rewatch)

- **Saves:** weave in one genuinely useful, save-worthy tip ("the step everyone skips") — saves are heavily algorithm-rewarded.
- **Comments:** a light open prompt — "which look?", "day or night?" — to bait replies.
- **Likes / follows:** a personality beat — a glance to camera, a wink, a relatable aside — the parasocial connection that earns the follow.
- **Rewatch:** design a **perfect loop** — the last frame flows seamlessly back into the first (AX.5).
- **Watch-through:** a curiosity caption that only pays off at the end ("wait for the eyes").

### BD.10 — Keep it real, on-model and suitable

- Every device above still passes AO.8 (alive, never robotic), AO.7 (don't overcook), AU (accuracy + identity lock), BA (spatial / physics / continuity logic) and the **fit-gate** (AX.0 / AT.6): a captivation trick that doesn't suit the reel's mood gets dropped. A dance bounce has no place in a calm self-care GRWM — **fit beats inclusion**.

---

## Part BE — Beauty-Ad Signature Twists & "Every Reel Competes" (no transformation crutch)

A transformation (spin / swirl / portal / petals-on-water — AT.5 / AT.5-T) is *one* way to be catchy, not *the* way. Most beauty ads won't use one — and a straight product reel must never end up the weak one on the feed next to the flashy transformation reels. This part does two jobs: a bench of unique beauty-ad enhancers (BE.1), and a hard rule that **every** beauty ad — transformation or not — clears the same scroll-stop bar (BE.2).

### BE.0 — Catchiness is not a transformation

- **Never let "no magic transformation" mean "less catchy."** A clean product reel competes on idea, craft and *benefit-drama* — not on a spin. The transformation engine is optional flavor; over-using it is itself repetition (AO-N / BC). Many of the strongest beauty ads have zero transformation.
- **The catchiness lives in the hook, the benefit made visible, the elevation and the sound** — all available to a reel that never spins once.

### BE.1 — Signature beauty-ad twists (unique enhancers — none require a transformation)

Roll one or more per reel where they fit; they elevate a *straight* ad without any spin/swirl/portal.

- **Make the benefit *visible* (the biggest AI-only lever):**
    - **Sensory translation** — show the *feeling*: cooling → frost blooming on skin · warming → soft embers · hydration → a parched landscape going lush · brightening → sunrise breaking over her face.
    - **Problem dissolves** — render the concern (a dull grey film, frizz-static, a fog) and visibly *wash or bloom it away* into glow/color.
    - **Ingredient-bloom** — what it's *made of* erupts around her: rose serum → rose storm, vitamin-C → citrus light, honey mask → golden flow.
- **Reactive world / glow-cast** — color saturates, flowers bloom, or **light emanates from her skin** where she applies (inner glow made literal — the one impossible move, AO.4).
- **Hero macro "wow texture" beat** — one extreme-macro tactile shot (droplet surface tension, cream swirl, powder grain, brush bristle) + foreground ASMR (AZ.4 / AR).
- **Split-world before/after** — the frame splits dull-desaturated vs glowing-vibrant, and the line sweeps across as she applies.
- **Mono-color drench** — a fully color-drenched world (one bold hero color on set, light and styling) with the product as the single contrast pop — editorial and screenshot-able.
- **UGC-to-magic flip** — open raw / handheld / "real girl," then *snap* into the elevated cinematic world on the product touch (authenticity → magic).
- **Dive-into-the-product / scale-flip + texture match-cut** — a single drop becomes an ocean/cloudscape she's inside, then pull back to hero; rhyme the product texture with the world (cream ↔ clouds, gold oil ↔ liquid sunset, powder ↔ dunes).
- **Weightless product choreography** — products orbit her like a constellation and assemble into the hero in her hand (premium, one impossible move).

### BE.2 — The "every reel competes" gate (run it on *every* beauty ad, transformation or not)

If a straight reel only works because it's "clean," it is **not done** — push it until it's arresting on its own. Every beauty ad must carry:

- **A killer first second** — result-flash, bold macro, or a spoken hook lands in ≈1s (AO-S / AX.5).
- **At least one "wow" beat** — a hero macro, a benefit-made-visible moment, a striking reveal, or a single impossible micro-move. **It does *not* have to be a transformation.**
- **Elevation maxed (AZ)** — light, color richness, depth, texture and composition pushed to campaign grade; vibrance floor held (AO.1).
- **Sound that carries it** — foreground ASMR + a bold, meaningful spoken line (AR), beat-locked and loop-designed.
- **A reason / micro-story or POV where it fits** — stakes and a finish line drive watch-through (BD.2 spirit).
- **A reveal/payoff that over-delivers** — the "after" must beat the hook's promise (BD.6 applied to all beauty ads, not just GRWM).
- **Pass/fail test:** *"Set against the flashiest transformation reel on the feed, would this still stop a thumb?"* If it's merely *nice*, push the light / color / idea / benefit-drama until it's genuinely arresting. Catchy-or-cut (AX.3c) applies to **every** beauty ad.

### BE.3 — Rotate so straight reels don't all look alike (BC)

- **Vary the enhancer per reel** — don't default every non-transformation ad to "glossy hero on a color wall." Roll a different BE.1 twist, a different hook type and a different hero beat each time; log it (BC).
- **Fit-gate (AX.0):** pull only the twists that suit the product, register and mood — an unsuitable twist hurts more than its absence (**fit beats inclusion**).
- **Net:** transformation reels and straight reels sit at the *same* quality bar — the feed reads premium and varied either way, and no beauty ad is ever "below" the others.

---

## Part BF — Micro-Magic / Sparkle Touches (the small details, controlled)

The small "magic-type" touches that make a *single frame* feel special and stop a thumb — a glint travelling across a cap, a catchlight sparkle in the eye, a droplet suspended mid-air, a glow pulsing off the skin. These sit *on top of* the big mechanics (AT.5 transformation, BE benefit-magic) as fine detail. The whole point of this part is the discipline that lets you push them **further without turning the frame into messy chaos** — more magic, always controlled.

### BF.0 — The control law (more magic, never messy)

- **One hero touch + at most one or two whisper-quiet supports per frame.** Each frame gets a *single* lead magic detail the eye goes to, plus at most one–two subtle background touches. Never a frame full of competing sparkles.
- **Coordinate, don't scatter — this is the key to "more but controlled."** To do *more*, layer touches that all serve the *same* moment and share the *same* logic (same light source, same direction, same beat) so three coordinated touches read as **one rich moment**, not three random effects. Stacking *unrelated* touches is what looks messy.
- **Motivated + real physics (except the one impossible move).** Every touch has a cause — light catches because she turned, powder puffs because the brush tapped. Only **one** physics-breaking touch per shot (AO.4 / BA.3); everything else obeys real physics.
- **Slow-mo + negative space = readable.** Give each touch room and time — a touch the eye can't register isn't magic, it's clutter. Speed-ramp the hero touch so it actually lands (AT #7).
- **Escalate across the reel, don't front-load.** Tiny touches early (a glint, a dew-catch), building to the one big sparkle / impossible beat on the reveal — controlled escalation, not constant fireworks.
- **Restraint gate:** if a frame already has a strong hero beat, *cut* the extras. When in doubt, fewer. The magic must read intentional and premium — never busy, gimmicky or "filtery" (AO.7).

### BF.1 — The micro-magic bench (roll 1–2 per frame)

- **Light & sparkle:** a glint travelling across the product label / cap · a tiny "ting" sparkle on a glossy lip / tooth / wet eye-highlight · a catchlight bloom in her eyes · a soft lens-flare or god-ray sweep as she turns · a one-beat bokeh shimmer behind her.
- **Product & liquid:** a single serum drop falling in slow-mo with a clean ripple · the cap clicking open / floating off by itself (impossible — one per shot) · a droplet suspended mid-air before it falls · a brush-tap powder puff · dew / condensation beading on the bottle · a swipe that blooms color like ink in water.
- **Skin & glow:** a glow pulsing *out of* the skin after application · a dewy light-catch rolling across a cheekbone · frost crystals blooming (cooling) or soft heat-shimmer (warming) · a water droplet tracing slowly down glowing skin.
- **Air & particle:** a few petals / sparkles / fairy-dust drifting through (subtle, not a storm) · soft steam curling up · a sparkle trail following a fingertip / applicator · glitter settling like slow snow · a breeze lifting her hair with a light-sweep.
- **Face & moment:** a wink with a sparkle · the surprise → smile bloom timed to the reveal · a soft caught breath before the payoff · a mirror turn where the reflection catches light a beat before she does.
- **Tiny impossible touches (one per shot):** products assembling into her hand · a flower blooming where she dabs the product · a ripple of color spreading from where her finger touches the mirror.

### BF.2 — Pushing it "more" — controlled amplification recipes

- **Coordinated combo:** pair touches that reinforce one moment — e.g. on the reveal: glow-pulse from the skin + a single catchlight sparkle in the eye + one drifting sparkle, all on the *same* beat in the *same* warm light. Three touches, one feeling.
- **Cause-chain:** let one touch trigger the next in sequence — brush tap → powder puff → it catches the light → settles. A tiny choreographed chain reads rich *and* controlled, never random.
- **Hero + echo:** the big touch happens once (the impossible beat), then a faint echo lingers (a last sparkle drifting down) — depth without clutter.
- **Make the magic *mean* something:** match the medium to the product — frost for cooling, embers for warming, dew for hydrating, citrus-light for vitamin-C — so it reads as the benefit, not decoration (ties BE.1).

### BF.3 — Fit & rotation

- **Fit-gate (AX.0):** match every touch to the product, register and mood — a sparkle-storm in a clinical skincare demo reads wrong; a calm reel gets gentle dew, not bursts. Unsuitable touch → drop it (**fit beats inclusion**).
- **Rotate (BC):** vary which touches you pull per reel and log them; never the same signature sparkle every time.
- **Still passes AU / AO.7 / BA:** no invented detail, real skin, coherent physics; the one-impossible-move cap always holds.

---

## Override notes to existing Sys Directive 3 sections

Apply these targeted edits to the base file so the defaults stop pulling muted:

- **Colorist / grade section:** add a top-line rule — "For beauty / GRWM / social content, Part AO overrides all muted colorist references. Use bright, glossy, saturated commercial-beauty grading."
- **GRWM section:** replace the "heavy emotional stakes + muted/intimate" default with Part AO-R (contemporary vivid; rooted opt-in).
- **Register defaults:** note that beauty/GRWM/social default to electric / curious-confident / mischievous (Part AO.5).
- **Negatives block:** append the MUST-POP positive mandates (Part AO.6) so frames can't drift dull.
- **Identity lock:** unchanged — explicitly note hair color/texture and Aira's Indian identity still hold; only styling/setting modernizes.
- **Refine — "one impossible move per shot":** keep the cap, but scope it precisely. It limits **physics-breaking miracles only** (levitation, materialization, self-pouring, teleport, particle assembly) — **max one per shot, always** (protects believability + render quality, per AO.7). It does **not** limit **real-physics energy** (bursts, splashes, whips, sparkle, hair swing), which AO.4 makes unlimited for beauty / GRWM / social.
- **Conflict — VO frame-slotting in GRWM (Part Q frames 4–5):** **Part AR overrides it** — the spoken line's placement is randomized across concepts, not pinned to the pivot/closer frames.
- **Don't double up:** Part AS and Part AO-S now defer to Part P and the scroll-stopper checklist respectively — when merging, extend those existing sections, don't paste duplicates.
- **Frame count:** the base GRWM "default 6 frames" becomes **6–8 frames, randomized per concept** (Part AV) — the 6-frame arc stays the core; 7th/8th are added beats.
- **Two-format → multi-format:** GRWM and Beauty Ad are now two entries in the **Concept Category Library (Part AX, 26 categories)**. Don't treat them as the only formats — pick the category by goal and pull the matching environment (Part AY).
- **Visual elevation & logical coherence:** continuously push visual quality higher (Part AZ) and enforce full spatial / light / physics / continuity / narrative logic via a first-time-viewer clarity test (Part BA) — extend the base directive's existing spatial-logic and anti-drift handling rather than duplicating it.

## Quick-apply checklist (before generating any beauty / GRWM / social reel)

- [x]  Commercial Beauty Energy mode ON (AO.0)
- [x]  Hero color world chosen; vibrance floor met (AO.1)
- [x]  High-key glossy light; no grain/lifted blacks (AO.2–AO.3)
- [ ]  No festival-kitsch lighting — no Diwali-style fairy / twinkle / diya / rope lights anywhere; clean cinematic light only. Any Holi-like color-powder rendered as abstract pigment, never the Indian festival (AO-N)
- [x]  Multiple kinetic elements + beat-synced cuts (AO.4)
- [x]  Subject alive & human — natural hands / body / expression, never robotic or static; body moves like fluid everywhere + living stillness even when standing (breathing, micro-shifts, never frozen); energy matched to register — high-energy dynamic, calm serene-but-alive (AO.8)
- [x]  Aira is the hero — her charm / presence carries the frame; outfit / makeup / product flatter her but never upstage her; charisma preserved everywhere (amplitude per register) (AO-H / AO.8)
- [x]  Electric/curious-confident/mischievous register; bright pillar (AO.5)
- [x]  MUST-POP mandates satisfied (AO.6)
- [x]  Beauty: grand surreal world, hero-locked face/product (AO-G)
- [x]  Scroll-stopper checklist applied + phone-bright + 9:16 safe zones (AO-S)
- [x]  GRWM: contemporary vivid, rooted only if festive (AO-R)
- [x]  GRWM: single-location Captivation Kit applied — reveal-first hook, a reason / stakes, transformation momentum, varied framing within one room, pace ramp, signature reveal turn, ASMR + bold line, one surprise beat, and a like / save / comment / rewatch lever (BD)
- [x]  GRWM eye-line choreographed — doing-gaze on mirror / product while applying, camera-gaze (direct or through-mirror) on every spoken / address beat and the reveal turn; switched on the beat, eyelines spatially correct & reflection matches (BD.4-G)
- [x]  Hair style rolled from the 30, best-fit confirmed (AP)
- [x]  Vivid but believable — "don't overcook" guardrail passed (AO.7)
- [x]  Makeup look rolled from the library, best-fit confirmed (AQ)
- [x]  Audio set: trending track + beat-map + ASMR layer (AR)
- [x]  Spoken line is bold, confident & meaningful to *this* reel + placement randomized (opener / mid / reveal / aside) (AR)
- [x]  Delivery sounds human, not robotic — natural rhythm, breaths, emphasis; clean lip-sync; no flat TTS (AR)
- [x]  Every video prompt's audio section itemizes each SFX — source · action · moment · full envelope · room acoustics; include the subject's own Foley (footsteps, door, clap, snap, clothing rustle, pick-up / set-down); accent SFX synced exactly to the move (no move = no accent) + a subtle ambient bed under every frame so none feels empty; diegetic SFX only, no in-clip music; regenerate don't post-patch (AR)
- [x]  Concept ends with a precise Master Track Brief (genre · mood-arc · instruments · tempo/key · energy-arc with hit-point timecodes · reference · length · instrumental + VO headroom) for Gemini music-gen; subtle LOW-volume bed (never full — only fills the silence/void, ducks under VO + SFX), one track for the whole reel (AR)
- [x]  Part P applied (re-lit bright) + swatch / application / before→after beats (AS)
- [x]  Camera move chosen per beat + start/end keyframes designed to encode it; every image prompt states the exact camera angle / height / lens / framing, since the start still *is* the clip's opening frame and the animation begins from that exact position (AT / AT.0)
- [x]  Continuity-reel keyframe pairs built bit-by-bit & clean — only the intended move/action differs start→end, deliberate non-cluttered staging, no impossible bridge, exact delta stated, passes clarity test (AT.0-K / BA.0)
- [x]  Cross-frame object lock — every recurring object (chair, vanity, mug, etc.) described in precise detail & reused verbatim; object/set continuity sheet kept; position / state / count held across frames (AT.0-K / BA.4 / AU.4)
- [x]  Image prompt = static frame only (no motion verbs); video prompt = one move + action + audio; no contradictions, one idea per prompt (AT.3)
- [x]  VEO prompt includes a timestamped timeline (2–4 segments) so beats run in sequence, not all at once (AT.4)
- [x]  No hallucination: product / label / logo accurate, no garbled or invented text (AU.1–AU.2)
- [x]  Anatomy clean, identity locked, continuity + reflections consistent (AU.3–AU.4)
- [x]  No invented claims or stats in spoken line / captions; QC pass done (AU.5–AU.6)
- [x]  Frame count rolled 6–8, varied across concepts (AV)
- [x]  Outfit rolled from the 30, pillar/register + color-world fit, varied across concepts (AW)
- [x]  Concept category chosen by goal — not defaulting to GRWM / Beauty; spans core / lifestyle / surreal / Tier-3 engagement formats (Unboxing / BTS / Listicle / Myth-bust) (AX / AX.4)
- [x]  Environment rolled & matched — vast/vivid for beauty-editorial, intimate-aspirational for GRWM; for GRWM make the room catchy via richness not scale — a hero feature, color pop, real depth, dynamic light & background life, beautifully styled (AY.3-C); vibrance floor + hero-lock (AY)
- [x]  Visual-elevation pass: light / depth / texture / color / composition pushed to campaign-grade; one hero "wow" texture moment; still believable (AZ)
- [x]  Logical-coherence pass: spatial / light / physics / continuity / action / narrative all make sense; passes the first-time-viewer clarity test — nothing confusing (BA)
- [x]  Engagement structure layered where it fits — plot-twist / hook-swap / perfect loop; consider a carousel cut + shoppable tags (AX.5 / AO-S)
- [x]  If surreal / transformation: transformation mechanic × deployment × medium rolled & not repeated — vary the grammar, not just the medium (AT.5 / AT.5-T); reaction staged as trigger → surprise → smile (AX.3a); optional color-story arc considered (AZ.7)
- [x]  Signature micro-move added where it fits — a mini swirl / bounce / hair-flick / pivot; beat-synced, rotated, small & fluid not robotic (AT.6)
- [x]  Stills built to move — negative space for the action, posed mid-gesture, moveable elements staged, camera move in the keyframe delta (BB)
- [x]  Anti-Sameness logged — no back-to-back repeats; 3–4 dials changed from the last concept (BC)
- [x]  Fit-gate passed — every included element (micro-move, dance beat, swirl, engagement structure, surreal beat, SFX flourish, color arc) suits the concept's category / register / mood; anything unsuitable deliberately left out (AX.0 / AT.6)
- [x]  Fast Audio Finishing pass run before publish (AR)
